How the land of England was first named Albion / And by what encheson it was
so named
In the noble land of Sirrie / there was a noble king and mighty and a man of
great reno^me / that me callid Dioclisian, that well and worthily him governed
and ruled through his noble chyualrye / so that he co^querd all the lands about
him / so that almost all the kings of the world to him were entendant / Hit
befell thus that this dyoclisian spoused a gentil damisel / that was wonder fair
that was his emes daughter labana / and she loved him as reason would / so that
he gate upon her xxxiij daughters / of the which the eldest me callid Albyne /
and these damisels when they come unto age bicome so fair that it was wonder /
wherefore that this dyoclisia^ anon let make a somenyng / and commanded by his
lre^s / that all the kings that helden of him should come at a certain day. as
in his lre^s we re contained to make a ryal feste / At which day thider they
comen / and brought with hem amyrals princes and dukes, and noble chiualrye /
The feste was ryally awayed / and there they lived in joy and myrthe enough,
that it was wonder to wit / And it befell thus that this dyoclisian thought to
marye his daughters among all tho kings that tho were at that sole^pnyte /
and so they spaken and did that albyne his eldest daughter / and al her
sustres richely were married unto xxxiij kings / that were lords of greece
honor and of power at this solempnyte / And when the solempnite was done,
every king took his wife and lad hem in to her own country / and there made
hem queen's / And it befell thus afterward / that this dame Albyne bycome so
stout and so stern / that she told little prys of her lord / and of him had
scorn and despyte / and would not done his will / but she would have her own
will in diverse matters / and all her other sustres euerychone bear hem so evil
against her lords that it was wonder to wit / and for as much as hem thought
that her husbondes were naught of so hye parage comen as her fader / But tho
kings that were her lords would have chastysed hem with fair speech and
behestes, and also by yeftes / and warned hem in fair manner upon al love and
friendship that they should amend her lither conditions / but al was for naught
/ for they dyden her own will in all thing / that hem lyked. and had of power
/ wherefore tho / xxxiij / kings upon a time and oftymes beten their wynes for
they wend that they would have amended her tatches / and her wicked thewes /
but of such conditions they were / that for fair speech and warning, they
dydden all the wers / and for setynges ^ones much wers / wherefore the king that
had wedded albyne wrote the tatches and conditions of his wife albyn and the
letter sent to dioclisian her fader, And when the other kings herd that
albynes lord had sent a letter to dyoclisian / anon they sent lre^s ensealed
with her seals the conditions / and the tatches of her wives. When the king
dyoclisian saw and herd so many playntes of his daughters / he was soore
ashamed / and byoome wonder angry and wroth toward his daughters / and thought
both night and day if he might tho amend it / that they so mysdid / and anon
sent his letters unto the xxxiij kings / that they should come to him / and
bring with hem her wives euerychone at a certain day / for he would there
chastyse them of their wyckednes / if he might in any manner wise / so that the
kings comen al at that day and time that tho was set bitwene hem and the
king. Dioclisian hem vnderfeng with much honor and made a solemn fest to all that were un der his lorship / and the thyrdde day. after this solempnyte. the
king Dioclisian sent after his xxxiij daughters that they should come and speak
with him in his chamber / and when they were come / he spa^ unto hem of their
wykkednesse and of her cruelte and despitously hem reproved and vnderna^ / and
to them he said / if they would not be chasty sed / they should his love lose for
evermore / and when the ladies herd all thie they bycomen abashed and gretely
ashamed. and to her fader they said that they would make al amends / and so
they departed out from her faders chamber / and dame albyn that was the eldest
suster lad hem al in to her chamber / and tho made wide all that were therein so
that no life was among hem / but she and her sustres y fere / Tho said this
albyne, my fair sistres well we known that the king our fader us has reproved
shamed and despised for enchesen to make us obedye^t unto our husbondes / but
certes that shall I never whiles that I live / sith that I am come of a more
hyer kings blood than mine husbonde is / And when she had thus said all her
sustres said the same / And tho said albyne / full well I wot fair sustres that
our husbondes have pleyned unto our fader upon us / wherefore he has us thus
fowlo reproved and despised / wherefore susters my cou^seyl is that this night
when our husbondes ben a bed / al we with one assent cutten her throtes / and
than we may ben in pees of hem / and better we may do this thing under our
faders power. than else where / And anon all the ladies consented and granted
to this counseyl / And when night was come the lords and ladies went to bed
/ and anon as her lords were in sleep they cut al her husbondes throtes. and
so they slowen hem all when that dioclosyan the king her fader herd of this
thing, he bycome hugely wroth against his daughters / and anon would hem al /
have burnt / but all the barons and lords of firrie cou^seylled not so for to
do such sternesse to his own daughters / but only should wide the land of hem
for evermore / so that they never should come ayene / and so he did / And
dioclisyan that was her fader anon commanded hem to goo in to ship / and
delyuerd to hem vytaylles for half a year / And when this was done / all the
sustren went in to the ship. and sailed forth in the sea / and bytoke all her
friends to appolyn that was her god / And so long they saylled in the sea / til
at last they come and arrived in an isle that was al will dernesse / And when
dame albyne was come to that land / and all her sustres / this albyne went
forth out of the ship / and said to her other sustres / For as much quod she
as I am the ol (...) suster of all this company / and first this land have
taken / and for as much as my name is Albyne / I will that this land be called
albion after mine own name / And anon all her sustres granted to her with a
good will, Tho went out all the sustres of the ship / and token the land
albion as her suster called it / and there they went up and down / and fond
nether man ne woman ne child but wild beestes of diverse kinds / and when her
vytayl les were dyspended and hem failed / they fed hem with herbs and
fruits in season of the year. and so they lived as they best might / and after
that they took Flesh of diverse beestes / and bycame wonder fat / and so they
desired mannys company and mannys kind that hem faylled / and for hete they
woxen wonder coragyous of kind / so that they desired more mannys company than
any other solace or mirth / when the devil that perceived and went by diverse
countries / and took body of the eyr and lykyng natures shad of men / and ^e in
to the land of albion and lay by tho wymmen / and shad tho natures upon hem /
and they conceived. after they brought forth geantz. of the which me called
one Gogmagog. and another laugherigan / and so they were named by diverse /
names / and in this manner they come forth and were borne horrible geants in
albion / and they dwelled in caves and hills at her will / and had the land
of albion as hem liked unto the time that Brute arrived and come to Totnesse /
that was in the isle of albion / and there this brute conquered and discomfyted
these geants above said

(...) ends the prologue of Albion. that tho was an isle and her^eneth now how
brute was gotten / and how he slow first his mother / and afterward his fader /
and how he conquered Albion / that after he named Brytayn after his own name /
that now is called England after the name of Engyst of Saxon

Ca / j

In the noble Cite of great Troy there was a noble knight / and a man of great
power that was called Eneas / and when the Cite of troy was lost and destro
yed through hem of greece / this encas with all his meyne fled thens and come in
to lombardye that tho was lord and governor of that land a king that was call
led Latin / and another king there was that was called turocelyne that strongly
werrid upon this king latin and oftymes did him much harm / And when this
king latin herd that eneas was comen / he vnderfenge him with much honor /
and him with held / for as much as he had herd of him / and wist well that he
was a noble knight and a worthy of his body and of his deeds / This ene as
help king latin in his werre / and shortly for to tell so well and worthyly /
he did that he slow Turocelyne and discomfyted him and all his people / and
when all this was done / king latin yaf all that land that was turecelinis to
eneas in marriage / with lauyne his daughter the most fair crature / that any
man wist / and so they lived to geder in io^ and murthe all her lyfes time. and
after he wed ded a wife / and upon her he bygate a sone / that was called
Silueyne / and this silueyne when he could some reason of man vnwyting his fader
and against his will acqueynted with a damisel that was cosyn to lauyne / that
was king latynes daughter the queen / that was eneas wife / and brought the
damysel with child / and when ascamus his fader it wyste / anon let enquere of
the wysest maistres and of the grettest clerks / what child the damisel shol
de bring forth / and they ansuerd and said / that she should bring forth a sone
that should slay both fader and mother / and so he did. for his mo der dyed in
beryng of him / and when this child was born / his fader le^e call him Brute /
And the maystres said that he should do much harm and sorrow in many diverse
places / and after he should co me to great honor and worship. This king ascam^
deyde when god would / and silueyne his sone received the land / and made him
won derlych well byloued among his people / and when brute that was silueynus
sone was xv year old / he went upon a day with his fadre for to play and
solace / and as this brute should shete unto an heart his arowe myshapped and
glaced / and so there Brute quelled his fader /

How Brute was driven out of the land / And how he held him in greece / Ca /
ij
And when this myschance befalle was the people of the land made sorwe ynow /
and were sore an angered / and for encheson thereof / they driven brute out of
the land / and would not suffer him amongys hem / and he saugh that he must not
abide / and went fro the^s in to Greece / and there he fond / vij / (...) me^
/ that were of the lineage and kynred of Troy that were comen of great blood as
the storye tellyth as of men and women and childeren / the which were all
holden in thraldom and bondage of the king Pandras of greece for the death of
achilles / that was bitraid and slain at troy This Brute was a wonder fair
man and a strong and huge of his age and of glad chere and semblaunt / and
also worthy of body and was well beloved among his people / This king Pandras
herd speak of his goodness and his conditions / and anon made him duelle with
him. so that brute bycome wonder prive and much beloved with the king / so
that long time brute duelled with the king / so at the last they of Troy and
brute spaken to geder of kynred and of lignage and of acqueyntau^ce / and there
pleyned hem unto brute of her sorrow and of her bondage and of many other
shames that the king paudras had hem done and to brute / they saiden upon a
time / Ye be a lord of our lignage. and a strong man and a mighty. be ye our
capitayn and lord / and we will bycome your men / and your co^mandementz done
in all manner things / and bring ye us out of this wrecchednesse and bondage
and fight we with the king / for thorugh the grace of the great god we shall him
overcome and we shall make you king of the land and to you done homage / and of
you we shul hold evermore / Brute had tho great pity of her bondage that they
were brought in / and preuelich went him from the kings court / and al tho
that were of Troy went and put hem in to wodes and in to montaygnes and hem
held / and sent unto king pandras / that he should give hem leave sauelych for
to wend out of the land / for they nold no longer duelle in his bondage / The
king pandras was tho sore an noyed / and tho swore that he would slay hem
euerychone / and ordained a great power. and went toward hem al for to fight
/ but brute and his men manlyche hem defended / and fyersly foughten and slew
all the kings men that none of hem escaped and token the king and him held in
prison and ordained cou^ceyll between hem what they might done / some said that
he should be put to death / and sum said that he should be exyled out of the
land / and sum said that he should be (...). And tho spak a wise knight that
was called memprys and said to bru^ and to al tho of Tooye / if kyn^ Pand^as
would yield him and have his life / I counseylle that he give unto Brute that is
our duke and our soueraygne his daughter Gennogen to a wife and in marriage with
her an honderd ships well arayd and all his tresoure of gold and silver of
corn and of wyn / and as much as us needs to have of one thing and other and
than goo we out of his land / and ordeyne we us land elleswher for we ne none
of our kynred that comen after us shall never have pees in this land among
hem of greece / for we have slain so many of her knights and of her other
friends that evermore war and contake should been among us / brute tho and
all his folk consentyd well to that counseylle / and this thing they tolden to
king pandras and therefore to have his life granted as much as they axed. and
anon yaf unto Brute Gennogen his daughter to wif and the honderd shippis with
as much as hem neded of all vitayllis as before was ordained / bru te tho took
his wife / and all his men that forsook the land of gre ce and wenten hem unto
the sea and hadden wind and weder at wyss / and comen the thyrdde day in to an
isle that was called ^or g^ / Brute anon sent of his men a land for to aspye
the manner of the contre / and they founden an old Cite al wasted and forlet
that na^ theryn nether man ne woman / ne no thing duellyng and in the myddel of
this Cite they fou^den an old temple of a fair lady that thas called Dyane the
goddess and they comen ayene un to Brute and told him what they had seen and
founden and counceylled him to gone and to do sacryfyce unto dame Diane. For
she was woned to give answer of what thing that ever men prayde her / and
namely un to them that her honored with sacrifice / Brute went to that image
and said Diane noble goddess lady that al thing have in might and in thy power
/ wyn des wat^s wodes feldes and all things of the world and all manner
beestes that there in been to you / I make my prayer that ye me conncelle and
tell where and in what place I shall have a couenable duellyng for me and for
my people / and there I shall ma ste (...) honor of you a well fair temple and
noble / wheryn ye shull evermore ben honored / when he had done his prayer dy^
n^ ansuerd in this manner Brute quod she go even forth thy wey over the sea in
to france toward the west / and there ye shul find an yse that is called
Albion / and that isle is bycompassed al with the sea / and no man may come
theryn / but it ben with ships / and in that ^ude ^ere wont to be geantz /
but no wit is not so but al wilderness and that land is to you destenyed and
ordained for you and for your people

How Coryn became brutes man / And how king Gossar was dysconfyted Capitulo
tercio
When Brute herd this ansuer of dyane the goddess / an^ne he let the ankers
wind up and sailed in to the high (...) when he and his men had sailed. xx
/ days and moo they fou^den fast beside a cost of the se^ a thousand men of
the lygnage* kynred of Troy / and her sovereign and her master of al was call
led Corin / And when brute wist whennes they were / he (...) un derfenge hem
with mochel joy in to his ships / and hem lad fo^th with him. This Coryn tho
become brutes man / and to him (...) fea^lte and homage and so long they
sailed forth in the s^ till they comen in to gascoyn / and anon they arrived
in the ^auen of liegers / and there they dwelled. viij / days hem for to
rest: hy^ sailles to amend there that it was need / ^idyng sone come to ^ng
Goffar that was lord of the land / how that much f^lk of (...) ge land weren
arrived in his land in the haven of l^gers* w^* fore he was sore angered and
ano^ed that they comen and (...) in his land without love / and anon he
ordained him a great (...) to driven out and to shend brute with his people /
but king goffar was discomfyted and all his folk / and him self fled in to
^rau^ce to seek help and socour / And in that time reigned in france / ^n kyn
ges* and the x^ assembled a great power for to help goffar for to fight against
brute / Goffor duelled with them of france half a year and more / and brute
in the mean time and his company destroyed all the land of gascoyne / and let
take all the tresou^ that king gof far had and let bring it in to his ships /
and this brute fond in that land a fair place and a couenable / and there
Bru^ made a fair castle and a strong / when that was done king Goffar come
froo france / and x^ kings with him and broughten xx* (...). men for to fight
with brute and his company / and (...) had but un m and C C C men / netheles
when the two hoostes met ^n to gedre / brutes folk thorugh help of him self and
of turin his co syn and of Coryn that well and manlych him defended and fought
so that in a little time they had slain of the frensshmen / ij / m and mo / And
tho that were alive fled a wey. And in this bataill Turyn that was brutes
cosyn was slain and Brute let^e en^er worthyly him when he had space and
leyser in the castle that he had made / and tho let call the castle Tours for
the name of Turyne that there was entered / and yet in to this day there is a
noble cite that is called Tours / when king goffar wist that Turin was deed /
he come again with his men and after yafe a strong bataylle unto Brute / but
Brute and his men were so weary o^ fyghtyng that they might no longer endure /
but maugre him and all his / Brute went in to his castle with all his men and
made the yates fast for to save hem self / and for to taste counseyl among hem
what were best for to done / Brute and coryn took cou^seyl and ordey ned that
Co^n p^uely should go out and bussh him in a Wode till a (...) / So that in the
morning when brute should fight with his enemies. Coryn should come with his
folk in that one side / and (...) / and done all the harm that he might / And
amornyng in the d^wenynge / brute went out of the castle and fought with his
enemies and they fyersly defended / but within a little time Brute and his folk
slew. viij / C / of goffars men / and tho come Coryn fro the busshement / and
smete to ground he and his co^pa nigh all that would stand or abide / so that
king Goffar and his folk were disconfyted / and fast they ganne to flee. And
brute and Coryn with her company fiersly hem poursued and quelled mo of hem in
the fleyng than they dyden in bataylle / And in that manner Brute had the
vyctorye / and netheles brute made much sorrow for his cosyn Coryn / that there
was slain / and for other also that he had lost of his men / that is to seyn /
vij / c / and x^ the which nobly he let entier in the castle of Tours / there
that he had entered Turyn his cosyn

How Brute arrived at Totnesse in the isle of Albion / And of the / bataylle
that was bitwene Coryn / and Gogmagog Capitulo quarto
When all this was done / brute would no longer there duelle for to fight. ne no
mo lose of his people / For king Goffayus people might every day encresse mo and
mo / and Brutes lassen / and therefore he took al his men. and went unto the sea
/ and had wynd and weder at will / and the fyfthe day afterward they arrived in
an haven at Totnesse and comen in to the isle of Albion and there fond nether
man nethir woman as the storye tellith* but Geants / and they dwelled in hills
and in caves / Brute saw the sonde was fair and at his lykyng. and good also
for him and for his folk as dyane the goddess had him byhyght / Tho was brute
wonder glad / and late assemble upon a day all his folk to make a solemn
sacrifice and a great fest in honor and reverence of diane the goddess through
whose counsel he was comen in to that land / And when they had her sole^pnite
made / as they upon a day sat at mete / there comen in upon hem suddenly xxx
geantz / and slew of brutes men xxx / Brute and his men anon starten up and
foughten with the geantz and slew hem euerychone / but one geant that was
master of all that was called gogmagog that was stronger and higher than any
of the other geants / and brute kept him and saved his lif / for enchesen that
he should wrestel with Corin / for corin was gretter and higher than any of
brutes men from the gerdelstede upward Gogmagog and Corin undertook for to
wrastlyn y fere / and so to geder they wrestled long time / but at the last
gogmagog held Corin so fast / that he brake two rybbes of his side / wherefore
Corin was sore angry / and took tho gogmagog bitwene his arms and cast him
down upon a roche / so that gogmagog brake al to pyeces and so dyed an evil
death / and therefore the place is called yet unto this day the saute of gogmagog
/ and tho yaf brute all that country to Corin / and Corin called it after his
name cornewayle and his men he called Cornewaylles. and so shall men of that
country ben callid for evermore / And in that country duellid Corin and his men
and made tounes and howses and inhabyted the land at her will /

How Brute made london and called this land Brytaygne / and Scotland Albyne /
and walys Cambyr / Capitulo quinto
BRute and his men wenten forth / and saw about in diverse places where they
might find a good place and couenable / that they might make a Cite for him
and for his folk / so at the last they comen by a fair river / that is
called the thamys / and there brute bygan a fair cite and let call it new
Troy in mind and remembrance of the great troy / from which place all her
lygnage was comen / and this brute let fall a down wodes / and let erye and
sow lands and done mow medes for sustenaunce of him and of his people / and
he departed the land to hem / so that euerychone of hem had a certain place
for to duelle upon And Brute let call all this land britayne after his own
name and his folk he let call bretons / And this brute had gotten on his wife
Gennogen three sons / that were worthy of deeds / the first was called lotryn
/ the second albanac / and the third Camber / and Brute bare corone in the cite
of new troy. xx. year after time that the cite was made / and there he made
the laws that the bretons holden / and this Brute was wonderly well byloued
among all men / and brutes sons also loved wonderly well to geder / And when
brute had sought all the land in length and in bread / he fond a land that
Joined to brytayne in the north / and that land Brute yaf to albanac his sone
and let call it Albania after his name / that now is called Scotland / And
Brute fond an other country toward the weste / and that yaf to cambyr his other
sone / and he let call it Camber after his name / and now it is called wales
/ And when brute had reigned / xx. year / as before is said* he dyed in the cite
of new troy / and there his sone him entered with much honor / and lotryn
brutes sone was crouned king with much solempnyte of all the land of Britayne /
and after when he was crowned albanac and camber his two brethren went again
in to her own country* and lived with mykel honor / And lotryn her brother
reigned and was king and governed the land well and wisely for he was a good man
and wonder well byloued of all his land / And it befell so that Albanak duellyd
in his own land with much honor and worship / and then came king humbar
of hunland with a great power and arrived in albanye / and would have conquered
the land / and began to werre upon albanac and him slew in batayl / when
Albanac was slain the folk of the land fled unto lotryn / and told him for he
was king of bretayne / how that his brother was slain and prayed him of help
for to avenge his broders death /

Lotryne anon let assemble all the Brytons of kent of dover in to derewent
of Norfolk and Southfolke of kestefen and of lyndesey / and when they were al
assembled they sped fase toward their enemies for to give hem batail / Lotrine
had sent to Camber his brother that he should come also to him with all the power
that he might make him for to help / and so he did with good will / and so
they comen al to geders / and took her wey preuelyche for to seche humbar /
where they might him find / And so it befell that this humbar was besides a
water that was (...) gre te river with his folk / him for to disporte / and tho
come Lotryn and camber his brother with all her folk suddenly / ^r that any of
that other wist / And when humbar saw hem come he was sore adrad / for as much
as his men wist it not / and also they were un armed / and Anon humbar for
dread lepte in to the wa^er / and drenchyd him self* and so dyed he / and his
men were all slain that none of hem escaped / and therefore is that water
called hum bar / and evermore shall be called thus for enchesen that king
humbar was theryn drenchyd /

And after that Lotryne went to his ships / and took there gold and silver.
and as much as he fand unto him self / and all that other pilfre / he yaf
unto other folk of the host / (...) they fou^den in one of the ships a fair
damisel that was king humb^rs daughter / and was called estrylde / And when
Lotryne saw her he took her with him for her fayrenesse / and for her was
ouert^ with love / and would have wedded her / Thise tidings come ^o (...) ryn
/ anon he thought to avenge him upon lotryne / For as much as Lotryne had made
covenant for to spousen Corines dough^r that was called guentolen / And Corin
in have went to him unto the new Troy / and thus said to Lotryne / now (...)
quod (...) ye reward me full evil / for all the pains that I suffryd and have
had many times for Brute your fader / and therefore I will now anenge me upon
you / and dro^e his fauchon an (...) and would have slain Lotryne / but the
damisell went between hem / and made hem acorded in this manner. that Lotryne
should spo^ se guentolen that was Corynes daughter / And so Lotryne did And
netheles that he had spoused Guentolen Corynes daughter preuelych he come to
Estryld / and brought her with child and gate on her a daughter that was called
Abren / Hit befelle anon after that Corin dyed and anon as he was (...)
Lotryne forsook guentolen his wif / and made estrylde queen / And Guento len
went thens al in wrath in to Cornewayll and seysed all the folk / so at the
last they comen by a fair river / that is called the thamys / and there brute
bygan a fair cite and beat call it new Troy in mind and remembrance of the
great troy / from which place all her lygnage was comen / and this brute let
fall a down wodes / and let erye and sow lands and done mow medes for
sustenaunce of him and of his people / and he departed the land to hem / so that
euerychone of hem had a certain place for to duelle upon And Brute let
call all this land britayne after his own name and his folk he let call
bretons / And this brute bad gotten on his wife Gennogen three sons / that were
worthy of deeds / the first was called lotryn / the second albanac / and the
third Camber / and Brute bare corone in the cite of new troy. xx. year after
time that the cite was made / and there he made the laws that the bretons
holden / and this Brute was wonderly well byloued among all men / and brutes
sons also loved wonderly well to geder / And when brute had sought all the land
in length and in bread / he fond a land that Joined to brytayne in the north
/ and that land Brute yaf to albanac his sone and let call it Albania after
his name / that now is called Scotland / And Brute fond an other country toward
the weste / and that yaf to cambyr his other sone / and he let call it Camber
after his name / and now it is called wales / And when brute had reigned / xx.
year / as before is said / he dyed in the cite of new troy / and there his
sone him entered with much honor / and lotryn brutes sone was crou ned king
with much solempnyte of all the land of Britayne / and after when he was
crowned albanac and camber his two brethe ren went again in to her own
country. and lived with mykel honor / And lotryn her brother reigned and was
king and gouer ned the land well and wisely for he was a good man and wonder
well byloued of all his land / And it befell so that Albanak duellyd in his own
land with much honor and worship / and then c^in king humbar of hunland
with a great power and arrived in albanye / and would have conquered the land /
and began to werre upon albanac and him slew in batayl / when Albanac was
slain the folk of the land fled unto lotryn / and told him for he was king
of bretayne / how that his brother was slain and prayed him of help for to
avenge his broders death /

Lotryne anon let assemble all the Brytons of kent of dover in to derewent
of Norfolk and Southfolke of kestefen and of lyndesey / and when they were al
assembled they sped fast toward their enemies for to give hem batail / Lotrine
had sent to Camber his brother that he should come also to him with all the power
that he might make him for to help / and so he did with good will / and so
they comen al to geders / and took her wey preuelyche for to seche humbar /
where they might him find / And so it befell that this humbar was besides a
water that was (...) gre te river with his folk / him for to disporte / and tho
come Lotryn and camber his brother with all her folk suddenly / er that any of
that other wist / And when humbar saw hem come he was sore adrad / for as much
as his men wist it not / and also they were un armed / and Anon humbar for
dread lepte in to the water / and drenchyd him self. and so dyed he / and his
men were all slain that none of hem escaped / and therefore is that water
called hum bar / and evermore shall be called thus for enchesen that king
humbar was theryn drenchyd /

And after that Lotryne went to his ships / and took there gold and silver.
and as much as he fand unto him self / and all that other pilfre / he yaf
unto other folk of the host / and they fou^den in one of the ships a fair
damisel that was king humbers daughter / and was called estrylde / And when
Lotryne saw her he took her with him for her fayrenesse / and for her was
ouertake^ with love / and would have wedded her / Thise tidings come to Coryn /
anon he thought to avenge him upon lotryne / For as much as Lotryne had made
covenant for to spousen Corines dough^r that was called guentolen / And Corin
in have went to him unto the new Troy / and thus said to Lotryne / now certeo
quod he ye reward me full evil / for all the pains that I suffryd and have
had many times for Brute your fader / and therefore I will now anenge me upon
you / and drowe his fauchon an hyg^ and would have slain Lotryne / but the
damisell went between hem / and made hem acorded in this manner. that Lotryne
should spou se guentolen that was Corynes daughter / And so Lotryne did And
netheles that he had spoused Guentolen Corynes daughter preuelych he come to
Estryld / and brought her with child and gate on her a daughter that was called
Abren / Hit befelle anon after that Corin dyed / and anon as he was deed
Lotryne forsook guentolen his wif / and made estrylde queen / And Guento len
went thens al in wrath in to Cornewayll and seysed all the land in to her
hand / for as much as she was her faders heyr / and vnderfong feaulte and
homages of all the men of the land / and after assembled a great host and a
great power for to ben upon Lotryne auengyd that was her lord / and to him come
/ and yafe him a strong batail / and there was lotryne slain / and his men
discomfyted the / v^yere of his regne / Guentolen let take estrild and Abram
her daughter / and bind both hondes and feet and cast hem in to water And
so they were drenchyd / wherefore that water was evermore called after abram
after the name of the damysel that was estril dys daughter. and englyssh men
callith that water Seuerne and walsshmen call it abram in to this day / And
when this was done Guentolen let crown her queen of that land / and governed
the land full well and wisely unto the time that madan her sone that lotryne had
begete upon her were of xx winter age that he might be king / so that the queen
reigned xv year / and tho let she croune her sone / and he reigned and governed
the land well and honorably and she went in to cornewayl. and there she duellid
al her lifs time

Of king Madan how he reigned in pees al his life / and of menprys and of Mawlyn
his sons / And how Menprys slow maulyn his brother / and how wolves drow him
al to pyeces / Ca / vj
When Madan had reigned xxx year / he dyed / and lies buried in new troy /
and he had two sons / that one me called menprys / and that other maulyn. and
these two brethren after her faders death stryuen fast for the land / and
Menprys for encheson that he was the eldest sone would have had all that land /
and maulyn would not suffer him / so that they token a day of love and acorde /
And at this day menprys let quelle his brother through treson and him self
afterward held the land / and anon let crown him king / and reg ned / and
after bycame so lither a man / that he destroyed in a while all the men of his
land / and at last he bycame so wykked and so lecherous / that he forsook
his own wif / and used the sin of sodo mye / wherefore almighty god was wroth
/ and upon him took vengeance. For on a day as he went in a wode a huntyng /
he lost his folk / and went al one up and down cryeng after his men. and
there come wolves / and al to drow him in to pyeces / when he had reigned xxiiij
year. And when his people wist / that he was deed / they ma de Joy ynowe / And
anon made ebranc his sone king / and reigned with much honor /

Of king Ebranc how he conquered France. and bygate. xx soues / and xxiij
daughters /
THis Ebranc reigned ^x year / and a strong man was and a mighty / And this
ebranc through his might and help of his bretons conquered al France / and wan
there so much gold and filuer / that when he come again in to his land. he
made a noble cite / and after his name let call it ebranc / that is called
euerwik And this king made the castle of maydenes / that now is callid
Edinburgh / This king had xx / sons / and xxiij daughters. by die uerse wymmen
gotten / and the sons were callid / as ye shall here / brute grenescheld /
Margand / Seisel / Morghwith / Flengham / Bladud / Iakyn / Kymbar / Rocelyn /
Spadoch / Godeherl / Thormnan Eldaugh / Iozkangut / Haibor ketin / Rother kater
/ and assaruth And the daughters highten. as ye shall here after / Elegyne.
ymogen / Oghdas / Guenbran gnardych. Angarel guenthold / Tangus tell / Gorgon /
Myckel / medhan / maylour. Ondur / Cambredan. Ragan / Renthely / Neest /
Cheghan / Skaldud / Gladus / Herberhin / abalage / and Blandan / and these were
tho xxiij daughters / and the brethren bycame good knights / and worthy in
many Countrees /

Of the king Brute grenesheld the first sone of Ebranc the king / Capitulo / 8
AFter the death of king ebranc / reigned Brute grenesheld his sone xxx year /
that was Ebranks first sone / that well and nobly reigned / And when time came /
he dyed / And lies at york /

Of king leyl / Capitulo / ix
ANd when Brute grenesheld was deed / reigned his sone (...) xxij year / and he
made a fair town / and let call it Carlylle after his name / and was a
worthy man / and much byloued of his people And when he had reigned xxij. year
he dyed / and lies at Caerlyll And in his time reigned king Salamon in I^in /

and see if It were soth / that men spekyn of the great and noble wit and
wisdom of king Salamon / and she fond it soth that men had her told /

Of king lud ludybras / that was king leyles sone / Ca / x

Of king Bladud / that was ludibras sone how he reigned / and was a good man /
and a nygromancer / Ca / xj /
ANd after this. lud ludibras reigned bladud his sone a great nygromancer / and

Of king leyr / and of the answer of his youngest daughter that graciously was
married to the king of France / Ca / xij /
AFter this king bladud reigned leyr his sone / and this leyr made the town of
leycestre / and let call the town after his name / and he governed the town
well and nobly / This king leyr had three daughters. the first was called
gonoryll. the second Rygan / and the third cordeyl / and the youngest daughter
was fairest / and best of conditions / The king her fadre bycame an old man and
would that his daughters were married / er that he deyde / but first he thought
to assay / which of hem loned him most / and best / for she that loved him
best / should best ben married / and he axed of the first daughter / how much
she him loved. and she answered and seid better than her own life / now certes
quod the fader that is a great love Tho axed he of the second daughter / how
much she him louid / and she said more and passing all the creatures of the
world / per ma foy quoth the fadre / I may no more axe / and tho axed he of the
third daughter / how much she him loved / certes fadre quod she. my sustres ha
ue told you glosyng words. but forsooth I shall tell troth / for I love you as
much / as I ought to love my fadre / and for to bung you more in certain how I
love you / I shall you tell. as much as ye ben worth / so much shall ye be
loved / The king her fadre went that she had scorned him / and become wonder
wroth and swore / by beuen and earth she should never have good of him / but his
douhtres that loned him so much / should ben well auaunced / and married / And
the first daughter he married to maugles king of scotland / and the second he
married to hauemos earl of cornewaylle and so they ordained and spoke between
hem that they should depart the royame between hem two after the death of king
leyr her fadre / so that Cordeill his youngest daughter should no thing have of
his land / but this Cordeyl was wonder fair / and of so good^ condycyons and
manners / that the king of France agampe herd of her speak. and sent to the
king leyr her fadre for to have her unto his wif / and prayed him thereof / and
king leyr her fader sent him word that he had departed the land unto his two
daughters and said he had no more land wherewith her to maryen / And when
agampe herd this ansner he sent anon again to leir and said that he axed no
thing with her / but only her / clothyng and her body / and anon king leyr
sent her over the sea to the king of feaunce / And he resseyued her with much
worship / and with much solempnyte her spoused / and made her queen of France
/ How king leyr was driven out of his land through his folly / and how
Cordeyll his youngest daughter halp him in his need /

Capitulo xiij

THus it fell afterward that tho ij eldest doughtre^ would not abide till leyr
her fadre was deed / but werryd upon him / whiles that he lived. and much
sorrow and shame him did / wherefore they bynome him holy the royalme / and
between hem ordained that one of hem should have king leyr to foiourne al his
life time with xl knights and Squyers that he might worshipfully gone and ride
whyder that he would in to what country that him liked to play and to solace.
So that managles king of Scotlond had king leyr with him in the manner / as is
above said / and or other half year were passyd / Corneill that was his eldest
dough ter and qnone of scotland was so annoyed of him and of his people / that
anon she and her lord spoke to geder / wherefore his knights half and his
squyers from him were gone. and no ^o lest but only / xxx / and when this was
done / leyr bygan for to make much sorrow for encheson that his estate was
empeyred / and men had of him more scorn and despite / than ever they had
before / where for he nyst what for to done / and at last thought that he
welde wend in to Cornewayll to Rygan his other daughter / and when he was come
/ the earl and his wife that was leyres daughter him welcomed / and with him
made much joy. and there he duellid with xxx knights and squyers / And he ^ad
naught duellid there scar sely xij months that his daughter of him nas full
and of his company / and her lord / and she of him had scorn and despyte. so
that from xxx knights they broughten unto x / and afterward five / and so there
left with him no mo / Tho made he sorrow enough and said sore weeping / Alas that
ever he come in to that land / and said / yet had me better to have duellyd
with my first daughter / And anon went thens to his first daughter / but anon
as she saw him come she swore by god and his holy names / and by as (...) as
she might that he should have no mo with him but one knight if he would there
abide. Tho began leir again to weep / and made much sorrow and said tho / allas
now to long have I lived that this sorrow and meschyef is to me now fall / for
now am I pourer that some time was rich / but now have I no friend ne styn that
me will do any good / But when I was rich al men me honored and worshipped /
and now every man has of me scorn and despyde / And now I wot well that
Cordeyll my youngest daughter said troth when she said as much as I had so
much should I be by loved / and all the while that I had good. tho was I
byloued and honored for my richesse, but my two daughters glosed me tho / and
now of me they set little prys and soth told me Cordeyll / but I would not
believe it / ne understand / and therefore I let her gone fro me / as a thing
that I set little prys of, and now woe be I never what for to done / sith my ij
daughters have me thus deceived / that I so much loved. and now mote I needs
sechen her that is in another land that lightly I let her gone fro me with out
any reward or yefors / and she said that she louid me as much as she ought to
love her fader by all manner of reason / and tho I should have ayed of her no
more / and tho that me other wise behyghte^ through her falls speech now me have
deceived. In this manner leir long time began to make his moan, and at last he
shope him to the sea / and passed over in to France / and asked and aspyed
where the queen might be founden / and men told him where she was / And when he
come to the cite that she was in / preuelyche he send his squire unto the
queen to tell her that her fader was comen to her for great needs / and when
the squire was comen to the qnene / he told her every dele of her sustres from
the beginning unto the end / Cordeyl the queen anon took gold and silver plente.
and took it to the squire in cou^ceill that he should gone and bear it vuto her
fadre and that he should go in to a certain Cite / and him arayen laten and
wasshen. and than come again to her / and bring with him an honest company of
knights xl at lest with her meyne / and than he shol de send to her lord
the king / and sayn that he were come for to speak with his daughter and him
for to seen / and so he did, and when the king and the queen herd that they
comen with much honor / they him resseyned. And the king of france tho let
send through all his royame and commanded that al men should be entendant to
king leyr the queen's fadre in all mauer of thing as it were to him self / when
king leyr had duellyd there a monethe and more / he told to the king and to
the queen his daughter / how his ij eldest daughters had him served / agampe
anon let ordeyne a great host of france. and sent it in to britayne with
leyr the que nes fadre for to co^quer his land again and his kingdom / and
cordeil also come with her fader in to Brytayne for to have the royame after
her faders death / And anon they went to ship, and passed the sea and come in
to Britayne / and foughten with the felons / and hem scomfyted and slew / And
tho had he his land ayene / and after leued iij year / and held his royalme in
pees and afterward deyde and cordeyl his daughter him let entier with mykel
honor at leycetre

How morgan and Conedage that were neueus to Cordeyll werred upon her / and put
her in to prison / Ca / xiiij /
When that king leyr was deed / cordeyl his youngest daughter held and had the
land v year / and in the mean time died her lord agamp, that was king of
France / and after his death she left wydue / and tho came morgan, and conedage
/ that were Cordeyl sustres sons / and to her she had enemyte for as much as
their au^te should have the land / so that between hem they ordeyued a great
power and upon her werryd gretely / and never they rest till they had her taken
and put her unto death / and tho morgan and Conedage seized all the land / and
departed it bitwene hem, and they held it / xij year And when tho xij year
were goon there bygan between hem a gre te debate / so that they werryd strongly
y fere / and every of hem did other much dysese / For morgan would have had all the land fro beyond humbar, that conedage held / But he come against him
with a strong power / so that morgan durst not abide / but fled awey in to
wales / and conedage pursued him, and took him / and slew him / Tho come
conedage again / and seysed all the land in to his hand / and held it / and
reigned after xxxiij year / and tho dyed / and lies at new Troy /

How Reynold that was Conedages sone reigned after his fadre / And in his time
it rayned blood iij days in tokenynge of great death / Ca. xv
ANd after this Conedage reigned Reynold his sone a wise knight / and an hardy
and curteis that well and nobley governed the land. and wonder well made him
beloved of al manner of folk and in his time it rayned blood, that lasted iij
days as god would / and sone after there come great death of people / for hoostes
without nombre of people foughten til they were deed / whereof no man might have
ne let, til that almighty god thereof took mercy and pity and tho began it cese
and this reinold reigned xxij yer and died and lies at york

How Gorbodyan reigned in pees that was Reynolds sone / and after he died and
lies at york / ca xvi
AFter this reynold reigned Gorbodyan his sone, xv year / and dyed and lies at
york /

How Gorbodyan had ij sons / and how that one slew that other for to have the
heritage, and how ydoyne her mother slew that other. wherefore the land was
destroyed, Ca / xvij
When this gorbodyan was deed his ij sons that he had / becomen stout and
proud and ever werryd to geder for the land / that one was called ferres and
that other porres / and this fer res would have all the land. but that other would
not suffer him Ferres had a felons heart and thought through treson to sle his
bro der / but preuely he went in to france and there abode with the king Siward
til upon a time when he come again and fought with his brother porres / but full
evil it happed tho / for he was slain first / when ydoyne her mother wist that
porres was deed / she made great sorrow for encheson that she louid him more
than that other and thought him for to slay privily. and prinely she come to
her sone upon a night with two knyues / and therewith cut his throat / and the
body also in to small pyeces / who herd / ever such a cursid modre that slew
with her own hondes her own sone / and long time after last the reprove and
shame to the mother that for encheson of that one sone murdryd that other / and
so lost hem both

How four kings curtoysly held al britayne / and which ben her names. Ca /
xviij /
When the two brethren were so deed they and left behind hem nether son ne
daughter / ne none other of the kynred that might have the heritage / and for
as much as the strengest men dri nen and scomfited the feblest / and token al
her lands / so that in every country they had great war and strife under
hem but among all other things there were among hem in the country that over
come al tho other / and through her strength and might they token all the lands
/ and every of hem took a certain country / and in his country let call him
king and one of hem was called scater / and he was king of scotland / and that
other was called dawallyere / and he was king of loegers and of all the land
that was lotrinus / that was bru^es sone / the third was callid rudac / and he
was king of walys / and the iiij was called Cloten, and he was king of
cornewaylle / but this Cloten should have had all the land by reason / for there
was no man that wiste none so rightful heyr as he was but they that were
stre^gest set litel by hem that were of less esta te and therefore this cloten
had no more la^d among hem than cornewail

Of king donebaud that was clotes sone / and how he had wo^ne the land Ca / xix
THis Cloten had a sone that was caylld donebaud that after the death of his
fadre become an hardy man and a fair and ^r to is / so that he passed althe
kings of britayne of fayrenesse and of worthynes / And anon as he was knight,
he wist well. when that his fadre lived / he was most ryghtful heyr of all the
land and should have had by reason / but other kings that were of more strength
than he bynome him his land / and afterward this donebaud ordained him power,
and first he conquered all the land of logi ers / and after he would have
conquered al scotland / and walys and scater came with his men and yaf him
battle / and rudac come again with his walshmen for to help him / But so it
be fell that rudac was slain and scater also in plain battle. and so donebaud
had the vyctorye, and conquered all the land / and well mayntened it in pees and
in quyete that never before it was so well mayntened,

How donebaud was first king that ever wered crown of gold in Brytayne, Ca /
xx.
THis donebaud let make him a croune of gold, and wered the croune upon his
head as never king did before / and he or deyned a statute that had a man done
never so much harm / and he might come in to the temple. should no man him
mysdo, but goon therm sauf and in pees / and after goon in to what country that
he would without any harm, and if any man set any hand upon him ^e than should
lose his life / And this donebaud made the town of malmesbury / and the town
of the vise / And when he had reigned well and worthily xl year he dyed and lies
at new Troy /

How Brenne and belyn departed between hem the land after the death of donebaud
her fadre / and of the werre / Ca xxj
ANd after that this donebaud was deed his sons that he had departed the land
bitwene hem as her fadre had ordained so that belyn his eldest son had all the land of britayne on this half humber / and his brother brenne had all the
land from humber unto scotland / but for as much that belyn had the better
part / brenne therefore wax wroth and would had more of the land. and belyn his
brother would grant him no more / wherefore contak and werre aroos between hem
two, but brenne the younger brother badde no might ne strength against belyn /
and therefore brenne through cou^ce^l of his folk went fro the^s in to norwey to
the king olsynges and pra id him of help and socour for to co^quer all the
lord upon belyn his brother upon that covenant that he would have his daughter
to wif and the king olsinges him granted / belin ano^ as his brother was go to
norwey he seysed in to his hand all the land of northumberlond and took all the
castles / and let hem array and keep the costs of the sea that brenne should
not arryue in no side / but that he were take / The king olfynges let assemble
a great host and delyuerd his daughter to Brenne and all the people that he had
ordained / and this danusel samye had long time loved a king that was called
gut laghen / and to him she told al her counseyl / how that brenne should her
have and her led with him for evermore. and so he should lose her but that she
might forsake Brenne / and when gutlach had herd this tidyng / he lay for to
aspye brenne with as many ships as he might have / so that the two fletes
metten to gyder and long time foughten / so that brenne and his ships turned
ayene and were disco^ fited / and king gutlach took samye / and put her in to
his ship / and brenne shamefully fled thens / as a man discomfyted / And
gutlagh would have went in to his own country / but there come upon him a great
tempest / that v days lastid / so that through that tempest he was driven in to
britayn with. iij, ships and no moo / and tho that kept the costs of the sea token gutlach and samye / and al his folk and hem presented to belyn / and
belyn put hem in to prison /

How Belyn droof out of this land king gutlach of den mark and Samyee Ca, xxij
HIt was not long after / that brenne ne come again with a greet nauye / and
sent to his brother belyn / that he should yield ayene his land his wif and his
folk / and his castles also / or else he would destroy his land / Belyn drad
no thing his manace / and would no thing done after that he said / wherefore
brenne come with his folk / and fought with belyn / and brenne was discomfyted
and his folk slain / and him self fled with xij men in to France / and this
belyn that was brennes brother went tho to york and took cou^seyl what he might
done with king gutlach / For king gutlach proffered to become his man and to
hold his land of him yeldyng by year a thousand pound of silver for evermore
/ and for sykernes of this covenant to behold / gutlagh should bring him good
hostages / and to him should done homage and al his folk. and yet should swear
upon the book that these couenauntes shol de never be broke ne falsed / Belyn
tho by connseylle of his folk granted him his axynge / And so gutlagh bycome
his man and Belyng vnderfenge of him his homage by oath and by writing the same
covenants / And upon these couenaunts king gutlagh took samye and his folk /
and went thens and turned ageyn to denmarc Evermore after were the couenauu^tes
holden, and the truage paid til the time that hones^s was king of denmark,
and also of this land through his wif gyldeburgh / that she had spoused / for
she was the right heyr of this land / This belyn duellyd tho in pees and
worshipfully him held among his barons / and he made iiij real weyes / one
from the eest in to west / and that was called watling street / and another
from the north unto the south that was called Ikelmestrete / and two other
weyes he made in bossyng thurghout the land. that one is called fosse, and that
other fossedyke, and be mayntened well the good laws / that Donebaud his fadre
had made and ordained in his time / as before is said /

How acord was made between brenne and belyn through cor newen her mother / Ca /
xxiij
BRenne that was belynus brother had long time duellyd in france. and there had
conquered a great lordship through ma ryage / For he was duk of burgoyne through
the daughter of the duke Fewyn that he had spoused / that was right heyr of

he was overcome and yaf trua ge unto belyn / and to his brother / And after that
they wenten forth to Rome / and conquered rome and al lumbardye, and germanye /

How this land was long without a king / and how the bretons chosen a king /
Ca / xl /
THis king lucye had none heyr of his body bigote^ that was afterward great
harm and sorrow to the land / For after this king lucyes death / none of the

debate among hem / L year without king / but it befell afterward that a great

might / so that the two hosts metten upon steynesmore / and strongly smote to
geder / and tho was oc taiuan discomfyted and fled thens in to Norwey / and
taberne seysed all the land in to his hand / Towns / castles / as much / as
they there had / And sith Octauian come ayene fro Norwey with a greet power /
and seysed ayene all the land in to his hand / and drofe out all the Romans /
and was tho made king and reigned

How Maximian that was the Emperors Cosyn of rome spoused octauians daughter
and was made king / Ca / xlviij /
THis king Octauian governed the land well and nobly / but he had none heyr
sauf a daughter / that was a young child that he loved as much as his life /
and for as much that he wax syke / and was in point of death / and might no
longer regne / he would have made one of his neueus to have been king / the
which was a noble knight / and a strong man that was called conan meridock and
he should have kept the kings doughtir and have married her when time had been /
but the lords of the land nold not suffer it / but yaf her counceyll to be
married to some high man of great honor. and than might she have all her lust /
And the counceil of the emperor acorded thereto / and at this cou^seill they
acorded and chose tho cador of Cornewaile for to wend to the emperor / and
do this message / and he took the wey / and went to Rome / and told the
Emperor this tydyng well and wisely / and the emperor sent in to this land
with him his own cosyn / that was his uncles son a noble knight and a strong
that was callid maxymyan / and he spoused Octauuians daughter. and was crowned
king of this land /

How Maxymyan that was the emperors cosyn conquered the land of Armorican /
and yaf it to Conan merydoc / Ca / xl^x
THis king maximian bycome so ryall / that he thought to couquere the land of
Armorican for greet riches that he herd tell that was in that land / so
that he ne left man that was of worthynes / knight sqnyer ne none other man
that he ne took with him to great damage to all the land / for he left at home
behynd him no man to keep the land / but took hem with him froo this land xxx /
M. knights / that were doughty mennys bodies / and went over in to the land
of Armorican / and there sl^w the king. that was called Imbal / and conquered
all the land /

And when he had so done / he callid Conan / and said / For as much as king
octauian have you made king of britayn* and through me ye were let and
distourbled that ye were not king I give you all this land of armorican / and
you there of make king And for as much as ye ben a briton and your men also /
and by come fro britayne / I will that this land have the same name and no more
Armorican / but be called little britayn / and the land fro whens ye ben comen.
shall be called much Brytayne / And so shall men know that one britayn fro
that other / Conan Meridok than ked him hendly / and so was he made king of
little britayne.

And when all this was done / maximian went thens to Rome / and was tho made
emperor after Constantin Conan Meudock duellyd in little britayne with much
honor / and let ordeyne two thousand ploughmen of the land / for to erye the
land to ^r we it / and saw / and feffed hem richely after that they were / And
for as much as king Conan and none of his knights / ne none of his other
people would not take wyfes of the nation of France he tho sent in to great
Britayn to therle of Cornewayle tha^ me called dyonothe that chees through out
all the land xj M of maidens that is to say viij M for the mean people / and
iij M for the grettest lords that should hem spouse. and when dionoth
vnderder^g this co^ma^dement he let seche through all great britayn as many as
the no^bre ca^ to for no man durst withsto^de his co^ma^deme^ts / for as much
do all the land was take him to ward and to keep, to do all thing / that him
good lyked / And when all the maidens we re assemblyd / he let hem come before
him to london, and let ordeyne for hem ships hastily / as much as hem neded
to that vyage and took his own daughter that was called ^rsula / that was the
fairest creature / that any man wist / and would have sent her to king Conan,
that should have spoused her. and made her queen of the land / but she had made
privily to god a w^e of chastise / that her fadre wist not / ne noman else /
that was living upon earth

How ^rsula and xj M vyrgyns, that were in her company went toward little
britayne / and all were martred at Coleyne / Capitulo quinquagesimo
THis ^rsula chese unto her company xj M maidens / that of all other she was
lady and maystresse / and al they went in to ship at one time in the water
that was callid the thamyse, and commanded her kyn / and all her friends to
almighty god / and sai led toward litel britayn / but when they were come in to
the high see / a strong tempest aroos / as it was gods will / And ^rsu la
with her ships and her company were driven toward hund land through tempest /
and arrived in the haven of the Cite of coloyne / The king of the land that was
called gowan was tho in the cite / And when he wist the tydyng / that so many
fair may dens were there arrived / he took Elga his brother and other of his
household with him. and went to the ships to seen that fair company / and
when he saw hem so fair / he and his company would have onerlayne hem / and
bytake from hem her maydenhode / but ^rsula that good maid cou^ceilled / prayed
/ warned / and taught hem that we re her felawes / that they should defend hem
with all her might / and rather suffer death / than suffer her body to be
defouled / So that all tho maidens bycome so steadfast in god / that they
defended hem through his grace / so that none of hem had power to done hem any
shame / Wherefore the king gowan wax so sore annoyed. that he for wrath let slay
hem euerychone anon right / and so were al tho may dens martred for the love of
god / and lain at Coleyn.

How king gowan come for to destroy this land / and how a man of great power /
that was called gracian defended the land / Capitulo quinquagesimo primo /
When all this was done, king Gowan that was a sarasyn called his brother elga /
and said to him / that he should goo to conquer the land that all tho fair
maidens were in borne, And he ordained tho a great power of ^ehytes of denmark
/ of or koney, and of norwey. And they come in to this land / and brent tou nes
/ and slew folk / and cast a down chirches / and houses and rest gyon / and
robbed the land in length and bread / and put to death all that would not
forsake the right believe and cristendome / for as much as there was no
sonerayne that might hem help, For the king Maximian had taken with him all
the worthy men he went to co^ quere little britain / And in the same time /
that ye here now ^lle was saint albone martred through the wode tyrant
dyoc^sian in the same place / where is now an Abbaye made of saint Albone /
whiles that he was a paynym, But he converted him to God, through the
predicacion of a clerk and a wise man / that was called An^l / that was lodged
a night in his house, And this was after the Incarnacion of Ihu criste cc xxvj
year / And men sh^e understand that saint albone suffered his martirdeme before
that saint edmond was martryd / And her for saint Albone is called the first
martyr of england / this Gowanes brother and hye (...) that were sarasyns went
thurghoute the land / and destroyed all thing that they found / and no thing
they ne spared / When this tydyng came to Rome / how that king gowan had bygonne
for to destroy this land / the Emperor and they of Rome sent a strong man
and of great power that was called gracian with xx^ij M men well fyghtyng for to
cast out sarasenes out of this land / and al they arrived at portesmouth /
Maximian might not come him self / for as much as he was chosen Emperor
after the death of Constantin that was saint eleynes sone. When this gracian ^e
arrived with his host / he let espy privily / where the king go wan might be
found / and he come upon him suddenly as they say in her beds / and
discomfyted him / and sle we hem in her beddes^ uerychone / that none of hem
escaped sauf Gowan that fled with much sorrow in to his country / Sone after
it befell that maximian was slain at Rome through treson / And when gracian wist
that tydyng he let croune him king of this land.

How gracian made him king. when maximian was slain and afterward the britons
slew him for his wykkednes / Ca lij
THis gracian when he bygan to regne / he bycome so wys^sted and so stern and
so much sorrow did to the britons that they slow him among hem / Tho the
king Gowan had understand that Gracian was slain and done to death / he
assembled a great power and come ayene in to this land / and if he had erst
done harm / tho did he much more / for tho he destroyed all this land / and
the christian people that was in much britayn / so that no man was so bardye for
to name god / And he that so did anon he was put to strong death / But the
bishop of london that was tho that was callid gosselyn escaped / and went thens
to them of Rome to seche socoure to help destroy the sarazenes that had
destroyed this land / And the To mayns said that they had be so often a^noyed
for her sendyng after folk in to britayne all for to help the brytons, and
they would no more so done / And so the bishop gosselyn went thens without any
socour or help / And tho went he to the king of little britain that was called
Aldroye. and this was the third king after Gowan merydoc / as before is said /
The bishop prayed this king Aldroye of help and socour / The king had great
pity in his heart when he had herd how the bishop fled / and how the Christian
men were slain in great britayne through paynyms and sarazenes. he granted him
Constantin his brother him for to help with power of folk / and hem did array
horse armure and ships and all thing that hem neded to that vyage / And when
al thing was ready / he called the bishop and to him said / I take you here to
help and socoure Constantin my brother upon this covenant that if god give him
grace the paynyms and the sarazenes to shen de and discomfyte / that than ye
make him king / And the Bishop it granted with good will, Constantin and the
bishop took leave of the king Aldroye / and betoke him to god. and took her
men xij M and went to her ships / and sailed toward great Britayne and
arrived at Cotnesse / When the britons herd the tidings / that to hem come
socour / they were strongly helped. and ordained hem an huge nombre of people
and come to hem / and under feng hem with much honor, Gowan anon as he wist of
thise things he assembled all the sarazenes and come against hem / and yaf hem
battle, and Constantin slow him with his own hondes. And all tho other
sarasyns were discomfyted and slain, that none escaped but tho that were
converted unto god.

How Constantin that was the kings brother of litil britayn was crouned king of
much Britayne for his worthynes / Capitulo quinquagesimo tercio /
Anon after the bataylle they went to london / and crouned there Constantin /
and made him king of this land and the Bishop Goselyne set the croune on
his head and anointed him as fallyth to a king for to ben / ^and tho bygan
Crystendeme This king Constantin when he was crouned anon after he spou sed his
wife through counceyll of the britons / and he bygate three so nes on her / the
first was called Constance / that other Aurilambros / and the third ^ter.
Constance the elder brother when he came to age / he made him a monk at
wynchestre / Co^stantyn her fadre was slain through treason / for it be fell on
a time that a (...) come to him upon a day in message as it were and said that
he wol de speak with the king privily in counceyll / The king let wide his
chamber of tho men that were within / and there abode no mo but the king and
the pehyte / and made a contenau^ce as though he would have spoke with the king
in his ere / and there he slew him with a long knyf / and after went queyntely
out of the chamber in to another chamber / so at the last no man wist / where
he was bycome / When the kings meyne wist that her lord was so deed / they
made so much sorrow / they nyst al what to done / for as much as his two sons
Aurilambros and ^ter weren so young that none of hem might be king / and the
thyrdde brother was monk at wyn chestre / as is a fore said / But ^ortiger that
was earl of wes^seye thought privily in his heart through queyntyse to be king
and went to wynchestre there that Constance was monk and to him said /
Constance said he your fadre is deed / and your two b^rtheren that been with
Goselyn the bishop of london to norissh ben so young that none of hem may be
king / Wherefore I counceyl you that ye forsake your abyte and come with me / and
I shall done so to the Britons that ye shall be made king /

Of Constance that was king Constantines son / that was monk at wynchestre /
and how he was made king after her fadres death through counseill of ^ortiger
that was earl of westsexe for as much as Aurilambros and vter his two
brethren w^ but young of age / And ^ortiger let slay him to be king him self.
Capitulo liiij /
THis ^ortiger counceyled this Constance so much till he forsook his abbot /
and went with him / And anon after he was crouned and made king by assent of
the britons /

This king Constance when he was crouned and made king he wist ne knew but
little of the world / ne could nothing what knyghthode axed. he made ^ortiger
his chyef master. and counceyl l^r, and yafe him all his power for to do
ordeyne / and to do as much as to the Royame apperteyned / so that him self no
thing entermelled, but only bare the name of king / when wrtiger saw that he
had all the land in his ward and gouernayl at his own will / he thought a
prive treson and to slay Constance the king / that he might him self ben
crouned and made king and regne / and let sen de after an honderd knights of
pehytes the worthyest of all the land / and hem held with him to duelle with
him as to ben kep^rs of his body / as he would wend through the land to ordeyg
ne things that apperteyned to a king / And this vortiger honored so much the
hond^rd knights. and so much yaf hem of gold and silver / and so rich
Iewellys. robes / horse / and other things plente / wherefore they held him more
lord than they did the king / and vortiger told hem if he most be king ye as it
were through treson he would make hem rychest of the land / so at the last through
great yef^s that he had give largely / they cried through the court that
^ortiger were better worthy to be king than Constance / wherefore ^ortiger made
semblaunt as he had been wroth / and departed thens. fro the court and said he
must gone else whyder for thing that he had to done, and so the treytour said
for encheson that they shol de slay him that is to say. constance / when this
vortiger was go ne it be fell sone after that tho honderd knights of pehytes
breken the doors of the kings chamber, and there they him slow and smyten of
his head / and bare it to ^ortiger, there that he duellyd / and when vortiger
saw that head, he wept full tenderly with his eye / And netheles he was
somdele glad of his death / And anon let take the honderd knights of ^ytes.
and bind her hondes be hynde hem and led hem to london / and there they were
dampened to the death as falls traitors / And anon after all the britons of the
land by common assent crouned vortiger / and made him king of the land /

How the wardeyns that had tho two children to keep that we re Constantines
sons lad hem to little Britayne for the treson and falsenesse of ^ortiger
Capitulo quinquagesimo quinto /
THis king vortiger when he was crouned / they that had the two children in
keeping Aurylambros and vter through ordy naunce of Gosselyne / that was bishop
of london at his death durst not duelle in the la^d with the children / but lad
hem to the king of little brytayne / for as much, as he tho wist of the treason
of ^ortiger that tho was made king / through whom Constau^ce her brother was
slain / wherefore the honderd knights of pehy^s were put to death / and beren all the blame / as that vortiger had not wist there of another there to consented /
And so the kepars of tho two children dred lest Mortiger would put hem to death
through his treason and falsenes / as he had done her brother beforne / And
therefore they were lad over in to lytil Britayne, and the king hem resseyued
with much honor / and leete hem to norysshe / And there they duellyd til they
bycome fair knights / and strong and fires / and thought to be auengyd upon
the death of Constance her brother when they saw her time / and so they did / as
ye shull here tell afterward / Hit was not long after that the tidings ne
come oner see to the kynred of tho honderd knights of peh^s / that were
dampened and put to death through vortiger in this land therefore they were
wonderly wroth and sworen that they would ben auengyd of her kynnes death / and
comen in to this land with a great power / and robbed in many places / and
slow and did all the sorrow that they might / When Mortiger it wist, he made
much sorrow and was sore annoyed. And in another place also tidings came to
him / that aurilambros and ^ter his brother or deyned and assembled a great
hooste for to come in to much Britaigne / that is to say in to this land to
ben auengid upon Constance her broders death. So that in one half and in that
other he was brought in to so much sorrow that he ne wyste whydder to wend

How Engyst and xj thousand men come in to this land to whom vortiger yafe a
place that is callid thongcastell / Ca / ^vj
ANd sone after this sorrow tydynge come to vortiger that a great nauye of
strangers were arrived in the country of kent But he wyste not whens they were,
ne wherefore they were come in to this land / The king sent anon a messager
thither that some of hem should come and speak with him for to wit what folk
they were. and what they axed / and in to what country they would gone / There
were two brethren maystres and princes of that strong company / that one was
called Engyst / and that other horse / Engyst went to the king / and told him
encheson wherefore they were there arrived in his land / And said / Sir we len of
a country that called is saxon that is the land of ger main / where (...) is
so much so^we that of the people ^e so much / that the land may not hem
sustain / The maystres and princes that have the land to govern and rule make
to come be fore hem men and women that boldest ben among hem for to fight and
that best may trauayll in to diverse lands /

And so they shul hem give horse and harnoys / Armu^ and all thing that hem
needs / And after they shall say to hem that they gone in to another country /
where they mo^e lyuen as her auncestres did byforne hem. And therefore s^re king
if ye have ought to do with our company. we be come in to your land and with
good will you will serve and your land keep help and defend from your
enemies / if that you needs*

When wrtiger herd this tydyng / he said he would gladly hem with old upon
such cou^nant / if they might deliver his land of his enemies / he would y^ue
hem reasonable lands / where they should duelle for evermore / Engyst thanked him
goodly / and in this manner he and his company with x^ M should dnelle with the
king ^r tiger / and so much they did through her ^oldenesse that they deliuerd
the land clean of his enemies / Tho prayed Engyst the king of so much land /
that he might make to him a Cite for him and for his meyne / The king ansuerd*
it was not for to done without cou^ceyll of his britons / Engyst prayed him
eftsoon of as much place as he might compass with a thong of a skin*
whereupon he might make him a manner / and for him to duelle on / And the king
granted him freely* Tho took engyst a bulle skin and cut^ it as small as he
might al (...) to a thwonge al round* and therewith compassed he as much land
/ as he made up a fair castle And when this castle was made / he let it call
thwongcastel / For as much as the place was markyd with a thwonge*

Of Ronewen / that was Engystes daughter / and how the king Mortiger spoused
her for her beauty / Capi^ quinquages^mo septimo /
When this castle was maked / and full well a^ayed / Engyst sent by letter
p^nely in to the country / that he came of after an honderd ships filled
with strange men that were bol de and well fyghtyng in all batails / and that
they should b^nge with hem Ronewen his daughter that was the fairest creature*
that any man might see* And when the people was come that he had sent after* he

the king / and prayed him there worthily that he would come / and see his new
manner / that he had made in the place that had he compassed with a thong of the
skyn / The king anon granted it him freely* and with him went thither / and was
well apayd with the Castle / and with the fair work* and to geders there they
eten and dronken with much ^ye And when night come that the king Mortiger
should gone in to his chamber for to take there his night rest / Ronwen that was

mean / ne what he should ansuer / for a^ much as him self / ne none of his
Britons yet could none Englyssh speken. ne understand it / but speken tho the

understanding there of ^assaylle / and that other should ansuere drynk haylle And
that was the first time that wassayle and drynk haylle come up in this land /
and from that ^me unto this time / it is well vsyd in this land* The king
Mortiger saw the fayrenesse of this Ronewen / (...) his arms laid about her
neck / and thryes swetely kyssed her / and anon right he was anameryd upon
her* that he desired to have h^ to wif / and asked of Engist hi^ fad^ / And
En^yste graun^ him upon this conenaunt that the king should give him a^e (...)
country of kent that he might duelle in and his people* The king him granted
preuely with a good will. and anon after he spo^ sed the damisell that was
much confusion to him self /

And therefore all the britons bycome so wroth for (...) that he hadd spoused a
woman of mysbyleue / wherefore they went all from him / and no thing to him took
keep / n^ help him in thing that he had to done /

How Mortimer that was Mortigers son was made king / and Engyst driven on^ /
and how Mortimer was slain / Capitulo lviij /
THis Engyst went in to kent / and seysed all the land in to his band for
him* and for his men* and bycome in a little while of so great power / and so
much people had that men wyste not in little time / which were the kings men /
and which were engystes men / wherefore al britayne had of him dred^* and said
among hem / that if they ne took other counseyll between hem all the land should
he bytrayd through engyst and his people / Mortiger the king had bygoten on his
first wife three sons* the first was called Mortimer / that second Cartagren*
and the third passent /

The britons euerychone by one assent chosen Mortimer to be her lord and
sovereign* and her counceyllour in every batayl and crou ned him and made him
king. and would suffer Mortiger no longer to regne for encheson of the alliance
between Engyst and him / The Britons ordained a great host to drive out
Engyst and his company of the land. and yafe him three batayls / that first was
(...) kent there he was lord / the second was at ^edford / And the third was
(...) a shyre a this half cool in a more / And in this battle hem met
Cartagren and horse Engystes brother so that each of hem slew other / but for
as much as the country was yeuen long before to horn through vortiger / tho he
had spoused his cosyn there he had made a fair Castle that me called
hornecastel after his own name / And Mortimer was so annoyed for his broders
death Cartagren that he was deed in such manner / wherefore anon he let fell the
castle to ground / And after that he ne lest night ne day till he had driven
out engyst and al his people of the land / And when engist was driven awey*
ronewen his daughter made sor^ we enough and quentelyn spak to hem that were
next the king Mortimer* and pryuyest with him / and so much she yaf him of yef

and there he lies /

How the Britons chosen another time Mortiger to ^en her king / and Engyst come
in to this land ageyn* and they foughten to geder / Capitulo / Lix /
AFter Mortimers death / the Briton^ by her commyn assen^ ^ones made vortiger

of knights / and with much sorrow many of hem escaped. And the king Mortiger

And Mortiger tho for to have his life / granted hem as much as they would
