And Engyst went through the land* and seysed all* the land with fraunchyses /

seventh had oxenford / gloucestre. wynchestre* warwyk. and der^y shyre*

How vortiger went in to wales / and bygan there a castle* that* would not
stand without mortier tempred with ^de / Ca lx /
When Engyst had departed all the land in this manner bitwe ne his men / he
delyuerd Mortiger / out of prison / and suffered him freely to gone* whyder that
he would / and he took his wey^* and went in to wales / there that his britons
duellyd / for as much as that land was strong and wicked to win. And Engyst
ne uer come there ne knew it never before that land / Mortiger held him
therewith his britons / and axed cou^ceill / what him was best all for to done /
And they yaf him counseyll to make a strong castle that he might him self
therein keep and defend / if need were / Masons in have tho were fet and bygan
the work upon the hill of B^ygh / But certes thus it befell / all the werk
that the maso^s made a day / a down it f^ a night* and wist not what it might
ben. and there of the king was sore annoyed of that chance. and wyste not what
to done / wherefore he send after the wysest clerk^s and also lered men / that
weren through out wales / that might be found / For they should tell / wherefore
the fundament so failed under the work. and that they should him tell what was
best to done And the wisest men long time had studied they said to the king
that he should done ^ke a child borne of a woman that never ha^ with man to
done And that child ^e should slay and tempre with his blood the mortier of the
work and so should the work ever endure without end /

How the king let seche merlyn through al wales for to (...) with him /
Capitulum / lx^ /
When the king herd this / he commanded his messagyers anon to wend through
out al wales / to seek that child / if they might him find / and that they
should bring him forth with hem unto him / and in record and in witness of
this thing he had take hem his lettre / that they ne were distourbled of no
man / ne let / And tho the messagers went thens and sped so ^aste that they
come in to a town that was called Carmardyne And as they passed forth her wey*
they founden two Children / of xxiiij year age chyden to geder. with hasty
words* and one of hem said to that other / (...) quod he / ye done all wrong
to chyde or strive with me / For ye have no wit ne reason as I ha ue / Certes
merlyn quod he / of your wit ne of your reason / I make no force / for men
tellyn communely / that ye have no thing of god almighty / since ye had never
fadre* but every man knows well / who is your mother / The messagyers of the
king Mortiger when they herd this strif between these two gromes / they ^xed
of hem that stood besides / whens that merlyn was borne / and also who him
norysshe^ / and the folk him told / that a gre^ gentil woman him bare in
Carmardyne that was callid Adhan. But ne uer might man wit / who might be the
childs fadre / when the kings messagers herd this tidyng / they went anon to
him that was wardeyn of the town. and told him the kings will / and his
lettre showed him* wherefore they were come thither. Merlyn and his mother anon
were send before the war^yne of the town. and he commanded hem / that they
should gone to the king / as it was ordained by his messagers / Merlyn and his
mother went thens* and comen un to the king / and there they were vnderfong with
much honor / and the king axed of ^at lady* if that child were her sone / and
who him byga^* The lady ansuerd full tenderly weeping / and said she had never
company of man worldely But Sir quod she as I was a young maiden in my faders
chamber / and other of great lygnage were in my company / that of^ntymes were
wont to play and to ^o* lace / I beleft allone in my chamber* an^ would not
gone out for brennyng of the son* And upon (...) there come a fair ba^ ler /
and entrid in to my chamber there (...) allone. but how (...) come in to me /
and where* I wist it n^ (...) wot it not* for t^ doors were fast ba^ and with
me he did ^me of love for I ne had might ne power ^ym to defend fro me / and
often he come to me (...) foresaid manner / so that he bygate this child / but n^
(...) wit what he was

Of the ansuere of merlyn wherefore the king ayed / why his werk might not stand
/ that he had bygonne ner prove / Ca / Lxi^
When merlyn had herd all that his mother had said / spoke to the king in this
manner. Sire, how I was begoten* ay ye no more, for it falls naught to you, ne
none other to wit / but tell me encheson wherefore I am to you y brought, and
wherefore ye have sent after me / Certes quod the king / my wise cou^ceisours
have me done to understood that the mortier of a werk that I have bigo^ne
behooved to be tempered with your blood / or the fundament shall fayll for
evermore, Sire quod merlyn would ye slay me for my blood for to te^pre with your
mortier-ye quod the king or else shall never my castle stand / as my
counceyllours done me understand / Tho ansuerd merlyn to the king / Sire he
said let hem co me before me tho wise counceyllours / and I will prove that
they say not well ne trewely / And when the wise were y com^ merlyn axed if his
blood were encheson to make the werst stand and endure, All these wise were
abashed / and could not ansuere / merlyn tho said to the king / Sire / I shall
tell you then cheson wherefore your werk thus fallyth and may not stand /
There is under the montayne there that ye have bygonne your tou r a gr^ ponde of
water / and in the botome of the ponde under the water there ben two dragons
that one white that other reed that fyghten to geder against your werk Do ye
mine deep til your men come to the ponde and does your men take a way the water
al out and than ye shall see the d^gons as I have you told that to geder fight
against your werk And this is the encheson ^trs wherefore the fundament faylleth
/ The king anon le^ dig under till that men come to that ponde and let done
away at that water and there they found two dragons / as merlyn had told that
egrely for ghten to geders / The white dragon egrely assaylled the reed* and
laid on him so strongly / that he might not endure / but withdro we him / and
rested in the same cave / And when he had a while rested / he went before. and
assaylled the reed dragon angrely. and (...) de him so sore, that he might not
against him endure / but withdro we him / and rested / And ^r come ayene the
white dragon / and strongly fought with the ^ed dragon / and bote him eu^ / and
him overcome that he fleygh the / and no more ^me again /

Of the signyfycation of tho two dragons that were in the ^t tom of the ponde /
that foughten to geder / Ca / lxiij
This king Mortiger and his merry that faughte this bataylle had great marvel
/ and prayed merlyn to tell him what it might betoken / Sir quod merlyn I shall
you tell / The reed dragon bytokeneth your self / and the white bytokeneth
the folk of saxonye that first ye toste / and held in this land that no we
fyghten against you, and you have driven and enchaced / But britons of your
lignage ouercomen hem / and driven hem a wey and sythe^ at the coming again
of the saxons they recovered this land / and ^de it for evermore / and driven
out the britons and did with this land her will / and destroyed cristendome
through out this land / She had first joy with her coming / but now it* is
turned to you great damage and sorrow / For tho two brethren of Constance /
that was king / the which ye let slay / shall come before a quynzyeme passed
with a great power from little (...) and shall avenge the death of her brother. and
they shull brenne you first with sorrow / And after they shall slay a great
party of saxons and shul out drive all the remenaunt of the land. and therefore
abide ye here no longer to make Castle / ne none other werk / but anon go else
where your life al for to save to god / I you by^ke for troth / I have said
to you of thing that shall byfall. And understand well that Aurilambros shall be
king / but he shall be en poysened / and little time regne /

Of king Aurilambros how he pursued Mortiger and engyst / and how they dyden.
Ca / lxiiij /
OErlyn and his mother departed fro the king / and turned (...) to karmardyne /
And so after tydyng come to the Briton^ that Aurilambros and ^der his brother
were arryned at Totnesse with a great host. and the britone anon assembled
hem. and went to vnderfonge Aurilambros and ^ter with great noblesse, and lad
hem to london / and crouned there aurilambros / and made him king / and dyden
to him homage / And he axed. Where vortigr that was king might be found / for
he would be auengyd of his broders death / and after he would werre upon paynyms
/ And they told him that vortiger was in walys / and so they lad him thiderward
/ vortiger wist well that the brethren come him to conque re / and fled thens
in to a Castle that was called gerneth / that stood upon a high montayne / and
there him held / Aurilambros and ^r his brother and her fol^ had besyeged the
^stel full ^g time, For the castle was strong and well arrayed / So at the last
they cast wyldefyre / And burnt (...) and men and all her arraye / and as
much as was within the castle / So that vortiger was brents among all other /
and so dyed he with much sorrow Tho was Engyst in kent / and reigned there / and
herd this tydyng and anon fled and would have gone in to scotland for to have
had socour. but Aurilambros and his men met with him in the northcou^tre /
and yafe him battle, and engyst and his men hem defended whiles that they
might / but he and his folk were discomfyted / and slain / And Otta his sone
fled unto york. And Aurilambros him followed egrely / Otta a little while against
him stood but afterward he put him to his mercy / And Aurilambros un derfenge
him / and to him and his men he yaf the country of gale weye in Scotland. and
there they duellyd / The king Aurilambros went tho through out the land / and
put awey the name of Engysteland that engist after his name had called it
before / Tho let he it call ageyn great, britayne / and let make ageyn
Chirches howses of reli gyon / Castles Cytes and burghes and Towns that the
saxons had destroyed / and come to london. and let make the walls of the cite
/ which eugist and his folk had cast a down / / The britons led him to the
mount of Anbrian / where sometime was an hows of relygi on, that tho was
destroyed through painyms, whereof a knight was called Anbry / that sometime was
founder of the hows / and therefore the hylle was called the mount of brian / and
after was called Ambresbury and shall for evermore /

How Aurilambros did redress the land of great Britayn that was destroyed
through saxons / Ca, lxv /
HOw the king Aurilambros let amend and redress the house of Amlesbury / and
therm put monks / but now there be nonnes a little from the place / that was
called Salysbury / there tho the saxons slew the britons / where Engyste and he
should have made a love day, in which time there were slain a / M. lxi
knights through treson of engyst / The king thereof had great pity / and thought
to make in mind of him a monument of stone / that might endure to the worlds
end. And of this thing they toste her counceill / what there of was best for to
done. Tho spaste to the king the bishop of london that was called Ternestyn
that he should enquere after merlyn / for he could best tell how this thing
might be made / and merlyn after was sought and solid. and come to the king /
and the king told him his will of the monument that he wol de have made / Tho
ansuerd merlyn to the king and said There ben great stones in Irland and long
upon the hill of kydn that men called geants kawll. and if they were in this
place as they ben there / here they would endure for evermore in remembrance of
tho knights that here ben entered / ^r ma foy quod the king as hard stones be
in my land as in Irland Soth quod Merlyn But in all your land ben none such,
For geanntes set hem for great good of hem self / For at every times that
they were wou^ ded / or in any manner hurt / they wes^hen the stones with hot
water / and then wesshe hem therewith / and anon they were hoole /

How the Britons went for to seche the great stones in Irlond Capitulo / lxvj /
When thise britons had herd of this thing they went and swo re among hem that
they would go seche the stones / and took with hem meet the kings brother to ben
her chyueteyne / and xv. M men / and merlyn counceylled hem for to gone in to
Irland / and so they diden / And when the king of Irlond that was called gui^
somer herd tell that stranngers were arrived in his land / he assembled a
great power / and fought against hem, but he and his folk were discomfyted /
The Britons went before till they come to the mou^te of kylyan and clymed unto
the mount. But when they s^ we the stones and the manner how they stood / they
had great (...) ylle and said bitwene hem / that noman should remeue for no
strength ne engyne / so huge they were and so long / but merlyn through his
^afte and queyntise reineued hem / and brought hem in to her she and come
again in to this land / And merlyn set the stones there that the king would
have hem / and set hem in the same manner / that they stoden in Irlond / and
when the king saw that it was made / he thanked merlyn / and richely him
rewarded at his own will / and that place let call stonhenge for evermore /

How passent that was vortigers son and the king guyllomer come in to this
land / and how a traitor that was called Co^ enpoysoned the king Aurilambros /
Ca / lxvij /
And men shall understand that passent that was mortigers sone lived in the
same time / and come in to this land with a great power / and drryued in the
north country / and would ^n avenged of his faders death Mortiger. And strongly
trusted upon the company that he had brought with him out of the land of
germanye / and had conquered all the north country unto yor^, and when king
Aurilambros herd this / he assem^d a great power of britons / and went for to
befyght him / and (...) his people were discomfyted / but passent escaped thens
with some of his folk / and fled thens in to Irlond / and come to king gui^met
and prayed him of help and socour / The king granted him with good will, and
said / he would help him with good will upon that covenant that I my self
must gone with you with all my power in to Britayne / and I would avenge me
upon the britons rather than they in to my land comen, and token the stones
with strength that called is geau^ts ^ll / the styng guyllomer (...) ordeyne
his ships and went to the sea with xv M men / and arrived in walys / and
bygonne to rob and much sorrow done / hit bfell so that king Aurilambros lay
seek at wynchestre / and might not help him self / So that he sent in his name
(...) his brother with a great power to help walys / and thyderward he went as
much as he might / The king of Irlond and passent had herd tell that
Aurilambros was syke, and to him come a ^seyn that was callid Coppa and said /
Sir quod he / duelle ye here al in pees with your host, and I behote you
through my queyutyse that I shall slay the king aurilambros that is seek / if ye
do so quod passent / I shall you rychely anau^ce. This Trayceur, Coppa put
upon him an abyte of Relygyon / and beat shave him a broad crown / and come
to the kings court / and said that he would hele the king of his ma lady / Tho
said the Traitor Coppa unto the king / Sir ben of good comfert. for I shall
give you such a medyeyne / that ye shall sweten anon right and lusten to sleep
/ and have good rest / and the trai tour yaf him such poison / that he sleep
anon right. and dyed in his slepyng / And the traitor said that he would gone
in to the field till he were awaked / and so escaped he awey / For no man had
to him suspection for encheson of his abyte, that he was in clothed and also
for his broad croune / But when the kings men wyfte that he was deed / they
bycomen wonder sorry / and fast sought the trai tour / But they might not find
him / for Coppa toened again to the host. fro whens that he come /

When Aurilambros was deed a sterre in the morn was seyne with a clear light /
and at the bought of the beme was fey^ the (...) of an horrible dragon / Ca /
lxviij
When the king Aurilambros was thus deed and enpoysened at wynches^e / a morn
after that he was deed about the time of p^e there was seyne a ^rre greet and
clear / and the beme of that sterre was bryghter than the son / and at the
bout of the beme appeared a drago^s head, and out of his mouth come ij huge
lights that were as bright, as any fire brennyng / and that one beme went
toward France / and straught over the sea thyderward And out of that beme come
vij bemes full clear and long as it we to the light of fire / This sterre was
feyn of many a man / but none of hem wist what it bytokened / mere that was the
kings brother that was in walis with his host of bertons saw that sterre and
the great light that yafe he wondered thereof gretely what it might bytoken / and
let call merlyn / and prayed him for to tell / what it might bytoken.

Of the betokenyng of the sterre / Ca / lxix /
OErlyn saw that sterre and beheld him long time and sythen^s he quoke and
wept tenderly, and said allas allas that so no ble king and worthy is deed.
And I do you to understand that Anrilambros your brother is enpoysened / and
that I see w^ in this sterre and your self bytokened by the head of the dragon
that is seyn at the bought of the beme that is your self that shall be king and
regne / And by the beeme that stand toward the est is to un derstonde that ye
shall geete a sone that shall conquer all France and all the lands that been
longing to the croune of france that shall be a worthyer styng and of more
honor than ever was any of his auncestres, And by the beme that stretches
toward Irlond is bytokened that ye shall get a donghter that shall be queen of
ir land / And the seven bemes bytokenen that she shall have seven sons / and
every of hem shall be king and regne with much honor and abide ye no longer
here. but go and ^ue battle to your enemies and fight with hem boldly / for
ye shall overcome hem and have the vyctorye. mere thanked hertely merlyn / and
took his men and went toward his enemy. and they foughten to geder mortaly /
and so be discomfyted his enemies all / and destroyed / and him self show
passent that was Mortigers sone. And his britons slew guyllomer that was king
of Irlond and al his men. And mere anon after that batuyll took his wey toward
wynchestre for to done entere Auri lambros king that was his brother / but tho
was the body borne to stohenge with much honor that he had done made in (...)
brau^ce of the britons that there were slain through treson of engist that same
day that they should have / ben acorded. and in the same place they entered
aurilambros the / ij / xere of his ^gne with all the worship that longed to
such a king / on whose so^ god have mercy

Of Vter pendragon / and wherefore he was called so after ye shall here / And
how he was overtake with great love of Igerne that that was therle of
Cornewaylles wife / Ca. lxx /
AFter the death of Aurilambros Vter his brother was crowned and reigned well and
worthily, and in remembrance of the dragon that he was lyked to / he let make
two / dragones through cou^seill of his britons / that one to be bow before him
/ when he went in to bataylle, and that other to abide at wynchestre in the
bisshops church / And for that encheson he was called ever after Vter
pendragon / And Otta that was Engystes sone / commended but little Vter / that
was made new king and ageynste him bygan to meue war / and ordained a great
company of his friends and of his kynne and of Ossa his brother / and had take
all the land from humber unto york / but they of york held strongly ageyn hem /
and would not suffer hem to come in to the town, another to yield the Cite to hem
/ and he besyeged the town anon ught / and yaf there to a strong assaut / but
they of the cite hem kept well and strongly / And when Vter herd thereof / he
come thither with a gre te power for to help and rescue the town / and put
awey the syege and yaf a strong battle. and otta and his company hem defended
as well as they might / but at last they were discomfyted / and the moose part
of hem slain / and otta and ossa were taken and put in to prison at london /
And Vter him self duellyd a while at york / and after he went to london / and
at the ester after suyng he would bear crown / and hold a solemn fest, and
let sompne al his earls and barons that they should come to that fest / and all
tho that had wives shol de bring hem also to that feste / and al comen at the
kings commandment as they were commanded, The fest was richely holden and al
worthy set to mete after that they weren of estate / so that earl go^wys of
Cornewayle / and Igerne his wife setten al there next the king / and the king
saw the fayrenes of that lady that she had And was rauysshed for her beauty /
and often he made to her nyce semblaunt in lokyng and laughyng / so at the last
the earl perteyned the prive lokyng and laughyng and the love bitwene hem and
aroos (...) from the table all in wrath / and took his wife and called to him
his knights / and went thens al in wrath without taking leave of the king / The
king anon sent after him that he should come ageyn and go not thens in despite
of him, And therle would not come ayene in no manner wise / wherefore the king was
full wroth, and in wrath him deffyed as his dedely enemy / And the earl went
thens in to Cornewayle with his wife in to the castle of Tyntagell / And the
king let ordeyne a great host and come in to Cornewayl for to destroy the
earl if he might / But he had put him in such a castle that was strong and well
arrayed of Tyntagel / and would not yield him to the king / The king anon
besieged the castle and there duellyd xv days / that never might speed. and
ever thought upon ygerne / and upon her laid so much love / that he no wise
what to done / So at the last be called to him a knight that was called Mlfyn
that was pryue with him / and told him al his counseyll and axed of him what
was best for to done / Sir ^d he. does send after Merlyn for he can tell you
the best counceylle of any man living. Merlyn anon was sent after / and come
to the king, and the king told him all his will / Sir ^d merlyn / I shall done
so much through craft that I can / that I shall make you come this night in to
the castle of Tyntagel / and shall have al your will of that lady /.

How Vter bygate on Igerne that was the earls wife of Cor newayl Arthur king /
Ca / lx^ /
OErlyn through craft that he could changed the kyng^ figu re in to the
likeness of therle / and vlfyn garsoys his cha^b^rlayn and to the figure of
Jordan that was therles chamberlayn So that each of hem was transfigured to
other lykenes / And when merlyn had so done. he said to the king / Sir ^d be
now mow ye gone suddenly to the castle of Tyntagel / and axen (...) ^er and
have your will / the king took privily all the hoose to gouer ne and led to a
knight that he much louid* and took his way toward the castle / and with him
vlfyn his cha^berlayn and merlyn And when they come thither the portier went
that it had been his own lord. and when time come for to gone to bed / The king
went to (...) with Igerne the earls wife. and did with her all his will / and
bygo te upon her a sone that was called Arthur, upon the morrow the noble
mighty king took his leave of the lady / and went ayene to his host* And the
same night that the king lay by Igerne in bed y fere with therles wife, the
kings men yeuen a strong assaut to the castle / and the earl and his men manly
hem defended / But at the last it befell so that at at the same assaut the earl
him self was slain and the castle taken /

And the king anon turned ayene to Tyntagell and spoused ygerne with much
honor / and made her quent. and sone after time come that she should be
delyuerd / and bear a child a sone that was call led Arthur / And after he gate
on her a daughter that was callid Amya / And when she come to age / she was
nobly married to a noble baron / that was called Aloth / that was lord of leons
/ when Vter long time had reigned / there come upon him a greet sikenes / as it
were a sorrow / And in the mean time they that had to keep Otta that was
Engystes sone / and ossa his brother / that tho were in prison / men let hem
gone for great yeftes that they hem yaf and went with hem / And when tho two
britheren were escaped and comen again in to her own country / they ordained
hem a greet host and a great power / and bigonne to werre eftsoon upon the
king

How king Vter chees aloth to keep the land of britayne whiles that he was syke
/ for as much as he might not for his sickness / Capitulo, septuagesimo
secundo /
ANd for as much as king Vter was seek / and might not help him self / he
ordained aloth sone of eleyne that tho was chosen to be wardeyn and chyueteyne
of all his folk / and he anon and his Britons assembled a great hooste / and
yaf bataylle to Otta and to his folk / but Otta at last was discomfited / Hit
byfelle thus afterward that thise britons had dedygnacion of Aloth and would not
to him ben attendaunt / wherefore the king was annoyed wonder sore, and let put
him in a lytter in the host among folk And they lad him to beroloyne that
tho was a fair cite there that saint Allone was martred / and after was that
cite destroyed with paynyms, through werre / and thydder they / had sent otta
and ossa / and her people / and entrid in to the town / and let make fast the
yates / and there they held hem / and the king come / and hem besieged / and
made a strong assaute / but they that were within manlych hem defended The king
let ordeyne his gonnes and his engyns for to break the walls* and the walls
were so strong / that nothing might him mysdoo / Otta and his people had great
despyte, that a king lyggyng in a lyttyer had hem besyeged. and they token
conuceill among hem for to stand up in the morrow. and come out / and give
battle to the king / and so they diden* and in that bataill were both otta and
ossa slain and al tho other that escaped alive fled in to scotland / and made
colegryne her chyuetayn / and the saxons that were alive and escaped fro the
bataylle broughten again a great strength, and among hem they sayden / that
if king vter were deed / they should well con quere the la^d / and among hem
they thought enpoysen the king / and ordained men for to done this deed / and
yaf hem of yef^s great plen te this thing to done / and they ordained hem
thyderward there that the king was duellyng and clothed hem in pouer wede the
better all for to speed her lyther purpose / but netheles for all her falsenes
and queyntyse they might never come to nygh the king / But so at^ last they
espied that the king drank none other lycour but only water of a clear well /
that was nygh besides / and these falls tray tours upon a day preuelych went to
the well / and put therm wy sen / so that all the water was enpoisened / And
anon after as the king had drunk of that water / he bygan to suclle / (...)
sone after he deyd / and as many as dronken of that water deyde also / And anon
as this falsenes was aspyed* folk of the town let stop the well le for
evermore, when the king was deed. his folk bear him to stonhenge with great
solempnyte of bisshops and of barons that we re there / that beryed him beside
aurylambros his brother / and after turned again tho euerychone / and let
send after Arthur his so ne* and they made him king of the land with much
reverence after his faders death the seuententh year of his regne /

How Artur that was the sone of Vter was crouned after his fadres death / and
how he drofe Colegryne / and the saxons / and (...) of Almayne out of this
land / Ca, (...). (...)
When Arthur was made king of the la^d / he was but young of age of xv year /
but he was fair / and bold / and doubty of body / and to meke folk he was
good and courtoys. and large of spendyng / and made him well byloued among al
men / there that it was need / And when he bygan to regne / he swore that the
saxons never should have pees ne rest. til that he had drive hem out of his land
/ and let assemble a great host / and fought with Colegry ne / thr which
after time that Otta was deed, the saxons maynte ned / And this Colegryne was
discomfyted and fled unto york / and took the town. and there he held him /
And the king besyeged that town / but he might nothing speed / for the town
was so strong^. and they within kept the town well and orpedly / and in the
mean time Colgryne let the town to bladulf and fled him self to cheldri^ that
was king of Almayn for to have of him socour / and the king assembled a great
power, and come and arrived in scotland with (...) ships / and when Arthur
wist of this tydyng that he he had not power and strength ynouw for to fight
against cheldri^, he let ^en the siege / and went to london / and sent anon
his lettres to the king of (...) britayn that was callid ^oel his neuew his
sustres son / that he should come to him with all the power that he might /
and he assembled a great host / and arrived at southhampton / And when king
Arthur it wist / he was glad ynow / and went against hem / and hem re sceyued
with much honor, so that tho two hoostes hem assembled and token her wey even
to nychol / that chelderyk had besyeged / but naught yet taken / And they come
upon cheldryk / and upon his people er they it wist there that they were / and
hem egrely assaylled / The king cheldryk and his meyny defended hem manly by
her power / But king Arthur and his men slew so many saxons that ne uer er was
seyn such a slaughter / And cheldryk. and his men that were leften alive
fledden aweye. And Arthur hem ponrsued / and drofe hem in to a wode / that they
might no ferther pass / cheldrik and his men saw well that they were brought
in so much dysese and hem yolden to Arthur in this manner / that he should take
her horse and her armor / and all that they had they must only gone a foot
(...) to her ships / and so they would gone in to her own land / and never
come ageyn in to this land / and upon assurau^ce of this thing they yeuen him
good hostages. and Arthur by cou^ceylle of his men granted this thing / and
resseyued the hostages / And herupon the other went to her ships / And when
they were in the high see / her will changed as the devil it would, and they
returned her nauye and come again in to this land / and arrived at
tottenesse and went out of her ships / and took the land and clean robbed it,
and much people slew and token all the armure that they might find and so they
went forth til they come to bathe / But the men of the town shit fast her
yates / and would not suffer hem come within the tou ne / and they defended hem
well and orpedly against hem.

How Arthur yafe bataill to the saxons when they come again and besyeged the
tonne of bathe. and hem overcome / Ca / Lxxiiij
When Arthur herd this tydyng / anon he let honge the hostages / and left
hoele of britayne his neueu for to keep the march toward scotland with half
his people and him self went to help reskew the town of bathe. and when he
come thither / he yafe a strong battle to cheldryk / and slew al most all the
people that he had / for no man might him withstond / ne endure the stroke of
his suerde. And there both were slain Colgryne and (...) his brother / And
cheldrik fled thens and would have go ne to his ships* but when Artur it
wist / he took x M knights to Cador that was earl of Cornewayle for to let
and stop his co myng / And arthur him self went toward the march of scotlond
For messagers told him that the scotts had besyeged hoel of bri tayne. there
that he lay seek / and therefore he hasted thyderward / And Cador pursued after
Cheldryk / and took him er he might come to his ships. and slew Cheldryk,
and his people / And when Cador had done this vyage / he hasted him again as
fast as he might toward Arthur / and fond him in scotland there that he had
re seued hoel of britayn / But the scotts were al far within mon ref / And
there they held hem a while / but Arthur hem pursued and they fled thens in to
lymoygne that were in that country ^x Isles / and great plente of briddes / and
great plente of egles that were woned to cry and fight to geders and make
great noise / when folk come to rob that land and werren as much as they
might / and so they dyden / for the scotts were so great rauenours that they
to ke all that they might find in the land of lymoygne without any sparynge.
And therewith they charged again the folk in to scotland for to wend

How king Arthur axed of Merlyn the auentures of six the last kyn^ges that
weren to regne in england / and how the land should end / Ca / lxxv /
SIr quoth merlyn in the year of yncarnacion of Ihesu criste / M, CC, xv, shall
come a lamb out of wynchestre / that shall ha ue a white tongue and true
lyppes / and he shall have written in his heart holiness / This lamb should make
many gods houses / and he shall have pees the most part of al his life / And
he shall make one of the fairest places of the world that in this time shall
not fully be made an end / And in the end of his life a wolf of a strange
land shall do him much harm and sorrow through werre / but at the end the lamb
shall be master through help of a read fox that shall come out of the northwest
/ and him shall overcome. and the wolf shall dye in water / and after that time
the lamb shall live no while that he ne shall dye, His feed than shall ben in a
strange land / and the land shall be without a governor a little while /

ANd after his time shall come a dragon melled with mercy and este with wodenes
that shall have a berd as a goot that shall give in England shadow. And
shall keep the land from cold and hete / and his own foot shall be fet^ in
wy^e / and that other in london, and he shall enbrace inhabytacions, and he shall
open his mouth toward walys and the trembling of the hydour of his mouth his
eres shall stretche toward many habit^u^s and countries / and his breath shall be
full sweet in strange land / And in his time shall the Ryuers run with blood.
and with brain / and he shall make in places of his land walls that shull do
much harm unto his se ed after his time. Than shall there come a people out of
the northwest during his regne that shall be ladde through out a wykked hare that
the dragon shall done croune king that afterward shall flee over the sea without
coming again for dread of the dragon And in that time the son shall be as
read as blood / as me shull see through all the world / that shall bytoken great
pestyle nee and death of folk through dent of swerd / and that people shall ben
faderles til the time that the dragon shall dye through an hare / that shall meue
against him werre unto the end of his life that shall not fully ben ended in his
time / This dragon shall be hold in his time the best body of the world / and he
shall dye beside the marches of a strau^ ge land / and the land shall duelle
faderles without a good gouer nour / and me shall weep for his death from the
isle of shepey unto the haven of marcyll / wherefore allas shall be the commune
song of faderles folk / that shall ouerlyuen in his land destroyed /

ANd after this dragon shall come a goot out of kar that shall have horns and a
berde of silver / and there shall come out of his nostrel a domp that shall
betoken honger and sorrow and greet death of the people and much of his land in
the beginning of his regne shall be wasted / This goot shall goo over to France,
and shall opene the flout of his life and of death / In his time there shall arryse
an egle in Cornewayle that shall have feathers of gold that of pride shall be
without pere of the la^d and he shall despise lords of blood / and after he
shall flee shamefully by a bear at Gauerseche / and after shul be made bridges
of men upon the costs of the sea / and stones shall fall fro castles (...)
many other towns shul be made plain.

In his time shall seem that the bear shall brenne / and a bataylle shall be done
upon the arms of the sea in a feld ordained as a s^de. And at that bataylle.
shall dye many white heedes / wherefore his bataylle shall be called the white
bataylle /

And the foresaid bear shall done this got much harm. and it shall come out of
the southwest and of his blood / than shall the got ^se much of this land til
at the time that shendship shall him overcome, and than he shall clothe him in a
lion skin, and than shall he win that he had lost / and more thereto / For
a people shall come out of the northwest / that shall make the goot sore adrad /
and he shall avenge him of his enemies through counceyl of two owls that first
shall be in peril for to been undone, but the old oule shall wend a
certain time / and after he shall come again in to this land These two owls
shullen done great harm to many on and so they shall eoun^eylle the got that
he should arere werre against the for said bear / and at the last the goot and
the owls shall come at bur ton up Trent / and shall wend over / and for dread
the bear shall flee / and aswan with him fro his company to burton toward the
north, and there they shul ben with an hard shour / and the swan shall there be
slain with sorrow / and the bear taken and byheded alther next his nest that
shall stand upon a broken bridge, on whom the son ne shall cast her bemes, and
many shall him seek for ver^u that fro him shall come / In the same shall dye for
sorrow and care / a people of his land so that many lands shall ben on him the
more bolder af terward / and tho two owls shul do much harm to the forsaid
flour of lyse / and her shull led in destresse / so that she shall pass over
in to France for to make pees bitwene the goot / and the flower delise / and
there she shall duelle till a time that her seed shall come and se che her / and
they shullen he stylle / till a time that they shull hem clo the with grace /
and they shull seche the oules / and shul put hem to des pytous death / And
after shall this got ben brought to dysese. and great anguyssh / and in sorrow
he shall leave al his life /

AFtre this got shall come out of wyndesore a bore. that shall have an head of
white a lions heart / and a pytous so^yng His vysage hal be rest to seek men /
His word shall be stanching of ther^ / To hem that been a thyrste his word
shall be Gospel / His beryng shall be meke as a lamb /

In the first year of his regne he shall have great pain to Iustyfye hem that been untrue, And in his time shall his land be multyplyed with Alyens /

And this ^ore through fyersenes of heart that he shall have shall maste wulues
bycome lambs / And he shall be called through out of the world bore of
holiness fyersnes of noblesse and of mekenes, and he shall done mesurably all that
he shall have to done un to the burgh of Jerusalem and he shall whette his teeth
upon the ya tes of paris and upon four lands / Spain shall tremble for dre de
/ Gascoyne shall sweet In france he shall put his wynge his great tail shall
rest in england. and softely Almayne shall quake for dread of him / This bore
shall give mantels to two towns of England, and shall make the River run with
blood and with brain / and he shall make many mede was reed / and he shall
get as much as his auncestres dyden. and er that he be deed / he shall bear
three crounes, and he shall put a land in to great subjection / and af terward it
shall be releued but not in his time, This bore after he is deed for his
doughtynesse shall be entered at Coloygne. and his land shall than be fulfilled
of all good /

AFter this bore shall come a lamb that shall have feet of bid / an head of
bras / an heart of a loppe, a swynes skyn / and an hard / and in his time his
land shall be in pees the first year of his regne / he shall do make a Cite.
that all the world shall spe ke thereof. this lamb shall leave in his time a great
part of his lord through an hidous wolf. but he shall recover it and give a
lordship to an egle of his lands / and this Egle shall well govern it til the
time that pride shall him ouergone / Allas the sorrow / For he shall deye of his
broders suerd. and after shall the land fall to the foresaid lamb / that shall
govern the land in pees all his life time / And after he shall dye / and the
land be fulfilled of all manner good /

AFter this lamb shall come a mold warpe. cursed of gods mouth / a caytyf / a
coward / an hare / he shall have an erthely skin as a got and vengeance shall
fall upon him for sin / In the first year of his regne he shall have of al
good great plen te in his land and toward him also and in his land he shall
have great praysynge till the time that he shall suffer his people live in to
much pride without chastysyng / wherefore god will be wroth / Than shall arise
up a dragon of the north that shall ben full fyers and shall meue war against
the foresaid mold warpe / and shall give him battle upon a stone /

This dragon shall gadre again in to his company a wolf that shall come out
of the west to begin werre against the forsaid Moldwerpe in his side and so
shall the dragon and he bind her tails to geder / Than shall come a lion out
if Irlond that shall fall in company with hem / and then^e shall tremble the
land that than shall be called england / as an aspen leef / And in that time
shall castles be felled a down upon thamyse / and it shall seem that seuerne
shall be dry for the bodies that shul fall theryn / The u^ ehyef flodes in
england shull run in blood and great dread shall be and anguysshe that shall
arrisen / After the moldewarpe shall flee and the dragon / The lion and the
wolf hem shall dryne aware / and the land shall be without hem / And the
moldwarpe shall have no manner power sauf only a ship / wlerto he may we^ de.
And after that he shall go to land when the sea is withdrawn And after that he
shall give the third part of his land for to have the fourth part in pees and
rest / and after he shall live in sorrow all his life time / and in his time the
hot bathes shullen by come cold / and after shall the moldwarpe dye auentoursly
and suddenly / Allas the sorrow / for he shall be dreynt in a flode of the sea /
His seed shall bycome faderles in strange land for evermore And than shall the
land be departed in three parties / that is to say To the wolf / To the dragon
/ and to the lion / and so shall it be for evermore / And than shall this land
be called the land of con quest / And so shall the rightful heirs of england
end /

How Arthur overcome guyllomer that was king of Irlo^d And how the scottys
bycomen his men / Cao. / Lxxvjo.
When Guyllomer that was king of Irlond had tydyng that king Arthur was
entered at glastenbury / he ordained a great power of Irysshe men and come to
the sea with his Irysshe pe ple / and so come in to scotland over the sea and
arryned fast by there that king Arthur was with his host / and anon as he wyste
thereof / he went toward him / and yaf him battle / and overcome him anon
right / and guyllomer fled with his men ayene in to Irlond. And when this
discomfyture was so done / Arthur tur ned him ayene there that he was in to the
place / there that he hadd left the scotts / and would have hem all slain / But
the Bisshops Abbots and other folk of the coutre and ladies open ^ded come
before king athur / and cried him mercy / and said Sir gentil king and mighty
have mercy and pity of us / And as yo wre sylf ben of the right law to holden
and maintene cristendom full great dishonor it should be to quelle hem, that
believe in almygh ty god as ye done. and for gods love have mercy and pity of
us and suffer us for to live. For we have had much sorrow and pain / For the
saxons have many time through our land passed. but that is not ynow to you / For
oftentimes they haven us done sorrow and dysese / For our Castles they have
taken / and our beestes slain and eten / and much sorrow they have us done /
and if ye would now us slay / it were none honor to a king to sle hem that
cryen him mercy / For ynowe ye have y done and us overcome, and for the love of
^od suffer us for to live / and have mercy of christian people / that ^euen in
criste as ye done, when king Arthur herd this sorrow, he had pity of hem. and
yaf hem life / and lymme and they fill douue to his feet, and bycome his lyege
men / and he took of hem homages, And after that king Arthur turned again with
his host / and come again to york / and there abore during that vyage / And
tho yafe he al loegers to Aloth / that had spou sed his suster / and other
yeftes great plente / and tho was gawen his cosyn, but of young age / and to al
his other men that had him served in his werre / he yaf rich yeftes / and he
thanked hem much of her good seruyse /

How king Arthur spoused gunnore that was gunnores Co syn earl of Cornewayle /
and after he conquered of guyllomer all Irlond. Cao. / lxxvijo.
When Arthur had brought his land in pees and rest. and in good state and rest
was in every country / tho took he. and wedded a wife that was called gunnor,
and made her queen a fair lady and a gentel / that Cador the earl of
Cornewayle had long time norysshed in his chamber / that was his own cosyn,
but never they had child to geder / and netheles king Arthur loved her wonder
well and derly / And anon as winter was passed / he le te assemble a great
hooste / and all his barons, and said that he would wend in to Irlond for to
conquer the land / and he carried not long / that he ne passed over in to
Irlond. And guyllomer the king let assemble a great host, and yaf batail to
king Arthur But guyllomer was discomfyted / and yield him to the king Arthur /
and bycome his man / and to him did feaulte and homa ge / and of him held all that land fro that time forward.

And after passed king Arthur furthermore / and conquered gut land and yslande
/ and took homages of folk and of the land and there duellyd xij year in pees
/ and reigned with joy and mirth / and were red no manner man / ne no man upon
him / And he bycome so courtoys and large and so honorable that themperours
court of Rome / ne none through out all the world was not acompted to king
Arthure that any man wist. ne none so well preysed /

And therefore the best knights of al manner lo^des come to him for to duelle /
and hem resseyued with good will and reverence And all the knights were so
good that noman knew the werst And therefore king Arthur made a round table /
that when they should sytten to the mete / al should be alych high / and euenly
scrued at the table that none might make a vau^t / that none were hyer than
other / and king Arthur had at that Table / Batons Frenssh men* normans /
Flemynges / Burgoners. Mausers / Lotherms / and of all the lands a this balfe
mount of gorye and of his land of britayne / and of the great Cornewayle / of
walys / and of Irland / and of scotland / and shortly to tell of all the lands
that wolden worship and chyualrye seche comen to king Arthures court /

How king Arthur come in to France, and conquered that land of Frolle that
was a Romayn. and him sl^we / Cao / lxxv^
Sith it befell that king Arthur through counseyll of his barons and lords
would gone and conquer al france / that tho was called gallia through Romans
that tho held that land in her power / and in her lordship / and the Romans
had take that land to a noble knight and worthy of body, that was called frolle
/ and when he wist that Arthur come / he ordained an host / and a greet power
/ and fought with the king / and he and his folk were disconfyted / and thens
they fled unto paris / and entryd the tonne / and closed the yates. and there
hem held / Arthur wist that Froll was gone to pa ris / he pursued after / and
come thider / and him besyeged. but the Cite was so strong / and well arrayed /
and tho that were within / defended hem well and ma^ly / King arthur duellyd
there more a month / and there was so much people in the Cite / and dispended
al her vytaylles / that were within / and so great honger bycome among hem /
that ^ey deyden wonder thykke within the cite for honger, and comen to Frolle,
and prayed him to ben acorded with king Arthur for to ha ue pres / and they
would yield hem to him. and the town also / Frolle saw that no longer he might
hold the town ageynste her will and trust gretely upon his own strength / and
sent to king arthur that he should come fight with him body for body / and so
should they depart france between hem two / king Arthur anon granted it and
would not that one of his people undertook the battle for him / and upon the
morn both men were armed without paris there that they should fight / and anon
they smyten to geders so fyersly and so well they foughten in both sides that
no man could deem the beter of hem / and so it befelle, that Frolle yaf Arthur
such a stroke that he kneled to the ground / would. he nold he / and as
frolle withdrow his suerd / he wounded king Arthur in the forhede that the
blood fell a down by his eyes and his face / Arthur anon sterte up hertely /
when he felt him hurt as a man that seemed almost wode. and he took Tabourne his
good suerd*and drowe it upon high / and yafe Frolle such a stroke that
therewith he clafe his head down to the sholders / so that his helm might not
be his warrant / and so he fell a down deed in the place / and they of the
cite made great sorrow for Frolle / anon euerychone yield hem to king Arthur /
and the town also / and bycome his men and did to him homage and feaute / and
he vnderfenge hem / and took of hem good hostages / and king Arthur after went
forth with his host, and conquered Angyen / and An gyers, gascoyne pehyto /
nauerne / Burgeyne / Berry / Lotherne / Turyn and peythers. and all the other
land of Frannce he conquered holych / And when he had all conquered and taken by
homages and feaultes / he turned again to paris / and there he duel led long
time, and ordained pees long time over all the countray and through out al
France / And when pees was made over al through his noble knyghthode that he
had / and also for his own worthynes / And noman were he never so great a
lord durst not mean werre against him / another to arryse for to make the la^d
of france in quyete and pres / he duellyd there nine year / and did there ma ny
great wondres. and. reproved many proud men / and lyther ty vants / and hem
chastysed after her deseruyse /

How king Arthur auaunced all his men / that had trauaylin his service / Cao. /
lxxixo.
ANd afterward it befelle thus at Estren there that he held a fest at paris /
ry^lely he began auaunce his knights for her service, that had him helped in his
conquest / He yafe to his styward that was called kay / Angyeen and Angy ers /
And to Bedeler his boteler he yafe normandy that tho was called neustrye / And
to Holdyne his Chambyrlayne he yaf flaundres and maunce / and to do^ll his
cosyn he yafe bo^oyn. And to Rychard his neueu be yaf ponntyf / And to all
other he yaf large lands and fees after they were of estate / And when Arthur
had thus his knights feffed at auerill next after sewyng / he come again in
to britayn his own land, And after at whytsontyde next sewynge by counseyl of
his barons he would be crouned king of glomergon / and held a solemn fest and
let sompne / kings / Earls and batons, that they should come thider euerychone
/ there was scater king of scotlond / Cadwere king of southwales / Euyllomer
king of Northwales / Maded king of Irland / Malgamus king of gutland /
Achylles king of Iselande / Aloth king of denmark / Eonewas king of norwey, and
Hell his cosyn king of dorkeny. Cador king of litell butain / Mowitherle of
Cornewayl / Mauran earl of gloucestre. guerdon ^le of wynchestre / Boel earl of
hertford / ^reegy earl of oxenford / Cursall earl of bathe. Jonas earl of
C^stre. Enetal earl of dorchestre / ^ymare earl of salysbury, waloth earl of
Canterbury / Iu gerne earl of chichestre / Aral earl of leycetre / and the
earl of war wist. and many other rich lords / Britons also there ca in mo /
that is to say dyppon / Donaud / gennes and many other that been not here named
weren at that feste / and many a fair fest king Arthur had hold byforne / but
never none such / ne so solemn, and that lastyd xv days with much honor
and myeth.

Of the letter that was sent from the Cite of Rome for pride to king Arthur /
Ca / lxxx /
THe third day as king Arthur sat at his mete among his kings and among hem
that seten at the feste byforne hem come in xij aldermen of age rychely arrayed
/ and courtously salued the king and said they come from Rome sent as
messagyers feo thempetour / and took to him a letter / that thus much was to
understand / Gretely us meruayleth Arthur that thou art ones so hardy with
eyes in thy head to maken open were re and contaste against us of rome that owen
all the world to derne for thou have never yet byforne this time proved, ne
essayed the strength of the romans / and therefore thou it shall in a little
time /

For Julius caesar conquered all the land of Brytayne / and took thereof truage,
and our folk have it long y had, and now through thy pride thou witholdest it.
Wherefore we command the that thou it yield ageyn / and yet have thou more folly
done that thou have slain frolle that was our baron of france all with wrong
/ and therefore all the commons of Rome warnen / and comande the upon life and
lymme / that thou be in haste at Rome, amends to make of thy misdeeds that
thou have done / And if it so be that thou come not we shall pass the hylle of
Joy with strength / and we shall the se ke where ever thou may be found,and
thou shall not have a for of land of thine own that we ne shall destroy / and
afterward with thy body we shall done our will / when this letter was rad / and
al men it herd / they were annoyed all that were at that solempnyte / and the
butons would have slain the messagiers but the king would not suffer hem,and said
that the messagyers should have none harm and mow by reason none deserve / but
commanded hem to be worshipfully served / And after mete he took counseyll of
kings / ersts and barons. what ansuer he might give again to the messagers /
and they counceylled him attones that he should assemble a great power of all
the lands / of which he had lordship. and manly avenge him upon the emperor
of the despyte that he had sent him such a letter / and they sworen by god /
and by his names that they should him pursue / and brenne as much as they
might. and said that they would never faylle king Arthur / and rather to be
deed / and they let write a letter to send to the emperor by the same
messagyers in this manner /

Of the bold ansuet that king Arthur sent to the emperor of Rome and to the
Romans / Cao / lxxxj /
UNderstondeth among you of Rome that I am king Arthur of butayn / and
freely it hold and shall hold. and at rome hastily I will be / not to give you
truage, but for to axen true age / For Constantin that was eleynes sone that was
emperor of Rome and of all the honor that thereto bylongeth / and maximian king
conquered al france and almayne / and mount Joy passed and con querd al
lumbardye / and these two were mine auncestres / and that they held and had /
I shall have through gods will /

Of the reverence that arthur did to the emperors messagyers of Rome Ca /
lxxxij /
When this letter was made and ensealed / king Arthur to the messagyers yafe
great yeftes / and after that the messagyers took her lene and went thens and
come to the court of To me again and told the emperor how worthily they were
vnderfongen / and which a ryall company he had him to serve and (...) he was

How king Arthur fought with a geant in spain, that was called dynabus that
slew eleyne / that was king ho^ls cosyn of little britayne Capitulo lxxxi^
KYyng Arthur had not duelled in the country but a (...) why le / that men ne
told him that there was comen a great geant in to spayn / and had rauysshed fair
eleyn / that was cosyn to hoel of britayne / and had brought her upon an
hylle / that is called the mount of saint bernard, and there was no man in that
country so hold. ne so hardy, that dursie with him fight / ner come nere the
place / there that geant duellyd. and he was called Dynabus / that much sorrow
did in the country / when king Arthur herd this tydyng / he called key and
^dewere / and commanded hem to go privily and and espy where the geant might be
found and they comen to the ryua ge / there that men should go to the mount
that was all enclosed about with water and yet is and ever shall be / And they
saw a brennyng fire upon the hille / and there was also another hill nygh that /
there was thereupon another fire buennyng / Prey / and ^ede were come to the next
hille / and fou^den a wydueopen head syttyng besides a tomb sore weeping and
great sorrow made / and often she said Eleyne / Eleyne, and key / and Bedewere
axed what her was / and wherefore she made so much sorrow / and who lay in that
tomb / O quod she what sorrow, and misauenture fair lords seek ye here / for
if the geant may you here find ye worth deed anon / be still good wife quod
they / there of dismay ye not, but tell us the soth why thou make so much
sorrow and weeping / Syrs quod she for a damisel that I norisshed with my breast
that was called Eleyne that was nece to hoel king of britayne / and here lies
the body in this tomb / that to me was bytaken to noryssh / So there come a
deuel a Geant and cauysshed her and me also / and lad us both awey, and he
would have forlayne that maid / that was so young and tender of age / but she
might it not suffer. so great and so huge as the geant was and if he now come
as he is woned to do / certes he will you ^lee both to. And therefore fast wend
ye hens / And wherefore said they go ye not thens / Certes Sir quoth she / when that
eleyne was deed / the geant made me to abide to done and hau^te his will / and
me must needs it suffer / and god it wot I do it not with my good will / for
me lever were to be deed. than with him to dele / so much pain I have when he
me forlyeth, when stey and Bedewere bad herd all that this woman had told /
they returned ageyn. and come to king Arthur / and told him all that they had
seyn and herd / Arthur anon took hem both with him / and went preuelyche by
night that none of his host it wist. and come on the morrow erly to the geant /
and fought with him strongly / and at last him slow.

And Arthur bad bedewere smyce of his heed / and bring it to the host to
show hem for a wonder / for it was so great / and so huge when they comen
again to the hooste / they tolden wherefore they had been out / and showed to
hem the head / and every man was glad and Ioyeful of the worthy deed / that
king Arthur had done that was her lord / and hoel was full sorrowful for his
nece that was so lost / And after when he had space. he let make a fair
chapel of our lady over eteyns Tomb

How king Arthur yafe battle to the emperor / in which battle the emperor
was slain / Capitulo / lxxxv /
ARthur and his people had tydyng that the emperor had as sembled a great power
as well of sarazeyns ao of paynynts and christian men / where of the nombre was
lxxx / M / horsemen and so to men / Arthur and his people ordained fast forth in
her way toward the emperor and passed normandy and Frannce unto burgoyne and
would even have gone to the hooste. For men told him that the Emperors hooste
would come to lucye / The Emperor and his host in the beginning of august
remeued ^o Rome and come forth right the way toward the host, Tho comen king
arthures ^spyes and said if that Arthur would / he should find there fast by them
perour. but they said that the emperor had so great power with him of kings of
the land and of paynyms y fere / and also ^y ^ten people that it new but great
folly to king Arthur to meten with him. For the espyes told that the empprour
had v men or vj against one of his / king arthur was bold and hardy / and for no
thing ^ym dismayed / and said go we boldly in gods name ageyns^ the Romans
that with hem led samseyns and paynyms / that no manner trust they have to god
/ but only upon her strength / goo we now and seche hem sharply in the name
of Almighty god / and sle we the paynyms, and the christian men that been enemies
with hem for to destroy christian men / and god shall us help for we have the
right, and therefore have we trust in god. and do we so that the enemies that been to cristendome / and to god mow be deed and destroyed / and that men mow
record the worthynesse of knyghthode / when king Arthur bad thus said / they
cried al with a high voys / God fadre almighty worshipped be thy name without
en de, amen / And grannte us grace well to done, and to destroy our eve myes
that been against cristendom / In the name of the fadre / Of the sone / and of
the holy ghost / amen / and god give him never gra^ / ne worship in the world.
ne mercy of him to have that this day shall feynten well for to smiten and
egrely / and so they ryden sofaly and ordained his wings well and wisely /

The Emperor herd tell that king Arthur and his folk were ready a^yed for to
fight with him / and thither they come, And he ordained his wings in the best
manner that he might, and more trust upon his strength than in god almighty /
and that was (...) afterward / For when tho two hosts met. the Emperor lost
such four of his folk / as did Arthur / and so many were slain what in
that one side / and in that other / that it was great py^ to wyt^ and to seen
In this battle were sleyn through king Arthur v kings of the paynyms / and of
other wonder much people / And king Artures men foughten so well that the
romans and paynyms had no more strength to withstonde / than xx. sheep against
five wulues / And so it byfell that in this bataylle that was wonder hard and
long during in that one side / and in that other / the emperor among hem there
was slain / but no man wist forsooth who him slew /

How king arthur let entier his knights that he had lost in that bataylle,

/ lxxxvj
When the Romans wist that the emperor was deed / they forsook the field /
and the paynyms also. And king Arthur af ter hem chaced till it was night / and
so many of hem slew / that it was wonder to tell / And tho turned king Arthur
again tho it was night / and thanked god of his vyctorye. and in the morrow he
let look and see all the field for his knights that he there had lost that is

^rgeti earl of baak / Aloth earl of wynchestre / Cursale Earl of chestre / and

lost in that bataylle among other worthy knights / And some he let entiere in
Ableyes by the country / Sum he let be borne in to her own country. And

sent to say the Romans that for britayn and France / which that he held /
other truage would he none pay / And if they axed him any other truages /
right such truage he would hem pay / The king let here key to kenen his own
Castle / and there he was entered / and lygyer was borne to boloyne there he was

that same year in burgoyne with his host and thought the same year to pass

How mordred the traitor to whom king Arthur took his land to keep and his
castles / and held it against him / Ca / lxxxvij
When king Arthur had taken to mordred his reame to keep / and was gone against
the emperor of Rome. and was passed the sea / Mordred anon took homages and
feautes of all hem that were in this land / and would have had the land to his
own use And took Castles about / and let hem array / And after this false
nes / he did another great wrong / for against the law of christian t^ / he
took his own eames wife as a traitor should / and ordained him a great host
against Arthurs coming to hold the land against him with strength for
evermore / And to slay king Arthur if he might / and sent by the sea and land
/ and let assemble paynyms and christian people / and he sent to saxons / and to
danoys for to help him / And also mordred sent to cheldryk to done men to
come to him out of saxoyn / that was a worthy duk / and bihete him if that he
brought with him much people / he would grant him in heritage all the land
from beyond humber unto scotland / and all the land that engist had of
vortigers yeft / when that he spou sed his daughter / And cheldryk come with
great strength and power of people / and mordred also had assembled in his half
/ that they had xl / M / strong knights / when that they had need /

How arthur enchaced mordred the traitor. and how he was sla yne / and also
king Arthur wounded to death / Ca / lxxxviij.
When this tydynge come to king Arthur there that he was in burgoyne / he was
full sore annoyed / and took al France / to hoel for to keep with haluendele

self would wend in to britayne / and avenge him upon mordred that was his tray

that he might comen to land / For there was gawen his ne uew slain and
angnyssel that held scotland / and many other. whereof king Arthur was full
sorry / But after that they were co men to la^d / mordred might not against hem
endure / but an^ was disco^fyted / and fled thens the same night with his men /
and upon the morn to london / but tho of the cite would not suffer him to co me
in / and fled to winchestre / and there he held him with his people that with

angnissel / and let hem be born in to scotland in to her own country. and
there they were entered / and after anon king Arthur took his weye to destroy
mordred / and fled fro thens in to Cornewaylle / The queen gunn^e that was king
Ar thuris wife that tho soiourned at york / and herd that mordred was fled thens
/ and might not endure against king Arthur / she was sore adrad / and had great

to karlyone / and there she duellyd al her life that never was seyn among folk
her life during / Arthur wist that mordred was fled in to Cornewayle / and let
send after his men in to scotland and northumberlond unto humber / and let
assemble folk without no^bre / and comen fro thens in to Cornewayl to seche and
pursue after mordred / and mordred had assembled to him all the folk of
Cornewaylle / and had people without nombre, and wist that Arthur was coming /
and had lever to dye / and take his chance / than longer flee / And abode. and
yaf an hard battle to king Arthur / and to his people / so that much people was
slain. What of that one half / and in that other that no man wist / who had
the better party / but so it be fell at last that murdered was slain and all
his folk / and the good chyualrye that king Arthur had gadred, and norisshed of
diverse lands / and also the noble knights of the round table / that so
much were preysed through out all the world were there slain / And Arthur him
self was wounded to the death / but he let him be borne in a lyttyer to Auelon
to be heled of his wounds / and yet the Britons supposen that he live in
another land / and that he shall come yet and conquer al britayn / but certes
this is the prophe cye of merlyn / he said that his death shall be^doubtous and
said soth for men thereof yet have doubt / and shall for evermore as me says /
For men wit not whether that he lives or is deed / Arthur was born to Auelon /
the xxij year of his regne after the Incarnacion of our lord Ihu crist / v / C
/ and xlvj year /

When king arthur wist that he might no longer regne he let come before him

ha^ me was it that so noble a king and so doubty had no child of his body
bygoten / but all thing that god will have done / must be do ne / whose name be
blysshed withouten end /

How king Constantin was werred of mordredes two sons / Capitulo lxxxx
THis Constantin was a noble knight and a worthy of body / and tho two sons
that mordred had bigoten had great envy to Constantin / that tho was crowned
king / and so that they bygonne to meue werre against him, and assembled a
great hooste of hem that were to fore with mordrede / and had been driven awey
and that dyden much sorrow through all that land. that one brother ordeygned him
to london for to take the Cite / and that other to wynchestre / But Constantin
come to london and slow him that was there / and after he went to wynchestre /
and slow him that there was also, so that both his enemies were deed / And when
Constantyn had reigned worthily iiij year. he dyed and lies at london /

Of the kings Adelbryght and of edel / Ca / lxxxxj /
AFter king Constantins death / there were two kings in bri tayne / that one was
called Adelbright / that was a danoys And held the country of norfolk and
southfolk / that other hight Edel / and was a briton / and held nychol /
lyndesey / and all the land unto humber / These two kings fast werryd to
geders / but after they weren acorded / and loved to geder / as they had be
borne of one body, The king Edel had a sustre that was called Orewenne / and
he yaf her through great friendship to king Adelbright to wife / and he bygate on
her a daughter that was callid Argentill, and in the fourth year after come
upon him a strong sekenes / that needs he must dye / And he sent to king Edelf
his brother in law that he should come / and speak with him / and he come to him
with good will Tho prayed he the king. and coniured also in the name of god /
that after when he were deed / he should take Argentil his daughter and the land
/ and that he kept her well / and norysshe her in his chamber / and when she
were of age / she should be married to the strongest and wur thyest man that he
might find, and than he should yield up byr land ageyn / Edel it granted. and
by oath confermed his prayer And when Adelbryght was deed and entered. Edell
took the da misell Argentill / and norisshed her in his chamber. and she bycome
the fairest creature that might live or any man find / (...) were slain and
discomfyted. and whiles the battle dured the king pauely hyd him / and stale
awey in to wales / and men wist never where he bycome / and so was the town of
chichestre taken and destroyed. And after went gurmond and destroyed cytres and
tounes that never afterward were made again / as it is seen yet in many places
/

How this land was called England for the name of Engist and how many kings
were made after in the land Capitulo / lxxxxvj
When gurmond had destroyed all the land through out / he yaf the land to the
saxons anon / they took it with good will, for the saxons long time had
desired it / for as much as they were of Engystes kynrede that first had all
the land of bri tayne / and tho let hem be called English men for encheson
of Engystes name / And the land they let call it England in her langage, and
the folk ben called englysshme^ / for as much as in his time it was called
engystes land / when he had conquered it of Mortiger that had spoused his
daughter / but from the time that brute come first in to england this land was
called britayn / and the folk britons / but sith the time that this gurmond
eftsoon conquered it / and yafe it unto the saxons / and they anon right chau^
ged the name as before is said. And when this was done gurmond passed over in
to France / and there conquered many lands and destroyed al christian people there
that he come. and the saxons duel led in this land / and bygan it fast to
Inhabyte at her own will

And they would have made new kings and lords but they might never assenten
to have only one king for to be to hem en tendaunt / and therefore they made many
kings in diverse shyres as it was in engystes time, The first kingdom was kent
and that other southsexe / and the third westsexe / and the fourth estsex. and
the v northu^berlond / and the syxth estangle / that is to say norfolk and
southfolke / and the seuenthe merchenorth / and that is the Erldome of nychol /
hu^tingdone / herford / gloucestre / wynchestre / warwyck / and derby / and so
departed the englyssh al england in vij parties And after that it befell that
tho kings werryd oftyme to geder. and ever he that was strengest bynome him
that was feblyst / And so it was long time that they ^ad no king crouned
among hem / ne no christian man was tho among hem / ne Crystendome another /
But were Paynyms / tylle that Saint Gregorye was pope of Rome. that had seen
childeren of the Nacyon of England in the cite of Rome / that were wonder fair
crea^res / and had great will and desire hem to byholde / and axed of the
marchau^ts whens they were / and of what nation / and m^n told him that they
were of England, and Englyssh they were called. but they and all the people of
england were paynyms / and byleued not upon god / Allas quod saint gregorye well
mow they be called englissh / for they have the visage of angels / and therefore
well ought they to be christian. And for this encheson saint gregory sent saint
Austyn in to england, and xl good men with him that were of good life and holy
men to preche and teache and to conue ^te the englisshe people / and hem turn to
god / and that was in the sixth year that saint gregory had been pope / that is
to say after the Incarnacion of our lord Ihu crist v C lxxxvij year / as the
chronicles tellen

How saint Austyn baptized and converted king adelbright / and the bisshops
that made his felawes, Cao. / lxxxxvijo.
When saint Austyn come first in to england. he arrived in the I Will of Tenet /
and so passed forth / and come unto Caunterbury / and there soiourned / And
king Adelbryght of kent that was of the lygnage of Engyst fair under fenge
saint Austyn and his felaws with much honor / and hem fond all that hem neded
And ferthermore he yaf hem a fair place / that now is called the abbey of saint
austyns / in which place he lies him self shrined This king Adelbryght was a
good man / and with good will herd saint Austyns predicacions / and yafe him
leave to preche through al his land to torn and convert to him all the people
that he might It befell so afterward through gods grace / that in little time
the king him self was converted to god / and all his people of his land was
baptized / And in the mean time while the people turned hem to god Saint Anstyn
come to Rouchestre / and there preched gods word / The paynyms therefore him
scorned / and cast on him reygh taylles / so that / al ^s mantel was honged
full of reygh taylles / and for more despyte they cast on him the gutres of
reyghes and of fissh / wherefore the good man saint austin was so re annoyed and
grieved and prayed to god / that all the children that should be born afterward
in that Cite of Rouchestre must have tai les and when the king wist and herd
of this ve^geau^ce that was fall through saint Austyns prayer / he let make an
house in honor of almighty god. wherein women should be delyuerd of her children
at the bridges end / in which house yet women of the cite ben delyuerd of
child / when saint gregory had herd tell how the^g^ were tuurned to god, and
converted / he sent to saint Anstyn his passion by a bishop that was called
paulyn / and made him p^mat and Archebisshop of England / and sent word that he
than should ordeyne / and make bisshops in the land / And ^non as Austyn had the
passion of the dignyte of the archebisshop, he made two Bisshops of his felawes
that come with him from Rome / that one was called mellyte. and he duellyd at
london / And that other was called Iustyn, that held the dygnyte of Rochestre
/ and this Bishop mellite tho went to preche in to estsex / and baptized the
king of the country / that was called Sygeberte / that was king adelbryghtes
cosyn / his sustres sone. This Instyne went to preche in southsex / and turned
moc^ of the people to god / And saint Austyn went^ him self prechyng through out
England /

How saint Austyn went in to wales / there that the britons were / and how
they nold not be obedyent to the Archebisshop of ^u^ terbury / Cao. /
lxxxxviiio.
When all England was baptized and turned to god / Saint Austyn went in to

How king Adelbryght and the king olfryde slew brecinale that was a king of
britons that held the country of leycestre / Capitulo / lxxxxix /
HIt befelle so that there was a king Britone that held the country of beycestre
/ and all the country about named Brecinale / And this britone herd tell
that tho two englyssh kings would mete there at leycestre for to wend in to
walys / he let ordeyne all the power that he had for to fight with these two
kings / but little it auayled him / for his folk that he had were / layne and
him self fled and lost his lands for evermore. and these two kings Adelbryght
and elfryd duellyd a while at leycestre / and departed the land among hem /
and token homages and feautes of folk of the cou^ tree / And after they wenten
toward walys / and tho of walys had herd tell of the scomfyture that brecinal
had at leycestre / and were wonder sore adradde of tho two kings / and took
and chose among hem good men and holy of heremytes / monks and priests and
of other folk great plente that wenten barfoote and wellewerd for to have
mercy of the two kings. But tho kings were so stern and so wykked that they
nold never speak with hem / but slew hem euerychone / Allas for sorrow / for
they ne spared hem no more than the wolf does the sheep. but smyten of the
hedes of euerychone. and so al were there martred that to hem come / that is to
understand / v C / and xl / and afterward tho two kings went fro thens to
Bangore for to slay al tho that they might there find of the Britons And when
the britons that herd / they assembled and ordained all her power for to fight
with hem / tho was there a baron in wales that was called blederyk of Corn
wayle that sometime was lord of deuenshyre / but the king adelbryght had driven
him in to walys / and give him battle. And at that battle was king Adelbright
slain / and elfryd wounded sore / and forsook the field / and the most part of
his people slain / and elfrid fled in to northu^berlond that was his own land
/ And afterward the people of leycestreshyre made with strength Cadewan that
was brecynalys sone king of beycestre / and he after reigned nobly and with
great honor /

How Cadewan king of leycestre / and elfryde king of northu^berlond were
friends / and of the debate that after was between Edwyn and Cadwalyn that were

ANd after that this bataylle was done / the Britons ^ssembled hem / and went

he would g^ ne in to Northumberlonde to destroy king elfryde / and slay him y^
he might. And when he was comen thider. friends went so bitwe ne hem / and made
hem accorded in this manner / that elfryd should hol de all the land from humber
unto scotland / And Cadewen should have all the land a this side humber unto the
southe. and after that they bycomen good friends al her lives during / and
loved to gedre / as they had be two brethren / And this elfryde had a so ne
that was called ed wine / that had and held all the land of Nor thumberlond
after his faders death / as his fadre had hold all his lives time / And Cadewan
had another sone that was called ca walyn that held his faders land / as he
it held whiles he was a live / And they loved to gedre / as they had be
brethren / And the love last between hem but only two year /

And after bygan debate bitwene hem through a lyther ennious co syn of Cadwalyne
that was called briens / so that they assembled a great host in both parties /
and at^ last it befell that Cadwa line was discomfyt^d / and edwyn him pursued
/ and drofe him fro place to place / so at^ last he fled in to Irlond. and this
other destroyed his land / and cast a down castles / and bren^ his manners /
and departed all Cadwalyns land among his friends / And long time after come
Cadwalyn again from Irlond with a strong power and in plain battle slow
edwyn / and al his frendshippes / and name ly tho that withheld his lands
through edwyns yift

How king oswald was slain through king Cadwalyn / and peanda / And how oswy
that was saint oswaldes brother reigned after him / and slew peand^ / Ca / C /
j /
When that Edwyn was slain / Offrys his sone undertook the werre ageynste Cad

/ and drofe him to ward scotland* And when Cadwalyne (...) that he nold not
