tydyng that Cadwalyn turned home ageyn / he would no longer fl^ but abode peanda
/ and yaf him bataile / and peanda was discomfyted and fled and come again to

for to fight with oswald / so that he and peanda come unto northu^berlond and

place god has wrought for him many a fair miracle / both there and else where
/ And anon Oswy his brother seized in to his hand all the land that was (...)
and the folk of northumberlond loved him wonder well and hell de him for her lord
/ but he had men of his kyn worthy ynowg^ / that would have departed the land
/ and they werryd to g^dre / and for as much as they were not strong ynouw.
they comen to pean da and prayed him of help and socoure. and byhete him of
that long largely upon covenant that he would hem ghye / and help / and

that he should ordeyne a great host and fast ordeyne him in to northumberlond
for to fight with oswy / And Oswy was a meke man and much louyd pees and cha^e
/ and prayed Pean da of love and pees / and proffered him of gold and of silver
gret^ pl^n te. And this peanda was so proud / that he nold grant him pees

How king Cadewaldre that was Cadewaleyn^ sone reigned after his fadre / and was
the last king of briton^ / Capitulo / C / ijo /
AFter the death of Cadwaleyne / reigned his sone Cadwaladre well and nobly / and
his m^der was the suster of king peanda / and when he had reigned xij year he
fell in to a great sykenes / and than was there so great discord bitwene the
lords of the land that every werryd upon other / and yet in that time / there
fell so great derth and scarsyte of corn / and other vytaylles in this land
that a man might go iij days or iiij fro town to town that he should not fyn
de to bye for gold ne for silver bread wine ne none other vytaill werwith a man
might leave / but only the people lived by rotes of herbs / for other living
had they none so much was it failled all about / Fysshes wild beestes and al
other thing / so that yet to this mysauenture there fell so great mortalyte and
pestylence among the people by the corrupcion of the eyer / that the living
people / ne suffysed not to burye the deed bodies / fer they deide so suddenly
both greece and small / lord and servant / etyng going / spekyng / so that ne
uer was herd of more sudden death among the people / for he that went for to
burye the body / with the same deed body was buried They that myghten flee.
fledden / and forsook her lands and howses / as well for the great honger /
derth / and scarsyte of corn / and of other vytayle / as for the horrible
mortalyte and pestylence in the land / and wen^n in to other lands / for to
save her lines / and left the land all desert and waste / so that there was not
any man to trauayll and till the land / ne ere / ne sow. so that the la^d was
bareyn of corns and all other fruits / for defaute of tylyers / and this
mysauenture (...) ^ed enlenen year / and moo / that no man might ere ne sow /

How Cadwaladre went out of this land in to little britayne
CAdwaladre saw the great honger mortalyte and pestylence / and the land al
pour / and faylyng corns and other vytaylles and his folk perysshed. and
saw also the most party of his land al wasted and wide of people. he
apparaylled him and his folk that were left on live / and passed over in to
little britayne with a little nauye unto king aleyne that he much loved / that
was his cosyn and that his fader had much loved in his time / and as they
sailed in the sea / he made gre^e lamentacion. and so did al tho that were with
him and said / Dedisti nos domine tamquam oues escarum / and in gentibus
dispersisti nos /

ANd than bygan Cadwaladre to compleyn him to his folk pytously / and said /
Allas said he to us wretches and Caytyf. For why for our great sins. of the
which we would not amend us while we had space of repentance is comen upon
us this mysauenture / which chaceth us out of our own realm / and propre
soil / fro and out / of which sometime Romans Scotts* Saxons ne danes
might not exylen us / But what au a yleth it now to us that before time
oftsides have gotten many other lands. sith it is not the will of god that we
abide and duel le in our own land / God that is very Judge / that al things
knows before they be done or made / he sees that we would not cesse of our
sins / and that our enemies ne might not us ne our lygnage exylen fro and out
of our realm / he would that we amend us of our folyes / and that we seen our
propre defaultes and therefore has he showed to us his wrath and will chastyse
us of our misdeeds / Since that he does us without bataylle or strength of our
enemies by great companyes wretchedly to leave our own realm and propre land /
Turn again ye Romans / turn again ye scotts / Turn again ye Saxons /
turn again ye Fraunsoys now shows to you Brytayne al desert / the which
your power might never make desert ne yet your power has not now put us in
exyle / but only the power of the king almygh ty whom we have often offended by
our folyes / the which we wol de not leven until he chastysed us by his dyuyne
power / Among the words and lamentacion that the king Cadwaladre made to his
folk / they arrived in little britayne / and come to king aleyne before said /
And the king resseyned him with Joy / and made him to be served wonder nobly
/ and there he duellyd long time after / The englyssh people that were left on
live and were escaped the great honger and mortalyte lived in the best wise
that they might / and much people sprung and come of hem

And they senten in to Saxon / where they were ^rne to hy^ fre^ des for men /
women and children to restore the cytees with people and other tounes that were
al wide of people / and for to labor traua ylle and tillen the earth / when the
saxons had herd this tydyng they comen in to this land wonder thykke in great
companyes / And lodged and herburghed hem in the country al about / where
they would / For they found no man hem to let ne withstonde / And so they
woxen and multyplyed gretely / and used the custom mes of the countries /
whereof they were comen / and the laws and the langage of her own land / And
they changed the names of citees tounes castles and burghes. and yaf hem names
and called hem as they be now called / And they helden the Countres baronages /
lordshippes / and trees / in manner as the britons before time had compaced hem
/ And among other great companyes that co me fro germanye in to this land. came
the noble queen / that was called sexburga with men and women / without nombre
/ and ar ryued in the country of northumberlond / and took the land from
Albyone in to Corn wayle for her and for her folk, For there was none that
myghten letten hem / for all was desolat and wide of people But it were a few
pour britons / that were left in montaynes and wodes un till that time / And
fro that time forth losten Bri tons the royame for all days / And the english
people begone to regne / and departed the land between hem. and they made ma ny
kings about by diverse parties of the land / as here ben devised / the first
of westsex / the second merchenrich. the thyrdde estangle / the fourth kent /
the fyfth southsex / All these reigned in this land after Cadwaladre was passed
out of this land / and duellyd in little Britayne with king Aleyne his cosyn /
and true friend / And when he had long duellyd there / and had knowing that
the mortalyte and pestylence was over passed / and that the land was
replenysshed of Alyene people / he thought to turn again in to his own land
/ And prayed king Aleine his cosyn of socour and help that he might be
restored in to his pro pre realm / and first dygnyte / And king Aleyne
granted him his prayer / Than did he apparayllen him to take his weye / and
vyage in to this land. and prayed god Almighty devoutly that he would make to
him demonstracion / if his prayer in to this land were to him plesaunt / or
none / for again the will of god almighty he would nothing done / when he had
thus devoutly ma de his prayer. a voys fro heaven to him said / ^and bad him
leave that Journey awey in to england / and that he go to the pope of To me /
For it was not the will of almighty god that britons regne no more in Britayne /
ne never recover the land un to the time that the prophecye that merlyn said
before / be fulfilled / and that should never ben unto the time were comen.
that the relyques of his body shall be brought fro Rome / and translated in
britayn / and when the relyques of other saints that have been hyd for the per
secucion of the paynym folk / shall be founden / and openly showed / than shall
they recover her land again / which they have so long time lost through her
deserts / When Cadwaladre had herd this ansuere / he merueyled gretely / and
told it to king Aleyne / Than king aleyne did send for the clergy of his land
/ and made hem to bring the stories and prophecyes that merlyn and sibi^ had
said in her prophecyes / and when he knew that the prophecye that festome had
prophesied of the egle / and other prophecyes acorded to the dyuyne ansuere /
that Cadwaladre had herd / he cou^ceilled him to leave his people and his nauye /
and submytte him to the disposiaon of god / and done all that the angel had
commanded him / Than cad waladre called ynor his sone and yuory his cosyn / that
was his sus tres soue. and said to hem / Take said he my folk. and my nauye /
that is here al ready / and pass in to walys / and be ye lords of britons that
no dishonor come to hem by Interupcion of the paynyme folk for defaute of
lords / And he him self left his reame of bri tayne and his folk for evermore
/ and took his way to Rome to the pope Sergius / the which worshipped him
much / and so he was confessyd / and took penannce for his sins / And he had
not long duellyd there that he ne dyed the yij kalend of may / the year of
grace / v / C^ / lxxix /

How king offa was sovereign about all the kings of England / and how every
king werrxd upon other / Ca / C. ij
IT befelle so that all the kings in that time that were in the land as they
of westsex / merchenryche Estangle of kent and of southsex and of other costs
each werryd upon other / and be that was most mighty took the land of him that
was most feeble / But there was a king among hem that was called Offa that
was saint oswaldes brother / This offa conquered all the kings of the land /
and reigned above hem al / And so great was the werre in every country between
kings that no man might wit how the land went / But Abbots. Pryours / and men
of relygyon written the lives and the deeds of kings / and how long every
reigned had and in whose ceuntrey and in what manner every king dyed and of
bisshops also And thereof made great books and let call le hem the chronicles And
the good king Alured had that book in his ward and let bring it at
wynchestre and let it fast be (...) ked unto a pyler that men might not remeue
ne bear it thens so that every man might it see and thereupon look For therein
be the lives of all the kings that ever were in england

How the king of northumberlond osbright forlay the wife of Buerne bocard through
strength and after this buerne conquered the king with power and strength Ca C
iij
ANd thus it befell in the same time / that there was a king in northumberlond
that was callid Osbryght / and soiourned in york / and this king went him upon
a day in to a wode / him for to disporte. and when he come again / he went
privily in to a good man's hows that was called Buerne / And the good ^n of
that place was gone that time to the sce / for oftymes he was woned there aspye
and awaite thieves and robbours / that oftymes were woned to come in to the land
/ to rob. brenne / and slay / The lady that was this buernes wife was a /
wonder fair woman / and welcomed the king with mochel honor / and worthily
him served in all thing / when the king had eten / he took the lady by the
hand. and lad her in to a chamber / and said that he would speak with her a
counceyll / and all the folk from the chamber he ma de void sauf only the lady
and he / but the lady wist not where for he it did / til that he had done with
her his will / and when he had done this deed / he turned again to york. And
the lady he lefre there wonder sore weeping for the deed that he had y done /
and when her lord was com^ home and saw her weep and such sorrow and morning ma
ke / he axed of her what she had done / and why she made such sorrow Sir quoth she
queyntely / and falsely the king Osbryght me has do ne shame and vylonye
against my will / and told him treuthe / how the king had her forlayne with
strength. wherefore she said / she had lever to deye than live / Fair leef be
stylle quod he / for ageynste strength feblenesse is little worth / and therefore
of me shall thou never the less be loved / and namely / for thou haste me
told treuthe / and if almighty god grant me life / I shall the well auen ge /
This buerne was a great man and a mighty lord / and was well beloved and great
friends had and let send for the grettest lords of the land and to hem made
his compleynt of the despite that the king to him had y done and said that he
would been avenged how so that ever it were / and al his friends connceyled and
granted to wend to ward york / there that the king was / And buerne took his
meyne / and come to the king / and when the king him saw / he called him
courtously buerne by name / and buerne him ansuerde / and to him said / Sir I
you deffye / and yield up feautes. homa ges / and lands / and as much as I
have hold of you / and so fro this time forward / I will never of the nothing
hold / And so he de parted from the king without more speech / or any abydyng
/ and took leave of his friends. and went to denmark / and playned to the king
godryne. and told him the despyte / that king osbright to him had done of his
wife / and prayed him of socoure / and of help him to avenge / when king
godryne of denmark and the danoys had her de the pleynt of this buerne / and of
the prayer that he bad / they we re wonder glad in heart / for as much that
they might find cause for to gone in to england for to werre upon the
englisshmen / and al so for to avenge buerne of the despyte that the king had
done to his wife / and for as much as Buerne was Sybbe to the king of denmark /
Anon they let ordeyne a great host of men / and let ordeyne ships / and
as much as was need to that vyage / And when all the host was a ready / the
king made his two brethren chyuetayns / that were noble knights and bold /
that one was call lyd hungar / and that other hubba /

How the danoys took york / and slew the king Osbryght / and after ward king
elle / Cao. / C / iiijo.
When al thing was ready / tho two brethren took leave of the king godryn /
that went toward the sea for to wend in to England as fast as they might speed
/ Now is buerne so well co^ forted / and fast hyed him with the danoys that they
ben arrived in the northcountre / and comen through out holdeines / and
destroyed all the countreye / and burnt towns / and robbed folk / and slew all that might be take / til they come to york / And when king osbright saw hem
come / he took his people that he had / and come out of the cite / and fought
with hem / but no foyson he and ageynste hem And much was the people / that
there was slain in both parties. And king Osbright him self there was slain /
and the Cite anon was take / and the danoys wenten in / And there was also
another king in northumberlond that buernes friends had chosen / and held him
for king / a man that was called elle. for as much as they would not to king
osbright ben attendaunt / for the despyte that he had done to buerne her cosyn
/

Hit befelle thus that the king elle was gone to wode him for to dysporte / and
of venyson somdele he had take / and as he sat in the wode at mete to a knight
he said. we have well y sped and much venyson taken. and with that word there
come in a man / and to him said. if ye so much of venyson have wonnen / an
honderd ty mes so much more there against ye have lost. For all this country
the danoys have get / and take the cite of york / and against you shall it
hold that never ye shall not come therein And for sothe they have slain the
king osbryght And when king elle these words herd he let assemble all the
folk of the country and ordey ned all the power that he might have and would
have get the tou ne of york with strength / but the danoys come out anon /
and yaf him battle / and slew the king and the most part of his men that he
brought with him / and the same place there they were slain shall ever be
called Ellecroft / and that place is a little from york / And tho abode the
danoys never til they had conquered al northu^ berlond / And in that country
they made wardeyns / and went ferther in to the la^d / and token notyngham /
and there they abyden all the win ter / and dyden the sorrow that they might / And
after when somer time come / they remeued fro Notyngham / and come in to nychol
and to lyndesey / and to holond / For no man might hem withstonde so much
power and strength they had /

How saint Edmond the king was martred / Cao / C. vo.
ANd so fer had the danoys passed from country unto country and evermore
brennynge and robbynge / and destroyed all that they might till they comen unto
Thedford / And in that country they founden a christian king / that much loved
god and his works / that was called Edmond / And he was king of norfolk / and
south folk / This saint edmond king ordained as much folk / as he might and
fought with the danoys / but he and his folk were disco^fyted / and the king
him self driven unto the castle of Framelyn ham / and the danoys him pursued /
and come unto the same castle / And when king edmond saw that the castle
might not hem withstonde he come against hem with whom the danoys first spe
ken / and anon they axed of him where king edmond was now forsooth said he when
I was in the castle / there was the king / and when I went out of the castle /
he went out also / and whether he shall escape or dye / at gods will more it
be / When saint edmond had named god / by that they wysten well all that it was
he him self / and anon hubba and humbar took him / and said that he should god
forsake and al christian law. as many other had done him he forne / and saint
edmond said that he nold never but rather he would suffer death for gods love
and his laws to keep / tho took they saint edmond. and bound him unto a tree
/ and made her Archyers to him shete with arowes till that his body stykked as
fulle of arelbes. as an vrchon is full of pixckes / But for all the pain that
he had / he would never god forsake / and in the same pain and turment he dyed.
and betoke his soul to god / and when they saw that he was deed / they
smyten of his heed / And this manner was saint edmond martred /

How hubba and hungar took the town of red yng / Cao. / C / vjo.
When saint edmond was martred hubba and hungar went thens with all her danoys
unto redyng / And as they went thyderward / they burnt tounes / and cytees /
and slew al Cryste^ people / that would not god forsake / and cast a down
chirches / and come to redyng and took the town / and there held hem til that
the king Edelf of westsex come thider / with all his power for to take the to^
ne / Tho come out the danoys for to give battle to king edelf / and at that
battle was slain an earl of danoys that was called adrake upon the morrow come
the king elred and his brother Alured with a strong power and a great host /
And the king Edelf come again that had foughten the day before to that
battle / And the danoys tho comen out for to fight with hem / and the
bataylle was wonder strong. for many a man was there slain / and the danoys
that day had the vyctorye / and the king eldred and his brother alured that day
were disco^fyted / but the fourth day afterward the danoys and the englysshmen
foughten to geder another time upon Ekeldenne. And there was slain a king of
denmark. that was called Rafyn / and four earls of great power / And that day
had the danoys shame for they were driven unto engelfel^ / and the xv day after
the danes / and the englysshmen foughten another time at Rafynge / and there
were thenglysshmen discomfyted / and from thens a danoys / that was called
Roynt went to redynge with his host. and destroyed all that he might take /
And king el dred fought with him / but he was wounded so wherefore he was deed /
and he had not reigned but five year and lies at wonburne

Of king Alured / and how the danoys in his time prayed him of mercy that they
must goon out of the land / Ca / C / vij /
AFter the death of this Eldred / reigned his brother Alured / that Dolfynes was
called / Tho went the danoys and ass^ bled hem / and went for to seche Alured
that tho was the new king of southsex / and there they found him at wyltone
with a little pe ple / and netheles he fought with hem / but at last he fled
thens from the field / and went in to westsexe. and ordained so much people
of his own Royamme / and also of other so till that he had a strong host /
so that the danoys had no power against him to stand / and he come to london
with his hooste, and there where the danes soiourned. and there would he have
foughten with hem / but the danes durst not with him* fighten / but praid him
of pees / and that they must gone again in to her own countrry / and
neuermore in to england for to come again any harm to done / And upon this
covenant they should give him to pledge good hostages / and such as the
englysshmen would axen

How hubba and hungar were slain at Chippenham / and how the danoys brought
her king to our king / Cao. / C / viijo.
ANd the same day that the danoys departed from london so fast they riden
both night and day / and never took rest of going til that they comen unto
excetre / and took tho the town / and there held hem When king Alured herd
the tydyng / anon he let take the hostages. And went from thens to excestre
with all the power that he had / And when the danoys herd all of his co myng
they wenten fro thens in to westsex / and come to shippenam and there they dyden
much harm in the country / they robbed folk / and brought hem in prison /
The king alured hem pursiewed and come upon hem / and fyersly hem assaylled /
and there were slain both hubba / and hungar his brother and buerne / Bocard /
and in this bataylle was much folk slain in one party and in that other /
but the gore of the field left with the danoys / For as much as the king tho
come with little company / The king hasted him as much as he might for to wend
ayene / and when the Danoys founden hubba his body lyggyng deed / they entered
it, and made upon it a great lodge / and let call it hubbeslowe / and so it
is called in to this day / and that place is in deuenshyre / The barons of
Somersete. wylteshyre / and dorsete herd tell how that her king was
disco^fyted and ordained all the power that they myghten have and come to the
king there he was, and thanked god that they had him found alive, for they
had went that the danoys had him slain Tho took they a counceyll the king and
his barons that they would gone and seche the danes with hem to fyghten. and so
they ryden all that night hem for to seche and comen a morrow about prime to
abingdon there that the danoys were. The king tho Alured and his barons
assembled and there assaylled the danes egrely / and there yaf hem a strong
batail and the danes nobly put hem of long time that no man wist in whether
party more people were slain / But thus it befelle / as god would that the
king Alured had the vyctorye with much honor / For the daneys were so
driven that they ne wist whyder for to torn / and xv days the king hem
pursued at his will that glad and feign they were for to speken of pees and of
accord and token him good hostages / and said that they would never more upon
him werre / ne none debate arere / and more over they lehiht to the king Alured
/ that they would gone / and bring her own king unto him / and that her king
and they all should be baptystd And upon this condition king Alured him grau^tid
life and lym me / And said to him that they should gone her king for to seche
and at a certain day to comen again that to hem was set / and so they went
forth fast / and comen ageyn at her day that was assigned And all the danoys
brought her king with hem. The king Alu red anon let hem ben baptized / and
her names change-soo that the king of danoys called was Athelston / and xxx of
his fela des names were changed also / and the other were baptized to the
right believe / And all this was done at westmynstre / and after that the king
Alured held with him the king athelston / and al his danes xij days at
soiourne with much solempnyte, and yafe hem greet yeftes after that they were
baptized / and so they departed, Tho was Alured al at ese / when he had his
enemies overcome / and that they were turned to the right believe of Almighty
god /

How the dandys that comen in to Frannce with gurmond co men ageyn in to

ANd thus it befelle after ward that the danoys of northumberlonde that were

to destroy the christian people of England from place to place / and dyden much
sorrow / Hit befell thus as al mighty god would an hard chance in england /
For the good king Alured that was woned to a bate the danoys / deyde in the

could chastyse his enemies / for he was a good clerk and let make many ^ostes
/ And a book be made of englyss^ of auentures of kyngee and of batails that had been done in the lo^d and many other books of gestes he let hem write that were
of gre^ wisdom and of good lernyng through which ^okes many a man may him amide
that will hem ^de and upon ^oke / upon whose soul almighty god have mercy / And
this king alured lies at wynchestre

Of king edward that was king Aluredes sone / Cao. / C / xo. /

/ And after this eldred Ed wine sone of Edmond his brother reigned / and was a

that he should not regne no longer than vij year / and lies at wynchestre /

How king knoght that was a proud man conquered Norwey and how he bycome
afterward meke and mylde / Capitulo / C / xx /
Now have ye herd of Edmondes sons with Irensyde that king knoght wend that
they had been deed / as he had comman^d walgar before / And this knought had in
his hond all England and denmark / and after that he went to norwey that

and taken fea^tes and homages there he come after again in to england and held

and bycome so proud / and hauteyn / that it was great wonder / And so it befell
upon a day as he had herd mass at westmynstre / and would have gone in to his
palace the wawes of the thamyse so swyftely against him comen that almost they
tou ched his feet / Tho said the king with a proud heart / I command the
water to torn again / or else I shall make the / ^he wawes for his
commandment would not spare / but flowed over in ^e more and more / the king
was so proud of heart that he w^ld not ^e the water / but abode still in the
water / And beat the water ^th a small yerde that he held in his hond / and
commanded the water that it should wend no ferther / but for all his
commandemen^ the water would not cese / but ever wa^ more and more an high / so
that the king was al wete / and stood deep in the water / And when he saw
that he had abide there to long / and the water would n^thynge done his
commandment / tho sone he withdrowe him / and tho (...) he upon a stone. and
held his hondes an high / and said this word in heryng al people / This god
that makes the sea thus arise an ^gh he is king of al kings. and of myghtes
most / and I am a (...) and a man dedly. and he may never dye / and al thing
does his com^dement / and to him is obedyent / To that god I pray that (...) my
warrant. For I knowleche me caytyf fe^e and of no power / and therefore I will
go to Ro^ without any lettynge my wy^d nes to punysshe / and me to amend / For
of that god I claim my land for to hold and of none other / And anon made ^dy
his (...) and him self to Rome without any lettyng* and by the w^ did many
alms deeds / and when he come to rome also / and when he had ^en there and for
his sins done penance / he come again in to England / and bycome a good man

that other in Norwey. For as much as he loved specially saint Benet before all
other saints / and much also he loved saint edmond the king and of^e he yaf
great yeftes to the hows / wherefore it was made rich / and when he had reigned
xx year / he died and lies at wynchestre

Of king harold that lever had gone in foot. than ride ^n (...) Capitulo / C /

THis knoght / of whom we have spoken before had two sons by his wife emme

Of king hardeknoght that was harolds brother / Cao / C / xxij.
AFter this harold harefoote / reigned his brother hardeknoght a noble knight and
a worthy / and much louyd chyualrye. and al manner goodness / And when this
hardeknought had reigned a little while / he let uncover his brother harold, and
smite of his head that was his brother at westmynstre and let cast the head in
to a gonge, and the body in to thamyse / and after come fysshers and took the
body with her nets by night / and bear him to saint cl^me^ts church / and
there him beryed / And in this manner auengyd him Hard knoght of his brother /
For in none other manner he might be au^ ged / This king hardeknoght was so
large yeuer of mete and dryn ke, that his tables were set every day three
times / full with ryal metes and drynkes for his own meyne / and for all that
comen unto his court to be rychely served of ryal metes. And this king har
deknoght sent after Emme his mother / and made her come again in to england /
for she was drive out of england / whiles that ha rold harefoote reigned through
counseylle of the earl godewyn that tho was the grettest lord of england next
the king / and most might do what he would through al england / through his
co^ma^dement / for as much as he had spoused the daughter of the good king
knought, that was a danoys / which daughter he had by his first wif / and
when this queen was drive out of England / and come to the earl of flaundres
that was called baldewyne his cosyn / He fond her there al thing that her neded
unto the time that she went again in to england / that the king Hardeknoght
had sent for her that was her sone / and made her come ageyn with much honor
This king hardeknoght when he had reigned v pere. he dyed / and lies at
westmynstre /

Of the vylonye that the danes did to the english men / where for from that
time after was no danes made king of england / Capitulo / C xxiij /
AFter the death of this king hardeknoght for as much as he and nothing of his
body bygote / the earls and barons assem bled and made a counceyll / and never
more after no man that was a danoys / though he were never so great a man
among hem he should never be king of england for the despyte that the danoys
had done to english men / For evermore before hand if it were so that
englysshmen and danes happeden to mete to geder upon a budge / the englysshmen
should not be so hardy to meue ne stere a foot / but stand still til that the
danoys were apassed / And more over if the englysshmen had not abowed down her
hedes to done reverence unto the danoys, they should have been beat and defouled
/ and such manner despytes and vylonye dyden the danoys to our englysshmen /
Wherefore they were driven out of the land after time that hardeknoght was deed
/ For they had no lord that hem might mayn tene / In this manner voyded the
danoys england that never they come again / The Earls and barons by her comune
assent and counseyll senten unto normandye for to seche tho two brethren
alured and edward that were duellyng with the duke Rychard / that was her eme
in intent for to croune alured the elder brother and him make king of england /
and of this thing to make an end therfes and barons made her oath / But therle
goodwyn of (...) falsely and traytously thought to slay the two brethren
anon as they should come in to england in intent to make his sone Harold king.
the which sone he had bygoten upon his wife that was king knoghtes daughter
that was a danoys. and this godewyn pri uely went him in to southhampton for to
mete there the two bre theren when they should come to land / and thus it be fell
that the mes sagers that went in to normandy found not but only Alured that
was the elder brother / For edward his brother was gone to hu^ga rye / for to
speak with his cosyn edward the outlawe that was ed mo^ds sone with the
Irensyde / the messagers told and said to alured how that therles and barons of
england sent after him / and that he boldelyche should come in to england / and
vnde: fong the reame / For: king hardeknought was deed / and all the danoys
were driven out of the land,

How Godewyn the false traitor took Alured upon Gyldesdoune when he come f^o
normandye to be king of england / and did him ben martred in the yl^ of ely /
Cao. / C / xxiiijo.
When Alured herd this tydynge / he thanked god / and in to ship went with all
the have that he might / and passed the Sea. And arryned at south hampton there
that Godewyn the traytoure was / And tho this traitor saw that he was come /
he welcomed him and vnderfenge him with much Joy / and said that he would led
him to london there that all the barons of england him abode for to make him
king, and so they went in her weye to ward london And when they come upon
gildesdone tho said the traitor Godewyne to Alured / Take keep about you both
on the lift side and on the right side / And of all ye shul be king and of
such an hond^rd more, Now forsooth quod Alured I behote you / and if I be
king I shall make and ordeyne such laws whereof god and all fol k^ shu^en hem
hold well paid, Now had the traitor commanded al his men that were with him /
that when they were come v^on gyldesdone / that they should slay all that were in
alureds com panye / that come with him fro normandye / And after that taken
Alured and led him in to the I Will of Ely / and there put out both his eyes of
his head. and afterward bring him unto death / and they dyden so / for they
slew all the company that xij were in nombre of gentilmen / that were come
with Alured from normandye / And after token Alured / and lad him in to the isle
of ely / and put out his eyes out of his heed / and rent his womb. and
token the chyef of his boels / and put a stake in to the ground. and an end
of the boels there to fastened / and with nedels of iron prykked the good child
and so made him go about the stake / till that al his bowels were dra wen out
/ and so dyed there alured through treason of the earl godewyn / when the lords
of england had herd / and wist how Alured that should have been her king was put
unto the death through the false traitor godewyn. they were al wonder wroth / and
swore between hem god and by his holy names that he should dye in more werse
death / than did edryth of stratton / that had bytrayd his lord edmond Irensyde
/ and they would have put him to death / but the thef traitor fled thens in to
denmarck / and there held him four year / and more and lost al his land in
England

Of saint edward the confessor that was Aluredes brother / how he was king of
england. Ca / o. C / xxvo. /
ANd when this was done all the barons of england senten another time in to
normandye. for that edward should come in to england with much honor / And
this edward in his chyldehode louyd almighty god and him drad / And in honest
and clennes se lad his life / and hated sin as death, And when he was crouned
and ennoynted with a ryal power / he foryate not his good manners and conditions
that he first used / and foryate not al good customs for no manner honor / ne
for no manner riches / ne for no manner ^ghnes, but evermore and more yaf him to
goodness / and well l^ed god and al mekenes / and loved god and holy church
passing al manner thing / and pour men also / and hem loved and held / as
they had been his own brethren / and to hem often yaf great alms with good
will,

Of the first specyalyte that god showed for edwardes love by his life / Cao.
/ C / xxvjo /
IT befell on a day as he went from the church of westmynstre / and had herd
mass of saint Johan euangelyst / for as much as he loved saint euangelyst
more specially after god and our lady / than he did any other saint / And so
there ^me to him a pilgrim and prayed him for the love of god and of saint Johan
euangelyst sum good him for to give / And the king pre uely took his ring of
his finger that no man percerued it / and yafe it to the pilgrim / and he it
vnderfenge and went thens / This king edward made all the good laws of england.
that yet ben most holden / and was so mercyable and full of pity that no man
might be more /

How therle godewyn come in to england / and had again all his land. and after
ward saint edward wedded his daughter / Cao. / C. xxvijo.
When therle godewyn that was duellyng in denmark had much herd of the
goodness of saint Edward / and that he was full of mercy and of pity, And
thought that he would gone a geyne in to england for to seche / and to have
grace of him. and that he might have his land in pees / and arrayed him as
much as he might / and put him toward the Sea, And come in to England to
london. there that the king was that time / and all the lo^^^s of england / and
held a parliament / Godewyne sent to hem that were his friends / and were the
most grettest lords of the land and prayed hem to beseech the kings grace
for him / and that he would his pees and his land grant him / his enemies
ladden him before the king to seche grace / And anon as the king him saw / he
appelled him of treason, and of the death of Alured his brother / and these
words unto him said / Traitor Godewyne quod the king I thr appele that thou
have bytrayd and slain my brother Alured / Certes sir quod Godewyn save your
grace and your pees and your lordship. I never him bytrayd / ne slew him / and
therefore I put me in reward of the court / Now fair lords quoth the king / ye
that been my lyeges earls and barons of the land / that here ben al assembled /
Full well ye have h^rd mine appele / and the ansuere also of godewyn / And
therefore I will that ye award and do right / The earls and barons tho drowen
hem all to gedre for to done this award by hem self / and so they speken
dyuersly among hem / For sum said there was never allyau^ce by homage
serment service ne by lordship between Godewyn / and Alured / for which thing
they might him draw / and at the last they devised and demed that he should put
him in the kings mercy all to geders / Tho spak the earl leueryche of Couentre
a good man to god and to all the world / and told his reason in this manner / and
said the earl godewyn is the best frended man of England after the king / and
well might it not ben gayn said that without cou^seill of godewyn Alured was
never put to death / wherefore I award as touching my part that him self and his
sone and every of us / xij / earls that been his friends wend before the king
charged with as much gold and silver. as we mow bear bitwene our hands / and
prayeng the king foryeue his evil will to therle godewyn / and receive his
homage / and his land yield ageyn / and al they accorded unto that award / And
comen in this manner as is abone said every of hem with gold and silver as much
as they might bear between her hon des before the king / and they sayden the
form / and the manner of her accord and of her award / The king would not hem
gayn say / but as much as they ordained, he granted and confermed / and so
was therle godewyn accorded with the king / and had again al his la^d And
afterward he bear him so well and so wisely that the king loved him wonder much
/ and with him was full pryue.

And within a little time, the king loved him so much that he spoused godewyns
daughter / and made her queen / and netheles for all that tho the king had a
wife, he lived evermore in chastyte / and in clennes of body without any
flesshely deed doing with his wif and the queen also in her half lad holy life
two year and deyde / And afterward the king lived al his life without any wife /
The king yafe the erldome of oxenford to harold that was godewynes sone and
made him earl / And so well they were bilouyd both the fadre and he and so prive
with the king both the fadre and the sone / that they might done what thing
they would by right. For ageynste right would he nothing done for no manner man /
so good and true he was of conseyence, and therefore our lord Ihu crist great
specially lo ue to him showed

How king edward saw Sweyne king of denmark drenched in the sea in the
sacrament as he stood and herd mass / ca / C xxvij /
IT befell upon whytsonday as king edward herd his mass in the great church
of westmynstre right at the leuacion of Ihesu cristes body. And as al men were
gadred in to the church and come nere the auter sacryng for to see the king
his houdes ^te upon high, and a great laughter took up / Wherefore all that
about him stood gretely gonne Wondre / and after mass they axed why the
kings laughter was / Fair lords quod the king / Sweyne the younger that was
king of denmark come in to the sea with all his power for to have comen in to
england up on us to have werryd, and I saw him and al his folk drenched in
the high see / and all this saw in the eleuacion of Ihu cristes body between
the priests hondes, and I had thereof so much Joy that I might not my
laughter witholde / and the earl leueryche besides him stood at the leuacion,
and openlyche he saw the form of bread torn in to a likeness of a young
child / and took up his right bond and first blyssed the king and afterward
therle / and the Earl anon turned him toward the king to make him see that
holy syghte / And tho said the king / Sire earl said he I see well that ye see
thanked be god that I have honored my god my savior vys^ly Ihesu crist in
form of man whose name be blyssed in all worlds

Amen
How the ring that saint edward had give to a pour pilgrim for the love of
god / and saint Johan euangelyst come again unto king edward Capitulo / C xxix
THis noble man saint edward reigned xiij year / and thus It be fell upon a time
before er he died that two men of england were went in to the holy land / and
hadden done her pylgremage / and were going again in to her own country /
And as they went in the wey they met a pilgrim that curtoysly he in salued. and
axed in what land and in what country they were borne / And they said / in
England / Tho axed he who was king of england / and they ansuerd and said the
good king Edward / Fair friends tho said the pilgrim / when that ye come in to
your country again / I pray you that ye will gone unto king edward / and
oftymes him great in mine name / And often times thank him of his great curtosye
/ that he to me has done and namely for the ryng that he yaf me when he had
herd mass at westmynstre for saint John's love euangelyst / and took tho the
ring and took it to the pylgryms / And said I pray you for to gone and ^re
this ryng / and take it to king edward / and ^rl le him that I sent it him and
a full rycher yefte I will him give. For upon the. xij. day he shall come to me
/ and evermore duel le in bliss without end / Sir said the pylgryms / what
man l^n ye / and in what place is your duellyng. Fair friends quod le I am
Johan the euangelyst / and am duellyng with almygh ty god / And your king
edward is my friend / and I love him specialy for encwson that he ever has
lived in clennesse / and is cle ne maid / And I pray you my message al for to
done / ^o I ha ue to you y said / when saint Johan enangelyst had thus l^m
charged suddenly he wyded out of her sight /

The pilgrims tho thanked almighty god / and went forth in her way / And when
they had gone two or three mile / they bygonne to wo^e weary / And sat a down
him for to rest / and so fyl a sleep / And when they had slepte well, one of
hem a woke and lif^e up his heed. and looked about and said unto his felaw /
Arise up / and wend we in our weye / what said that one felawe to that other /
where be we now / Certes said that other / It seems me that this is not the
same countreye / that we laid us in for to wst and sleep / For we were from
Jerusalem but three miles / They token up her hondes and blessed hem / and went
forth in her way / And as they went in her weye / they saw shepeherdes going
with her sheep that speken none other langage but englisshe Leave fre^des qd^
one of the pilgrems what country is this / and who is lord chewf. and one of
the shepeherdes ansuerd / this is the country of kent in england / of the
which the good king edward is lord The pylgryms thanked almighty god / and
saint John euangelyste / and went forth in her wey / and come to Caunterbury.
and fro thens in to london / and there they found the king. and told him al fro
the beginning unto the end / as much as saint Johan had hem charged / and of
al things how they sped by the wey / and took the ryng to king edward / and he
vnderfenge it and thanked almighty god / and saint John euangelyst / And tho
made him a ready every day from day to day. for to we^de out of this life / when
god would for him send /

How saint edward dyed on the xij day / Ca, C / xxx /
ANd after it befell thus in cristemasse eve as the holy man Edward was at
gods service man's for to here of the high fest, he bycome full syke / / and
in the morrow endured with much pain the mass for to here / and after let
him be ladde in to his chamber there for to resten him / but in to his hall
amo^gs his bawns and knights might he not come hem for to comfort and sola ce
as he was woned for to done at that worthy fest / wherefore all her mirth and
comfort among all that were in the halle was tor ned in to care / and sorrow /
for encheson that they dred for to l^sc ler good lord the king / And upon saint
Iohans day euangelyst tho that come next / the king vnderfenge his ryghtes of
holy church as falls to every christian man, and abode the mercy and the will
of god. and tho two pylgryms he let before him come / and yaf him rich yeftes
and bytoke hem unto god / And also the abbot of westmynstre he let before him
come / and took him that ring in honor of god and saint marye / and of saint
John euangelyst / and the abbot took and put it among other relyques / so that
it is at westmynstre and ever more shall be / and so lay the king seek / til the
xij even / and tho di ed the good king Edward at westmynstre / and there he
lies / For whose love god has showed many fair miracles / and this was in the
year of Incarnacion of our lord ihu crist / in, lxv / year / And after he was
translated / and put in to the shryne through the noble martyr saint thomas of
Caunterbnry /

How Harold that was good wyns sone was made king / and how he escaped fro the
duk of normandye / Cao. / C / xxxi
When saint Edward was gone out of this world / and was gone to god / and
worthily entered / as it apperteyned to such a lord for to be / the barons of
the land would have had Edward Helyngus sone to Edward the outlawe that was
edmond Irensydes sone to be king for as much as he was most kyndeste kings
blood of the reame / But harold sone of therle godewyn through the strength of
his fadre good wyn and through other great lords of the roya^me that were of
his kyn / and unto him sibbe seysed al england to his hand / and anon let him
croune king after the enterement of saint edward / This harold that was
godewynes sone the second year tofore that saint edward was deed would have gone
in to Flaundres / but he was deyue through tem pest in to the country of pou^tyf
/ and there he was take and brought to the duke william / And this harold went
tho that duk william, would have been auengyd upon him for encheson that therle
Godewyne that was harols fadre had let slay Alured, that was saint edwardes
brother / and pryncypally for encheson that alured was queen enimes sone that
was rychardes mother duke of nor mandy that was ayell to the duke wylliam / And
netheles when the duk william had harold in prison / and under his power for as
much as this harold was a noble knight wise and worthy of body / and that his
fadre and he were accorded with good king edward / and therefore would not mysdone
him / but al manner thyn ges / that between hem were spoken / and ordeygned
Harold by his good will swore upon a book / and upon holy saints that he should
spouse and wedde due williams daughter after the death of saint ed ward / and
that he should besyly done his deuer for to keep and save the royame of england
to the profit and auau^tage of duk william / and when harold had thus made his
oath unto duke wylliam / he let him goo / and yafe him many rich yeftes / and
he tho went thens and come in to england / and anon deed in this manner / when
saint Edward was deed and as a man falsely forswore / he let croune him king
of england / and falsely brake the conenau^ts that he had made before with duk
william / wherefore he was with him wonder wroth and swore that he should upon him
ben auengyd what ever so him befell / And anon duk william let assemble a
great host / and come in to england to avenge him upon harold / and to
conquer the la^d if that he might / And in the same year that harold was
crouned harold harestrenge king of denmark arrived in scotland. and thout to
have been king of england / and he come in to england and slew / and robbed and
destroyed all that he might till that he come to york / and there he slew many
men of arms a / M / and an honderd priests / when this tiding come to the
king. he assembled a strong power and went for to fight with harold of
denmarck / and with his own hond him slew / and the danes were discomfyted /
and tho that left a live with much sorrow fled to her ships / And thus king
Harold of england slow king harold of denmark.

How william bastard duk of normandy come in to england / and slew king harold
/ Cao. / C. xxxijo. /
ANd when this battle was done / harold bycome so proud and would no thing
part with his people of thing that he had gotten / but held it al toward him
self / wherefore the most party of his people were wroth / and from him
departed. so that only with him left no mo but his soudyours / And upon a day
as he sat at mete / a messagyer come to him and said / that william bastard
duk of normandy was arrived in england with a great host / (...) had taken all the land about hastynge / and also mined the castle / when the king had herd
this tydynge / he went thither with a litel people with all the have that he
might for a litel people was with him left / And when he come thither / he
ordained for to give battle to the duk william / But the duk axed him of these
three things / if that he would have his daughter to wife as he had ma de and
sworen his oath / and behyght / or that he would hold the la^d of him in truage
/ or that he would determyne this thing through bataylle, This harold was a
proud man and a stout / and trusted wonder much upon his strength / and
fought with the Duk and with his people / but harold and his men in this battle
were discomfyted / and him self was there slain. And this bataylle was ended at
Conbrydge in the second year of his regne upon saint kalyxtes day. and he lies
at waltham /

Of king william bastard / and how he governed him well and wisely / and of the
werre between him, and the king of France / Capitulo C / xxxiij / w^ Han
william bastard, duk of normandy had conquered all the land upon crystemasse day
/ tho next sueng / he let him croune king at westmynster / and was a worthy
king / and yafe to En glysshmen largely lands. and to his knights

And afterward went over the sea / and come in to Normandy and there duellyd a
while / And in the second year of his regne le come again in to England / and
brought with him maude his wife / and let croune her queen of england on
whitsonday, And tho anon after the king of Scotland that was called malcolyn
began to strive and werre with the duk william. and he ordained him tho toward
scotland with his men to the by land and by see for to destroy king malcolyn
/ but they were acorded / And the king of scotland bycome his man / and held
al his land of him And king william resseyned of him his homage / and come
ayene in to england / and when king william had be king / xvij / year / maude
the queen dyed, on whom king william had bygoten ma ny fair children / that is
for to say Robert Curthose / william. le Rous / Rychard also that deyde / Henry
beauclerk / and maude al so / that was the earls wife of Bleynes. and other iiij
daughters / and after his wyfes death great debate bygan bitwene him / and the
kyn ge of france philip / but at last they were acorded / and tho duellyd
the king of England in normandy / and no man him werryd and he no man long time
/ and the king of france said upon a day in scorn of king william / that
king william had long time leyn in childbed / and long time had rested him /
and this word come to the king of england there that he lay in normandy at
Roen / and for this word was tho ylle paid. and eke wonder wroth toward the
king of frannce / and swore by god that when he were arise of his gysyn / he
would light a thousand candels to the king of frau^ ce / And anon let assemble
a great host of normandy / and of en glysshmen / and in the bygynnyng of
heruest / he come in to france / and burnt all the tounes that he come by
through all the country / and rob bed / and did all the evil that he might through
out al france / and at last he burnt the cite of mandos. and commanded his
people for to here wode / and as much as might brenne and him self help
thereto all that he might with a good will / And there was great hete what of
fire that was so great and of the son / that tho was wonder hot / that al
stuffed him self bycome / and fell in to a greet sikenesse, and when he saw
that he was so strong syke. he ordained and assigned al normandy unto Robert
Curthose his sone / and all england to wylliam the rous / and byquath to henry
beauclerk all his tresour / And tho he thus had done. he vnderfenge all the
sacramentis of holy church / and deyde the xxij year of his regne / and lies
at Caan in normandye.

Of king william Rous that was wylliam bastardes sone / that destroyed tounes
and houses of Relygyon for to make the new forest / Capitulo C / xxxiiij /
ANd after this william bastard reigned his sone william the Rous. and this
william was a wonder contraryous man, to god and to holy church, and let
amend and make the town of Cardeys that the paynyms had destroyed / This king
william destroyed holy church and al her possessions in what part he might hem
find / and therefore there was so much debate between him and the Archebisshop
of Caunterbury Anc^lme / for encheson that he vndernamme him of his wykkednesse
that he destroyed holy chir che / And for encheson thereof the king to him bare
great wrath and for that cause he exyled him out of the land / And the
Archebisshop tho went to the court of Rome / and there duellid with the pope /
and this king made the new forest / and cast and destroyed xxvj tounes / and
lxxx houses of Relygyon al for to make his foreste longer and bredder, And
bycome wonder glad and proud of his wode / and of his forest. and of the
wild beestes / that were therein / that it was marvel for to wit / so that
men called him kepar of wodes and of pastures. and the longer that he lived /
the more wykked he bycome both to god and to holy church / and to all his
men, And this king let make the great halle at westmynster / so upon a day of
whitsonday he held therein his first feste / and he looked about and said that
the halle was to little by the haluendele / And at last he bycome so
contraryorous / that al thing that plesed god displesyd him / and al thing that
god loved / he bated dedely / And so it befell that he dremed / and met upon a
night a little or that he dyed / that he was let blood. and blod a great
quantite of blood / and a streme of blood lept an high toward heaven more than
an / C / fathem / and the clerenes of the day was turned all in to derknes /
and the fyrmament also / And when he awoke he had great deed / so that he nyst
what to done / and t^ld his dreme to many of his counseylle, And said that he
had great dread / and supposed that him was sum myschaunce to come / And the
second night before / a ^o^ke dremed of the household / that the king went in
to a church with much people / and he was proud / that he despised all the
people that was with him / and that he take the image of the crucyfyx / and
shamefully bote it with his treth. And the crucyfyx mekely suffered all that he
did / but the king as a wode man rent of the arms of the crucifyx / and case
it un der his feet / and defouled it / and three we it al a broad / and a
greet flamme of fire c^m onte of the crucyfyx mouth, of which dreme many men
had great wonder / The good man that had dremed this dreme had told it to a
knight that tho was most pryue with the king of al me^ / and the knight was
called bamsides sone And the monk and he told the dreme to the king and said
that it should bytoken other thing than good and netheles the king lau ghed there
at twyes or thryes / and little set thereof / and thought that he would gone hunte
and play in the fovest / and his men him cou^ceyl led that he should not that
day for no manner thing come in the wode / so that he abode at home before mete
/ But anon as he had eten / no man might him let that he nold gone to the
wode for to have his disport / And so it befell that one of his knights, that
hight walter Tyrell would have shot to an heart / and his arowe gla^sed upon a
branch, and through mysauenture smote the king to the heart and so he fell down
deed to the ground without any word speking and so ended his life / and it was
no great wonder for the day that he deyde he had let to fermethe
archebisshopriche of Canterbury and xij abbeyes also / and ever more did great
destruction to holy church / thurugh wo^rgful taking and axyngs / for no man
durst withsay that be would have done / and of his lythernes he would never
withdraw another to amend his life / and therefore god would suffer him no longer
regne in his wykkednesse / and he had been king xiij year / and sixth wekes, and
lies at worcestre /

Of king henry beauclerke that was william Rous brother / and of the debate
between him and Robert Curthose his brother Capitulo / C / xxxv /
ANd when this william Rous was deed / henry beauclerke his brother was made
king for encheson that wylliam rous had no child bygoten of his body, and this
henry beauclerk was crouned king at london the fourth day after that his brother
was deed, that is to say / the fyfth day of August / And anon as Ancelme that
was Archebisshop of Caunterbury that was at the court of Rome herd that wylliam
Rous was deed. he come ayene in to england, and the king beauclerk welcomed
him with much honor / and the first year that king henry was crou ned he
spoused maude that was margaretes daughter / the queen of Scotland / And the
Archebisshop Ancelme of Caunterbury wedded hem / And this king biga^ upon his
wife two sons and a daughter / that is to say / william Rychard / and maude,
And this maude was after the emperesse of Almayne / And in the second year of
his regne, his brother Robert Curthose / that was duke of normandye come with an
huge company in to England for to challenge the land / but through connceylle
of the wise men of the land they were acorded in this manner that the king
should give the duke his brother a thousand pound every year / and which of hem
longest lived, should ben other heyr / and so between he in should be no debate
ne strife / and when they were thus acorded / the duk went home again in to
normandy / And when the king had reigned four year / there aroos a great debate
between him / and the Archebissho of Caunterbury Ancelme / for cause that the
archebisshop would not grant him for to take tallyage of chirches at his
will, And therefore eftsone the Archebisshop went over the sea to the court of
Rome / and there duellyd with the Pope / And in the same year duk of normandy
come in to England for to speak with his brother / And among other things the
Duke of normandy for yaf to the king his brother the foresaid thousand pound by
year that he should pay him / And with good love the duke went tho again in to
normandy / And when tho two year were a gone through enticement of the deuel /
and of lyther men / a great debate aroos between the king and the duk / so that
the king through counseyll went over the sea in to normandye / And when the
king of England was comen in to Normandy / all the great lords of Normandye
turned to the king of england / and held against the duk her own lord / and
him forsook / and to the king hem yelden and all the good Castles and towns of
normandy / And sone after was the d^k tasten / and lad with the king in to
england / and the king le^e put the duk in to prison / And this was the
vengeance of god / for when the duk was in the holy land / God yafe him such
might and thonour / there wherefore he was chosen to ben of ^emsasem king, and
he would not be it / but forsook it / and therefore sent him that shame and
despyte for to be put in to his broders prison / Tho seized king henry all
normandy in to his hand / and s^e it all his lives time / And in the same
year come the Bishop Aun^lme from the court of Rome in to England again /
and the king and he were acorded.

And in the year next coming after there bigan a great debate by twene king
philip of France / and king henry of england / wherefore king henry wend in to
normandy / And the werre was strong between hem two. And tho dyed the king of
France / and lowys his sone was made king anon after his death And tho went
king henry again in to england / and married man de his daughter to henry the
emperor of almayne /

Of the debate that was between king lowys of France / and king henry of
england / and how king henryes two sons were lost in the high see / Capitulo C
/ xxxvij.
WHenne king henry had been king xvij year / a great debate aroos between king
lowys of Frannce / and king henry of england for encheson that the king had
sent in to Normandye to his men / that they should ben helping to therle of
Bloys as much as they might in werre ageynste the king of france / and that
they were as ready unto him as they would ben unto her own lord / for encheson
that therle had spoused his sustre dame man de / for which encheson the king
of France did much sorrow to normandye, wherefore the king of england was wonder
wroth / and in have went over the sea with a strong power / and come in to nor
mandye for to defend that land / and the werre between hem lasted two year to
geder / til at the last they two foughten to geder / and the king of France
was discomfyted and uneath escaped awey with much pain / and the most part
of his men were take / and the king did with hem what him lyked / and sum of
hem let he go frelych and sum let he put to the death / but afterward tho
two kings were acorded / And when king henry had holych all the land of
Normandy / and scomfyted his enemies of France, he turned ayene in to england
with much honor / and his two sons william and Richard would come after her
fadre, and went to the sea with a great co^ panye of people / but or that they
might come to land / the ship come against a roche and break al in to pyeces
/ and all were drenchyd / that were therm sauf one man / that was in the same
ship / that escaped / and this was on saint kateryns day / and these were the
names of hem that were drenchyd / that is to say wylliam the kings sone /
richard his brother, therle of chestre / Otto^el his brother Geffroy ridelle /
wal^er emurcy / Godfrey archedeken / the kings daughter the Countess of
perses / the kings nece. the countess of chestre, and many other / when king
henry / and other lords arrived were in england / and herd these tidings /
they made sorrow ynow and al her mirth and joy was turned in to moruyng and
sorrow

How mawde the emperesse come again in to england. And how she was afterward
wedded to geffroy the earl of Angeo / Capitulo. C xxxvij
ANd when that two year were a gone that the earl had duel led with the king /

he was begynner and foundour

How stephen king henryes sustres sone was made king of england / Ca^ / C /
xxxviij^ /
AFter this king henry that was the first was made king his neuew his sustres
sone stephen earl of Boloyne / For anon as he herd tydynge of his uncles death
/ be passed the Sea / and come in to England through counseylle / and strength
and help of many great lords in england against her oath that they had made to
maude the emperesse took the royame and let cronne ste phen king of the land /
And the Archebisshop william of Canterbury that first made the oath of feaute
unto maude the emperes se set the croune upon king stephens head / and him
ennoynded and bishop Rogyer of salysbury mayntened the kings party in as
much as he might / The first year that king stephen bigan to regne / he
assembled a great host. and went him toward scotland for to have werrid upon
the king of scotland / but he come against him in pees / and in good manner / and
to him trusted, but he made to him none homage / for as much as he had made
homage to the em peresse maude / and the fourth year of his regne, maude the
emperesse come in to england, and tho bygan debate between king stephen, and
maude the^ peresse / This maude went in to the cite of nychol and the king her
besyeged long time / and might not speed so well the Cite was kept and defended
/ and tho that were within the cite queyntely ascaped awey without any manner
harm / and tho took the king the Cite and duellyd therein til candelmesse / And
tho come the barons that held with the emperesse that is for to say the earl
Randulphe of chestre / the Earl Robert of gloucestre hugh bygot / Robert of
morley / and brought with hem a strong power and fought with the king and yaf
him a great batayl / in which battle king Stephen was taken and set in
prison in the castle of Brystowe /

How maude the emperesse went fro wynchestre unto oxenford And after she
escaped to wallyngford / and what sorrow / and disease that she had / Capitulo,
C / xxxix.
When the king was take and brought in to ward in the Castle of Bristow /
this maude the emperesse anon was ma de lady of england and al men her held
for lady of the land / But tho of kent held with the king stephens wife, and

nombre of people / and tho went they y fere unto wynchestre / there that the
emperesse was, and would have take her / but therbe of gloucestre come with his
power / and fought with hem and the emperesse in the mean while that the
battle du^d escaped fro thens and went unto oxenford / and there her held /
And in that bataylle was therle of gloucestre discomfyted and taken / and with
him many other lords / And for his delyuerau^ce was king steven delyuerd out
of prison / and when he was de lyuerd out of prison, he went thens to oxenford
/ and besyeged the emperesse that was tho at oxenford / and the syege endured
fro Mychelmasse unto saint andrewstyde. And the emperesse let tho clothe her
all in white lyn^n cloth for encheson that she would not be know / for in the
same time was much snow / and so she escaped by the thamyse from hem awey /
that were her enemies / And fro thens she went to wallyngford / and there her
held / and the king would have besyeged her / but he had so much to done with
therle Randulf of chestre / and with hugh bygot that stronglych werryd upon him
in every place that he ne wist whyther for to torn / And the earl of
gloucestre halpe hem with his power /

Of king henry the second that was the emperesse sone / in whose time saint
thomas of Caunterbury was chaunceler / Ca / C. xlj /

the king was translated with much honor / And the x^ year of his regne he

and him / For if he had been founden in the morn he had be slain / and

was and went over the sea to the pope of Rome And this was the pryncypal
encheson for as much as the king would have put clerks to death / that we re
atteynt of felonye without any pryuelege of holy church / And the xij year
of his regne was Johan his sone borne / and the xiij year of his regne deyde
maude the emperesse that was his mo der / And in that same year was Johan his

Of king henry that was sone of king henry the emperesse sone. and of the
debate that was between him and his fudre while that he was in uormandye /
Capitulo / C xlij.
AFter the coronacion of king henry / the sone of king henry the emperesse sone
/ That same henry the emperesse sone went over in to normandy / and there he

archebisshop to Caunterbury again to his own church And this accord was made
in the beginning of aduent / and afterward he was slain and martred / the
fyfthe day of Crystemasse / that tho next come / For king Henry thought upon
saint thomas archebisshop upon Crystemas se day as he sat at mete, and these
words said / that if he had any good knight with him he had be many day passed
auengyd upon the archebisshop thomas / And anon Sir wylliam Breton Sire hugh
moruyle / Sir william Tracy / And sir reynold fytz vrse beres sone in englyssh
pryuely went unto the sea / and common in to England to the church of
Caunterbury / and him there they martred at saint benets auter in the mother
church / And that was in the year of Incarnacion of Ihesu cast / M / C / lxxij
/ year. And anon after henry the new king bygan for to make werre upon henry
his fadre / and eke upon his brethren also /

And so upon a day the king of France / and all the kings sons / and the king
of scotland / and the gre^ttest lords of En glond were arrysen against the
king henry the fadre / and at the last as god would he conquered all his enemies
/ and the king of frau^ ce and he were acorded / And tho sent king henry the
fadre specially unto the king of France / and prayed him hertely for his love
/ that he would send to him by letter the names of hem / that bygonnen the
