Rychard his brother. and Henry his sone the new king / Tho was henry the king
wonder wroth / and cursed the time / that ever he hem bygate. And while the
werre dured / henry his son the new king dyed sore repentyng his mysdede and
most sorrow made of any man for cause of saint thomas death of Caunterbury / And
prayde his fadre with much sorrow of heart mercy for his trespass / and his
fader foryafe it him. And had of him great pity / and after he dyed the xxvj
year of his regne / and lies at Redyng /

How the Christian lost the holy land in the forsaid kings time through a falls
christian man / that bycome a sarasyn / Cao / C / xliij /
ANnd while that king henry the emperesse sone lived and reigned / the great
batayl was in the holy land between christian men and the sarasyns / but the
christian men were there slain through great treson of the earl Tyrpe / that would
have had to wif the queen of Jerusalem / that sometime was balde wynes wife / but
she forsook him / and took to her lord a knight a worthy man that was called
Sir Guy perches / wherefore therle Tyrpe was wroth and went anon right to
saladyne / that was soudan of babyloyn / and become saraseyn and his man. and
forsook his cristendome and al christian law / and the christian men wist not of
his deeds / but wend for to have had great help of him / as they were woned
to have before / and when they come to the bataille / this false christian man
turned unto the saraysus and forsook his own nations / and so were the
christian men there slain with the sarasyns / and thus were the christian men slain
and put to horrible death / and the cite of Jerusalem destroyed and the holy
cross borne awey / The king of France and all the great lords of the land
let hem cross for to gone in to the holy land / And among hem went Rychard
king henryes sone first af ter the king of france that took the cross of the
Archebisshop of tours / but he took not the vyage at that time for encheson
that he was let by other manner weyes and needs to be done. And when king
henry his fadre had reigned xxxv year / and v months / and four days / he
dyed / and lies at founteuerard /

Of king rychard that conquered all the holy land that Christian men had lost /
Cao. / xliiij /
ANd after this king henry reigned Richard his sone a strong man and worthy /
and also bold. and he was crouned at west mynster of the archebisshop baldewyn
of Caunterbury the third day of September. and the second year of his regne /
king Rychard him self and baldewyn the archebisshop of Caunterbury / and hubert
bishop of salysbury and Randulfe earl of gloucestre / and other many lords of
england went in to the holy land / And in that vyage deyde the archebisshop of
Caunterbury. And king rychard went before in to the holy land / and rest not
til that he come forth in his wey unto Cypres / And took Cypres with great
force* and sythen king Rychard went forth toward the holy land / and get
there as much as the Christian men hadden lost before. and conquered the land
again through might sauf only the holy cross / And when king richard come to
the town of Acres for to get the cite / A great debate aroos between him and
the king of france / so that the king of france went ageyn in to frannce. and
was wroth toward the king rychard / but ex king Rychard went again / he took
the cite of Acres / And when he had taken it. he duellyd in the cite a while /
but to him come tydyng / that the earl Johan of oxenford his brother would have
seized al england in to his hand / and normandye also / and would crou ne him
king of the land / And when king Rychard herd this tydyng he went again
toward England with all the speed that he might / but the duk of Ostryche met
with him / and took him / and brought him to the emperor of almayne / And the
Emperor brought him in to his prison / and afterward he was delyuerd for an
huge rau^son / that is for to say / an / C / M / pou^te / and for which
^aunsonne to be paid / each other chaly^ of england was molte and made in to
money / and all the monks of the order of cysteaux yeuen al her books through
england to done hem to selle / and the ^aunsonne for to pay.

How king rychard come again from the holy land / and auengyd him of his
enemies / Cao. / C. xlvjo. /

Hyles this king rychard was in prison. the kyug of frau^ w ce werryd upon him
strongely in Normandye / and Johan his brother werryd upon him in England / but
the Bisshopes and barons of england withstode him with all the power that they
might get / and geten the Castle of wyndesore / and al other castles And the
foresaid Johan saw that he had no might ne power a geynst the barons of England
for to fight. but anon went him over see unto the king of France / And when
king rychard co me out of prison / and was delyuerd / and come in to england /
anon after Candelmasse in great have he went unto notyngham / and the castle
of notyngham to him was yolden / and tho discomfyted (...) Johan his brother /
and that with him held / And after he went unto the cite of wynchestre. and
there he let him croune king of en glonde / and after he went in to normandye
for to werre upon the king of France / and the king of france come with vj /
C / knygh tes toward gysors / and the king rychard met him / and tho wol de
have give him bataylle / but the king of france fled / and an honderd
knights of his were take / and ij C stedes were trap ped with yren. And anon
after went king richard for to besyege the castle of gayssard / And as he rode
upon a day by the Castle to take auysement of the castle / an Arbalaster smote
him with a quarrel that was enuenimed / and the king drofe out the shaft of the
quarrel / but the quarellys heed abode still in his heed / and it by began for
to rancle that he might not help him self / ne meue his arms / and tho he
wist that he had deths wound / that he might not be hole for no manner thing /
he commanded anon sharply al his men for to assail the castle / So that the
castle was taken or that he dyed / and so manlyche his men dyden that all the
people that were in the castle were al taken / and the king did with hem what
he would. and commanded his men that they should bring before him the man /
that him so wounded and hurt / And when be co me before the king / the king
axed what was his name / and be said my name is bartram guerdon / wherefore said
the king have thou me slain / sith that I did the nener none harm / Sir said
he though ye did me never none harm / ye your self with your ho^d slew my
fader and my brother / and therefore I have quytte now your trauayll / Tho said
king rychard he that dyed upon the cross to bring man's soul from pain of
hell foryeue the my death / and I also foryeue it the / Tho commanded the king
that no man should him mysdoo / But for all the kings defendyng some of his men
him followed / and pryuely him slough / and the syxth day after the king did
shryuen him and sore repentance having of his misdeeds / and was houseled and
ennoynted / and this king ne reigned but / ^x year. and xxxix wekes and deid and
lies besides his fadre at fou^teuerard

Of king Johan that in the first year of his regne lost al nor mandy / Ca / C /
xlvj
When king rychard was deed for encheson that he had none heir, nether son
ne daughter / his brother John was made king and crouned at westmynstre of
Huberd that was tho Archebisshop of Caunterbury And when he bygan to regne be
bycome so merueyllous man / and went over in to normandy and werryd upon the
king of france and so long they werryd to geder til at^ last king John lost
normandye and angeo wherefore he was sore annoyed it was no meruaylle Tho let he
assemble before him at london archebisshops bisshops abbotes and priours earls
and barons and held there a great parliament / and axed there of the clergy the x
of euerych chirch of england for to co^quere and get ayene normandy and angeo
that he had lost / and they would not grant the king wherefore he was wonder
wroth / And in the same time dyed Bishop hubert and the pryour of the coune^t
of canterbury chosen against the kings will to be archebisshop master
stephen of langewn / a good clerk that woned at the court of Rome / and sent
to the pope her election and the pope co^fermed it / and sacred him at vyterbe,
when the king wist this tydyng / he was wonder wroth / and drofe the pryour
and the convent fro Cannterbury / and exyled hem out of En glond / and coma^ded
that no manner letter that come from Rome / ne no mau^dement should be /
vnderfonge ne pleted in England. when this tydyng come to the pope / he sent
unto king John by his let ter / and prayed him with good will / and with good
heart, that he would vnderfonge steven the archebisshop of canterbury unto his
church and suffer the pryour and his monks to come again unto her own
duellyng / but the king would not grant it for no thing /

How king Johan would no thing done for the popes command meant / wherefore al
england was enterdyted and suspe^ded / cao. C / xlvij
ANd at last the pope sent^ by his auctoryte / and enjoined to the bisshops
of england / that if the king would not under fong the pryour of Caunterbury /
and his monks that they should dene general enterdytyng through out al England
/ and granted full power to four bisshops to pronounce the interdyting / (...)
we re need / che first was bishop william of london / and that other bis shop
^stace of ely. and the third was bishop walter of wynchestre and the fourth
was bishop gyles of Herford / and these four bisshopes prayed the king knelyng
on her knees and sore weping / that he wol de done the popes commandment /
and showed him the bulls of the enterdytyng. but for no prayer that they might
pray he would not consent thereto / And when the bisshops saw this they went
from the king / And in the morn after the annunciacion of our lady they
pronounced the general enterdytyng through out al england so that the chirch
doors were shytte with keys / and with other fast nynge and with walls, And
when the enterdytyng was pronounced than the king bygan for to wex all out of
mesure / and took in to his hond all the possessions of the four bisshopes / and
of all the clergy through out all the land. and ordained men for to keep it
that the clerkys might not have her living / wherefore the bisshops cursed all
hem that put or should meddle with holy chirch gods ayenste the will of hem that
hem owed, and when the king would not cefe of his malice for no manner thing the
four bisshops before said went over the sea. and went to the bishop of
Canterbury and told him all the thing And the Archebisshop to hem said that
they should gone again to Caunterbury / and he would come thydder to hem / or
else he would send thider certain persons (...) his stead that should done as
much as him self were there / And when the bisshops herd this they turned
again in to England / and comen unto caunterbury / The tydyng come to the
king that the bisshops were comen again to Caunterbury / and him self might
not come thither that time he sent thither bisshops / Earls and abbots for to
trete with hem / that the king should vnderfonge the archebisshop stephen / and
the pryour and all the monks of Caun terbury / and that he should never after
that time no thing take of holy chirch against the will of hem that owed the
goods / and that the king should make full amends to hem. of whom he had any
goods taken / and that holy church should have al fraunchyses as ferforth. as
they had in saint edwards time the Confessor /

How Stephen of langeton come in to england through the popes commandment /
and he went again / Cao. / C / xlviijo /
When the form of accord thus was ordained / hit was in a payr of Endentures
/ and they put her seals unto that one (...) and they that comen in the kings
name putt her seals to the other part of endentures. and the four bisshops
above said to see that one part of the endentures to hem / and that other part
of the en dentures they bare with hem to show the king when the king saw the
form and understood / he held him full well paid of all manner thing as they
had ordained saving as touching the resty tucion of the goods for to make
ageyn, to that thing. he nold not acord / and so he sent word ayene to the four
bisshops / that they should done out / and put awey that one point of
restitucion / and they ansuerd that they nold not done one word out / Tho sent
the king to the archebisshop by tho four bisshops / that he should come to cau^
terbury for to speak with him there, and sent unto him saufeenduit under
pledges. that is to sey his Justices / gilbert peytewyn / william de la brener
/ and John le fitz hugh that in her co^duyt saufly be should come. and gone
again / at his will / and in this manner the arche bishop stephen come to
canterbury / and when the archebisshop was come the king come to chilham for
he would come no ner to caun terbury / at that time / but he sent by his
tresorer bishop of wynchestre / that he should done out of the end^tures the
clause of resci tucio^ for to make of the goods / and the archebisshop made
his oath that he would never out done one word thereof / ne change of that the
bisshops had spoken and ordained / and tho the archebisshop went again to
Rome without any more doing / king Johan was tho wrother than ever he was
before / and let make a comune cry through out at england / that al tho that
had holy church rentes / and went over the sea / that they should come again
in to En glond at a certain day / or else they should lose her rentes for ever
more / and that he commanded to every shereue through out al England / that
they should enquere if any bishop / Abbot, (...) your or any prelate of holy
church fro that day afterward resceyned any mau^dement that come fro the pope
that they should take the body and bring it before him / and that they should
take in to the kings hand al her lands of holy church / that were yeuen to
any man / by the archebisshop stephen / or by the pryour of Canterbury from
the time of election of the archebisshop / and commanded that all the wodes
that were the archebisshops should be cast a down. unto the ground and al
sold /

How king Johan destroyed the order of Cisteaux / cao. C xliy
ANd in the same time the Irysshmen bygonne to werre upon king Johan / and king
Johan ordained him for to wend in to Irlond / and let arere an huge tax
through out al England that is to say / xxxv / M / marc. and sent through al
England to the monks of the order of Cysteaux. that they should help him of
six / M / marc of silver / and they ansuerd and said that they durst nothing
done without her chyef abbot of asteaux. wherefore king Johan when he come
again from Irland / he did hem so much sorrow and care / that they nyst where
to abide / for he took so much rau^sonne of every house of hem that the sum
amounted to ix / M, and CCC / mark / so that they were clean lost and destroyed
and boy ded her how / and her lands through out al england. and the abbot of
wa uersey drad so much his manace / that he forsook all the abbey / and went
thens / and pryuely ordained him over see to the house of Ciste aux / when the
tydyng come to the pope / that the king had done so much malice / tho was he to
the kyngward full wroth / and sent ij le gats unto the king, that one was callid
pandolf / and that other du ra^t that they should warn the king in the popes
name that he shol de cese of his persecucion that he did unto the holy chirch /
and amend the wrong and the trespaas that he had done to the archebisshop of
ca^ terbury and to the priour and unto the monks of canterbury and to all the
clergy of england / and that he should restore the gods again that he had
taken of hem against her will / and else they should curse the king by name /
and to do this thing and to conferme the pope to ke hem his lettres in bulls
patrnts / These two legates come in to England. and comen to the king to
northampton / there that he hell de his parliament / and full curtoysly they him
salued, and sayden Sir we ben come fro the pope of Rome / the pees of holy
chirch / and of the land to amend / And we amonest you first in the popes half
/ that ye make full restitucion of the goods / that ye have rauy shed of holy
church and of the land / and that ye vnderfonge stephen Archebisshop of
caunterbury in to his dygnyte / and the pryour of Caunterbury. and his monks /
and that ye yield again unto the Archebisshop al his lands. and rentes
without any witholdyng / And Sir ye more over / that ye such restitucion hem
make as holy church shall hold her paid / Tho ansuerd the king / as
touching the Pryour and his monks of caunterbury, all that ye have said I will
gladly done / and al thing that ye will ordeyne But as touching the
archebisshop / I shall tell you in mine heart as it lies that the Archebisshop
let his Bisshopryche / and that the pope than for him would pray / and than
upon adventure me should like sum other bisshopryche for to give him in england
And upon this condition I would him resceyue / and vnderfonge And netheles in
england as archebisshop yif he abide / he shall never have so good saufconduyt
/ but he shall be take /

Tho said pandolf unto the king / Holy church was woned never to dyscharge an
Archebisshop. without cause reasonable / but ever she has be woned to chastyse
princes / that to god / and holy church were inobedyent / What how now quod
the king / Manace ye me / Nay said pa^dolf / but ye now openly have told as it
stands in your heart / And to you we shall tell. what is the popes will /
and thus it stant / that he has you holy enterdyted and acursed for the
wrongs that ye have do to holy church / and to the Clergy / And for as
much as ye duelle / and be in will to abide in malice / and will not come
to none ammendement / ye shall understand that fro this time afterward the
sentence is upon you yeuen / and holds stead / and strength / and upon al
tho that with you have communed before this time / whether they ben Earls /
Bawns / or Knights / or any other / what so ever they be / We hem assoylle
saufly unto this day /

And fro this time afterward of what Condition ever that they be / we hem
acurse that with you comen / and so do we sentence upon hem openly and
specially / And we assoylle quytely Earls / barons knyghts / and al other manner
men of her homages seruyces and feau tes that they should unto you done / and
this thing to conferme. we give pleyne power to the bishop of wynchestre / to
the bishop of northewiche / And the same power we give in scotland to the
bisshopes of rouchestre and of salysbury / And in walys we give the same power
to the bisshopes of saint dauyd and of landaf / and of saint ass / And more
over we send through al crystendome that all the bisshops beyond the sea that
they done acurse al tho that hell pen you / or any counseyll yeuen you in any
manner need / that ye have to done in any party of the world. And we assoylle
hem al so al by the auctoryte of the pope / and commau^de hem also with you for
to werre as with him / that is enemy to all holy church / Tho ansuerd the king
/ what mow ye done me more / Tho ansuerd pan dolf we seyne to you in verlo dei
/ that ye / ne none heyr that ye ha ue never after this day may be crouned /
Tho said the king by him that is almighty god / and I had wist of this thing er
that ye come in to my land / that ye had me brought such tydyng / I should have
made you ride al an hole year. Tho ansuerd pa^dolf. full well wend we at our
first coming / that ye would have been obedyent to god and to holy chirch / and
have fulfilled the popes commandment and now we have showed to you / and
pronounced the popes will. as we were charged therewith / And as now ye have
said / that if ye had wist the cause of our coming / that ye would have made us
ry de al an hole year / and as well ye might have said. that ye would ha ue take
an hole year of respyte by the popes leave / but for to suffer what death ye
could ordeyne / we shall not spare for to tell you holych all the popes message
/ and his will / that we were charged with /

How pandolf delyuerd a clerk / that had falsed / and cou^terfeted the kings
money before the king him self / Ca. C / L /
ANd anon tho commanded the king the sherenes and bailyfs of northampton that
were in the kings presence / that they should bring forth all the prisoners
that they might be done un to the death before pandolf / for encheson the king
wend that they would have gayn said her deeds. for cause of death al thing that
he had spoken before. when the prisoners were come before the king he comau^ded
some to be honged / and sum to ben draw / and sum to draw her eyes out of
her heed / and among al other there was a clerk had falshed the kings money /
and the king commanded that he should be honged and draw / And when pandolf
herd this commandment of the king / he sterte him up smertely / and anon axed
a book / and a candel. and would have cursed al hem that set upon the clerk any
hand / and pandolf him self went for to seche a cross / and the king followed
him / and delyuerd him the clerk by the hand that he should do with him / what
that ever he would / and thus was the clerk deliuerd. and went thens / and
pandolf and durant his felawe went fro the king Johan / and come again to the
pope of rome and told him that king Johan would not amended ben / but ever abide
so acursed / and netheles the pope granted that year through out england that
men might sing masses in couenable chirches and make gods body / and give it
to syke men / that pass should out of this world / And also that men might
christian children ouerall And when the pope wist and saw that the king would not
ben under the rule of holy church for no manner thing / the pope tho sent to
the king of france in remissyon of his sins / that he should take with him
all the power that he might / and wend in to England for to destroy king
Johan / when this tydyng come to king Johan / tho was he sore annoyed / and
sore drad lest that he should lose his reame / and him self be done to death /
Tho sent he to the pope messagyers / and said that he would ben Ius tyfyed /
and come to amendment in all things / and would make satisfaction to al manner
men after the popes ordinance / Tho sent the pope again in to england pandolf
and other messagyers comen to Caunterbury there the king abode / and the xiij
days of may / the king made an oath for to stand to the popes ordinance before
pandolf the legate in all manner things / in which he was acursed / and that he
should make full restitucion to al men of holy church / and of relygyon / and of
the goods that he had take of hem against her will / and all the great lords
of england swore upon the book / and by the holy dome. that if the king would
not hold his oath / they said that they would make him hold it by strength /

Tho put the king him to the court of Rome / and to the pope and tho yaf up the
reame of England and of Irlond / for him and for his heirs for evermore that
should come after him / So that king Johan and his heirs should take tho two
reames of the popes hand. and should hold tho two wyaines of the pope as to
ferme payeng every year unto the court of Rome a thousand mark of silver. and
tho took the king the croune of his heed. and set him on his knees / and
these words he said in heryng of all the great lords of england / here I
resygne up the croune / and the reame of England in to the popes band Innocent
the thyrdde / and put me ho lych in his mercy and in his ordynannce / Tho
vnderfenge pandolf the croune of king Johan / and kept it v days as for seysen
taking of two reames of england and of Irlond / and confermed all manner things
by his chartre that follows after

Of the letter oblygatorye that king Johan made unto the court of Rome /
wherefore the petres pens ben gadred through out al En glond / Cao. C / ljo. /
TO all christian people through out the world duellyng / Johan by the grace of
god king of england gretyng to your vnyuersyce / and know thing it be. that
for as much as we have grieved and offended god / and our mother church of
Rome / and for as much as we have need to the mercy of our lord Ihu criste /
and we may no thing so worthy offer / as competent satisfaction to make / to
god and to holy church / but if it were our own body / as with our reames of
England and of Irlond, Than by the grace of god we des^re for to meke us for
the love of him that meketh him to the death of the cross / through cou^ceyll of
the noble earls and barons we offren and freely graunten to god / and to the
appostles saint peter and saint paul. and to or mother church of Rome / and to
our holy father the pope Innocent the third. and to all the popes that come
after him all the reame and patronages of chirches of England / and of Irlond
with her apperteuau^ces for rmission of our sins / and help, and l^lthe of
our kyn souls and of al christian souls. so that fro this ty me afterward we
will resceyue and hold of our mother church of Rome as see ferme doing
feaute to our holy fadre the pope Inno cent the third / and to all the popes
that come after him in the manner above said / and in the presence of the wise
man pandolf the popes sub del^ene we maken lyege homage as it were in the popes
presence / and before him were, and we shall done al manner things above said
and thereto we bynden us / and all that come after us / and our heirs for
evermore without any gayn saying to the Pope / and eke the ward of church
wcants / And in token of this thing ever for to last we will conferme and
ordeyne that our special ren tes of the foresaid Royamme / saving Saint Peter's
pens in all thing to the mother chirch of rome paie^g by year a / M / marc of
silver at two terms of the year for all manner custommes that we should done for
the foresaid royames that is to say at myche l inas. and at estren / that is to
say / vij / C / marc for england / and CCC marc for Irland / saving to us and
to our heirs our Iusty ces and our other frau^chises / and other realces that
apperteynen to the croune, And all these things that before ben said we will
that it be ferme and stable without end / and to that oblygacion we and our
successors and our heirs in this manner ben bound / that if we or any of our
heirs through any presumpcion fall in any point a yenst any of these things
above said / and he be warned / and he will not right amend him / he shall than
lose the forsaid reame for ever more / ^and that this chartre of oblygacion /
and our warrau^t for evermore be ferme and stable without gain saying we shall
fro this day afterward be true to god / and to the mother church of rome and
to the pope Innocent the thyrdde / and to all that comes after him / and the
reames of England and of Irlond we shall mayntene trewely in all manner points
against al manner men by our power through gods help,

How the clerks that were outlawed out of England come again / and how king
Johan was assoylled / Ca / C, lijo.
When this chartre was made and ensealed / the king under fenge again his
crone of pandolfes hand, and sent anon unto the archebisshop steven and to al
his other clerkys / and lrwd, men / that he had exyled out of his land / that
they should come again in to england. and have again al her lands, and her
rentrs and that he would make restitucion of the goods that he had taken of her
against her will / The king him self tho and pandulfe and earls and barons
went tho unto wynchestre against the arcwbis shop stephen. and when he was come
the king went against him / and fell a down to his feet / and said to him fair
sire / ye be welcome and I cry you mercy for encheson that I have trespaced
against you / The archebisshop took him up tho in his arms / and kyssed him
curoysly oftymes / and after lad him to the door of Saint Swythynes church by
the hand / and assoylled him of the sentence. and him reconciled to god / and
to holy church, and that was on saint margarets day / and the Archebisshop
anon went for to sing mass. and the leyng offered at the mass a marc of gold
/ And when the mass was done al they went to vnderfonge all her lands
without any manner gayn saying / And that day they made all mirth and joy
enough / but yet was not the enterdytyng rele ced / for encheson the pope had
set that the enterdyting should not be undone til the king had made full
restitucio^ of the goods that he had take of holy chirch / and also that him
self should done homage to the pope by a certain legate that he should send in
to england Tho took pandolfe his leave of the king and of the archebisshop and
went again unto Rome / And the archebisshop anon lets come before him
prelates of holy church at redyng for to trete and cou^seill how much and
what they should axe of the king for to make restitucion of the goods that he
had take of hem / and they ordained and said that the king should give to the
archebisshop three, M / mark for the wrong that the king had done unto him / and
also to other clerks by porcyons xv / M / marc / and in the same time Nycholas
bishop of Tuscan cardynall / penytauncer of Rome come in to en glond through
the popes commandment the v kalend of october and come to london the fifth
nonas of october for encheson that king Johan and all the kings that come
after him should evermore hold the reames of england / and of Irlond of god and
of the pope payeng to the pope by year / as is above said /

How the enterdytyng was undone in england / and of the debate that was between
king Johan / and the barons of the reame. Capitulo. C / quinquagesimo tercio /
When king Johan had done his homage to the legate that showed him the popes
letter / that he should pay to Iulyane and yield again that was king
Rychardes wife the third part of the land of england and of Irlond that he had
witholde sith that king rychard deyde / when king Johan herd this he was wonder
wroth. for vtterlych the enterdytyng might not ben undone till that he had made
gree and restitucion to the foresaid Iulyane of that she axed / The legate went
tho again to the pope after cristemasse / and the king sent tho messagyers
over see to Iulyane that was king Rychardes wife for to have a relese of that
she axed of him. and so it befell that Iulyane deyde anon after ester And in
so much the king was quyte of thing that she axed / But tho at the feste of
saint Johan that come next after through the popes commandment the enterdytyng
was first relesed thurugh al england / the vij day of Inyll / and vij year was
the land en terdyted / and in the morrow men ronge and said masses through out
london / and so after through out al england / And the next year after there
bygan a great debate between king Johan and the lords of england for encheson
that he would not grant the laws and hold the which saint edward had
ordained and had been vsyd / and hold un to that time that he had hem broken /
for he would no law hold / but did all thing that him lyked / and dysheryted
many men with out consent of lords and perys of the land / and he would
disherite the good earl Randulf earl of chestre for encheson that he undertook
him of his wykkednes. and by cause he did so much shame and vylo ny to god and
to holy church / and also for he held / and haunted his own broders wife /
and lay also by many other women great lords daughters / for he spared no
woman that him lyked for to have wherefore all the lords of the land were with
him wonder wroth and went to london and took the cite / And for to cese this
debate and sorrow the king and the archebisshop / and other great lords of
the land of england assembled hem before the fest of saint John baptist in a
medewe besides the town of stanes that is called Romne mede / And the king made
hem there a charire of fraunchyses such as they would axen / and in such manner
they were acorded / and that a cordement last not full long / for the king him
self sone after did ayenste the points of the same charter that he had made.
wherefore the most party of the land of lords assembled hem and bygonne to
werre upon king Johan / and burnt his tounes and robled his fol ke. and did
all the sorrow that they might, and made hem as strong as they might with all her
power / and thought to drive him once of england, and make lowys the kings
sone of france king of england / And king Johan sent tho over see and
ordained so much people of normans and of pycardes and of Flemynges so that the
land might not hem sustain but with much sorrow / and among al these people
there was a man of normandy / that was called Fonkes of brent / and this normand
and his company spared another church ne house of relygyon. that they ne burnt
and robled it / and bare a wey all that they might take / so that the land was
all destroyed what in one side, and in that other / The barons and lords of
england ordained among hem the best spekers and wysest men / and sent l^m
over see to king philip of france / and prayed him that he would sen de lo wys
his sone in to england to ben king of england and to under fonge the croune /

How lowys the kyngys sone of france come in to england with a strong power
of people to be king of england, Cao / C / Liiij /
When king philip of France herd this tydyng / he made c^e reyne alyaunce
between hem by her commune election that lowys king philippes sone of france
should goo with hem in to england / and dryne out king Johan of the land / and
all that were in presence of lowys made unto him homage / and bycome his men /
And the barons of England held hem still at london / and a by den lowys the
kings sone of france / and this was the next sacer day before the ascencion
of our lord that lowys come in to england with a strong power / and that time
king Johan had taken all the castles of england in to Alyens hondes / And lowys
come tho and be sieged at rouchestre the castle / and took it with strength /
and the thurs day in whitsonweke let honge all the alyens that were therein /
and the thursday tho next sueng he come to london / and there he was un der
fonge with much honor of the lords that a byden him there and all to him made
homage / And afterward in the tewysday next after the trynyte sunday / he took

And in the same time the pope sent in to england a legate that was called
swalo / and of king Iohans death / Cao. / C / lvo. /
ANd in the same time the pope sent in to England a legate that was called
swalo. and he was priest Cardynal of Rome for to mayntene king Iohans cause
against the barons of england / but the baarons had so huge part and help
through lowys the kings sone of france / that king Johan wise not whydder for
to torn / ne to gone / And so it fell that he would have gone to Ny chol, and
as he went thyderward / he come by the abbey of swyneshe de / and there he abode
two days. and as he sat at mete he axed a monk of the house how much a loofe
was worth that was set before him upon the table and the monk said that the
lofe was worth but an halfpeny / O quod the king / here is great cheepe of
bread, Now quoth the king / And I may live such a lofe shall be worth xx
shyllyng / or half a year begoan and when he had said this word / much he
thought / and often he syghed / and took, and ^te of the bread and said / by god
the word that I have spoken shall ben sothe / The monk that stood before the
king was for this word full sorry in heart, and thought / rather he would him self
suffer pytous death / and thought if he might ordeyne therefore sum manner
remedy / and anon the monk went to his abbot / and was shryuen of him / and
told the abbot all that the king said / and preyd his abbot for to assoylle him
/ for he would give the king such a wassayle that al england should be glad
thereof and ioyefull, Tho went the monk in to a gardeyn / and fond a great tode
therein / and took her up / and put her in a cup and prykked the tode through
with a broche many times. tille that the benym come out in every side in to
the cup / and tho took he the cup / and filled it with good ale / and
brought it before the king and knelyng said / sir quoth he wassayle / for never
days of your life ne drunk ye of such a cup / begin monk quoth the king /
and the monk dra^k a great draught / and took the king the cup / and the king
also drank a great draught / and set down the cup / The monk anon right
went in to the fermorye, and there dyed anon / on whose sou le god have mercy /
amen, and v monks sing for his soul specyal ly and shullen whiles the abbey
stant / The king aroos up anon full euel at ese / and commanded to remeue the
table / and axyd after the mo^ ke / and men told him that he was deed / for his
womb was broke in sunder / when the king herd this he commanded to trusse /
but al it was for naught, for his belly bygan so to swelle for the drynk that he
drank that he dyed within two days. the morrow after saint lukes day / and this
king Johan had fair children of his body bygoten. that is to say / henry his
sone / that was king after his fadre / and rychard that was earl of Cornewayle,
and Iabel that was Emperesse of Rome, and elyenore. that was queen of scotland
/ and this king Johan when he had reigned xvij year / v / months / and v,
days / he deide in the castle of new work / and his body was bu ryed at
wynchestre /

Profecye of merlyn of the king henry the first expouned that was king Iohans
sone / Ca / C / lx /
ANd of this henry profecyed merlyn / and said that a lombe should come out of
wynchestre in the year of Incarnacion of our lord. M CC / and xvj with true
lyppes and holiness written in his heart / and he said soth for the good henry
the king was bore in wynchestre in the year above said, and he spaak good
words / and sweet and was an holy man and of good conscience / And merlyn
said that this henry should make the fairest place of all the world that in his
time should not full be ended / and he said soth / For he made the new work of
the Abbeye of saint Peter's Church at westmynster / that is fayrer of sight
than any other church / that men know through al Crystendom / but king henry
dyed er that work were fully made / and that was great harm, And yet said
Merlyn that this lamb should have pees the most time of his regne / and he
said full sothe. for he was never annoyed through werre ne dyseased in no manner
wise til a little before his death / And yet said merlyn in his prophecye more /
and in the regne, and end of the foresaid lamb a wolf of a strange land /
should done him great harm through his werre / and that he should at last ben
maystir through help of a reed fox / that should come out of the north west /
and should him overcome / and that he should drive him unto the water / and that
profecye full well was know / for within a little time or the king dyed Symond
of mountford earl of Leycestre that was borne in france bigan against him
strong werre through which doing many a good bachiler was shent / and deed /
and disheryted / And when king henry had the vyctorye at Euesham / and Symond
therle was slain through help and might of Gillebert of Clare earl of
gloucestre / that was in keeping and ward of the foresaid Symond through
ordinance of king henry that went a^^ne to the king with much power / wherefore
the foresaid Simond was shent / and that was great harm to the communes of
England that so good a man was shent for troth / and dyed in charity, and for
the comune profit of the same folk / and therefore Almighty god for him has
Sythenes showed many a fair miracle to diverse men and women of the sykenesse
and dysesse / that they have had for the love of him

And merlyn also told and said in his Profecye that after that time the lamb
should leave no while / and than his seed should ben in strange land without
pasture^ / And he said sothe. For king henry lived no while after when Symond
mountford was deed that king henry ne deyde auon after him / And in the mean
time Sir edward his sone that was the best knight of the world of honor was
tho in the holy land / and get there Acre^ / and in that country he bygate on
dame clyenore his wife Jane of (...) cres his dought^r / that afterward was
countess of gloucestre / and he made in the holy land such a vyage that all the world spoke of his knyghthode / and every man drad him / high and low /
through out al crystendome / as the storye of him tells / as after ward ye
shul here more openly / and from the time that king henry deyde til that sir
edward was crouned king all the great lords of england were as faderles
children without any socour that him might ma yntene / and govern and defend*
against her dedly enemies /

Of king edward that was king henryes sone* ca / C* lxj /

How lewelyn through eggynge of david his brother werryd again upon king edward
/ Ca / C lxiij /
HIt was not long after that time that king Edward ne yaf to diuid lewelyns
brother the lorship of frodesham / and made him a knight / and so much honor

a good knight / that is to say Sir Rogyer of Clyfford / Sir william of lyndesey
that was sir Iohans fytz robert and sir rychard tanny / and an huge nombre of
other and all was through her own folly / for if they had had good espyes they
had not ben harmed. When king edward herd tell that his people was so drenchyd
/ he made sorrow ynow / but tho come Sir John of vessye from the king of aragon
/ and brought with him much folk of bachilers and of gascoyns / and were
soudyours / and duel lyng with the foresaid sir Johan of vessye / and vnderfonge
of him wages and with him were witholde / and noble men it were for to fit and
burnt many towns and slew much people of walsshmen all that they might take /
and al tho with strength and might made assaut to the castle of swandone / and
get the castle* and when david the pryn^s brother herd this tydyng / he
ordained him to flight / and lewelyn the prince saw that his brother was flowen
/ and sore was abashed / for he had no power to his werre for to mayntene /
And so Lewelyn began for to flee and wend well for to have escaped* but on a morrow
Sir Rogyer Mortimer met with him only with (...) knights / and set him round
about / and to him went and (...) of his head and presented him unto the king
Edward / And in this ma ner the prince of walys was taken and his heed smyten
of. and al his heirs disheryted for evermore through rightful dome of all the
lands of the ^ame*

How David that was lewelyns brother prince of wa^s was put to death / Cao. / C.
l^iiijo. /
Auyd that was the princes brother of walys through pride d wen^e for to have been

But many great lords of Scotland sayden Nay^* Wh^fore gre (...) debate aroose

How Sir Johan bayllol king of scotland withsayd his homage / and of sir

ANd when sir John bayllol king of scotland understood that king edward was

Of the Conquest of Berewyk / Ca / C lyviij^
When tho two Cardynals were went again in to France for to treat of the
pres at (...) / the king sen^ thydder of his earls and barons. that is to say
Sir edmond his brother upon gods body / That is to say Sir Johan of Common /
and the Earl of the strathorne the earl of Carryk and also four bisshops
undertook for all the clergy, and so the king delyuerd hem / and yafe hem
sauf conduyt to wend in to her own land. And it was not long afterward / that
they ne arysen against king Edward / for encheson that they wist well that king
Edwardys folk was take in gascoyn / as before is said / but sir Johan bayllol
king of scotland wist well that his la^d should have sorrow and shame for her
falsenesse / and in have went him over the sea to his own lands / and there
held him and come never more ayene / wherefore the scotts chose^ to her king
william waleys / a ribaud, and an harlot come^ up of not and much harm did to
the englisshmen / and king edward thought how he might have delyuerau^ce of his
people that were taken in gascoyne / and in have went over the sea in to
Flau^dres for to werre up on the styng of france / and the earl of Flaundres
vnderfenge him with much honor / and granted him al his lands at his own
will And when the king of france herd tell that the king of England was
arrived in flau^dres and come with an huge power him for to destroy / he preyd
him of true for two year / so that englissh marchau^ts and also frenssh might
sanfly gone and come in both sides The king edward granted it / so that he
must have his men ou^ of prison that were in gascoyne / and the king of france
granted ^non and so they were delyuerd / And in the same time the Scotts sent
by the bishop of saint andrews in to france to the king / and to Sir Charlys
his brother that Sir charles should come with his power / and they of scotland
would come with her power / and so they should gone in to england that land for
to destroy from scotland till that they come to kent / and the scot^es trust
much upon the fre^ssh men, but of that thing they had no manner grant / And
nethelos the scottee bigo^ne to rob and slay in no^thu^berla^d / and did
much harm.

How william walleys let slay her hugh of Cressyngham / and of the battle of
Fonkyrke. Ca. / C, lxx^
When this tidyng was come to king Edward that william walleys had ordained
such a strong power / and that all Scot land to him was attendaunt. and ready
to slay Englysshmen and ^e destroy the land he was sore annoyed and sent anon
by lettres to the earl of garren / and (...) Sir henry Percy / and to Sir
William latomer / and to sir hugh of cressyngha^ his tresorer that they should
take po^er / and wend in to northumberlond / and so forth in to Scotland for
to kept the countries / And when william waleis herd of her coming / he began
for to flee / and the Englysshmen him followed / and drofe him till he come to
Stryuelyn / and there he held him in the castle / and the walsshmen every day
hem escryed and manaced / and did all the despyte that they might / So that the
englissh men upon a time in a morning went out from the Castle the mountance
of x mile / and passed over a bridge / And william wa ^eys come with a strong
power and drofe hem a bak / for the Englysshmen had ageynste him tho no might /
but fled. and they that might take the bridge escaped / but sir hugh the kings
tresorer there was slain and many other also / wherefore was much so^the / Tho
had king edward sped al his needs in flau^dres / and was again come in to
england / and in haste took his wey toward Scot land, and come thither at
ascension tide. and all that he found / he set a fire, and burnt / But the
pour people of Scotland come to him wonder thykke / and prayed him for gods
love that he would have on them mercy and pity / where for the king tho
commanded / that no man should done harm to hem that were yolden to him / ne
to no man of order / ne to no hows of relygyon / ne no manner church But let
aspye all that he might, where that he might find any of his enemies / Tho come
a spy to the king / and told him were the Scotts were assembled for to give
bataylle / and on saint mary magdalene day the king come to fonkirk / and yafe
bataylle to the Scotts / And at that battle were slain xxxiij thousand / and
of englisshmen, but xxviij / and no mo / of the which was a worthy knit slain
that was a knight an hospyteler / that was called Friar Brian Iay / For when
william waleys fled from the bataylle that same Friar Brian him pursued
ferslyche / and as his horse ran it stert in to a mire of mareys up to the belly,
And william waleys turned tho again, and there slew the foresaid Brian / and
that was much harm, And that while king Edward went through Scotland for to
enquere if he might find any of his enemies, And in that land he duellyd as
long as him lyked / and there was none enemy that durst him abide, and sone
afterward king edward went to sonthampton, for he would not abide in scot land
in winter season for esement of his people / And when be come to london, he let
amend many misdeeds that were done against his pees and his law while that he
was in Flaundres

Of the last marriage of king edward / and how he went the third time in

ANd afterward it was ordained through the court of Rome that king edward
should wedde d^me margarete king philyps suster of france / and the arche

made pe^s between king edward of England / and king philip of France King

/ sauf tho that were in the castle of estreuelyn that wa^ well vitaylled and
astored for vij year

How the castle of Estreuelyne was besyeged / Ca / C. lxxij. /
KKyng Edward come with an huge power to the Castle of Estreuelyn, and besyeged
the castle / but it little auayled / for he might do the scotts none harm.
For the castle was so strong and well y kept / And King edward saw that / and
thought him upon a queyntyse. and let make there anon ij peyre of high
galowes before the tour of the castle. and made his oath that as many as were in
the castle / were he earl or baron, and he were take with stre^gthe, but if he
would the rather him yield / he should ben hanged up on the galowes / and when
tho that were in the castle herd this they come and yield hem al to the kings
grace and mercy / and the king foryafe him al his maletalent / And there were
all the gre to lords of Scotland / swore to king Edward that they should co me
to london to every parliament / and should stand to his ordenau^ce /

How Troyle bastone was first ordained / Ca / C / lxxiij /
THe king edward went thens to london / and went have had rest and pees of his
werre / with which werre he was occupied xx year / that is to say in walys /
in Gascoyn / and in Scot land / And thought how he might recover his tresour /
that he had spended about his werre / and let enquere through the reame of mis
takynges and wrongs done through mysdoers in England of all the time that he
had been out of his reame that men called tro illebaston / And ordained thereto
Justices / and in this manner he re couerd tresour without nombre. And his
encheson was for he had thought for to have gone in to holy land for to werre
upon god des enemies / For encheson that he was ^oysed long time before / And
netheles that law that he had ordained did much good through out al England
to hem that were mysbode / For tho that trespaced were we^ chastysed / And
afterward the meker and the lettre / and the pour commons were in pees and in
rest, and the same time king edward enprisoned his own sone Edward for
encheson that walter of langeton bishop of chestre / that was the kings
tresorer had made upon him complaynt / and said that the foresaid Edward through
counceyll and procurement of one pyers of ganastone a squire of gascoyne had
broke the parkes of the foresaid bishop / and the foresaid pyers counceylled and
lad the same Edward / and for this cause king edward exyled the said pyers ou^
of England for evermore /

How Robert the brus chalengyd Scotland / Ca. C. lxxv^
ANd after this Robert the Brus Earl of Ca^yest sense by his letter to the
earls and barone of Scotland that they should come to him to Soon in the morrow
after the conc^pcion of ou^ Lady. for high needs of the land / And the
lords come a^ the day assigned / and at the same day sir Robert the brus said
fa yr lords full well ye know that in my person duelled the right of the
reme of Scotland / and as ye wit well am rightful heyr / Sith that Sir Johan
bayllol that was our king us bath forsake and left his land. And though it so
be that king Edward of england with wrongful power has made me to him assent
against my will / if that ye will grant that I be king of Scotland I shall
keep you against king edward / and against al manner men and with that word the
abbot of Scone aroos / and before hem al said that it was reason for to help
him / and the land to keep and defend / and tho said in presence of hem all
that he would give him a M pound for to mayntene that land / and all the other
granted the land to him and with her power him for to help / and defied king
Edward of en glond / and said that Robert the Brus should be king of Scotland

How Sir Johan of Common gaynesayd the crounyng of Sir Robert the Brus / Ca.o. C
/ lxxvijo /
LOrdynges said Sir Johan of Common thinks upon the troth and the oath that
ye made unto king Edward of En glond and touching my self / I will not break
mine oath for no man / and so he went fro that company at that time / wherefore
To bert the brus and all that to him consented were wonder wroth and tho
mana^ed Sir Johan of Common / Tho ordained they an other counceyle at donfrys /
to the which come the foresaid Sire Johan Common / he duellyd but two mile from
Donfrys / there that he was woned for to soiourne / and abide /

How Sir Johan was traytoursly slain / Ca / C / lxxviij /
When Robert the brus wist that all the great lords of Scot land were come to
do^fris sauf Sir Johan Common / that so iourned tho nygh do^fris / he sent
after him specially that Sire Johan Common should come and speak with him. and
upon that he sent after him Johan Comyns his brother / and prayed him for to come
and speak with him at gray Frerys at donfrys / and that was the thursday
after Candelmasse / and Sir Johan granted him for to wend with him / And when
he herd mass / he took a soppe / and drank / and afterward he bestrode his
palfray / and rode his wey / and so come to donfrys / And Robert the brus saw
him come at a wyn dowe as he was in his chamber / and tho made joy ynow / and
come against him and colled him about the neck / and made with him good
semblaunt / And when all the e^s. and barons of Scotland were present / Robert
the Brus spoke and said Syres quoth he ye wit well the encheson of this coming /
and wherefore it is / if ye will grant that I mote be king of Scotland / as
right heyr of the land / and all the lords that were there said with one voys
that he should be crouned king of Scotland / and that they would him help and
mayntene against al manner men alive / And for him if it were need dye / The
gentil knight tho John of Common ansuerd / and said. Certes never for me / ne
for to have of me as much help as the value of a botonne / For that oath that
I have made to king Edward of England I shall hold while my life last / and
with that word he went fro that company / and would have went upon his palfray
/ And Robert the Brus pursued him with a draw swerd / and bare him through the
body / And Sire John Common fell down to the earth / But when Rogyer that was
Sir John Comyns brother saw the fall senesse and stert to Sir Robert the Brus /
and smote him with a knyfe / but the false traitor was armed under / so that
the stroke might done him none harm / And so much help come about sir Robert
the Brus / So that Rogyer Common was there slain / and al to hew m to small
pyeces /

And Robert the Brus turned again. there that Sir John Common the noble baron
lay wounded and pyned toward his death besides the high auter in the chirch of
the gray frerys / and sa yd unto Sir Johan Common. O traitor thou shall be deed
/ and ne uer after let mine auauncement. and shoke his swerd at the high auter
and smote him on the head / that the brain fell a down upon the ground / and
the blood stert an high upon the walls / And yet unto this day that blood is
seyn there that no water may wasshe it awey / and so dyed that noble knight in
holy church /

ANd when the Traitor Robert the brus saw that no man tho would let his
coronacion / he commanded al hem that were of power should come to his
crounyng^ / to saint Johannes tonne in scotland / and so it byfell that on our
lady of An^ciacion / the Bishop of glastone / and the Bishop of saint Andrewe
crouned for her king Robert the Brus in saint Johannes Town and made him king
/ And anon after he drofe out ass the Englysshmen out of Scotland / and they
fled and come / and playned unto king Edward / How Robert the brus had drive he
m out of the land / and disheryted hem /

How king edward dubbed at westmestre xxiiij score knights. Cao. / C. lxxx
ANd when king edward herd of this meschyef he swore that he would thereof ben
auengyd / and said that all the Traitors of Scotland should ben honged and
draw / and that they should never be raunsoned / And king edward thought upon
this falsenesse that the scotts had done / and sent after all the bachyllerye
of england that they should come to london at witsontyde / and he dubbed at
westmestre xxiiij score knytes / Tho ordained him the noble king edward for to
wend in to scotland to werre upon Robert the brus / and sent before him in to
scotland sir aymer the valau^ce earl of penbroke / and sir henry percy baron /
with a fair company that pursued the scotts / and burnt tounes and castles
/ and afterward come the king him self with earls and barons a fair company /

How Robert the brus was scomfyted in bataylle / and how Symond Frysel was
slain / Ca / C lxxxj /
THe friday next before the assumpcion of our lady king edward met Robert the
brus besides saint Iohans Town in scotland and with his company / of which
company king Edward slew vij M / When Robert the brus saw this meschyef he
began to flee and hyd him that no man might him find / but sir simond frisel
pursued him sore / so that he turned ayene and abode battle. For he was a
worthy knight and a bold of body / and the englysshmen pursued ever sore in
every side. and slew the stead that sir Symond Frysel rode upon / and they
took him / and lad him unto the hooste / And sir Symond bygan for to flater /
and speak fair / and said / Lords I shall give you iiij M marc of silver /
and mine horse mine harnoys and al mine armure / and bycome a beggar / Tho ansuerd
Theobaude of Peuenes / that was the kings Archyer, Now god me so help it is
for naught that thou spekest, for all the gold in england I would the not let
gone / without commandment of king edward / And tho was he lad to king
Edward / and the king would not see him / but commanded to lead him away to
have his dome at london, and on our ladies even natiuyte he was honged and
drawn / and his heed smyten of / and honged (...) with cheynes of yren upon
the galowes. And his head was set upon london bridge upon a spear, and
against cristemasse the body was brent, for enche son that the men that kept
the body by night they saw so many deuyls raumpand with great Iren erokes
rennyng upon the galowes / and horrybelyche tormented the body and many that
hem saw / anon after they dyed for dread / and sum woxen mad or sore
sykenesse they had. And in that batail was take the bishop of baston / the
bishop of saint Andrews / and the abbot of scone well armed with iron, as men
of arms as falls traitors and falls prelates against her oath / and they were
brout to the king / and the king sent hem to the pope of Rome / that he
should done with hem what his will were.

How Johan earl of atheles was take / and put to the death / Capitulo / C
lxxxijo. /
ANd at that bataylle fled sir Johan earl of Atheles, and went in to a chirch
and there hyd him for dread / but he might have there no refute for encheson.
that the church was enterdyted through a general sentence / and in the same
church he was take / And this sir Johan went well to have had escaped from the
death for encheson that he claymed kynered of king Edward / and the king nold no
longer be tarried of his traitors / but sent him to london in have / and there
he was honged / and his head smyten of / and his body burnt al to asshis. But
at prayer of the queen margarete For encheson that he claymed of king Edward
kynred / his drawyng was foryeue him /

When the grettest maystres of Scotland were thus done to euel death. and

How Robert the brus fled from scotland to Norwey / Capitulo C lxxxiiij /
ANd at that same day was Robert the brus much bated among the people of
Scotland / so he wist not what was for to done / and for to hyde him he went in
to norwey to the king, that had spoused his suster, and there held him socour
for to have / And Robert the Brus might not be found in Scotland / king Edward
tho let cry his pees through out all the land / and his laws were vsyd. and
his mynystres served through out all the land

How king edward dyed / Capitulo / C / lxxxvo. /
When king edward had abated his enemies / ^e turned again southward / and a
maladye took him at burgh up sand in the march of Scotland / and he wyste well
that his death was fnl nygh and called to him sire henry the lacy earl of nychol
/ Sir^ Guy earl of war wyk / sire aymer valence earl of penbroke / and sir
robert of clifford baron and prayed hem upon the faith that they him owed that
they should make edward of Carnariuan king of england his sone as rathe as they
might / and that they should not suf fre pyers of ganeston come again in to
england / for to make his sone to use ryotte / and they granted him with good
will, and the king took the sacrament of holy church as a good christian man
shol de / and de^de in very repentance / and when he had be king xxxv year he
deyd / and was buried at westmynstre. with much solempnyte / upon whose soul
god have mercy /

Of merlyns prophecyes that were declared of king Edward that was king henryes
sone / Ca / C / lxxxvj /
ANd of this king edward profecyed merlyn / and called him a dragon the second
king of the vj last kings that should be for to regne in england / and said
that he should be meddled with mer cy / and also with strength and with sternesse
/ that should keep england fro cold and he^e / and that he should open his mouth
toward walis / and that he should set his one foot in wyke / and that he should
closen with walls that should do much harm to his seed / and he said soth /
For the good king edward was meddled with mercy / and with fiersnes with mercy
against his enemies of walys / and after of Scotland / with fiersnesse when he
put hem to death for her falsenes and traytrie as they had deserved it / and well
kept he england from cold and hete since he kept it from al manner enemies /
that ^o^ne upon him to done him any wrong / and well he opened his mouth toward
walys / and made it quake through the hydour of his mouth / when he co^querd it
thurght dynt of swerd / for the prince lewelyn and david his bro der rys and
morgan were put unto the death for her falsenesse, and her folly / and he set
his one foot in to wyke / and co^querd Berwyck / at the which conquest were
slain xxv M and vij C, out take hem that were burnt in the reed halle / And
the walls that he let make shall be noyous unto his seed. as men shall here
after see in the life of Sir edward of Carnariuan his sone / And yet merlyn said
that he should make Ryuers run in blood / and with brain. and that seemed well
in his werres there that he had the maystrye / And yet merlyn said that there
should come a people out of the north west during the regne of the foresaid dragon
that should be ladde by an ylle Grehounde that should the dragon croune king /
that afterward should flee over the sea for dread of the Dragon without coming
again / and that was proved by Sir Johan bayllol / that king edward made for
to ben king of Scotland, that falsely aroos ageynste him / and after he fled
unto his own lands of france / and never come again in to Scotland for
dread of king edward / and yet said merlyn that people that should led the
foresaid grehond should be fadreles until a certain time / and he said soth.
For the people of Scotland gretely were dysesed sith that Sir Johan bayllol her
king fled from scotland / And yet said mer lyn that the son should bycome in
his time as reed / as any blo de in tokenyng of great mortalyte of people / and
that was well known when the Scotts were slain / And sith said merlyn that
ylke dragon should norysshe a fox that should meue great werre against him that
should not in his time ben ended / and that seemed well by Robert the brus, that
king edward norysshed in his cha^ bre / that sythenes stale aweye. and meued
great war against him / which werre was not ended in his time / And afterward
Merlyn told that this dragon should ben hold the best body of all the world /
and he said sothe / For the good king edward was the worthyest knight of all the world in his time / And yet said mer lyn that the dragon should dye in the
march of another land, and that his land should be long without any good kepar
/ and that me^ should weep for his death from the I Will of shepey un to the I Will of
marcyl / wherefore allas should be her common song among people fadreles in the
land wasted / and that prophecye was know oueral full well / For the good king
Edward dyed at Burgh up sand that is upon the march of Scotland / wherefore the
Englysshmen were discomforted and sorowed in northumberlond / For encheson that
king edwardys sone set by the scotts no force for the Riott of pyers of
ganaston / wherefore allas was the song th^rugh out al England / for defaute
of a good wardeyn from the I Will of shepey unto the isle of marcyl the people made
much sorrow for good king Edwardys death / For they wend that good king
edward should have gone in to the holy land, for that was hollyche his purpose.
upon whose soul god for his high grace ha ne mercy /

ANd after this king Edward / reigned Edward his son. that was bore in

And anon as the good king edward was deed / Sir Edward his sone king of

that he called him his brother / and anon after he yaf him the lordship of

How the Scotts robbed northumberlond / Cao. / C / lxxxxo.
ANd in the same time come the scotts ayene in to England and destroyed

How the Scotts would not amend her trespaas / and therefore Scotland was
enterdyted / Ca / C / lxxxxjo. /
ANd when pope John the xxij after saint Peter herd of the great so^we and
meschyef that the scotts wrought he was wonder sorry that cristendome was so
destroyed through the scotts and namely they destroyed so holy church. wherefore
the pope sent a general sentence under his bulls of led unto the
archebisshop of Caunterbury and to the Archebisshop of york / that if Robert
the B^us, of Scotland would not be Iustyfyed / and make amends unto the king of
England Edward her lord and make amends of his loss and of his harnoys that
they had done in England / and also to restore the goods that they had taken
of holy Church that the sentence should be pronounced through al England / and
when the scot tes herd this they would not let her malice for the popes comma^
dement / wherefore Robert Brus. James douglas, and Thomas Randulph earl of m^ref
/ and all tho that with him comuned / or hem halpe in word or in deed were
acursed in every chirch through england every day at mass three times / and no
mo mass should be song in holy church through out al Scotland / but if the
Scot tes would make restitucion of the harms that they had made un to holy church / wherefore many a good priest and holy men therefore were slain through
the Reame of scotland for encheson that wol de sing no mass against the
popes commandment / and ageynste his will / and to done and fulfill the
tyrunts, will /

Of the syege of Thykhylle / Capitulo / C lxxxxvjo.

and went thither ward to reske we the Castle, and his power encresed from day to
day / When the Earl of lancastre / and the Earl of Herford. and the barons of
her company herd this thing / they assembled al her power / and went hem to
Burton up Trent / and kept the bridge that the king should not pass over / But
it bifell so on the tenth day of march in the year of grace M CCC / and xxi /
The king and the Spencer Sir Aymer Malau^ce earl of penbroke / and Johan earl
of Arundel / and her power went over the water. and discomfyted therle thomas
/ and his company And they fled to the Castle of Tutbery and fro thens they
went to pountfret / And in that vyage dyed Sir Rogyer Dammorye / in the Abbay
of Tutbery / And in that same time the Earl Tho mas had a traitor with him,
that was called Robert of holond a knight that the Earl hadd brought up of
naught / and badde norisshed him in his ^otelerye / and had yeuen him a
thousand marc of land by year / and so much the Earl loved him / that he
might done in the Earls court al thing that him lyked both among high and
low / and so queynt^lyche the thief bare him against his lord that he trusted
more upon him than upon any man alive / And the Earl had ordained by his
lettres for to wend in to the Erldome of lancastre for to make men arise to
help him in that vyage that is to say / v C, men of arms / But the false
Traitor come not there no manner men for to warne'ne to make arise for to (...)
his lord / And when the traitor herd tell that his lord was discomfyted at
Burtone / as a falls thief traitor he stale a way and robbed in ^enesdale his
lords men that come fro the scomfyture / and took of hem horse and harnoys /
and all that they ^ad / and slew of hem all that he might take / and tho come
and yield him to the king / When the good Earl Thomas wyste that he ^as so
bytrayd he was sore abashed / and said to him self / O almighty god quod he.
how might Robert Holand find in his heart me to bitraye. sithenes that I have
loved him so much / O god well may now a man see by him / that no man may
deceive an other rather. than he that he trust most upon he has full euel yield
my goodness / and the worship that I to him have done / and through my
kyndenes have him auaunced / and made high from low / and he makes me go from
high unto low / but yet shall be dye in evil death /

Of the scomfiture of Burbrudge / Cao / C lxxxxvijo. /
THe good Earl Thomas of lancastre Humfrey de Bohoune Earl of herford / and the
barons that with hem were token counceylle between hem at Friar prechours at
pountfret / Tho thought thomas upon the Traytrye of Robert Holand and said in
reprove / Allas holand has me bytrayd, Ay is in the reed of some euel shrede /
and by common assent they should al wend to the castle of dunstanburgh / the
which pertryned to the erldom of lancastre and that they should abide there til
that the king had foryeue hem her maletalent / But when the good earl thomas
this herd, be ansuerd in this manner and said / lords quod he if we go toward
the north / the northeren men will seyn that we go toward the scot^s and so we
shall be hold traitors, for cause of distau^ce / that is bitwe ne king edward
and robert the brus that made him king of scotland / and therefore I say as
touching my self that I will go no ferther in (...) the north than to mine own
castle of pountfret / And when Sir Rogyer clyfford herd this / he aroos up anon
in wrath and drowe his swerd and swore by almighty god, and by his holy names /
but if that he would gone with hem, he should be deed / and that he would slay him
there, The noble and gentil earl Thomas of lancastre was sore adrad and said
fair syrs I will gene with you whyder so ever ye me led / Tho went they to
geders in to the north / and with hem they had seven / C / men of arms and

false counceylle through Sir hugh the spencer the fadre / and Sir Hugh his sone
/ and Sir Johan earl of Arondele. and through Maystyr Robert Baldoke a falls

he nold not consent to him for no ma ner thing / Sir Andrew he said / will ye

hol de for a traitor, and more than ye hold us now / and in wers death ye shall
dye than ever dyed any knight of England / And understands well that ye did
never thing that sorer shall you repent and now goth and does that you good
lyketh / And I will put me unto the mercy / and the grace of god / And so went
the false traitor sir Andrew of herkela in his wey as a falls traitor tirant
and as a falls forsworen man / For through the noble earl Thomas of lancastre he
vnderfenge the arms of Chyualrye / and through him he was made knight.

Tho might men seen archyers draw hem in that one side / and in that other /
and knights also / and foughten to gedre wonder sore / and also among other
Sir humfrey de boughon earl of Herford a worthy knight of renomme through al
cristendom / stood and fought with his enemies upon the bridge. and as the
noble lord stood and fought upon the bridge / a thyef a ribaud skulked under
the bridge / and fiersly with a spear smote the noble knight in to the
foundament / so that his bowels comen out there. Allas the sorrow / For there
was slain the flour of solace and of comfort and also of curtosye / And Sir
Rogyer of Clyfford a noble knight stood ever and fought / and well and nobly him
defended / as a worthy Baron / But at last he was sore wounded in his head /
and sir Wylliam of Sustayand / Sir Rogyer of Bernefeld were slain at that
bataylle / When Sire Andrewe of Herkela saw that Sir thomas men lancastre
lassed and slaked / anon he and his company come to the gentil knight Sir
Thomas of lan castre and said / yield the traitor yield the / The G^ntille
Earl ansuerd tho and said / Nay lords Traitors be we none / and to you will
we never us yield while that our lyfes lasten but lever we have to be slain in
our treuth / than yield us to you And sir Andrew again grad upon Sir thomas
company / yollyng as a wode wolf and said yield you traitors taken / yield you
/ and with an high voys said / be the, ware sirs that none of you be hardy upon
life and lymme to mysdone thomas body of lancastre And with that word the good

vyleyns egrely hem discryed / and grad an high yield you traitors yield you /
And when they were y yolde they were robbed / and bound / as thefes / Allas
the shame and despyte / that the gentill order of knyghthode there had at that
battle / and the land tho was without law / For holy church tho had no
more reverence than it had been a bordelhows / and in that batayl was the fadre
against the sone / and the uncle against his neuew, For so much vnkendenesse
was never seyn before in england / as was that time among folk of one nation /
for one kynred had no more pite of that other than an hungary wolf has of a
sheep / and it was no wonder / for the great lords of england were not all of
one nation / but were meddled with other nations / that is for to say / some
britons / some saxons. sum danoys / some Pehytes / some Frensshmen / Some
normans / Some spaynardes / Sum Romans, sum Henaudes / Some Flemmynges /
and of other diverse nations. the which Nations acorded not to the kind blood
of England. And if so great lords had been onlych wedded to Englyssh people
than should pees have been and rest / among hem without any envy /

How king Edward went in to Scotland with an honderd thousand men of Arms
and might not ^pede, Ca. C, lxxxxixo.
ANd when king Edward of England had brought the Flower of Chyualrye un to
her death through counceylle of Sir hugh the spencer the fridre / and sir hugh
the sone he bycome a^ wode as any lion / And what so ever the sp^cers would have
/ it was done / and so well the king loved hem that they might done with him al
thing that they would / wherefore the king yafe unto sir hugh spencer the fadre
the erldom of wynchestre / and to sir Andrewe of herkela the Erldome of
cardoyll in pr^dyce / and in harmyng of his croune / And king edward tho through
counseyll of the spencers disheryted al hem that had been against him in any
quarrel with thomas of lancastre / and many^ other were dis heryted also for
encheson that the spencers couerted for to have her lands / and so they had all that they would desire with wrong and against all reason / Tho made the king
Robert of Baldoc a falls pylled cler ke chaunceler of England / through cou^ceyll
of the foresaid spen cers and he was a falls ribaud and a cou^itous / and s^ they
cou^seylled the king much that the king let take to his own ward all the
goods of the lords that wrongfully were put to the death / in to his own hand
/ and as well they token the goods that were in holy church as the goods
that were without / and let hem be put in to his tresorye in london / and
let hem call his for faytz / and by her ^n ceyll the king wrought for
evermore, he disherited hem that the goods oughten / and through her counseylle
let a^re a tallyage of all the goods of England / wherefore he was the rychest
king that ever was in England after william bastard of normandye that conquered
England / And yet through counceyll of hem him seemed that he had not ynow but
made yet every Town of England find a man of arms upon her own costages for
to gone and were re upon the scotts that were his enemies wherefore the king w^
in to Scotland with an honderd thousand men of arms at wytsontyde in the year
of our lord Ihu crist / M / CCC / and xxij / But the Scotts went and hyd hem
in montaynes and in wodes and ^ed the Englysshmen fro day to day that the king
might for no manner thing hem find in plain field / wherefore many englyssh men
that hadden few vytaylles for honger there deyden wonder fast / and suddenly
for honger in going and in coming / and namely^ tho that had been against thomas
of lancastre / and had robbed his men upon his lands

When king Edward saw that vytaylles failed him* he was tho wonder sore
discomforted for encheson also that his men dyed / and for he might naught
speed of his enemies / so at the last he come ayene in to England / And anon
after come James douglas / and also thomas randulf with an huge host in to
england in to northu^berlond / and wi^h hem the englysshmen that were driven
out of england. and come and robbed the contray / and slew the peple^ and also
brent the town / that was called nortallertone and many other towns unto york
/ And when the king herd this tydynge he let sompne al manner men that myghten
trauaylle. and so the englysshmen met the scotts at the abbey of Beygland the
xv day after mychelmasse / in the same year above said / and the en glysshmen
were there discomfyted / and at that sco^fiture was take sir Johan of britayne /
Earl of richemond that held the country / and Erldom of lancastre, and after
he paid an huge ^unsonne, and was let gone / and after that he went in to
France / and come never afterward again /

How Sir Andrew of herkela was take / and pnt unto the death that was earl of

ANd at that time Sir andrewe of herkela that new was made Earl of Cardoylle /

thyn honor / and worship upon thy body / be al brought to nout / and thy
estate undone that other knytes of lower degree mow after the beware / the
