Of the miracles that god wrought for saint thomas love of la^ castre / wherefore
the king let close the chirch doors of the prioryr of Pountfret, for no man
should come therein to the body for to offren Capituso, CC / j /
ANd sone after that the good Earl thomas of lancastre was martred a preeste
that long time had been blind dremed in his slepynge that he should gone un
to the hille / there that the good Earl thomas of lancastre was done unto the
death / and he should have his sight again, and so he dremed iij nyghtes sewyn^^
and the priest let led him to the same hylle / and when he come to that place
that he was martred on / deuontly he made there his pra yers and prayed god and
saint thomas / that he might have his slghte ayene / and was in his prayers /
he laid his right hond upon the same place that the good man was martred on /
and a drope of dry blood and small sond cleued on his hond / and therewith
striked his eyes. and anon through the mit of god and of saint thomas of
lancaster he had his sight ayene / and thanked tho almighty god / and saint
thomas / and when this miracle was known among men / the people come thy der on
every side, and kneled and made her prayers at his to^be / that is in the
priorye of pou^tfret / and prayed that holy martyr of socour and of help, and
god herd her prayer / Also there was a yo^g child drenchid in a well in the
town of pou^tfret / and was deed iij days and iij nites and men comen, and
laid the deed child upon saint thomas tomb the holy martyr / and the child
aroos there from death to life / as many a man it saw / and also much people were
out of her mind. and god has sent hem her mind ayene through virtue of that
holy martyr / and al so god has yeuen thereto / to crepels her going / and to
crooked her hon des and her feet / and to blind also her sight / and to many
seek folk her hele of diverse maladyes / for the love of his good martyr / Also
there was a rich man in cou^dom in gascoyn. and such a maladye he had that al
his right side roted / and fell aweye from him / that men myt see his liver
and also his heart / and so he stanke that uneath men might come nigh him /
wherefore his friends were for him wonder sorry. But at last as god would they
prayed to saint thomas of lancastre that he would pray to almyty god, for that
prisoner and be hight to gone to pou^tfret for to done her pilgremage, than the
mar tir saint thomas come unto him / and anointed over al his syke body / and
therewith the good man awoke / and was al hole and his flessh was restored ayene
that before was roted and fall a wey / for which miracle the good man and his
friends loved god and saint thomas ever more after, and this good man come in
to england / and took with him four felawes. and come to pou^tfret unto that
holy martyr, and did her pilgremage / but the good man that was syke come
thither al naked sauf his breche, and when they had done / they turned home
ayene in to her country / and told of the miracle where so ever they come / And
also ij men have been heled there of the mormal through help of that holy martyr
/ though that euel be hold Incurable / when the spencers herd that god did
such miracles for this ho ly martyr, and they would believe it in no manner wise
/ but said open liche that it was great he resye such virtue of him to believe
/ and when sir hugh the spencer the sone saw all this doing / anon he sent
his messagers from pou^tfret there that he duellid to the kyn ge edward that tho
was at grauene at shipton for cause that the king should undo that pilgremage,
And as the Ribaude the mes sager went toward the king. for to done his message
/ he come by the hylle on the which the good martyr was done to death / and in
the same place he made his ordure / and when he had done he went toward the
king / and a strouge flyx him come upon er he come to york / and shed al his
bowels at his fundament / and when Sir hugh the spen cer herd this tydyng
somdele he was adrad / and thought for to undone the pilgremage / if he might
by any manner way / and tho the king went and said that they should be in
great sklau^der through out al cristendome for the death of thomas of lancastre
/ if that he suffered the people done her pylgremage at pou^tfret / and so he
cou^cey led the king. that he commanded to close the church doors of pou^t
frete / in the which church the holy martyr saint thomas was entered / and
thus they dyden again al fraunchyses of holy chirch so that four year after
might no pilgrym come to that holy body / and for encheson that monks suffered
men to come and honor that holy body of saint thomas the martyr through
cou^ceylle of sir hugh the spencer the sone / and through cou^ceill also of
master Robert of bal dok the false pylled clerk that was the kings chau^celer
the king consented that they should be set to her wages. and beat make
wardeyns over her own good long time / and through commandment of the foresaid
Sir hugh the spencer xiiij gascoynes well armed kept the hille that the good
man saint Thomas was done unto his death / so that no pilgrim myt come by that
way / Full well went he to have be take cristes might and his power and the great
lose of miracles that he showed for his martyr saint thomas through all
cristendom, and that same time the king made Robert of bal dok the pylled
clerk and falls through prayer of sir hugh the spe^cer the son Chaunceler of
england / And in the same time was the castle of walyngford holden against the
king through the pri soners that were within the Castle For saint thomas quarrel
of Lancastre wherefore the people of the contre come and took the castle up on the
foresaid prisoners / wherefore sir Johan of goldyngton knit and sir edmond of the
beche prysonner. and a squire that was callid rogyer of walton were take / and
sent to the king to pontfret / and there they were done in to prison / and the
foresaid rogyer was sent un to york and there he was draw and honged / And anon
after sir rogi er mortimer of wygmore brake out of the tour of london in this
manner / the foresaid sir rogyer herd that he should be draw and honged at london
in the morn after saint laurence day / and on the day bifo re he held a fair
fest in the tour of london / and there was sir stephn segraue Constable of the
tour and many great me^ with hem / and when they should soap, the foresaid steven
sent for all the officers of the tour and they come and souped with him. and
when they should take her l^ue of him a squire that was called stephen / that
was full prince with the foresaid Rogyer / through his counseyll yafe hem all
such drink that the lest of hem all slepte ij days and ij nyghtrs / and in
the mean time he escaped awey by water that is to say by the thamyse and went
over the sea / and held him in france / wherefore the king was sore annoyed / and
tho put the same stephn out of his co^stabelry

How the queen Isabel went in to France for to treten of pees between her lord
the king of England / and the king of france her brother. Ca / CC / ij
THe king went tho unto london / and there through counceyl of sir hugh the
spencer the fadre and of his sone and of master to bert baldok / a falls pylled
clerk his chaunceler let seyse tho all the queen's lands in to his own hand
/ and also all the lands that were sir edwardes his sone / and were so put to
her wages against al manner reason / and that was through the falsenesse of the
spencers / And when the queen of France that was queen Isabels brother herd of
this falsencs he was sore annoyed against the king of en glond and his false
counceyllours / wherefore he sent a letter unto king edward under his seal that
he should come in to france at a certain day for to done his homage / and thereto
he somened him / and else he should lose al gascoyn / And so it was ordained in
England through the king! and his cou^ceill that queen Isabel should we^de in to
france for to treat of pees between her lord and her brother / And that Olyuer
of yngham should we^de in to gascoyne / and have with him seven thousand men and
more of Arms to ben seneshall / and wardeyne of gascoyn / and so it was
ordained that queen Isabel wet tho once see and come in to france / and with
her went sir Aymer of va lance earl of penbroke that was there mordred suddenly
in prive sege / but that was through gods vengeance. for he was one of the
Instyces that consented to saint thomas death of lancaster, and would never after
repent him of that wykked deed / and at that time sire Olyuer of yngham went
over in to gascoyne / and did much harm to the king of france / and tho get
ageyn that king edward had lost / and much more thereto.

How king Edward sent sir edward his sone the eldest in to france / Cao. CC
iijo. /
THe queen Isabel nadd but a quarter of a year in France duellyd that sir
edward her eldest sone ne axed leave for to wend in to france for to speak

will / and said to him / go my fair sone in gods blyssyng and mine and thenke
for to come again as hastily as thou might / and he went over see and come in

and said unto him / fair sone ye be welcome / and for cause that your fadre

were wont for to do I give you that lordship to hold it of me in heritage as
al manner au^cestres diden to fore you wherefore he was callid duk of gu^he^ne

How the king exyled his queen Isabel / and edward his eldest sone. Cao. CC /
iiijo.
When king edward of England herd tell how the king of France had give the
Duchye of guybenne unto Sir Edward his sone without consent and will of him /
and that his son had vnderfonge the duchye / he bycome wonder wroth / and
sent to his sone by his lettre, and to his wif also that they should come ayene
in to england in all the haste that they might / The queen Isabell and sir
edward her sone were wonder sore adrad of the kings manace / and of his wrath
and principally the falsenesse of the spencers both of the fadre and of the
son / and at this commandment they would not come / wherefore king edward was
full sore annoyed / and let make a cry at london that if queen ysabel and
Edward her eldest sone come not in to England that they should ben holden as our
enemies both to the Royame and to the cronne of England, And for that they
would, not come in to england / both were exiled the mother and her sone / when
the queen Isabell herd these tidyn ges she was sore adrad to be shent through
the false congettyng of the spencers / And went with the knyghtrs that were
exyled out of England / for saint thomas cause of lancastre that is to say sir
Rogyer of wigmore. sir william Trussel / sir Johan of Cromwell and many other
good knights / wherefore they took her counseyll and ordained among he in for
to make a marriage between the duk of guyhenne the kings sone of england and
therles daughter of he naud that was a noble knight of name / and a doughty in
his time / And if that thing might be brought about than stood they trowynge
with the help of god and with his help to recover her heritage in England
whereof they were put out through the false congettynges of spencers /

How king edward through counceyll of the spencers sent to the douzepers of
france / that they should help that the queen Isabell and her son Sir edward
were exyled out of france / cao. / CC / vo.
When king edward and the spencers herd how queen Isabel and sir Edward her
sone had alyed hem to the Earl of Henaud / and to them that were exyled out of
England / For enche son of thomas of lancastre they were so sorry that they nyst
what to done / wherefore Sir hugh spencer the sone said unto Sir hugh his fadre
in this manner wise / Fader acursed be the time. and the counceylle that ever ye
consented that queen Isabell should gone unto France for to treaten of acord
between the king of England and her brother the king of france / for that was
your co^ ceyll / For at that time forsooth your wit failed / For I dread me sore
lest through her and her sone we shall be shent / but if we take the better
counseyll / Now fair sirs understands how meruayllous felonye and falshede
the spencers ymagyned and cast for pri uely they let fylle v barel ferrors
with silver / the some amou^ted v thousand pound / and they sent tho barelles
over see pryuely by an alyen that was called Arnold of spain that was a
brocour of london / that he should gone to the douzepers of france that they
should procuren and speak to the king of France / that queen Isa bell and her
sone Edward were dryne and exyled out of france And among al other things
that they were brought to the death as privily as they might / But Almighty god
would not so for when this arnold was in the high see, he was take with
sela^dres that met him in the sea / and took him and ladde him to her lord
earl of henaud, and much joy was made for that taking / and at last this
arnold privily stale awey fro thens and come to london / and of this taking and
of other things the earl of henaud said to the queen Isabel / dame make you
merry and be of good chere / for ye be more richer than ye went have been / and
take ye these five barelles full of silver / that were sent to douzepyers of
france for to slay you and your sone edward, and thenketh hastily for to wend
in to england / and take ye with you Sir Johan of henaud my brother and v C men
of arms / for many of hem of France in whom ye have had great trust had
great deynte, you for to scorn / and Almighty god grant you grace your
enemies to overcome / The queen Isabel sent tho through henaud and flau^dres
for her scudy^ ours, and ordained her every day for to wend in to england ageyn
/ And so she had in her company Sir Edmond of wodestoke that was earl of kent
that was sir edwardes brother of England

when king edward let keep the Costs by the sea and let try all the price
men of arms and footmen through England / Capitulo CC vjo.
When king Edward herd tell that Queen Isabell and Edward her son would
come in to England with many alyens / and with hem that were outlawed out of
England / for her reb^lnesse / he was sore, adrad to be put a down and l^se
his kingdom / wherefore he ordained to keep his castles in walys as well as in
England with vitaylles / and her apparaylle. and let keep his Ryuers and also
the sea costs / whereof the v ports token to keep hem and also the sea, And at
the feste of decollacion of saint Johan baptist the cytezeyns of london sent
to the king to po^ches tree an C men of Arms / And also he commanded
ferthermore by his lettres ordained that every honderd and wapentake of england
should try as well of men of arms as of men a foot. and that they should be put
in sum xx and in some an C, and commanded that al tho me^ were a ready when any
out he se or cry were made for to pursue and take the alyens that comen to
England for to benymme him the land and for to put him out of his kingdom.
And more over he let cry through his patent in every fair, and in every mar
kete of England that the queen Isabell and Sir Edward his eldest sone. and the
earl of kent that they were take and saufly kept without any manner harm unto
hem doing / and al other manner people that come with hem / anon to smite of her
hedes without any manner rau^sonne / And what man that might bring sir rogyers
heed mortimer of wigmroe should have an C p^u^d of money for his trauaylle /
And ferthermore he ordained by his patent and com manded to make a fire upon
every high hylle besides the rivers and in low countries for to make hye
bekenes of tymbre that if it so were that the alyens come unto the land by
night that men should tend the bekenes that the country might be warned / and
come and mete her enemies / and in the same time dyed sir rogyer mor timer his
uncle in the toure of london /

How the queen Isabell / and sir Edward duke of guyhenne her son^ come to land
at here wiche / and how they dyden / Ca / CC / vijo. /
THe queen Isabel / and sir edward her sone duk of guyhenne Sir edward of
wodestoke Earl of kent and sir Johan therlys brother of henaud and her company
dradde not the manace of the king ne of his traitors. for they trust al in
gods grace / and come unto here wyche in south folk / the xxiiij day of
September / And in the year of grace M CCC xxvj / And the queen and sir edward
her sone sent lettres to the mayer and comynalte of london requyringe hem that
they should ben helpyng in the quarrel and cause that they had bygo^ne / that is
to say to destroy the traitors of the reame / But none ansuer was sent
again / wherefore the queen and sir edward her son sent another pa^nt letter
under her seals the tenoure of which letter here follows in this manner /
Isabell by the grace of god queen of England / lady of Irlond / Countess of
pou^tyf / and we edward the eldest sone of the king of England duke of guyhenne
earl of Chestre of pountyf and of moustroylle to the mayer and to all the
comynalte of the cite of London sends gre tyng / For as much as we have
before this time sent to you by our lettres how we become in to this land with
good array, and in good manner for the honor and profit of holy church / and
of our right dear lord the king / and all the Royame with our might and power
to keep and mayntene as we and all the good folk of the forsaid royame are
holden to done / And upon that we pray you that ye would ben helpyng to us in
as much as ye may in this quarelle / that is for the commune profit of all
the royame And we have hadd unto this time none ansuer of the foresaid lettres /
ne know not your will in that party / wherefore we send to you again / and
pray and charge you that ye bear you so against us that we have no cause to
grieve you, but that ye ben to us helping by all the weyes that ye may or may
known / for weteth well in certain that we and all tho that been comen with us
in to this reame / ne thenke not to done if it like god any thing but that shall
be for the comune profit of all the reame but only to destroy hugh spencer our
enemy / and enemy to all the royame / as ye well know wherefore we pray you and
charge you in the feith that ye owe to our lord the king, and upon us / and
upon all that ye shall mow forfet again us that if the foresaid hugh the spencer
our enemy come within your power / that ye done him hastily to ben taken. and
saufly kept until we have ordained of him our will / and that ye leave it not
in no manner wise, as ye desire honor and profit of us all and of all the
royame / Understanding well that if ye done our prayer and mau^dement / we shall
the more be behold unto you / And also ye shall get you worship and profit
if ye send us hastily ansuer of al your will / yeuen at baldok the syxth day
of October / which letter erly in the dawenynge of the day of saint denis was
takked upon the new cross in Chepe / and many Copyes of the same letter were
takked upon wyndowes and doors, and upon other places in the Cite that all men
passing by the weye might seen and read / And in the same time king edward was
at london in the toure at his mete, and a messager come in to the halle / and
said that the Queen Isabell was come to land at herewyche / and has brought in
her company Sir Johan of henaud. and with him men of Arms without nombre /
And with that word sir hugh the spencer the fadre spak / and thus to the king
said my most worshipful lord king of england Now mow ye make good chere / For
certeynly / they ben al ours

The king saw this word comfortable / yet he was full sorrowful / and pensyfe
in heart, And the king had not yet full y^^ eten that there come in to the halle
another messagyer and said that the queen Isabel was arrived at herewiche
beside yepswhiche in Southfolk / Sir hugh the spencer the fadre spak to the
messager and said tell soth in good feith to the messager my fair friend is
she come with strength / Certis sir soth for to say, she ne has in her
company but vij honderd men of Arms / And with that word Sir hugh the spencer
the fadre cried with an high voys and said Allas allas we ben al bytrayd / for
certes with so litel power she had never come to land / but folk of this land
were to her consent And therefore after the mete they took her cou^ceyll / and
went toward walys for to arere the walshme^ again queen Isabell and edward her
sone al for to fight / and so they were in purpose euerychon /

How master waltier Stapylton Bishop of excetre that was the kings tresorer
was byheded at london / Ca / CC / viij /
ANd in the same time king Edward was sore adrad lest men of london would
yield hem unto the queen Isabell, and to her sone Edward / wherefore he sent
master walter stapylton his Tresorer for to ben wardeyne and kepar of the cite
of london with the mayer / And so he come to the gyldehall of london / and axed
the keys of the yates of the Cite through virtue and strength of his
commyssyon / and would have had the keeping of the Cite / and the comuners
ansuerd and said that they would keep the cite to the honor of king edward /
and of Isabell the queen / and of the duk the kings sone withouten any more /
The bishop was so sore annoyed / and swore oath / that they al should abye it
anon as king edward were come out of walys / And the Comuners all anon of the
cite token the bishop / and lad him amyddes chepe and there they smyten of his
head. and set^e his head in his right hand / And after they byheded two of his
squyers / that held with the bishop / and one of hem was callid william of
wall / that was the bisshops neuew / that other was called Johan of padyngton
/ And also they took a burgeis of london that was called Johan marchal that was
sir hugh the spe^cers aspye the fadre / and smyten of his head also / And in
that same time that bishop had in london a fair toure in making in his close
upon the river of the thamyse / that was without temple bar, and him faylled
stone to make thereof an end / wherefore he co^ mau^ded his men to gone to the
church of friar carmes / and there they token stone to maken therwyth the tour
/ and much sand / and mortyer and old robous that was left / And for the
despyte that the bishop had done unto holy church, he and his two squyers
were buried in that sand as though they had been hou^des / And they there leyn xj
wekes til that the queen Isabell sent her lettres to the comuners and prayed hem
that they would suffer and grant that the bishop must be taken out of that
place / and ben buried at excetre at his own church. and so he was / and his
two squyers were buried at saint Cle ments chirch without temple bar. and it
was no wonder though the bishop dyed an evil death / For he was a coueytous man
and had with him no mercy / and evil counceyled the king / And sone after was
arnold of spayn taken / he that was assentau^t to have lad the v M pound of
silver in v barellys ferryers unto the douzyepyers of france for to help and
have the queen Isabel to her death. and edward her sone also / And this Arnold
was put unto death without the Cite of london.

How king edward and sir hugh spencer, and the earl of Arun dell were taken /
Cao. / CC ixo. /
When king edward had sent Master walter stapilton his Tresorer in to london
for to keep the cite unto him ayene the Queen Isabel his wife / and again

/ and over in to walis for to arere the walshmen ayene dame Isabel the queen

god would and the king him self was in sauf keeping in the castle of kenelworth.
and him kept sir henry that was saint thomas brother of lancaster / And Sire
Hughe spencer the fadre came and put him in the queen's grace / and sir edward
her sone duk of guyhenne / but sir hugh the spencer after the time that he was
take nold ete no manner mete another drink no manner drink for he wist to have
no mercy sauf only to be deed And the Queen and her counseylle tho had ordained
that he should have been do to death at london / but he was so feeble for his much
fa styng that he was deed almost / and therefore it was ordained that he should
have his Judgment at herford / and at that place of the tour his hoode was take
from his head / and also from ro^ert of bald^ that was a pylled clerk and a
falls / and the kings Chau^celer and men set upon her hedes chappeletz of
sharp netteles. and two squyers blewe in her ^rs with ij great bugles horns
upon tho ij prisoners that men might here there blowyng out with horns mo re
than a mile / And one symond of Redyng the kings marchal before hem bare her
arms upon a spear reuersed in token that they should be undone for evermore /
And upon the morrow was sir hugh spencer the sone dampened to the death / and was
draw and honged / byheded / and his bowels taken out of his body and burnt
and after he was quartred and his four quartres were sent to four towns of
England / and his head sent to london brudge / And this Symond for encheson
that he despised queen Isabell / he was draw and honged in a stage made a
mydde the forsaid sir hughes ga lowes / And the same day a little fro thens was
sire Johan of Arundel byheded / for he was of Sir hugh spencers councelers /

And anon after was sir hugh spencer the fadre draw / honged and byheded at
B^sto we / and after honged ayene by the arms w^h two strong ropes / and the
fourth day after he was hewn al to pe ^s and hounds eten him / and for that
encheson that the king had yeuen him the erldom ^f wynchestre his head was lad
thydder / and ^t ^n a spear / And the f^ls Baldok was sent to london and t^r he
d^de in prison among the the^ / for men did him no more re (...) ^n they would
done unto (...) hou^d, and so deyden the trai tours of england blissed be
almighty god / And it was no wonder for through her counceill the good earl

How king Edward was put a down / and his dygnyte beno^me. Cao. / CC / xo. /
ANd anon after as this was done the Queen Isabel / and Edward her sone / and
all the great lords of england at one assente sent to king Edward to the
Castle of Kenelworth / there that he was in keeping under the ward of sir Johan
hachim that was the bishop of Ely. and of sir John of percy a Baron for
encheson that he should ordeine his parliament at a certain place in en glond for
to redress and amend the state of the reame / And king Edward hem ansuerd and
said / lords quod he / ^ye see full well how it is. Loo haueth here my seal / I
give you all mine power to ordeyne a parliament where that ye will / And they
took her leave of him and come again to the barons of England, And when they
had the kings patent of this thing they showed it to the lords / And tho was
ordained that the parliament should ben at westmynstre at the vtas of saint
Hillarye / And all the greet lords of england let ordeyne for hem there against
that time that the parliament should ben / And at which day that parliament was
the king would not come there for no manner thing / as he had set him self and
assigned / And netheles the barons sent to him o time and other / And he swore
by gods soul that he nold come there o foot wherefore it was ordained by all the
great lords of England that he should no longer ben king but ben deposed / and
said that they would croune king Edward his sone the elder / that was duk of
Guyhenne / and sent so tydyng unto the king there that he was in ward under Sir
Johan earl of garenne / And sir Johan of Bo thun that was bishop of Ely / and
sir henry percy a baron / and sir william Trussel a knight that was with the
earl sir Thomas of lancastre for to yield up her homages unto him, for all
them of England / And sir william Trussel said these words /

Sir Edward for ^cheson that ye have trayed your people of england / and have
undone many great lords of england without any cause / But now y^ ben
withstonde thanked be god. And also for encheson that ye would not come to the
parliament as y^ or deyned at westmynster as in your own letter patent is
co^^yned for to treat with your lyege men as a king should / And therefore
through all the commune assent of all the lords of England I tell unto you
these words / ye shall understand sire that the Barons of England at one
assent will / that ye be no more king of England / but vtterlych have put you
out of your realte for evermore, And the bishop of Ely fayd tho to the king /
Sire Edward / here I yield up feaute and homage for all the Archebis shoppes
and bisshoppes of England and for all the Clergy / Tho said Sir Johan Earl of
Garenne / Sir Edward I yield up here unto you feaute and homage for me and for
all the E^les of England. And Sir Henry percy yafe up also there his homa^ for
him and for all the Barons of England /

And tho said Sire wi^iam Trussel / I yield up now unto you Sire mine homage
for me and also for all the knights of England / and for all them that holden by
seriauntrie / or by any other manner thing of you / So that fro this day
afterward ye shall not be claymed king / another for king be hold / But from this
time afterward ye shall be hold for a synguler man of all the people / and so
they went thens unto london / there that the lords of en glond hem abode / and
sir Edward abode in prison in good keeping And that was the day of conversion of
saint paul in the xx year of his regne /

Profecye of Merlyn declared of king Edward the son of king edward / Cao. CC
/ xio. /
OF this king edward prophesied merlyn and said that there should come a got
out of Carre / that should have horns of sil^ and a berde as white as snow
and a doppe should come out of his nosethillers that should bytoken much ^me
honger and death of the people / and great loss of his land. and the in the
beginning of his regne should be hau^ted much lecherye / He said soth / alls
the time for king Edward that was king edwardes sone was borne at Carnariuan in
wa^s / Forsooth he had horns of silu / and a berd as snow when he was made
prince of walys / to much he yaf him to riotte and to folly / and soth said
merlyn in his propherye that there should come out of his nose a doppe / for in
his time was great hunger among the pour people and strong death am^ the
rich that deide in strange land with much sorrow and in we^e in Scotland and
afterward he lost scotland and gascoyne / and whiles that him (...) was king
there was much lecherye haunted / And also Merlyn told and said that this got
should seche the flour of ly^ and of death And he said soth / for he spoused
Isabel the kings daughter of brud ges / And in his time merlyn said that there
should be made brudges of folk upon dyches of the sea / and that was well seyn
at bannokkesborn in Scotland when he was dyscomfyted there of the Scotts / And
Merlyn told also that stones should fall from castle les / and many towns
should be made pleyn / And he said sothe for when king edward was discomfyted in
Scotland and come tho southward / the scotts besyeged tho castles / and did
hem much harm and burnt towns unto the hard earth /

And afterward Merlyn t^ld that an Egle should come out of Corn wayle. that
should have feathers of gold / that of pride should have no pyere. And he should
despise lords of blood / and after (...) should dye through a here at gauersiche
/ and that prophecye was (...) well know and found sothe / For by the Egle is
understand Sir Pyers of ganastone / that tho was earl of Cornewayll that was a
wonder proud man that despised the baronage of England / but afterward he was
byheded at Gauersich through the Earl of lancestre / and through the Earl of
war wyke /

And Merlyn told that in his time it should seem that the here should brenne /
and that battle should be upon an arm of the sea in a field arrayed like a
shield where should dye many white hedes /

And he said sothe for by the brennyng of the here is bitokened great dread
through cuttyng of sword at that bataylle ordained in a field as a shield upon
an arm of the sea is bitokened the batail of mytone / for there comen the
scotts in manner of a shield / in ma ner of a winge and slew upon swale men of
religyon prestes and secu lers / wherefore the scotts called that battle in
despyte of Englissh men the white battle / And after merlyn said that the
foresaid bear should done the got much harm and that should be upon the south
west and also upon his blood / and said also that the got should lose much dele
of his land til the time that shame should him oucome and than he should clothe
him with a lyone skyn / and should win ayene that he had lost and much more
through people that should come out of the northwest that should make him ben
dradde and him avenge of his enemies through cou^ceyle of ij owls / that first
shol de ben in peril to be undone / And that tho two owls should we^de over
the sea in to a strange land / and there they should duelle til a cer tryne time
/ and after they should come in to England again / And tho two owls should do
much harm unto many one and that they should cou^ceylle the got for to meue
werre against the forsaid here / And that the got and the owls should come unto
an arm of the sea at Barton up Trent / and should wend over / and that for
dread the here should flee with a swan in his company unto bury toward the
north through an unkind outepulter / and that the swan than should be slain
with sorrow. and the here should be slain full nyghe his own nest. that should
stand upon pou^tfeete upon whom the son shall shede his bemes / and many
folk him shall seche for the much virtue / and he said full soth / For the good
Erl^ Thomas of lancastre was born in the north west / and cosyn to the king and
sone of his uncle / And by law he made the king lose much la^d / the which he
had purchaced wilfully til at the last the king thereof took shame / and him
self filled with cruelte. And after he gate again that he had lost / and much
more through fel^ that he let assemble out of the northweste that made him to
(...) adrad and auengyd him of his Barons through counseylle of Sire hughe the
Spencer the fadre / and of Sire hugh the son that before were outlawed out
of England for her wykkednes But afterward come ageyn in to england sir hugh
spencer the fadre out of france / and so much counseylled the king that he
shol de werre upon thomas of lancastre / so that the king and the spen cers
and the earl of Arundel / and her power met with thomas of lancastre at burton
up trent / and him there dyscomfyted / and sir Humfrey earl of Herford was in
his company / And after fled den the foresaid thomas and humfrey with her
company at bur brudge with sir Andre we of herkela that is called / the
unkind out putter And also sire Edmond ward earl of york they comen and
met with thomas of lancastre with an huge compapanye / and hem there
discomfyted / and in that scomfyture the earl of herford was slain upon the
bridge cowardly with a spear in the fu^dament And the earl thomas was take /
and lad unto pou^t fret / and tho he was byheded bysyde his own castle / But
afterward many men him sought for miracles that god did for him And in that
time merlyn said for sorrow and harm should dye a pe ple of his land / wherefore
many lands should be upon him the hol dre. And he said soth / for by encheson
of his barons that were do ne to death for saint thomas quarrel of lancastre
people of many lo^ des bycome the holder for to meue werre upon the king. for
her blood was turned to many nacione / And afterward Merlyntolde / and said
that the foresaid owls should done much harm unto the flour of life / and of
death / and they should bring her unto mo che dysese / so that she should wend
over the sea in to france for to make pees to the flower delyse / and there
should abide til on a time / that her seed should come and seche her / And tho
they should abide both til a time that they should clothen hem with grace / and
tho two owls she should seek. and put hem unto spytous death / And that pro
phecye was well known / and was full sothe / For Sire Hughe spencer the fadre /
and sir hughe the son did much soro we and persecucion unto queen Isabell
through her procurement to her lord the king / So they ordained among hem that
she was put un to her wages / that is to say xx shyllyng in the day / Wherefore
the king of France her brother was wonder sore annoyed / and sent in to
England by his lettres unto king edward / that he should come to his parliament
to paris in France / but king Edward was sore adrad to come there / For he
wend to have been arested / til / that he had made amends for the trespace
that sir hugh spencer the fadre and the sone had done / and for the harm yt
they had done to Queen Isabel his suster / Wherefore through her ordinance and
consent of the spencers the queen Isabell went over see in to france / for to
make acord between king edward and the king of france her brother / And there
duellyd she in france til edward her eldest sone come her to seche / and so
they duellyd there both / til that alyau^ce was made between hem / And the
gentil earl of henaud that if they with her help might destroy / and overcome
the venym and the falsenesse of the sponcers. that sir edward should spouse dame
phi lip the worshipful lady / and the earls daughter of henaud / Wherefore the
queen Isabel / and sir edward her sone / and sir edmond of wodestok the kings
brother of england / and sir Johan of henaud / and sire Rogyer mortymer of
wygmore / and sir thomas rocelyn / and sir Johan of Cromwell / and sir william
trussel / and many other of the Alyaunce of the gentil earl thomas of lancastre
that were exyled out of England for his quarrel / and were disherited of her
lands ordained hem a great power and arrived at herewych in southfolk / And
sone after they pursueden the spencers til that they were taken / and put unto
pytous death. as before is said and her company / and also for the great
falsenesse / that they did to king edward / and to his people / And merlyn said
also more that the got should be put in to great disease / and in great
anguyssh / and great sorrow he should led in his life / And he said soth / For
after the time that king Edward was take / he was put in to ward til that the
spencers were putt unto the death. And also for encheson that he nold not come
unto his own parliament at london / as he had ordained and assygned him self
and to his barons / and also would not govern and rule his people / ne his
realm / as a king should done / Sum of the barons of England come and yield
up / her homages unto him for hem for all the other of the reame in the day of
Conversion of saint paul / and in the year of his regne xx / and they put him
out of his royalte for evermore / and ever he lived his life afterward in much
sorrow and anguysshe /

Of king Edward the third after the conquest / / Cao / CC xij
ANd after this king Edward of Carnariuan reigned Sire Edward of wyndesore his
son / the which was crouned king and anointed at Westmynstre / through
consent and will of all the great lords of the Royamme the sunday in
Ca^delmasse eve in the year of grace M / CCC xxvj / that was of age at that
time / but xv year / and for encheson that his fadre was in ward in the Castle
of kenelworth / and eke was put down of his royalte the royame of england was
as without king / fro the fest of saint katheryne in the year above said unto
the fest of can delmasse / and tho were al manner plees of the kings benche
aftent And tho was commanded to all the shereues of england through writ to
warn the parties defendau^ts through somnyng ayene And also ferthermore that al
prisoners that were in the kings gaylles that were attached through shereues
should be let gone quite / The king edward after his coronacion at the prayer
and bese chyng of his lieges of the reame granted hem a chartre of steadfast
pees to al hem that would it axe / and sir Johan of henaud and his co^pa nigh
took her leave of the king and of the lords of the reame / and turned home to
her own country again / and each of hem had full rich yeftes eueryche man as
he was of value and of estate / and tho was england in pees and in rest / and
great love between the king and his lords / and comunely englysshmen said
among hem / that the devil was deed / but the tresoure of the king his fadre
and the tresoure of the spencers both of the fadre and of the sone / and the
tresour of therle of Arundel. and of master robert baldock / that was the
kings chau^celer was departed after the queen Isabellys ordinance / and sir
rogyer mortimer of wygmore / so that the king had no thing thereof but at her
will and her delyueraunce naught of her lands / as afterward ye shall here /

How king edward went to stanhope for to mete the Scotts Capitulo / CC / xiij
/
ANd yet in the same time was king edward in the Castelle of kenelworth under
the keeping of sir henry that was earl thomas brother of lancastre / that tho was
earl of leycestre / and the king granted him the erldom of lancastre / that
the king his fa dre had seysed in to his hand / and put out thomas of
lancastre his brother / And so was he earl of lancaster and of leycestre / and
eke Styward of england / as his brother was in his time / but sir edward that
was king Edwardes fadre made sorrow without end / for cause that he myt not
speak with his wif ne with his sone / where for he was in much meschyef / for
though it were so that he was lad and ruled by falls cou^ceyll / yet he was king
edwardys sone call led Edward with long shankes / and come of the worthyest
blood of the world / And thylk to whom he was woned to give greet yeftes and
large were most prive with the king his own sone / and they were his enemies
both by night and by day / and procured for to make debate and contake between
him and his sone / and Isabell his wif But the Friar prechours to him were good
friends ever more and cast and ordained both by night and day how they might
breng him out of prison / And among her company that the freres had privily
brought there was a friar that was called dunhened / and he had ordained and
gadred a great company of folk to help at that need but the friar was take /
and putt in the castle of pou^tfret / and there he deyde in prison / And sir
henry earl of lancaster that had the kings fadre in keeping through commandment
of the king delyuerd edward the kings fadre by endenture unto sir thomas of
berkeley And so Sir Johan mautreuers / and they lad him from the cas tell of
kenelworth unto the castle of barkley / and kept him there sauf ly / And at
estren next after his coronacion the king ordained an huge host for to fight
against the scottis / And Sir Johan therles brother of henaud fro beyond the sea
come for to help king ed ward / and brought with him vij C men of arms and
arrived at do uer. and they had leave for to gone forth / til that they come to
york / there that the king abode hem / and the scotts come thider to the king
for to make pees and acord. but the acordement bitwene hem last but a little
time / And at that time the englysshmen were clothed al in cotes and hodes
peynted. with lettres and with flowers full semely with long berdes. And
therefore the scotts made a bylle that was fastened upon the church doors of
saint petre toward stangate / and thus said the scripture in despyte of
Englysshmen /

Long berde hertelees / Peynted hood witlees. Gaye cote gra^lees. makes
england thriftlees /
ANd the Trinite day next after bygan the contake in the Cy te of york between
the englysshmen / and the Henewers / And in that debate were slain of the
Erldome of Nychol / and mordred lxxx / and after they were buried under a stone
in saint cleme^tz Churcheyerde in Fossegate And for encheson that the Henewers
come to help the king / her pees was cried on pain of life and lymme / And in
that other half it was found by an Enquest of the Cite that the englysshmen
bygonne the debate /

How the englysshmen stopped the scotts in the park of stanhope / and how
they turned ayene in to Scotland / Ca / CC / xiiijo. /
ANd at that time the scotts had assembled al her power / and comen in to
England and slew / and robbed all that they' myghten take, and also brenten
and destroyed all the north cou^ tree through out til that they come to the park
of stanhope in wy redale / and there the scotts held hem in a busshement / But
when the king had herd through certain espyes / where the scotts were anon
right with his host besyeged hem within the foresaid park so that the scotts
wist never where to gone out / but only unto her arms. and they abyden in the
park / xv days / and vytaylles hem faylled in every a side / so that they
were gretely empeyred of her bodies / And sith that brute come first in to
britayne unto this time was never seen so fair an host what of Englysshmen and
of Alyens / and of men a for / the which ordained hem for to fight with the
stottes through eggynge of sir henry earl of lancastre, and of sir Johan henaud
/ that would have goone over the wa ter of with for to have fought with the
scotts / But sir rogyer mortimer consented not thereto / For he had privily
taken mede of the scotts hem for to help that they might we^de again in to
her own cou^treye / And the same mortimer counceyled so much Thomas of
brothertone the earl marchal / that was king edwardes uncle / that the foresaid
thomas should not assemble at that time unto the scotts and he assented, but
he wist not the doing between the scotts / and the foresaid mortimer, And for
encheson that he was marchal of England / and to him perteyned ever the
vauntwarde / he sent hastily to therle of lancastre / and to Sir Johan of
henaud that they should not fight. upon the scotts in prejudice and harmyng of
him / and his fee / and if they did that they should stand to her own peril
/ And the forsaid earl marchal was all arrayed with his battle at the reredoos
of the earl of lancastre / for to have fought with him and with his folk / if
he had meued for to fight with the scotts / and in this manner he was deceived
and wist no thing of this treson / And thus was the king prin cipally deceived
/ And when it was night Mortimer that had the wach for to keep of the host
that night distourbled the wach that no / thing might be done / And in the mean
while the scotts stele by night toward her own country as fast as they might
/ And so was the king falsely bytrayd / that wend that that all the traitors
of his land had be brout to an end as it was said before / Now here ye lords
/ how traytoursly king Edward was desceyued / and how meruailously and boldly
ye scotts did of werre / for James douglas with CC men of arms riden thurugh
out the host of king edward the same night the scotts we re escaped toward hit
own country / as is above said / till that they come to the kings pauylon /
and slew there many me^ in her beds and cried some naward naward and anothir
time a douglas a douglas wherefore the king that was in his pauylon and much
other folk were wonder sore effrayed / but blyssed be almighty god the king
was not taken / and in great peril was tho the royame of england And that
night the moon shone full clear and bright / and for all the kyngesmen the
scotts escaped harmele^s, And in the mo row when the king wist that the
scotts were escaped in to her contre. he was wonder sorry. and full hertely
wept with his yo^g eyes and yet wist he not who him had done that treson / but
that falls tree son was full wely know a good while after as the storye tells
The king edward come again tho to york full sorrowful / and his host departed,
and every man went in to his own country with full heavy chere / and morning
semblau^t / and the henewers took her leave / and went in to her country / and
the king for her trauaylle hem hugely rewarded / and for encheson of that vyage
the king had dispended much of his tresour and wasted / and in that time were
seen two mones in the firmament. that one was clear and that other was derk as
men myt tho seen through out the world / and a great debate was that same time
against pope John the xxij after saint peter. and the emperor of almayn tho made
him emperor against the popes will, that the held his see at auinion / wherefore
the emperor made his cry at rome and ordeygned another pope that hight nycholas
/ that was a friar menour / and that was against the right of holy church /
wherefore ^e was acursid / and the power of that other pope sone was leid / And
for encheson that such merueylles were seen / men said that the world was nygh
at the end /

Of the death of king edward of Carnariuan / Ca / CC / xvo. /
ANd now gone we ayene to sir edward of Carnariuan that was king sometime of
england / and was put down of his dygnyte / Allas for his tribulacion and
sorrow that him byfelle through false counceille that he leued and trust upon
to much that afterward were destroyed through her falsenesse, as God would /
And this Edward of Carnariuan was in the castle of berkeley under the keeping of
sir morys of berkeley and sire Johan of mautreuers / and to hem he made his
compleynt of his sorrow and of his dysese, and oftymes he axed of his wardeyns
/ what he had trespaced ageyst dame Isabel his wife. and sire Edward his son
that was made new king that they would naught vysyte him. Tho ansuerd one of
his wardeyns / My worthy lord dysplese you not / that I shall tell you the
encheson is / for it is done hem to understand that if my lady your wife come
any thing night you / that ye would her strangle and slay / And also that ye
wol de do to my lord your son that same / Tho ansuerd he with simple chere /
Allas allas am I not in prison / and al at your own will / now god it wot I
thought it never / and now I would that I were deed so would god / that I were /
for than were al (...) sorrow passed / Hit was not long after that the king
through co^yl of mortimer granted the ward and keeping of sir edward his fadre
^o sir thomas Toiourney and to the foresaid sir John Mautreuers through the
kings letter and put out holy the forsaid sir moryce of the ward of the king,
and they took and lad the king unto the castle of Corffe / the which castle
the king hated as any death / and they kept him there saufly ^l it come un to
saint mathewes day in septem b^ in the year of gra^ M ccc xxvij that the
forsaid sir rogyer mor timer sent the manner of the death how and in what wise he
should be do ne to death / And anon as the foresaid thomas and Johan had seyn the
letter and commandment they made king edward of carnariua^ good chere and
good solas as they myt at that soper / and nothing the king wist of yt
trecherye / And when time was for to go to bed the king went unto his bed and
lay and slept fast / and as the king lay / and slept / the traitour^ falls
forsworen ay^ns her homage and her feaute comen privily in to the kings
chamber / and her company with hem / and leyden an huge table upon his womb /
and with men presseden and helden fast a down the iiij cornyers of the table
upon his body ^r with the good man a woke and was wonder sore ad^d to be deed
there and slain and turned his body tho vpsodoune / Tho took the false
traitors and as wode tirauntes an horn / and put it in to his fundament as
deep as they myt / and took a spyte of coper bren nyng and put it through the
horn in to his body / and often times ^lled there with his boweles / and so they
slew her lord / that no thing was perceived / and after he was entered at
Gloucestre /

How king edward spoused philip the earls daughter of He naude at york / Cao. /
CC / xvjo. /

aNd after Cristemasse tho next sewyng sir Johan of henaude a brout with him
philip his broders daughter that was earl of henaude his nece in to england /
and king edward spoused her at york with much honor / and sir Johan of
Bothom bishop of ely and sir william of melton archebisshop of york songen the
mass the souday in the eve of conversion of saint paul in the year of grace a
M ccc xxvij / but for encheson that the king was but yo^g and ten dre of age /
when he was crou^ed full many wro^ges were don whi le that his f^dre lived / for
encheson that he trowed the cou^ceilers that were falls about him that
cou^ceilled him to d^ne other wise than reason would / wherefore great harm was do
unto the Reame / and to the king and al me^ directed it the kings deed and it
was not so al myty god wot / wherefore it was ordained at the kings crou^yng
that the king for his tender age should be governed by xij great lords of
england without which no thing should be done that is for to say the
archebisshop of canterbury / the archebisshop of york / The bishop of
wynchestre, and the bishop of herford / the earl of lan castre / the earl
marchal. and the Earl of kent / that were the kings uncles and the earl of
garenne, Sir thomas wake / Sire henry of ^ercy, Sir Olyuer of yngham / and
Johan of Roos Barons And these were sworen trewely for to cou^ceylle the king
/ And they should ansuere every year in the parliament of yt that should be done
i^ the time of that gouernaille / but that ordinance was sone vnd^ne / and
that was much loss and harm to al england / for the king and all the lords
that should govern him were governed and ruled after the kings mother dame
Isabell / and by sir Rogyer Mortimer And as they would al thing was done both
among high and low And they took unto hem Castles tounes lands and rentes in
great harm and loss to the croune and of the kings state out of mesure

How the pees was made between the englysshmen / and the scot tes / and also of
Iustyfyeng of Troylbastone / Cao. / CC / xvijo /
THe king Edward at wytsontyde the second year of his reg ne through counceylle
of his mother / and of sire Rogyer mortymer ordeygned a parliament at northampton
/ at the which parliament the king through her cou^ceil and none other of the
land within age granted to ben acorded with the scotts in this manner / that
all the feautes and homages that the scotts should done unto the croun^ of
england foryaf hem unto the scotts for ever more by his chartre ^nfeled / And
ferthermore an endenture was made of the Scotts unto king Edward that was king
henryes sone / which endenture they callid it rageman / in the which were
contained all the ho mages and feautes / First of the king of Scotland and of all the prelatez Earls and barons of the Reame of Scotland with her seals set
thereon and other chartres / and remembraunces that king Edward and his Barons
had of her right in the reame of scotland it was foryeue hem ayene holy church
/ And also with the black cross of scotland. the which the good king Edward
co^ querd in scotland / and brought it out of the Abbay af Scone / that is a
full precious relyque, And also ferthermore he relesed and foryaf all the lands
that the barons of England had in scot land by, old conquest / And this pees
for to hold and last the scot tes were bound unto the king in xxx thousand
pound of silver to be paid within iij year / that is to say every year x
thousand pound by even porcyons / And ferthermore above all this they speak
bitwene the parties above said that dauyd dritonantier that was Robert the Brus
is sone the false tirant and traitor. and falls forswore against his oath that
arose against his lyege lord the noble king Edward, and falsely made him king
of Scotland. that was of age of v year / And so through this cursed counseyll
David spoused at Berewyk dame Johan of the tour that was king Edwardys suster
as the g^est tellyth upon mary magdale ne day in the year of grace a M CCC and
xxviij to greet harm and empeyryng to all the kings blood / whereof that
gentil lady came / Allas the time / For wonder much was that fair damysel
dysparaged since that she was married against all the comune assent of England /
And fro the time that Brute had conquered albion and named the land after his
own name Britayne / that now is called England after the name of Engyst /

And so was the Reame of Scotland holden of the Reame of England and of the
croune by feaute and by homage /

For Brute conquered that land / and yafe it to Albanak his second sone. And he
callid the land Albanye after his own name / So that the heirs that comen
after him helden of Brute / and of his heirs the kings of Britayne by feaute
and homage and from that time unto this king Edward the reame of Scotland was
holden of the reame of England by feautes and seruy^s a boue said as the
Chronicles of england and of Scotland beren wit nesse more plenarly / And
acursed be the time that this parliament was ordained at Northampton / For there
through falls cou^ceil the king was there falsely disheryted / and yet he was
within age /

And yet when king Edward was put a down of his Royalte of england / yet men
put him not out of the feautes / and ser uyces of the reame of Scotland / ne of
the fraunchises disheryted him for evermore. And netheles the great lords of
England were against to conferme the pees / and the trewes above said sauf only
the queen Isabel that was the kings mother edward and the bishop of Ely / and
lord mortimer, but reason and law would not that a fynal pees should be made
between hem without the commune assent of England /

Of the debate that was between queen Isabell / and sir Henry Earl of lancastre
and of leycestre / and of the ridynge of ^edeford / Cao. / CC / xvijo. /
When the foresaid dauyd had spoused Dame Jane of the tour in the town of
Berwyk as before is said the scotts in despyte of the Englysshmen called dame
Jane the Countess make pees / For the cowardo^ pees that was ordained but the
kings person bare the wy^e and the blame with wrong of the making of the
acord / and all was done through the Queen and Rogyer mortimer / And it was not
long aft^r that the Queen Isabell ne took in to her own hand all the lordship
of pountfret almoost all the lands that were of value that apperteyned to the
croune of england / So that the king had not for to dyspende / but of his uses
and of his escheker / For the queen Isabelle and mortimer had a greet meyne
of her ^naunce that followed evermore the kings court, and went and took the
kings prises for her penny worthes at good chepe, wherefore the country that they
comen in were full sore adradde / and almost^ destroyed / Tho bygon the
Comynalte of England for to ^ate Isabell the Queen that so much loved her.
when she come ayene for to pursue the false traitors the spencers fro France /

And that same time the false traitor Robert of Holond that bitrayd his lord
Sir Thomas of lancastre was tho deliuerd out of prison / and was wonder prive
with the Queen Isabelle and also with Rogyer the Mortimer, But that auayled him
but litel for he was take at mychelmasse that tho come n^ sewing after as he
rode toward the queen Isabell to london and sir thomas wither smote of his head
besides the town of saint albones / And this Sir thomas duellid tho with Sir
Henry earl of lancastre and he put him in hydyng for dread of the queen / for
she loved him wonder much and prayed unto the king for him that the same
Thomas must ben exyled out of england / And the Noble Earl Sir Henry lancastre
had oftymes herd the commune cla mour of the englysshmen of the dyseses that
were done in england and also for diverse wrongs that were done among the
comune people of the which the king bare the blame with wrong / for he ^as but
full young and tender of age / and thought as a good man for to done awey and
slake the sklaundre of the kings person if that he might in any manner wise /
So as the king was thereof no thing gylty / wherefore he was in peril of lyth and
lymme And so he assembled al his retenaunces / and went and spoke unto them of
the kings honor / and also for to amend his astate And Sir thomas brotherton
Earl marchal and Sir Edmond of wodestoke that were the kings uncles, and also
men of london made her oath him for to mayntene in that same quarelle.

And her cause was this that the king should hold his household and his meyny as
a king ought for to done and have also his rialte / And that the queen Isabell
should deliver out of her hond in to the kings hand al manner lordshippes
rentes tounes and Castelles that apperteyned to the croune of England as other
Que nes had done before her and meddle with none other thing /

And also that Sire Rog^er mortymer should duelle upon his own lands / for the
which lands he had help disheryte much pe ple / So that comune people were not
destroyed through her wrong full taking / And also to enquere how and by whom
the king was bytrayd and falsely desceyued at Stanhope / and through whose
counceylle that the Scotts went awey by night from the king, And also how and
through whoos counseyll the ordinance that was made at the kings coronacion
was put a down that is for to say that the king for amendment and helpyng of
the Reamme / and in honor of him should be governed and ruled by xij the
grettest and wysest lords of all the Reame and without hem should nothing be
granted / ne done as fore is said the which couenau^ts malyaously were put a
done fro the king wherefore many harms shames and reproues have fall unto the
king and his Reame. And that is understand for as much as Edward sometime king
of England was ordained by assent of the comynalte in plain parliament for to be
under the ward / and governance of Henry Earl of lancastre his cosyn for
sauacion of his body. he was take out of the castle of kenel worth there that he
was in ward / And through color of queen Isabell and of the Mortimer without
consent of any parliament they took and lad him there that never after none of
his kynrede might with him spe^e ne see / and after traytoursly took and him
mordred / For whoos death a foul sklaundre aroos through out al Crystendom when
it was done / And also the Tresour that sir edward of Carnariuan had left in
many places in england and in walye were wasted and bare awey without the
will of king Edward his son in destruction of him and of all his folk /
Also through whose counceyll that the king yaf up the kingdom of Scotlad For the
Which Reame the kings auncestres had full sore y trauaylled / and so did many
a noble man for her right / and was dely uerd unto David / that was Robert the
Brus son all the right that no right had to the Reame as all the world it
wyst^ / And also by whom the chartres and remembraunces that they had (...)
the right of scotland were take out of the tresorye and taken un to the
Scotts the kings enemies to dysherytyng of him and of his successors and to
great harm unto his lyea^s and great (...) prove unto al Englysshmen for
evermore / Also where for dame ^a ne of the tour the kings suster edward was
dysparaged and married unto David / that was Robert the Brus sone that was a
traitor and enemy unto England / And through whose counceille she was take in
to our enemies hondes out of England /

And in the mean time while the good Earl Henry of lancastre and his company
token counseylle how these (...) above said might ben amended unto the worship
of the king and to his profit, and to the profit also of his lyeges / The
(...) Isabel through coniectyng and subtylyte / and also of the Mortimer let
ordeyne a parliament at Salysbury. And at that same ^arleme^t the Mortimer was
made earl of the march against all the barons will of England in preiudyce of
the king and of his Coroune / And Sire Johan of Eltham the kings brother was
gurt with aswerd of Cornewayle and tho was called Earl of Curnewall And
evermore Queen Isabel so much procured a^ste her sone the king. that she had
the ward of the foresaid sir Edward and of his lands, And at that parliament
therle of of Lancastre would not come / but ordained al his power ayens the
queen Isabel / and the mortimer / and men of london ordained hem with v C men
of arms / when queen Isabell wist of the doing / she swore by god and by his
names full angrely / that in evil time he thout upon tho points / Tho sent
the queen Isabell and the mortymer after her retenue. and after the kings
retenue / so that they had ordained among hem an huge host / and they
counceyled the king / so that upon a night they rydden xxiiij mile toward
Bedford there that the Earl of lancastre was with his company / and thought to
have him destroyed / and that night she rode besides the king her sone as a
knight armed for dread of death / and it was done the king to understand that
the earl henry of lancastre and his company would have destroyed the king and
his counceyll for evermore / wherefore the king was somdele toward him heavy and
annoyed / when the Earl marchal / and the Earl of kent the kings brother herd
of this tydyng / they ryden so in message between hem that the king granted
him his pees to earl henry of lancaster for a certain raunsone of xj M pound /
but that was never paid afterward /

And these were the lords that held with sir henry of Lancastre / Sir henry
Beaumout. Sir fouke fitz waren / sir thomas rocelyn / Sire william Trussel, Sir
thomas wither / and about an honderd knights more that were to him consentyng
/ and all tho were exyled through counseyll of queen Isabell and of the
Mortymer. for the mortimer weyted for to have her lands if that he myt thu^gh
any manner coniectyng / for he was to covetous / and had to much his will /
and that was great pity /

How king Edward went over the sea for to do his homage un to the king of
france for the duchye of guyhenne / Cao / CC xix
IT was not long after that the king of france through counceylle of his
douzepyers sent to king Edward of England that he should come to Paris / and
done his homage as reason it would for the duchye of guyhenne / And so through
counceylle of the lords of england king Edward went over the sea and at
asce^cion tide he come unto paris the iij year of his regne for to do his
homage unto the king of france. and the king vnderfenge his homage and made of
him much joy and worship / but when king edward had made his homage, hastily
he was sent fore in to england thurugh the queen Isabell his mother / and anon
hastily he come ageyn in to England upon wythsonday without any taking leave of
the king of france / wherefore he was wonder wroth /

How sir rogyer mortimer bare him proudly and so hye / cao. cc xx
ANd now shall ye here of Sir rogyer mortimer of wygmore that destroyed and
coueyted to be at an hye astate. so that the king granted him to be called
earl of the march through out all his lordship / And he bycome so proud and
so hauteyne that he would lose and forsake the name that his au^cestres had ever
before And for that encheson he let him call earl of the march and none of
the comunes of england durst call him by none other name for he was called so
through the kings cry that men should, call him earl of the march / and the
Mortimer bare him tho so hauteyn and so proud that wonder it was for to wit /
and also disgised him with wonder rich clothes out of al manner reason both of
shapyng and of we ryng wherefore the englisshmen had great wonder how and in what
ma ner he might contreue or find such manner pride / and they said amo^ ges
hem al comunely that his pride should not long endure / And the same time sir
geffroy mortymer the young that was the Morti mers sone let call him king of
folly / and so it befell afterward in deed for he was so full of pride and of
wretchedness yt he held a rou^ de table in walys to al men that thider would
come and cou^trefece the manner and the doing of king arthures table / but
openly he f^ssed For the noble king arthur was the most worthy lord of reno^me
that was in all the world in his time / and yet come never none such after / for all the noble knights in crystendom of deed of arms a losed duellyd with king
arthur / and held him for her lord / and that was well seyn / for he co^querd
in battle a romayn that was call led Frolle / and get of him the reame of
france / and slew him with his hou^des / And also he fought with a geant that
was called die nabus and slew him that had rauysshed fair Eleyne that was king
hoeles ne^ king of little Britayne / And afterward he slew in bataill the
emperor of rome that was callid lucye that had assembled against king arthur
for to fight with him so much people of romans and phehyts and of sarazyns yt
no man could hem no^ bre / and he discomfited hem all as the story of him
tellyth / and in the same time comune loos sprung in england thurg comectyng /
and or dynau^ce of the friar prechours that fire Edward of Carnariuan that was
king edwardes fadre of whom the gest tellith saiden yt he was alive in the
castle of Corf / wherefore all the comunes al most of england were in sorrow and
in dread whether that it were so or not / For they wyste not how traytoursly
the mortimer had him done mordred /

How Edmond of wodestoke that was earl of kent / and the kings brother Edward
of Carnariuan was byheded at wynchestre Capitulo CC xxjo. /
ANd upon a time it byfel so that sir Edmond of wodestoke Earl of kent spoke
unto the pope Johan the xxij of Auynyon and said that almighty god had softymes
done for thomas love of lancastre many great miracles to many men and women
that were through diverse maladyes undone as unto the world and through his
prayer they were brought unto her hele / And so Sir Edmond prayed the pope
hertely that he would grant him grace yt the forsaid thomas myt be translated,
but the pope said nay that he should not be translated unto the time that he
were better certifyed of ye clergy of england and seyn by her obedyence what
thing god had done for the love of thomas of lancaster after the suggestyon yt
the foresaid Edmond earl of kent had unto him y made / And when this edmond saw
that he might not speed of his purpose as touching the translacio^ / he praid
him of his cou^ceil as touching sir edward of Carnariuan his brother / and said
that not long agone he was king of england what thing mit best be done as
touching his deliuerau^ce since that a comune fame is through england that he is
in lif and hole and sauf / when the pope herd him all that Sir edward was
alive / he commanded the earl upon his beneson that he should help with all the
power that he might that he were deliud out of prison / and save his body in all
manner that he myt / and for to bring this thing to an end he assoilled him
and his company a pena and culpa / and al tho that help to his delyuerau^ce /
Tho took Edmond of wodestok his leave of the pope / and come ayene in to england
/ and when sir Edmond was come / some of the Friar prechours come and said that
sir edward his brother yet was alive in the castle of corf under the keeping of
sir thomas gurnay / Tho sped him the forsaid edmond as fast as he might til
that he come unto the Castle of Corffe / and acqueynted / and spak so fair
with Johan Dauerill that was Conestable of the same castle / and yafe him rich
yeftes for to have acquaintance of him / and to know of his cou^ceyl / And
thus it byfel that the foresaid Sir edmond prayed specially to tell him privily
of his lord his brother Sir edward if that he lived or were deed / and if he
were alive he prayed of him ones to have a sight / And this Sir Johan Dauerill
was an high herted man and full of courage and ansuerd shortly unto sir Edmond
and said that sir edward his brother was in hele / and under his keeping / and
durst show him unto no man / since it was defended him in the kings half
edward that was edwardes sone of car narinan / and also through comau^dement of
queen Isabel the kings mother / and of sir rogyer the mortimer yt he should
show his body un to no manner man of the world sauf only unto hem upon loss of
life and lymme / and to disheryteson of his heirs for evermore / but the false
traitor falsely lied for he was not in his ward. but he was take thens and lad
unto the castle of berklee through Sir Thomas gurnay through comau^dement of the
mortimer til that he was deed as before is said, but sir edmond of wodestok
wist nothing that Edward his brother was deed. whereupon he took a lre^ unto the
foresaid sir Johan / and praid him hertely that he would take it unto king
edward his brother / as to his worthy lord / And be vnderfeng the lre^ of him
and behit him for to done his message without any manner faill / and with that
sir edmond took of him his leave then of the foresaid John / and went tho in to
his own country and lordship in kent that he had there / And anon as this same
John wise that sir edmond was gone in to kent his own lordship, anon he went
in all the have that he myt fro the castle of Corfe / and come unto sire Rogyer
the mortimer / and took him the lre^ that sir edmond of wode stok earl of kent
had take him closed / and enseled with his own seal / And when sir rogyer had
vnderfong the letter he unclosed the lre^. and saw what was contained therein /
and began it for to read / where of the beginning was this / worshippes and
reuerences with brothers legeaunce and subjection / Sire knight worshipful and
dear brother if it you plese / I pray you hertely that ye be of good comfort /
for I shall so ordeyne for you that sone ye shall come out of prison and be
delyuerd of that dysese that ye ben in / and vndersto^deth of your great
lordship that I have to me assentau^t al most all the great lords of england
with all her apparayll / that is to say with armure with tresour without nombre
for to mayntene and help your quarrel / so forsooth that ye shall be king ayene
as ye were be fore / and that they al have swore to me upon a book / and as well
prelates as Earls and Barons / when Sir Rogrer the Mortymer saw and understood
the might and the strength of the letter / anon for wrath his heart began holle
/ and evil heart bare toward Sire Edmond of wodestok that was Earl of kent, and
so with all the haste that he might / he went to Dame Isabelle the queen that
was the kings mother and showed her Sir Edmu^des letter and his will and his
purpoose / and how he had conice ted and ordained to put a down king edward of
wyndesore her sone of ryal^ and of his kingdom / Now (...) sir rogyer quod the
queen has sir edmond done so / by my fadres soul quod ^he (...) will be the^f
auengyd if that god grant me life / and that in a short time / And anon with
that the queen Isabel went unto king edward her sone, there that he was at the
parliament at wyn chestre for to have amended the wrongs and trespaces that
were done among the people in his royame / And tho took she and she wed him the
letter that sir Edmond of wodestok Earl of kent had made and ensealed with his
own seal / and bad upon her beneson that he should be auengyd upon him, as upon
his dedly enemy /

Tho was the queen so wroth toward Sir Edmond Earl of kente / and ^sid never
to pray until her sone til that he had sent in all have after him / And upon
that the king sent by his lettres after Sir edmond of wodestok that he should
come and speak with him at wynchestre al manner thing left. And when Sir Edmond
saw that the king sent after him with his lre^s ens^led he ^asted him in all
that he myt / til that he come to wynchestre / but tho the Queen wyste that sir
Edmond was come unto wynchestre / anon she prayed and so fast went unto king
Edward her sone that the good earl was aws^yd anon / and led unto the bar
before. Robert of Hamond / that was cowner of the kings house ho^d / and he
assocyed unto him Sir Rogyer the mortimer / and tho spoke the foresaid Robert
and said / Sir Edmond Earl of kente ye shall understood that it is done us to
wit* and principally unto our lyege lord sir Edward king of england that
almyty god save and keep that ye (...) his dedely enemy and traitor / and
also a comune enemy unto the r^ame / and that ye have been about many a day for
to make pre^y delyuerau^ce of Sir edward sometime king of england your brother /
the which was put a down of his (...) al^ by ^mune asse^t of all the lords of
england in pesyng of our lord the kings astate / and also of his reame / Tho
ansuerd the good man and said / forsooth sir understands well that I was never
traitor to my king ne to the reame / and that I do me on god and on all the
world / and ferthermore by my kings leave I shall preue it and defend as a man
ought to do / Tho said Mortimer Sir Edmond it is so forsothe y know that it
may not well ben gayn said / and that in presence of all that here ben it shall
well ben proved / Now had this fal^ mortimer the same letter that sir Edmond
had take to sir Johan dauerell in the castle of corff for to take unto king
Edward his brother that sir Edmond wist not of ne supposed no nothing that sir
Johan dauerel had be so falls to deliver his l^ in such wise to the mortimer and
thout no manner thing of that letter and said to sir edmond and showed a letter
se^d and axid him if he knew that letter and the seal / This sir Edmond looked
thereon and auised him long on the prynt of the seal / for he myt not see the
let ter within forth what was therein / and wiste well that it was his seal / and
thought that it had be some letter that had bore no great charge / and thought
nothing of that other letter / and said openly in heryng of hem al ye forsooth
this is my seal I will it not forsake ^o quod the mortimer sirs ye heren all
what he has said and that he knoulecheth that this is his letter and his seal
/ and now ye shall here al what is contained therein / And than this mortym^
opened the letter that he had folden a fore to geder / and red it open ly word
by word in heryng of hem all / and when the letter was red ^e said lo si^s ye
have herd al what is here w^n / and that ye has knoulecheth that this is his
letter / and his seal / and may not go there from / And than they al cried and
yafe dome that he should be honged and draw / and his heed smite of in manner
of a traitor / and he and his heirs dysheryted for evermore* and so he was
ladde forth and put in to prison / And when this was done and the queen wyste
that he was dampened by wey of law both of life and lymme and his heirs

thought that were good that the foresaid Sir Edmond were hastily y slain

death / and than that should torn hem to much sorrow so as he was empeched / And
anon the queen through counceylle of the mortimer and without any other

sir edmo^des heed of wodestoke earl of kente vithoute any manner abydyng or
respyte up pain of life and lymme / and that he should have none other execucion
by cause of ^ryeng not withsto^dyng the judgment Tho token the baillif^ sir
Edmond out of prison and sad hem besi* des the castle of wynchestre / and
there they made a gongfermer smite of his head / for none other man durst it
done* and so dyed he there Allas the time that is to say the x day of Octo^ the
(...) of king Edwardes regne / and when the king wys^ thereof he was wonder
