Of the death of sir Rogyer mortimer earl of the march. Capitulo / CCo. /
xxijo. /
ANd so it be fell at that time that sir Rogyer Mortymer Earl of the march was
so proud and so hauteyne that he held no lord of the Reamme his pere. and tho
become he so covetous that he followed Dame Isabell the Qnenes court / that was
king Edwardes mother and beset his penny worthes with the officers of the que nes
household in ye same manner that the kings officers did and so he made his
taking as touching vitails and also of caryages / and al he did for cause of
spences and for to gadre tresour / and so he did without no^bre in all that he
might. Tho made he him wonder prive with the queen ^abel / and so much lordship
and retenue had / so yt all the gre te lords of england of him were adr^d,
wherefore the king and his co^ ceyl toward him were agreued and ordained among
hem to undo him through pure reason and law for cause that king edward that was
the kings fadre traitoursly through him was mordred in the castle of berklee as
bifere is said more plenarly in the CC xvij chapter of this book / And some
that were of the kings cou^ceil loved the mortimer and told him in priuete how
that the king and his cou^ceyl were about from day to day him for to shend and
undone where for the mortimer was sore a^noyed and angry as the devil against hem
that were of the kings cou^ceyl and said that he would on hem ben auengyd / how
so ever he took on / ^it was not long after ward that king edward and dame
phelip his wife and dame Isabel the kings mother and sir Rogyer the mortimer ne
went unto no tyngham there for to soiourne / and so it byfell that the queen
Isabel through counsel of the mortimer took to her the keys of the yates of
the castle of Notyngham / so that no man might come nether in ne out by night
but through commandment of the mortymer ne the king ne none of his cou^seyl /
And that time it byfel so that the mortimer as a devil for wrath bolled / and
also for wrath that he had against the kings men edward / and principally
against hem that had him accused to the king of the death of sir edward his fadre
/ And privily a cou^ceylle was take between queen Isabel / and the Mortimer and
the bishop of lyncoln / and s^r Symond of Bereford and sir hugh of Trumpyngton
/ and other prive of her cou^ceyl for to undone hem all that had accusid the
mortimer unto the king of his fadres death of treson and of felonye / wherefore al
tho that were of the kings cou^ceyl when they wist of the mortimers castyng
pre uely come to king edward, and seyde that the mortimer would hem de stroye
for cause that they had accused him of king edwardes death his fadre and prayed
him that he would mayntene hem in her right And these were the lords to pursue
this quarelle / Sire william mountagu / Sir hu^frey de boghun. Sir william his
brother / Sire Rauf of stafford, Sir robert of herford / sir william of clyn^n
Sir Johan neuyl of horneby, and many other of her consent, and all these sworen
upon the book to maynten the quarrel in as much as they might / And it byfell
so af^r / that sir william mou^tagu ne none of the kings friends must not ben
herburg^ed in the Ca stel for the mortimer. but went and took her lodgyng in
diverse places in the town of notyngham / And tho were they sore adrad lest
that the mortimer should hem destroy. and in have there come un to king edward
Sir william mountagu / there that he was in the castle / and privily told him
that he ne none of his company should not take the mortimer without cou^ceyl
and help of william of ela^d Constable of the same castle / Now certes quoth the
king I leave yew well / and therefore I counceyll you that ye go^ to the foresaid
(...) ble and commau^de him in my name that he be your friend. and your help
for to take the mortimer al thing y left upon peril of (...) / and lymme / Tho
said mountagu / Sir my lord grant mercy / (...) went forth the foresaid
mountagu and come to the Conestable of the castle / and told him the kings
will / And he ansuerd and said that the kings w^l should be done in as much as
he might and that he would not spare for no manner death / and so he swore and
made his oath / Tho said Sir william mountagu to the Conestab^e in ^erynge of
al men that were helping unto the quarrel / Now certes dear friend us behooves
for to worche / and do by your ^yntise fo: to take the mortimer since that ye be
kepar of the castle / and have the keys in your ward / sir quoth the conestable /
will ye understood that the gates of the castle ben lokked with the lokkes that
dame ^abel sent hidder / and by night she has the keys thereof and lei^ hem
under the leuesell of the led unto the morrow, and so ye may not come in to the
castle by the yates in no manner wise / but I know an Aley that stretches out
of the ward under the earth in to the foresaid castle / that gothe in to the
weste which A^y da^e Isabel the queen / ne none of her men, ne the mortimer ne
none of his company knows it not / And so I shall feed you through that
Aley / and so ye shall come in to the Castle without aspyes of any man that been
your enemies / And the same night sir william mountagu / and all the lords of
his quarelle / and the same conestable also went hem to horse / and maden
semblaunt as it were for to wend out of the mortimers syghte /

But anon as the mortimer herd this tidyng he went that they would have gone
over the sea for dread of him / and anon he and his company token cou^seill
among hem for to let her passage and sent lre^s anon to the ports / so that
none of the great lords should wend home to her own country / but if they
were arested and take

And among other things william Eland Constable of the foresaid castle privily

Sire Symond of Bereford was lad with him / and was take to the Conestable of

before the king and before all the great lords of england for peril that might
fall to the Reame / and to enquere also which were assentyng to sir edwardes
death the kings fadre / and also through whom the scot^es escaped from stanhope
in to scotland without the will of king Edward / And also how the chartre of

were contained that the scotts should d^ne evermore unto the kings of england
for the reame of scotland / wherefore in his abse^ce he was dampened to be draw
and honged for his treson / and this me schyef come unto him on saint andrews
even (...) the year of Incarnacion of our lord Ihu crist a thousand CCC / xxx /

How king Edward get again unto him gracyously the ho mages and feautes of

^Owe ye have herd lords how sir Johan of Bayllol in time of pees was chosen

/ and put him over the sea unto Dunpier / and lived there upon his own lands

and trespace / and lad with him Sir Edward his son / whe^fore the Scotts in

and so he went his wey and come in to England without any harm / And when the

al his lands Tho duellyd Sir edward in prison unto the time that sir henry of

/ And anon as he was out of prison sir henry took him forth with him / and lad

h^rde tell how that sir Edward was privily come in to scotlond and come to him

Tho come Sir Henry of Beaumont to king edward of England / and prayed him in

upon this covenant granted her bone as touching him and tho that were of the

Scotland And these were the names of the lords that pursueden this ma ter /

But sir Edward Bayllol and his company there him dyscomfyded / at the which

Tho come sir edward Bayllol. and took the countray all about him till he come
unto the abbay of Dunfermelyne / and there be found vytaylles for him and for
his folk and among al other things he fond in a chamber about v honderd of

delyuerd hem to the most strengest men of his company / And anon after he
went fro thens, and lodged him in a field ij mile from saint Johannes town
and when the burgeis of the tonne herd how the Earl of Fyffe was discomfyted
through the Bayllol they were sore adrad and breken their brydges that they had
made over the water of Erue / so that the bayllol might not gone over wherefore
he lodged him there all that night / but litel head he took of rest / and said
unto his people / Now dear lords ye know full well, that we be now y lodged
between our enemies / And if they mow us hampre / there is no bote but death
wherefore if we abide here all this night stylle / I leave that it shall torn us
to much sorrow and harm / For the power of Scotland may every day weye and
increase / and we may not so done / And we ben but little people as against hem.
wherefore I pray you for the love of Almighty god make we us bold and hardy and
that we may myghtely take the scotts this night and boldly werre upon hem
and let us pursue hem this night, and if they be trauaylled through us / and
they see our hardynesse / so that other Scotts that comen and mete hem and see
hem so trauaylled and weary / the sorer will they be adrad with us for to fight.
and fiersly than we shall fight with hem / and upon hem pursue / so that through
the grace of God Amyghty all the world shall speak of the doughtnes of our
Chyualrye /

And sirs understands well that all the company that comen with sir Edward
bayllol granted well unto that counceyll / and were there of glad / and anon
pursued upon the Scotts / that they byco me wonder weary. And the Bayllol and
his company sore followed hem / and did hem much sorrow through her assaute / so
that they might not for feeble hem help and for little people / but tho said the
Scotts among hem what is now byfal / that so li cell a people. as the bayllol
has in wynge / done us so much traua ylle and sorrow / Now certes it seems
us, that he worcheth by grace / for he is wonder gracious in his quarrel / and
al we certes shall ben deed or that we may come to him us for to yield since that
his fadre set of us no prys And among all other things the Bayllol, and his
people passed the water of Erue / so that sire Rogyer of Swynerton the sone was
fyers and angry. and went forth / and they saw people of arms full well arrayed /
and forth they went un to hem, and with hem foughten / and slew as many as

geder / and rested hem a whrle But the while that the Eglysshmen rested hem the

in the best man as they myt

And tho pursued hem sir edward bayllol and his men and slew of hem til that

Tho made the bayllol his men that were wounded gone to ship for to we^de in

When this thing was know through scotland / how that the lords and knights

And king edward of England and edward king of Scotland had well apparaylled her

yet the scotts had well v men against one Englysshman. And that bataylle Was

were slain of the scotts xxxv M / vij / C / xij / And of Englisshmen but only
xiiij / and tho were fotemen / And this vyctorye byfell to the englissh men on

xxxij / And while this doing last the englyssh pages took the pylfre / of the

any man / And so after this gracious vyctorye the king turned him ayene unto
the same syege of Berewik / and when they besieged saw and herd how king
edward had sped they yolden to him the tou ne with the castle on the morrow
after that the battle was done that is for to say on saint margarets day / And

And in the same year through out all England about Saint Clements tide in

of the sea / and also of fressh rivers and sprynges that yt see brinkes walls
and costs brek^ up yt men beestes and houses in many places / and namely in

^eluet / or damask* Satyn / Baudekyn / ne none such other ne none wild ware /

/ In the xiij year of his regne king edward went over see in to braban with

we re put forth and promote as touching the kingdom of France / For which

gadred unto him a great host. and destroyed there in his parties and kingdom

where for king edward when he herd these tidings was strong ly meuyd / and

/ In the same time the king through counceyll of his true lyeges. and

How king edward come to the seluys / and discomfyted all the power of france
in the haven / Ca^ / CC^ / xxv^ /
ANd the next year after / that is for to say the xv year of his regne / he

sorcery and nygromancye of (...) france. wherefore the kings heart was full of

O blissed lady saint marye what is the cause that evermore going in to france
all things and wethers fallen to me Joyful and lykyng and gladsum / and as I
would have hem. but alwey tornyng in to England ward all things fallen

How king Edward sailed in to Normandye and arrived at hogs with a great
host / Ca^ / CC^ / xxvij /
IN the xxj year of his regne king edward through counceylle of all the great
lords of the Royame of England called and gadred to gedre in his parliament at
westmestre before estren ordained him for to pass over the sea ayene for to
dis sese and destrouble the rebels of france / And when his nauye was come
to geder / and made ready / he went with an huge host the xij day of Iuyll /
and saylled in to normandy / and arrived at hogs / And when he had rested him
there vj days for by cause of trauaylyng of the sea / and for to have out al
his men with all her necessaryes out of her ships / he went toward cadomum
bre^nyng wastyng and destroyeng all the tounes / that he found in his way And
the xxvj day of Iuyll at the bridge of Cadony manly / and orpedly y strengthed
and defended with nor^a^s. he had there a strong battle / and a long during
through which a great multitude of people were slain / And there were take
prisonners / the Earl of ewe / the lord of Tankeruylle / and an C other
knights and men of arms / and vj C footmen y nombred / and the town and the
subarbes unto the bar walls of al thing that might be bore and carried out
was robled and despoylled / Afterward the king passing forth by the country
about the bread of xx mile he wasted al manner thing yt he fond / when phelyp
of valoys parceyued all this al though he were fast by with a strong host he
would not come / no nerre but break all the bridges by yonde the water of seyne
fro Rone unto paris. And him self fled unto the same cite of paris with all
the have that he might / Forsooth the noble king edward when he come to paris
bridge and fond it broken within ij days / be let make it again / And in
the morrow after the assumpcion of our lady king edward passed over the water of
seyne going toward Crescy / and destroyed by the way tounes with the people
duellyng there in / And in the fest of saint bartholomew he passed over the
water of sum unhurt with all his host there as never before hand was any
manner way ne passage where ij (...) were slain of hem that let her passage
over / therefore the xxvj day of August king Edward in a field fast by crescy
having iij batayls of en glisshmen countred and met with philip of valoys
having with him iiij bataylles / of which the leest passed gretely the no^bre
of the english people / And when these two hosts metten to gedre / there fylle
upon him the king of beme the duke of loreyne / And Earls also of flaundres
Dalaunson Blois Harecourt / Aumar le and neuers / and many other earls / Barons
lords / knights / and men of Arms the nombre of a (...) v C xlij without
footmen and other men y armed that were nothing rekened /

And for all this the vngloryous ^hilippe withdrowe him with the resydue of
his people / wherefore it was said in comu ne among his own people / N^e (...) soy
retreyt / that is for to say our fair withdrawith him / Than king Edward and
our Englysshmen thanked god almighty for such a vyctorye after her great
labor token to hem al thing needful to her sustenannce / and saving of her
life for dread of her enemies / rested hem there. and full erly in the morning
after the Frensshmen with an huge pas sing host come ayene for to give battle
/ and fight with the englysshmen / with whom metten and cou^treden the earls
of warrewyke / Northampton and norfolk / with her company. and slowen two
thousand and token many prisoners of the gentiles of hem / And the remenaunt of
the same host fled three mile thens / And the third day after the batayl the
king went to Caleys ward destroyeng all the country as he rode whydder when
that he was come that is for to say the thyrdde day of septembre he began to
besiege the town with the castle / and continued his syege fro the foresaid
third day of September unto the third day of auguste / the next year after /
And in the same year during the siege of Caleys the king of Scotland with a
full great multitude of Scotts come in to england to Neuilles cross about
saint lucas day the euangelyst hopyng and trustyng to have found all the lo^d
destytute. and void of people / for as much as the king of england was beyond

and plo wmen / and such other laborers And there they robbeden and dyden much
prive sorrow / but yet fou^ de they ynow that hem wythstode by the grace of

And so a day of battle was assygned between hem and certain lords and men

Cite of duresme / at which day through the grace and help of almighty god the
scotts were over comen / and yet were they iij fold so many of hem as of

How king edward besyeged Caleys / and how it was y wonn^ and yolde to him /
Cao. / CC / xxviijo. /
IN the xxij year of king edwardes regne / he went over the sea in the winter
time / and lay all the winter at ye siege of Caleys / the which year the while
the siege lasted phelip the king of France cast and purposed trechouresly and
with fraud to put awey the siege and come the xxvij day of Iuyll in the same
ye re with a great host and a strong power and neyghed unto the siege of
caleys / the which phelyp the last day of Iuyl sent to king ed ward word that
he would give him plain battle the iij day next after that about euensong time
if he durst come fro the siege and abide it / and when king edward herd yt
without any long taryeng er long auyseme^t he accepted gladly the day and hour
of battle that phelyp had assigned / And when the king of france herd that
the next nyt after he set his tents a fire and remeued and went awey^ thens
cowardly / Than they that were in the town and in the castle besieged seeing all this how that they had none other help ne so cour of the king of france ne of
his men / And also that her vyta ylles within hem were spended and wasted and
for defaute of vytaylles and of refresshynge they eten horse hou^des cattes and
myse for to keep her troth as long as they might / And when they saw and was
found among hem at last that they had no thing among hem for to ete ne
live by / ne none socour / ne rescu enge of the frensshmen of that other side /
they wist well that they must needs dye for defaute or else yield the town /
and anon they wenten and token down the Baners and the arms of France on
every side that were honged out and wenten un to the walls of the town on
diverse places as naked as they were borne / sauf only her shyrtes and breches
/ and held her swerdes naked and the point dounward in her hondes / and putten
ropes / and halters about her nekkes and yelden up the keys of the town* and
of the Castle to king Edward of England with greet fere and dread of heart /
And when king Edward saw this / as a mercyable king and lord resseyued al to
grace and a few of the grettest persons of state and of governance of the
tou ne he sent in to England there to abide her rau^so^e / and the kyn ges
grace / And all the comynalte of the town the king let gone whider they would
in pees / and without any harm. and let hem ^ere with hem all her things
that they might here and carye awey keeping the town and the castle to him
self / Than through medyacion of Cardynals that were sent fro the pope trewes
was take there byt wene France and England for nine months than next
folewyng* and about mychelmasse king Edward come again in to England with a
glorious vyctorye / And in the xxiij year of his regne in the eest parties of
the world there aroos and bygan a pestylence and death of sarazeyns / and paynyms
that so great a death was never herd before. And that wasted awey so the people
/ that uneaths the tenthe person was left alive* And in the same year about
the south count^es and also in the west countries there fill so much rain /
and so great wa tres that from Crystemasse unto mydsomer there was uneaths day
ne nyt / but that it rayned somewhat / through which watres the pestylence was
so enfected* and so habundau^t in all countries and namely about the court of
Rome and other places and see costs / that uneath there were left living folk
to burye hem that were deed honestly / But maden great dyches and pyttes that
were wonder broad and deep / and therein buried hem* and maden a renge of deed
bodies* and cast a little earth to hele hem above / and than cast in another
renge of deed bodies / and another renge of ^th above hem / And thus were they
buried / and none other wise / But if it were the fewer that weren great men of
astate / that weren buried as honestly as they might / And after all this in the
xxiiij year of king Edwardes regne / hit was him to done to wit and
understand of a treson that was be gonne at Caleys / and ordained for to self
that town for a great sum of floreyns unto king phelyp of France through the
falsenesse and ordinance of a knight that was called Sir geffrey of Charney
that was wonder prive with the king phelip of Frau^ ce And when king Edward
herd this* he took with him the nobles and gentiles lords / and many other
worthy and orpe^ men of Arms that were there present with him for the solempny
te of that high fest. And well and wisely in all the have that he might / and
as privily / as he might / he went over see /

And that same year the good king Edward held his Cristemasse at bauerynge.
And the morrow after new years day the king was in the castle of Caleys with
his men of Arms. that noue of the Alyens wist thereof. And that falls conspy
tour and traitor geffroy of Charney sith that he myt not open ly have his
purpose of the Castle privily and stelyngly he come in and held the town with
a great host / And when he with his men was comen in* he paid the forsaid
sum of floreyns as co uenau^t was between hem to a gen^wey in the town that
was ke per of the castle / and consenting to the same geffroy in all this
falsenes and trecherye* and bounden the Englyssh mynystres and servants that
were in the castle that they might not help hem self* ne let hem of her
purpose / And than wenyng that they had be syker ynowe they speken all her
wykkednesse and falsenesse openly* an high that al men might here /

And now shall ye here how they were deceyned* for they comen in by a prive
posterne over a little bridge of tree / And when they were comen in / subtylly
and privily the bridge was drawn up and kept that none of hem that comen in
might gone ont n^ no mo come in to hem / And anon our Englysshmen wenten out
at prive holes and wyndowes / and over the walls of the town and of the castle
/ and wenten / and foughten manly with the frensshmen that were without / and
had the better of hem the which when they weren occupied by hem self on her
side / the king that was within the town having with him scarcely but / xxx /
men of arms drew out his swerd / and with a loud boys cried* an high / A
saint Edward / A saint George / And when folk herd that / they comen rennyng to
him / and yauen to her enemies so great assaute / that there were more than two
honderd men of arms / and many other slain / and many fledden awey / and so
by the grace of god Almighty the victory fill to the Englysshmen / Than the
king took with him this gef froy that was fynder of this trecherye / and also
many other fre^ssh prisones / And within a while after come ayene in to
England* And in this same year / and in the year before / and also in the year
next after was so great pestylence of men fro the eest in to the weste / and
namely through botches that tho that siked on this day dyed on the in day / to
the which men that so deyden in this pestylence hadden but litell respyte of
lyggyng / The pope clement of his goodness and grace yafe hem full remissyon /
and foryeuenes of al her sins that they were shriuen of / and this pestylence
lasted in london fro mych^ mass in to august next folewyng almoost an hoole
year / and in the se days was death without sorrow / weddynges without
friendship wylful penance and derth without scarcite and fleing without
refute of socour / for many fledden fro place to place by cause of the
pestylence / but they were enfect / and might not escape the death after that
the prophet Isaie says / who that flees fro the face of dread he shall fall
in to the dyche / And he that wendeth him ont of the the dyche / he shall be
hold and teyde with a grenne / but when this pestylence was seced / as god would
uneaths the x part of the people was left alive / And in the same year bigan a

How king Edward had a great battle with spaynardys in the sea fast by
wynchelsee / Cao. / CC / xxixo. /
ANd in the / xxv / year of his regne abonte saint Johannes day in heruest in

How the great company aroos in france / and the white company in lumbardye /
and of many other marvel / Cao / CCo. / xxxjo. /
King Edward in the xxxvj year of his regne anon after cristemasse in the fest
of Conversion of saint paul held his parliament at westmynster / in the which
was put forth and she wed the acord and the tretys that was stabylyssed and y
made bitwe ne the ij kings / the which acord plesyd to much folk / and
therefore by the kings commandment there were gadred / and come to geder in
westmestre church the first sunday of lent. that is to say the ij kal of
feuerer the forsaid englisshmen and frensshmen / where was so^ge a solemn
mass of the Trinyte of the Archebisshop of canterbury master simo^d Islepe /
And when agnus dei was done the king being there with his sons and also with
the kings sons of france and other noble and great lords with candels y
light and crosses y brout forth / all that were called there to yt were not swore
before / swore that same oath that was written upon gods body and on the mass
book in this wise / We / N / and / N / swere^ upon holy gods body / and on
the gospels stidfastly to hold and keep toward us the pees and the acord y made
bitwene ye ij kings and neu for to do the contrary / and when they had thus y
sworn / they token her scrowes that her oaths were comprehended in to the
notaryes / and this same year in the asce^cion eve a bout mydday was seyn the
eclyps of the son / and there followed su che a drought / that for defaute of
rain there was great barines of corn fruit and heye / And in the same month
the vj kal of Iuyn there fill a sanguyn rain almoost like blood in burgoyne /
And a sangneyn cross fro morn unto prime Was y seen and appeared at bo loyne
in the air / the which many a man saw / and after it meued / and fill in the
mydde see / and in the same time in france and in england and in other many
lands / as they that were in pleyn co^trees and desert baren wytnes suddenly
there appeared ij castles / of the which went out ij hoostes of armed men / And
that one host was clothed. and heled in white / and that other in black / And
when batayl bitwe ne hem was bygonne / the white overcome the black / And anon
after the blac took heart unto him / and overcome the white / And after that
they went again in to her castles / And than the Ca stelles and all the
hoostes vanysshed awey / And in this same year was a great and an huge
pestylence of people / and namely of men / whose wives as wymmen out of
governance token husbondes / as well strau^gyers / as other lewd and simple
people / the which foryetynge her own honor / and worship and birth
coupled and married hem with hem that were of low degree / and litel reputacion
In this same year dyed henry dust of la^^stre / And al so in this year Edward
prince of Walys wedded the Cou^trsse of s^nt / that was sir thomas wife holand /
the which was departed sometime and deuorced fro therle of Salisbury for cause
of the same knight / And about this time bygan and aroos a great company of
diverse nations gadred to geder / of whom her leders and governors were
englissh people / and they were cleped a people with out an head / the which did
much harm in the party of france And not long after there arose another
company of dyuse nations that was callid the white company / the which in the
parties and co^trees of lumbardye did much sorrow / This same year sir John of
gaunt the sone of king edward the iij was made duk of lancaster by reason and
cause of his wife that was the daughter and heyr of Hen ry sometime duk of
lancastre /

Of the great wind / and how prince Edward took the lordshype of guyhenne of
his fadre / and went thither. Cao. / C Co. / xxxijo. /
ANd in the xxxvij year of king Edward the xv day of Ianiuer / that is to say
/ on saint maures day about euensong time there aroos / and come such a wind
out of the south with such a fyersnesse and strength / that he brast and use
we down to ground byghe houses and strong byldynges / toures / chirches / and
steples / and other things / and all other strong works / that stoden stylle
weren shake therewith / that they ben yet / and shall be ever more the febler
and weyster while they stand / And this wind la sted without any tellyng vij
days co^tinuelly / and anon after there folewed such watres in hey time and in
heruest time that all fold works were strongly let and left undone / and in
the same year prin ce Edward took the lordship of guyhenne / and did to king Ed
ward his f^dre feaute and homage therefore / and went over see in to Gascoyne
with his wife and his children / And anon after king ed ward made sir leonel his
sone duk of Clarence / and Edmond his other sone earl of Cambridge / And in the
xxx viij year of his regne it was ordained in the parliament / that men of law.
both of the temperall / and of holy church law fro that time forth should
plete in her mother tongue / And in the same year comen in to England three
kings. that is for to say / the king of France / the king of Cypres / and
the king of Scotland / by cause to vysyte and speak with the king of England /
Of whom they were wonder welcome and much y worshipped / And after that they
had be here long time ij of hem went home ayene in to her own countries and
kingdoms / but the king of france through great sikenesse and ma lady that he
had abode stille in england / and in the xxxix year of his regne was a strong
and an huge frost / and that lastid long / that is for to say fro saint Andrews
tide unto the xiiij / kal / of Apul / that the tilthe and sowyng of the earth
and other such feld works / and hand works were much y let and left undo
for cold and hardness of the er the. And at Orrey in britayne that time was
ordained a greet dedely battle between sir Johan of mou^tfort duk of Britayne
and sir charlys of bloys / but the vyctorye fill to the foresaid sir Johan
through help and socour of the englysshmen / And there were take many knytes and
squyers / and other men that were vnno^bred / in the which batail was slain
charlis him self with all that stood about him / and of the englisshmen were
slain but vij. And in this year dei de at sauoy John the king of france / whose
service and exequyes king edward let ordeyne / and did in dyuse places
worshipfully to be done / and to dover of worshipful me^ ordeyne him worthily
to be led with his own costs and expens / and from thens he was fet in to
fra^ ce / and beryed at saint denis / In the xl year of king edward the vij kal
of feuerer was borne edward prince edwardis sone / the whi che when he was vij
year old he deide / and in the same year it was ordained yt saint peter's pens
fro that time forth should not be paid the which king yuo sometime king of
england of the co^tre of west saxons that bygan to regne in the year of our
lord / vj / C / lxxix first granted to rome for the scole of england there to
be continued / and in this same year there fill so much xxi yne in sey time /
that it was ^d and destroyed both corn and hey / and there was such a debate and
fiting of sparewes by dyuse places in these days that men fou^den innumerable
multitude of hem deed in feldes as they we^ten / and there fill also such a
pestylence. that never such was seen in no man's time that time alive / for
many men anon as they were go to led hole and in good point sodanly they deide.
Also that time a sikenes that men called the pokkes slow both men and women
through her enfectyng / And in the xlj year of king edward was bore at bur deux
Richard the second sone of prince edward of england / the whi che Richard king
Richard of Armorican heued at the fonstone after whom he was callid Richard.
and this same richard when his fadre was deed / and king edward was deed also /
was crouned king of england the xj year of his age through right line and
heritage / and also by common assent and desire of the comynalte of the reame /
About this time at king Edwardys co^mau^ dement of england when all the castles
and tounes were yold to him that long were holden in france / by a great
company assembled to geder Sir bartram cleykyn knight / an orped man and a good
werryour went and purposed him to put out pyers king of spain out of his
kingdom with help of the most party of the forsaid great company /
trustyng also upon help and favor of the pope / for as much as it came to his
eres. that the same pyers should led and use the most werst and synfullist life
out / the which Piers y smyten with dread of this tydyng fled in to gascoyn
to prin ce edward to have help and socour of him / And when he was fled out
of spayn, Henry his brother that was a bastard by assent of the most party of
spain / and through help of that fere full company, that I spak of e^rst / was
made and crouned king of spayn / And the nombre of that same company was
rekened and set^e at the nombre of lx M fightyng men / This same year in the
month of Iuyn there come a great company and nauye of the danes and gadred hem
to gedre in the north see purposyng hem to come in to england to run and to
rob / and also to slay / with whom they countred and met in the sea marpners
/ and other orped fyg^ tyng men of the country and disparpled hem / And they
asshamed went home ayene in to her own cou^treye / But among all other there
was a boystous / and a strong vessel of her nauye that was ouersailed by the
englysshmen / and was perisshed and dreynt In the which the styward and other
worthy and great men of Denmark were take prisonners / and by the king of
england and his cou^ceyll y prisoned / the which lords the danes afterward
comen and soughten al about for to have had with her goods yt they had lost /
and they not well apayd ne plesed of the ansuer that they hadd here turned home
wards again leuyng behind hem in her ynnes privily y written in s^rowes and
on walls / Yet shall danes wast the wanes / Than happed there an english
writer and wrote against the dane in this manner wise / Here shall danes fet her
banes, And in this time pyers king of spain with other kyn ges / that is to
say the king of nauerne / and the king of malogre being menes wenten between
and prayed counseyll and help of sir Edward the prince / through whoos cou^seyl
when he had understood her Articles and her desire that he was required of tho
kings / loath he was and ashamed to say nay and contrary hem, but netheles he
was agast' lest it should be any preiudyce ^yenst the pope and long time t^ryed
hem or that he would grant or consent there to til he had better counsel /
and auysement with good delyberacion of king Edward his gretter and his fadre /
But when he was with every days and continuel besechynges of many noble men y
required and spoken to / and with many prayers y sent and made between hem.
Than prince Edward send to his fadre both by pleynyng lettres / and also
comfortable conteynyng all her suggestyons and causes with all that other
kings Epystles and lettres for to have comfort and help of the wrongs not
only to the king of Spain y do / but also for such things / as myt fall to
other kings / Also if it were not the so^ner helped / and amended. through the
dome and help of knyghthode to hem that it asked and desired / The which
letter when the king and his wise counceyll had seyne and vnderstonden / he
had great compassyon and heaviness of such a kings spoyllyng and robbyng with
much meruaylle / And sent again comfortable lettres to prince Edward his
sone / and to that other foresaid kings / and warned hem for to arm hem. and
ordeyne against that mysd^er / and to wythstonde hem by the help of god that
were such enemies to kings / when this noble prin ce edward had resseyued
these lettres him self with that other kyn ges before said all her counseyl
called to geder or yt he would under take the quarrel, he bound and knett sore
the king that was deposed with a great oath / that is for to say / that he
should ever after mayntene the right bileue and feyth of holy church and holy
chirch al so with all her mynystres / rightes. and lybertees. to defend from al
her enemies and al euyls / And all that were there against bit^: ly to punyssh
and destrouble / and all the rightes / lybertees / priueleges of holy church
increase and mayntene / and amend / and all things that were wrongfully
betaken / withdraw / and bore a wey by him or by any other by cause of him
hastily to restore ayene / and to drive and put out sarasyns, and al other
mysbyleuyd people out of his kingdom with all his strength and power / and
suffer / ne admytte none such for no manner thing ne cause to duelle therein /
And that when he had take a christian woman / he should never come in none other
woman's bed / ne none other mannys wife to defoule / All these foresaid things
trewelych for to keep con tinue and fulfill / as all his life time he was bound
by oath before no^ryes in presence and witness of tho kings with other Princes
/ And than that graceous prince / Prince Edward undertook the cause and the
quarrel of the king that was deposed and behight him with the grace of god to
restore him ayene to his kyn gedom / and led ordeyne and gadre to geder forth
within al have his na uye with men of arms for to werre and fight in this
foresaid cause And in this same time upon the sonde of the scottissh see / that
ma ny a man it sye iij days to geder / there were seyne ij Egles, of the which
that one come out of the south. and that other out of ye north and cruelly and
strongly they foughten to gedre and wrastled to geder and the south egle first
overcome the north egle. and al to rent and tare him with his byll and his
clawys that he should not rest ne take no brethe / And after the south egle
flygh home to his own costs And anon after there folewed and was seyn in the
morn before thr son risynge / and after in the last day of october save one
day many sterres gadred to geder on an hepe and fyl down to the earth le uyng
behind hem fery bemes in manner of lytenyng / whose fla^mes brent and consumed
men's clothes and men's here walkyng on the earth as it was seyn and known
of many a man / And yet that northeren wind that is ever ready and destynat to
al euel fro saint kateryns even til iij days after destroyed good without
nombre unrecoverable / and in the same days there fill, and comen also such
lightnynges / thonder / snow / and haylle / that it wasted / and destroyed /
men / beestes / houses / and trees /

Of the battle of spain besides the water of Nazers that was bitwene the
prince Edward and sir henry bastard of spayn / Capitulo CCo. / xxxiijo /
IN the year of our lord / M / CCC / lxvij / and of king Edward / xlij / the /
iij / day of April there was a strong battle and a great in a large field y
callid priasers / fast by the water of Nazers in spain between Sir Edward the
prince / and Henry the bastard of spayn / but the vyctorye fill to prince
edward by the grace of god / And this same prince Edward had with him sir John
duke of lancastre his brother and other worthy men of arms about the nombre
of. xxx. M. And the king of spayn had on his side men of diverse nations to the
nombre of an / C / M / and passing / wherefore the sharpnes and fiersenes of his
aduersarye with his full boystous and great strength maden and driven the
rightful par tie a bak a great wey / but through the grace of almighty god
passing any ma^nys strength that huge host was disparpled myt fully by the
noble duk of lancastre and his host / or that the prince Edward come nyghe him
/ And when Henry the bastard saw that / he turned with his men in so great have
and strength to flee / that an huge company of hem in the foresaid flode, and
of the brudge there of fylle down and perysshed / And also there were take the
Earl of Dene, and Sir bartram Cleykyn / that was che fe maker and cause of the
werre / and also Chyuetayne of the vau^t ward of the bataylle with many other
great lords and knights to the nombre of two thousand / of whom two honderd
were of France / and many also of Scotland / And there were felled in the
field on our enemies side of lords and knights with other me ne people to the
nombre of vj thousand / and mo and of English men but a few, And after this
the noble Prince Edward resto red the same pyers in to his kingdom ayene / the
which Pyers afterward through trecherye and falsenesse of the foresaid Bastard
of spayn / as he sete at his mete was strangled and deyde / but af ter this
vyctorye many noble and hardy men and noble of england in Spayn through the
flyxe and other diverse sikenesse token her death / And in the same year in the
march was seyn Stella Come to between the north costs and the west / whose
beams stret^d toward france / And in the year next sewyng of king ed wards
regne xliij in April Sir Leonel king Edwardes sone that was duke of Clarence
went toward Meleyne with a chose meyne of the gentiles of England for to wedde
galoys daughter and have her to wife / by whom he should have half the
lordshippe of meleyne / But after that they were solempnly wedded / and about
the Natyuyte of our lady, the same duk of Clarence deide And in the same year
the frensshmen breken the pees / and the trewes riding on the kings gronnde /
and lordship of England in the shyre and country of pountyf / and token and
helden Castelles and tounes / and bear the englysshmen on hand falsely and
subtylly that they were cause of brekyng of the trewes / And in this same year
deyde the Duchess of lancastre / and is buried worshipfully in saint paul's
church / The. xliiij year of king Edwardes regne was the gretest pestylence
of men and of great beestes / and by the great falling of waters that fille at
that time, there fille great hyndryng and destroyeng of Corn / in so much that
the next year after a busshelle of whete was sold for xl pens / And in the same
year about the last end of May king edward held tho his parliament at
westmynstre / in the which parliament was treated and spoke of the oath and the
trewes that was broke between him / and the king of france / and how he might
best upon his wrong ^e auengyd / In this same year in the assu^p cion of our
lady dyed queen phelyp of England a full noble and good woman / and at
westmynstre full worshipfully is buried and en tered / and about midsomer the
duk of lancaster / and therle of herford with a great company of knights
wenten in to france. where they get him but little worship and name. For there
was a huge host of frensshmen upon chalkhull bridge, and another host of
englisshe men fast by the same bridge that long time had leyn there / And many
worthy men and great of the englysshmen ordained and yafe cou^ ceyll for to
fight, and give battle to the frensshmen. but the foresaid lords would nothing
consent there to ne assent for no manner thing / There anon after it happed that
therle of warwyk come thyd ^rward for to werre / and when the frensshmen herd
of his coming or yt he come fully^h to land / they left her tents, and
pauylons with ^l her vitailles / and fledden / and went awey privily / And when
there le was comen to land with his men / he went in all have toward nor mandye /
and destroyed the yfe of Caux through dynt of swerd / and through fire, But allas
in his retournyng to england ward home ayene at Caleys / he was take with
sikenes of pestylence / and dyed not leuyng behind him after his days so
noble a knight and orped of arms / in which time reigned and werryd thylke
orped knit sir Johan hawk wode, that was an englisshma^ born / having with him
at his governance thylke white company that is a fore y ne^pned / ye which
one time against holy church and another time against lords werryd and ordained
great bataylles / and there in that country he did many merueyllous things /
And about the conversion of saint paul / ye king when he had ended and done
the enteryng and ye exequyes with great costs and rialtees about the sepulture
/ and beryeng of queen phelyp his wife, h^ held his parliament at westmynster in
which parliament was axed of the clergy a three years disme yt is for to say a
great dyme to be paid three year during / and the clergy put it of / and would
not grant unto Estre next coming. and than they granted well / that in three
year by certain terms / that dysme should be paid / And also of the lay fee
there was a three years yv y granted to the king /

How Sir Robert knolles with other certain lords of the reme went over the sea in to france / and of her governance / Capitulo CC / xxxiiijo. /
ANd in the / xlv / year of king Edward in the beginning king Edward with
unwise cou^ceyll / and indiscreet borewed a great so^me of gold of the prelates
/ lords / mar chau^tes / and other rich men of his reame seyeng that it should
be di spended in defendyng of holy church and of his reame / Never the latter
it profited nout / wherefore about mydsomer after he made a great host of the
worthyest men of his reame / Among whom were some lords / that is for to say
/ the lord fitz water / and the lord grau^son and other worthy knights / of
which knytes the king ordained Sir Robert knolles a proved knight / and a
well assayed in deed of arms for to be governor / and that through his
cou^ceil and governance al thing should be governed and dressyd / And when
they comen in to france / as long as they duellyd and held hem hole to geder /
the frensshmen durst not fall upon hem / and at last about the beginning of
winter for envy and couetyse that was among hem / And also discord they
sondred and parted hem in to diverse co^panyes unwisely and folyly. But Sir
robert knol les and his men wenten and kepten hem sauf within a castle in Bri
tayne / And when the frensshmen saw / that our men were deu^ded in to diverse
companyes and places not holdyng ne strengthyng hem to geders / as they ought
for to do / they fillen fiersly on our men / and for the most party took hem
or slowen hem / and tho that they took led with hem prisoners / And in the same
year pope urban co me fro Rome to Auynyon for encheson and cause that he should
acord and make pees between the king of france / and the king of England for
evermore. but allas or he bygan his tretys / he dyed with sykenes the xxj day
of decembre / and was y buried as for the time in the Cath^dral church of
auynyon fast by the high auter And the next year after when he had leyn so /
his bones were taken out of the earth / and beryed new in the Abbey of saint
^tour fast by marcile of the which abbey he was sometime abbot him self / And in
both places that he was buried in there be many great miracles done and wrought
through the grace of god almighty to many a man's help and to the worship of
almighty god / And after whom folewed next and was made pope Gregorye Cardynal
deken / that before was called pyers Rogyer /

In the same year the Cite of Lymonge rebellid and fought a yenst the prince as
other Cytees in guyhene for great taxes costa ges and raunsonnes / that they

went home ayene And about the beginning of march when the parliament at west

And in this parliament at the request and as king of the lords m hadrede of men

This same year yt king with a great host entered ye see to (...) ye se ge of

Of the death of prince Edward and of the lord latymer and dame alice peers
through whom and her mayntenours the reamme many a day was mysgouerned / Cao. /
CC, xxxvijo. /
NOt long after the lj year of king edwardys regne / he let or deyne and hold
at westmynstre the grettest parliament yt was seyn many a year before / In which
parliament he axed of the comynalte of the reame / as he had done before a great
subsydye to be granted to him for defendyng of him. and of his reame / but yt
comu nes ansuerd that they were so often day by day grieved and charged with so
many tayllages and subsidyes / that they myt no longer suffer no such burthons
and charges / and that they knewen and wysten well / yt the king had ynow for
saving of him and of his reame if the reame were well and truly governed / but
yt it had be so long evil y governed by evil officers / that the reame myt
nether be plentiuous of chaffare and marchandyse / ne also with richesse / And
these things they proffered hem self, if the king would certeynly to preue and
stond by / And if it were found and preued after that / that the king had need
/ they would than gladly every man after his power and state him help and lene
/ And after this there were publysshed and showed in the parliament many playntes
and defautes of diverse officers of the reame / and namely of the lord latimer
the ^yn ges chamberlayne both to the king and eke to the Reame / And also at
the last there was spoken and treted of dame Alice peers for the great wrongs
and euel governance. that was done by her and by her counsel in the reame /
the which dame Alyce peers the king had hold long time to his lemman / wherefore
it was ye less wonder though thurugh the f^lte of the womannys exytyng and her
steryng he consented to her le wdenesse and evil cou^ceylle the which dame
alyce / and also the lord latimer and other such that ste red yt king to euel
gou^nau^ce against his profit and the reames also all the comynalte axed and
desired that they should be meued / and putt a wey and in her stedes wise men
and worthy that weren true and well assayed and proved of good governance
should be put in her stedes / So among al other there was one among the comunes /
ye was a wise knyt and a true and an eloquent man, whose name was pyers de la
mare / and this same pyers was chosen to be speker for ye comunes in the
parliament / And for this same pyers told and publysshed the truth / and
reherced the wrongs against the foresaid dame Alice / and other certain persons
and the kings cou^ceill / as he was bode by the co^munes / and also trustyng
much for to be supported and mayntened in this matter by help and favor of
the prince / anon as the prince was deed at the Instau^ce and request of the
foresaid dame alice this pyers de la mare was Iuged to ^petuel preson in the
castle of notyngha^ / in the which he was ij year / and m ye vj ka^ of Iuil
lastyng that same parliament dyed prince edward king edwardes first sone / yt is
to say in trinite so^day / in the worship of which fest he was wont every year
where that ever he were in the world to make and hold the most sole^pnyte yt he
myt / whose name and fortune of knythode but if it had be of another ectour al
me^ both christian and hethen while he lived and was in good point wo^dred much
and drad him wonder sore / whose body is worshipfully y buried in crychirch at
canterbury / And in this same year the men and the earls tenau^tes of warwyk
arisen mal^ciously against the abbot and co^ue^t of euesha^ and her tenau^ts and
destroyed fiersly the abbot and the town and wounded. and bet her me^ and
slowen of he m many one / and we^ten to her ma^ners and places and did much
harm / and breken down her parkes and her closes and brenten and slowe^ her
wild beestes / and chaced be in brekyng her fissh ponde hedes / and led the
water of her pondes stews and rivers run out and token the fissh and bear it
with hem / and did hem all the harm yt they myt / m so ferforth that forsooth
they had destroyed perpetu ^lly that abbey with all her me^bres and
apportenau^ces / but if ye king the so^ner had helped it / and taken head
thereto / and therefore the king sent his lettres to therle of warrewyk chargyng
him and commau^dyng that he should stynt redress and amend tho euel ^ers and
brekers of his pees* And so by men ye of lords and other friends of both sides
pees and good accord and love was made between hem / and for this hurlyng as it
was said the king would not be governed at that time by his lords that there
were in the parliament but he took and made his sone the duk of lancastre his
governor of the reame, the which sto^e so still. as governor til the time yt
he deyde / The same year anon after Ca^delmasse or the parliament was do / the
king asked a subsydye of the clergy / and of the lay fee / and it was granted
him / yt is for to say / that he should have of euy person of the lay fee /
both of the man and woman / that passed xiiij ye re age iiij pens. out take
pour beggars / that were know openly for nedy pour beggars / and that he
should have of every man of holy chirch yt was beneficed or promoted xij pens.
and of al other that we re not promoted iiij pens / out take the / iiij /
ordres of the friar beg gers / This same year after mychelmasse Richard prince
edwardes sone was made prince of walys / to whom the king yaf also the duchye
of cornewaill with the erldom of chestre / And about this time the cardynal of
england. the iiij day before marye magdalene day after mete suddenly was smyten
/ and take with a palsye / and lost his speech / and on mary magdaleyne day he
deyde,

Of the death of king edward / and sir John monsterworth a knight was draw and
honged for his falsenesse / Cao. / CC / xxxviijo. /
Right anon after in the lij year of king Edward in the beginning of October
pope gregory the xj brought and reme ued his court with him from Auynyon to

iiij chyef tounes of england / and his head set upon london bridge / for this
same John was full untrue to the king / and to ye reame / and full covetous and
unstable / for he took oftymes great so^mes of money of the king and his
cou^ceil for men of arms wages yt he should have paid hem / and took it to his
own use, and he dredyng that at the last he should be shent / and accused for
the same cause fled privily to the king of france / and was swore to him /
and become his man / and behyght him a great nauye onte of spain in to
confusion and destroyeng of england / but rightful god to whom no priuyte is
unknow suffr^d him first to be shent and spylt or that he so traitoursly and
falsely his lyege lord the king of england and his people and his reame / in the
whi che ground ye same John was bore wikkedly through battle should destroy or
bring his cursed purpose about / In the fest of saint gre gory tho next after

at Shent and is buried worshipfully at westmestre / on whose soul god ha ne
mercy / Amen / This king Edward forsooth was of a passing goodness and full
gracious among all the worthy men of the world for he passed and shone by virtue
of grace y you to him fro god a boue al his predecessors / that were noble
me^ and worthy / and he was a well and a hardy herted man / for he dread neu of
no myshappes / ne harms ne euel fortune yt myt fall a noble werryour and a
for tunat / for both on land and on see / and iij al bataylles and asse^bles
with a passing glory and Joy he had eu the victory he was meke and be nyngne
homely sobre and soft to al man of me^ as well to strangers as to his own
subgettis / and tho other yt were under his governance he was devout and holy
both to god and to holy church / for he worshyped halp and mayntened holy
church / and her mynystres with all man reverence he was tretable / and well
auysed in temporal and wordly ne des / wise in cou^ceyll and discrete, soft
and meke / and good to speak with In his deeds and manners full gentill and well
y taut having pite of hem that were in dysese / plentiuous in yeuyng benef^tes
and alm^sse besy and curyouse in bildyng / and full lightly he bear and suffered
wro^ges and harms / and when he was give to any occupacion he left al other
thing for ye mean time and tendid thereto. semely of body and a mean stature
having al wey to high and to low a good chere, and there spra^ge and shone so
much grace of him, that what man man had behold his face, or had dremed of him
/ he hoped yt day that al thing should hap to him ioyeful and likyng / and he
governed gloriously his kyngedome unto his age ^e was large in yeuyng and wise
in spences, he was fulfilled with all honest of good manners and virtues / un
der whom to live it was as for to regne / wherefore his fame and his loos sprang
so far that it come in to hethnes and barbarye she wynge and telling his
worthynes and manhood in all lands / and that no land under heaven had brout
forth so noble king. so gentylle and so blessed / or might reyse such another
when he were deed / Never the latter lechery and meuyng of his flessh haunted
him in his age / wherefore the rather, as it is to suppose for (...) fulfyllyng
of his lust his life shorted the sonner. And here of take good heed like as his
deeds before b^re witness / for as in his beginning al things were Ioyefull
and likyng to him and to al people / And in his mydde age he passed all people in
high Joy worship and blessedness / right so when he drew in to age
drawyng dounward through lecherye / and other sins little and (...) all tho
Ioyefull and blessed things and prosperyte (...) and myshapped / and
infortunat things and unprofitable harms with many euylles began for to
spring / and the more harm is / it conti nued long time after /

How queen Anne was wedded to king Rychard / Cao. / xlo. /
ANd in this same year come queen Anne in to england for (...) be spoused unto
king Rychard / and her fadre was emperor of almayne / And king of beme / and

and so forth unto westmyn stre unto the kings paleys / and there she was
spoused unto king Richard well and worthily in the abbey of westmynstre, and
there she was crouned queen of england / And al her friends that come with her
hadden great yeftes / and weren well chered and refresshyd as long time as they
abyden here / And in this same year was a battle done in the kings paleys at
westmynstre for certain points of treson between sir Johan Anskley knight

king of spain and his power / And there the king of portingale had the
vyctorye of his enemies thurugh help and comfort of our englysshmen / and when
that iourneye was done the earl of Cambridge come home ayene with his people in

year king Richard held his Cristemasse in the ma ner of eltham / And the same
time the king of Ermonye fled out of his own land / and come in to england
for to have socour and help of our king against his enemies / that had driven
him out of his Royame / And so he was brought unto the king to Eltham / there
as the king held his ryal feste of Cristemasse / And there our king welcomed
him, and did him much reverence and worship and commanded al his lords to
make him all the chere that they could / And than he besought the king of
grace and of help / and of his comfort in his need / And that he might be
brought again to his kingdom and lord / For the Turks had devoured and
destroyed much part of his land / and for dread how he fl^dde and come hydder
for help and socour /

And the king then having pity and compassion of his great meschyef and
grievous dysese. anon he took his cou^ceyll / and as ked what was best to done /
And they ansuerd and said / if it liked him to give him any good / hit were well
y do. and as touching his people to trauaylle so far in to out lands / it
were a great Ieopardye / And so the king yaf him gold and silver / and many
Rych yeftes and ^e wells / and betaught him to god / And so he passyd ayene
out of england / And in this same year king richard with a ryal power went in

hem trewes certain years unto her askyng / And our king turned him home ayene

theye / And there Sir Johan holond the Earl of kentes brother slow therles sone
of stafford / and his heyr with a daggar in the Cite of york, wherefore the king
was sore ameued and g^eued / and rem^ued thens and come to london / and the
mayer with the aldermen / and the comyns with all the solempnyte that myt be
done riden against the king / and brout him rially through the ate / and so forth
unto westmynstre unto his own paleys / And in the ^x. year of king Rychardes
regne / he held a parliament at westmynster, and there he made ij dukes / and a

uncle Sir Thomas of wodestoke, that was Earl of Bukkyngham him he made duk of

/ Sir Johan holand / that was the erl^ of kentes brother / him he made Earl of

And the Earl of the march at that same parliament holden at westmynstre in
plain parliament among all the lords / and comunes was proclaimed Earl of the
march and heir apparent to the croune of England after king Rychard, the
which Earl of the march went over sce in to Irland unto his lordshippes / and
and lands / for the earl of the march is earl of vlster in Irlo^d and by
right line and heritage / And there at the castle of his he lay that time. And
there come upon him a great multitude in bussheme^tis of wild Irisshmen him for
to take and destroy / and he come out fiersly of his castle with his people /
and ma^ly fought with hem / and there he was take and hew al to pyeces / and
there he deyde / on whose soul god have mercy Amen / And in the x year of king
Richardys regne / therle of Arundel went unto the sea with a great nauye of
ships enar med with men of arms. and good Archyers, And when they come in to
the broad sce / they met with the hole flete / yt comen with wyn y lade from
Rochel, the which wine were enemies goods / and there our nauye set upon hem
and took hem all / and brout hem unto die uerse ports and hauenes of england /
and some to london and there ye myt have had a tonne of Rochel wyn of the best
for xx shyllyngster lynges / and so we had great chepe of wine through out the
reame at that time thanked be god almighty /

/ For he was cast both horse and man / and ij of his ribles broke with that fall
And so he was borne home out of smythfeld home in to his in / And within a

Amen /
How king Richard spoused dame Isabel the kings daughter of france in the
town of caleys / and brought her in to england and let her be crouned queen in
the Abbey of saint peter's of westmynstre Capitulo / CC / xlij /
IN the / xx / year of king Richardes regne / he went him over the sea unto
Caleys with Dukes / Earls / Lords / and barons / and many other worthy Squyers
with greet array and commune people of the Royamme in good arraye / as than
longed to such a worthy king and prince of his nobley and of his own person
to done him reverence / and obseruau^ce / as ought to be done unto her lyege
lord / and so might a king and Emperor in his own to abide and resceyue there
that worthy and gracious lady that should ben his wife a young creature of xix
year of age d^me Isabel the kings daughter of france / and many other worthy
lords of great name / both barons / and knights with much other people that
comen unto the town of Grauenyng / and two dukes of france that one was the
duk of Burgoyne / and that other the duke of barry that would no ferther less /
than they had pledges for hem And than the king Rychard delyuerd two pledges
for hem to go sauf and come sauf his ij worthy uncles / the duk of Gloucestre
and the duk of york / And they ij wenten over the water of Grauenyng / and
abyden there as for pledges / unto the time that the ma riage and the fest was
done / And that these ij dukes of france we re come ayene unto grauenyng
water, And then these two worcester thy dukes come over the water at Grauenyng /
and so to Caleys with this worshipful lady dame Isabel / that was the kings
daughter of france / and with her come many a worthy lord / and eke lady and
knights and squyers in the best array that might be / And there they metten
thith our meyny at Caleys / the which well comed her and her meynye with the
best honor and reverence / that might be. and so brought her in the town of
Caleys. And there she was resseyued with all the solempnyte and worship that
might be done unto such a lady / And than they brought her unto the king / and
the king took her / and welcomed her and all her fair meyne / and made there all the solempnyte that might be done / And than the king and his counceyll asked
of the frenssh lords / whether all the couenau^tes and for wards with the
composicion that were or deyned and made on both parties should be trewely kepee
and ^l de between hem / And they said ye / And there they sworn / and took her
charge upon a ^oke / and made her oath well and trewely it to hold in all manner
of points and couenau^tes without contra diction or delay in any manner wise /
And than was she brought unto saint Nycholas church in Caleys / and there she
was worthily y wedded with the most solempnyte / that any king or Queen might
be, with Archebisshops and Bisshoppes / and all mynystres of holy church /
And than weren brought home unto the Castle / and set to mete / And there
were served with all manner of delycasye of al ryal metes and drynkes.
plentyuously to al manet of seraungyers / and al other / and no creature warned
that feste, but all were welcome / for there were great hales and tents set
upon the grene without the castle to resceyue al manner of people / and every
office ready to serve hem all And thus this worthy marriage was solempnly y done
and ended with all ryalte, Then these ij dukes of france with her people to
ken her leave of the king and queen / and wenten ayene to Grave nyng water / And
there the frenssh lords / that is to say / the two dukes / and al her meyny
were comen over the water to grauenyng and there they metten / And every took
leave of other. and so they de parted / and our lords come again to Caleys /
and the frenssh lords went over the water / and so home in to france ayene
/ And anon after the king made him ready with the queen / and al his lords and

brought hem unto saint Georges bar in Southe work / and there they took her
leave, And the king and the queen riden to kenyngton. and than the people of

much prese of people both on horse and a foot that there were deed on the bridge
x^ persons of men of women and of children / on whose souls Almighty god have

/ and there was holden an open and rial fest at her coronacion of al manner of

And than king Rychard made a clerk of his Sir Rogyer walden Archebisshop of

And that was utterly destruction and end to him that was so high and

Of Sir henry of Bolyngbroke earl of Derby / that reigned af ter king Richard.
which was the fourth henry after the conquest Capitulo / CC / xliijo. /
ANd after king Rychard the second was deposed and put out of his kingdom, The
lords and the Comyns al with one as sent / and al other worthy of the Reamme
chosen Sire Henry of Bolyngbroke earl of Derby sone and heir of Johan the duk
of lancastre for his worthy manhood. that oftyme had be found in him. and in
deed preued upon saint Edwardes day the confessor he was crouned king of
england at westmestre by all the reames assent next after the deposynge of king
Rychard / Than he made henry his eldest sone and heyr prince of walys / and duk
of Corn wa ill / and earl of Chestre / And he made Sir Thomas of Arundell

the Northcou^tre. For there he was enfamyned unto the death by his kepar / For
he was kept there four or five days from mete and drink / And so he made his

was alive many year after his death / but whether he were alive or deed forth
they held her falls oppynyons and believe that men hadden in much people /
which come to great meschyef and foul death / as ye shall here afterward

And when king Henry wist and knew verryly that he was deed / he sete tere
him in the best manner / and closed it in a fair cheste with diverse speceryes
and baumes. and closed hem in a lynnen clothe al sauf his vysage / and that was
left open / that men might see his person from al other men / And so he was

/ And when all this was done / he was brought from saint ^ou ses in to the

have mercy Amen /

And in the first year of king henryes regne he held his Criste mass in the

Amen /
Of king henry the fyfthe that was king henryes son / Capitulo, CC / xliiijo
/
ANd after the death of king henry the fourth. reigned king Henry his sone that
was borne at mo^mouth in walis that was a worthy king and a gracious man / and
a great conqueror / And in the first year of his regne for great love and
goodness he sent to the freres of langely / there / as his fadre had done
berye king Rychard the second / and l^e take his body out of the earth ayene /
and did bring it to westmynstre in a rial chare covered with blak velvet and
baners of diuse arms about / and all the horses drawyng the chare were trapped
in blak and beten with dyuse arms. and many a torche brennyng by all the wey
til he come to westmynstre. and there he let make for him a ryal and a solemn

Of the lawde of king henry the fyfthe / and what he ordeyued for king Rychard.
and for him self after his death. Capitulo ducentesimo / xlvjo /
HEre is to be noted that this king henry the / v, was a noble prince after he
was king and crouned / how be it to fore in his yongthe he had been wyld
recheles / and spared no thing of his lusts ne desires, but accomplysshed them
after his lykyng / but as soon as he was crouned / enoynted and sacred / anon
suddenly he was chau^ ged in to a new man / and set al his intent to live
virtuously in mayntenyng of holy church / destroyeng of heretykes. keeping Ius
tice / and defendyng of his reame and subgettes / And for as much as his fadre
had deposed by his labor / the good king Rychard / and pytously made him to
dye / and for thoffence done to him against his lygeau^ce / he had sent to rome
to be assoilled thereof / for which off^ce the pope our holy fadre enjoined him
to make him be prayed for perpetuelly, and like as he had done to be taken from
him his naturel life / therefore he should do found / iiij / tapers to brenne
perpetuelly about his body / that for the extynction of his bodily life his sou
le may ever be remembrid / and live in heaven in spirituel life / and also that
he should every weke on the day as it comes about of his death have a solemn
mass of Requie^ / on the even before a dirige with ix lessons / and a dole to
pour people alwey on that day of xj shyllyn ges. viij / pens to be delyd penny
melo / And ones in the year at his annyuersarye his terement to be holden in
the most honest wise, and to be deled that day / xx / pound in pens to pour
people, and to every mo^st to have xx shillynges / which al these things
performed this noble king for his fadre / for king henry ye iiij his fadre per
formed it not during his ^f / whom as it is said god touchid and was a lepre er
he deyde / Also then this noble prince let do call le all the abbots and
priours of saint benets order in england / and had them in the chapitre house of
westmynstre for the reformacion of the order wheryn he had comynycacion, And
also with bisshops and men of the spu^alte / in so ferforth that they doubted
sore / he would have had the te^poraltees out of their hondes. wherefore by thaus
labor and procuryng of the spiritualte encouraged the king to cha lenge
normandy / and his right in france / to then de to set him a werk there that he
should not seek occasions to enter in to such matters / and al his life after he
labored in the werrys in co^queryng great par te of the reame of france /
that by the agreement of the king charlys had all the governance of the reame of
france / and was proclaimed regent and heyr of france / And so not
withstondyng all this greet werre that he had / yet he reme^brid his soul^ /
and also that he was mortal / and must dye / for which he ordained by his life
the place of his sepulture / where he is now beryed / and every day three masses
per tuelly to be songen in a fair chapel over his sepulture / of which the
myddedel mass / and the first / and less mass shall be as is assigned by him
/ as it apperyth by these versys fool wynge /

And yet the noble king henry the. v, founded / ij / houses of relygyon, one
called Syon beside braynford of thordre of saint Brigitte both of me^ and

by the ryngyng of the bellis of either place / each knows when they have

alms deeds as in the chartrehous certain children ben found to sco le / and
at syon certain alms given daily / And yet beside all this he has founded a
recluse / which shall be alwey a priest to pray for him by the said chartrehous

here may al princes take ensample by this noble prince / that regnyng so little
time not fully, x / year did so many noble acts / as well for his soul to be
perpetuelly re me^brid and praid for / as in his wordly co^questis, and he
being in his most lusty ag^ despised and eschewid sin, and was virtuous and a

About this time pope martyn deyde, And after him Eugenye the fourth was pope
