How Caleys and guyues were besyeged by the duk of Bur^ goyne. and how they
were rescued by the duk of gloucestre / Capitulo CC / lo. /
^His year was a great noise through al England / how the du ke of Bourgoyne
would come and besyege Caleys / wherefore the Earl of Mortayne with his army
that he had for to have gone with in to france was cou^tremau^ded and
charged that he should go to Caleys / which was at that time well vitail bed and
ma^ned / for sir John Ratclyf was lyeutenau^t of the king in that town / And
the baron of dudley lyeutenau^t of the Castle And the / ix / day of Iuyn the
duk of Burgoyne with all the power of Flaundres and much other people come
before Caleys and set his syege about the town. and every town of
Flaundres had their tents by hem self. And this syege endured iij wekes / In
the mean while the duke of gloucestre being protector of England took the
most part of the lords of England / and wen te over the sea to Caleys for to
rescue the town or to fight with ye duke and his host if they would have
abyden / This time london and every good town of england sent over see to this
rescouse certain people well arrayed of the best and chosen men for the war, and
the ij day of August the said duke of gloucestre arrived at Caleys with all his
army / and / v / honderd ships and moo / And the duk and all his hooste
that lay in the syege as soon as they espied the saylles in the sea* before
they approached Caleys haven / suddenly in a morning departed fro the syege /
leuyng behind them much stuff and vytaylle / and fled in to flau^dres and
py^ardye / and in like wise did the syege that lay to fore guynes / where as
they of Guynes took the greet gonne of brass called dygeon / and many other
great gonnes and serpentynes / And then when the duk of gloucestre was
arrived with all his host, he went in to Flau^ dres / and was therein xj days
/ and did but little harm except he burnt two fair vyllages, Poperynge /
and Belle / and other houses / which were of no strength. and so he returned
home again / Also this same year the king of Scotland besyeged Rokesburgh
with much people / But Sire Rauf Gray departed fro the castle / and ordeygned
for rescouse / But as soon as the king understood his departing / he suddenly
brake his siege and went his way / and leuyng much ordinance behind him /
where he gate no worship. This same year the second day of Ianyuer queen
Katheryn which was the kings mother / and wife to king henry the fyfthe deyde
and departed out of this world / and was brought ryally through london, and so
to westmestre / and there she lies worcester shypfully buried in our lady chapel,
And also this same year the xiiij day of Ianyuer fylle done the gate with the
toure on london bridge toward southwerke with two archis and all that stood
thereon / This same year was a great trayttye holden between Grauenyng and
caleys between the king and duk of Burgoyn / where for the king / was the
cardynal of england / the duk of Norfolk and many other lords / and for the
duk was the duchess having full power of her lord as regent and lady of his
lands. When was taken by tha^uys of both parties an abstyne^ce of were (...)
for a certain time in the name of the duchess and not of the ^uk because he
had gone from his oath and ligeau^ce that he had ma ^e to king henry / therefore
the king never would write ne appoynte ne have to do with him after / but al in
the duchess name / Also this same year queen Jane dyed the ij day of Iuyll
which had been king henry the iiij wife, and was carried fro bermondesey unto
Canterbury / where she lies buried by king Henry the ^ij her husbond / This
same year dyed all the lions in the tour of london / the which had not be seen
many years before out of mind /

How Owayn a squire of walys that had wedded queen kate ryn was arestyd / and
of the scysme between Eugenye and felix Capitulo / CC / ljo. /
IN the xvj. year of king henry deide Sygismond Emperor of Almayne and knight
of the garter / whose terment the kyn ge kept at saint poules in london ryally
/ where was made a ry al h^rse / and the king in his astate clad in blewe was
at even at di ^ge / and on the morn at mass / And after him was elect and
chosen Albert duk of Ostryche / which had wedded Sigismu^dus dough ter for to
be Emperor, This was taken and resceyued to be king of beme and vngarye
because of his wife that was sigismu^dus dou^ter which left after him none
other heyr / This Albert was em perour but one year / for he was poysond and so
deide / some say he d^d of a flyxe / but he was a virtuous man and pyteful so
much that all the people that knew him said that the world was not worthy to
have his presence. This same year one Owayn a squire of wa^s a man of ^owe
birth / which had many a day tofore secretly wedded queen kateryne / and had
by her iij sons and a daughter was taken and comanded to newgate to prison by
my lord of gloucestre protector of the reame / And this year he brake prison
by the mean of a pressed that was his chapelayn, and after he was taken ayene by
my lord ^e mond and brought again to newgate / which afterward was deliue ^d at
large, and one of his sons afterward was made earl of ri chemo^d / and another
earl of penbroke / and the iij a mo^st of westmestre which monk deyde sone
after. This same year also on Newyeresday at baynardyscastel fill down a stacke
of wode suddenly at after none and slow three men meschieuously and foul hurt
other / Also at bedford on a shrireday were xviij men murdered without stroke by
falling down of a steyr / as they come out of their common halle and many
foul hurt, In the xviij year sir Rychard Beauchamp the good earl of warrewyk
deyde at Roan he being that time lyeutenau^t of the king in Norma^dye, and from
thens his body was brought to warrewyk / where he lies worshipfully in a new
cha pel on the southsyde of the quyre / Also this year was a great derth of
corn in all England / for a busshel of whete was worth xl pens in many places of
england. and yet men might not have ynowe / Wherefore stephen Broun that time
maire of london sent in to pull se and brought to london certain ships laden
with Rye. which eased and did much good to the people / for corn was so
skarce in England / that in sum places of England pour people made hem bread
of fern rotes / This year the general counseyl of basyle deposed pope Eugenye,
And they chese Felix which was duke of Sauoye / And than bygan the scysme /
which endured unto the ye re of our lord Thu crist M / CCCC. xlviij / This
felix was a denoute prince / and saw the sons of his sons / And after lived a
ho ly and devout life / And was chosen pope by the counsel of basil Eugenye
deposed. and so the scysme was long time / And this fe lix had not much
obedyence by cause of the neutralite, for ye most part / and well nyghe al
cristendom obeyed and reputed Eugenye for very pope, god knows who was the
very pope of them both for both occupied during the life of Eugenye / This
same year Sir Rychard wyche vycary of hermettesworth was degrated of his priest
hode at poulis / and burnt at tourhylle as for an heretik on saint Botulphus
day / how well at his death he deyde a good cri sten man / wherefore after his death
much people came to the place where he had be brent / and offered and made a
heepe of stones / and set up a cross of tree / and held him for a saint til
the mayer and sherenes by commandment of the king and of bisshops destroyed it
/ and made there a donghylle / Also this same year the shereues of london fett
out of saint Martyns the grant the sayntuarye five persons / which afterward
were restored again to the sayntuarye by the kings Justices / After Albert
the third, Frederyk was chosen emperor / This frederyk duk of Osteryke was
long emperor and differred for to be crouned at rome because of the scisme but
after that union was had / he was crouned with Imperyal dya deem with great
glory and tryu^phe of pope nycholas the iiij, This was a man pesible, quyete /
and of synguler pacyence not hatyng the church / he wedded the king of
portyngals daughter /

How the duchess of gloucestre was arestyd for treson / and committed to
perpetuel prison in the isle of man / And of the death of master Rogyer
Bolyngbroke / Cao. / CC / lij /
IN this year Elyanore Cobham duchess of Gloucestre was arested for certain
points of treson leyd again her / where upon she was examyned in saint
stephens chapel at westmestre before the Archebisshop of Canterbury / and
there she was enjoy ned to open penance for to goo through chepe beryng a taper
in her hand / and after to perpetuel prison in the isle of man under the keeping
of sir Thomas stanley / Also that same time was arestid Master Thomas south
well a chanon of westmynstre master Io han hume a chapelayne of the said lady /
master Rogyer bolyng broke a clerk vsyng nygroma^cye. and one margery
Iurdemayn called the witch of eye beside westmestre / these were arestid as
for being of counsel with the said duchess of gloucestre / and as for
master Thomas south well he deyde in the toure the nyt before he should have be
rayned on the morn / for so he said him self that he should deye in his bed and
not by Justice / And in the year xx / master Johan hume and master Rogyer
Bolyngbroke were brout to the guyldhalle in london / and there before the mayer
the lords / and chyef Justice of England were rayned and dampened / both to be
dra we^ honged and quartred / but master John hume had his chartre (...) was
pardoned by the king / but master Rogyer was drawn to tiborne. where he
co^fessid that he deide giltles / and never had trespaced in that he deyd fore
/ Notwithstondyng he was honged / srded and quartred / on whose soul god have
mercy / And margery Iurde mayn was brent in smythfeld / Also this year was a
greece (...) ye in fleetstrete by nytes time bitwene men of court and men of lo^
don / and diverse men slain and so^me hurt / And one ba^l was chyef cause of
the mysgouernaunce and affraye / Also this year at chesyng of the mayre of
london the comyns named Robert clop ton and Rawlyn holand Taylour / And the
Aldermen took Robert clopton and brought him at right hand of the mayre as
the cu stome is / And then certain Tayllours and other hond crafty men cried
nay nay, not this man / but Raulyn hola^d / wherefore the Maire that was padysly
sent tho that so cried to newgate / where they abode a great while / and were
punysshed / In this same year were diverse enbassatours sent in to guyan for a
marriage for the king for therles daughter of Armynack / which was concluded
But by the mean of the earl of Suffolk it was let / and put a part / And
after this the said earl of Suffolk went over the sea in to france / and
there he treated the marriage bitwene the kyn ge of England / and the kings
daughter of Secyle and of Iherusalem / And the next year it was concluded fully
that marriage by which marriage the king should delyuere to her fadre the duchye
of Angeo / and therldom of main / which was the keye of nor mandye / Then
departed therle of Suffolk with his wife and diverse lords and knights in the
most ryal astate that might be out of England with new chares and palfrayees
/ which went through chepe / and so went over the sea / and resceyued her / and
sith brout her in the lent after to hampton where she la^ded / and was ryally
resceyued / And on Ca^delmasse even before by a great tempest of thonder and
lyghtnyng at after none Paulus steple was set a fire on the mids of the
shaft in the tymbre / which was quen. chid by force of labor / and specially
by the labor of the morrow mass priest of the bow in chepe / which was
thought Impossible lauf only the grace of god / This year was therle of
stafford ma de and create duk of Bokyngham / the earl of warrewyk / duk of
warrewyk therle of dorset marquys of Dorset / and the earl of Suf folk was made
marquys of Suffolk /

How king Henry wedded queen Margrete / and of her Coro nacyon / Cao. / CC /
lijio.
IN this year king Henry married at Southwyke Queen Margrete / and she come to
london the xviij day of May And by the wey all the lords of england resseyued
her worshipfully in diverse places / and in especial the duk of gloucestre /
and on the blakheth the Maire aldermen / and all the craftis in blewe gounes
broudred with the deuyse of his craft yt they myt be byknowen met with her with
reed hoodes / and brought her to london / where were diverse pagentys and
contynaunce of diverse historyes showed in diverse places of the cite Ryally
and costle ^o And the xxx day of may the foresaid queen was crowned at
westmynstre / and there was Iustes three days during within the sayntuarye to
fore the abbey / This year the priour of kilmyan ap peled therle of ^rmond of
treason which had a day assygned to them for to fyt in smythfeld / and the
lystis were made and feld dressyd / but when it came to point the king comanded
that they should not fight, but took the quarellys in to his own hond / and this
was done at the Instau^ce and labor of certain Prechours and doctors of
london / as master gylbert worthyngton parson of saint Andrews in holborn and
other / Also this same year came a great enbas sade in to england out of france
/ for to have concluded a perpetuelle pees / but in conclusyon it turned unto a
tryews of a year / About this time deyde saint bernardyne a gray friar /
which bygan the new reformacyon of that order in many places / in so much
that they yt were reformed ben callid obseruau^tes / which obseruau^ces ben
encrecyd gretely in ytalye and in Almayne / This bernardyn was canonysed by
pope nycholas the / v / In the year, M / CCCC and l / Ioha^nes de capestrano
was his disciple / which profited much to the reformacion of yt order / for
whom god showed many a f^u miracle also / here is to be noted / yt from this
time forward kying Henry never proufyted ne went forward. but fortune began to
turn from him on al sides as well in france / Normandy / guyan as in England,
so^me men holden opoynyon that king lenry gafe co^myssion plenarly to sir
edward hulle sir Robert Roo^ / dene of saint seueryns and other to conclude a
marriage for him with the earl of Armynaks suster / which was promised as it
was said and concluded / but afterward it was broken / and he wedded queen mar
great as a fore is said, which was a dear marriage for the reame of england /
for it is known verily that for to have her was de^uerd the duchye of Angeo /
and the erldome of main / which was the keye of Normandy for the frensshmen
tentre / And above this the said marquys of Suffolk axyd in plain parliament a
/ yv. and an half for to fetch her out of france / lo what a marriage was this
/ as to the comparison of that other marriage of armynak. for there should have been delyuerd so many Castles and Towns in guy an / and so much good should
have been yeuen with her / that al England should have been there by enriched / but
contrary wise fill where fore every great prince ought to keep his promise / for
because of brekyng of this promise / and for marriage of queen margrete what
loss has had the reame of England by losing of Normandy and guyan / by
dyuysyon in the reame / the rebellyng of Comyns against their prince and lords
/ what dyuysyon among the lords. what murdre and sleyng of them / what feldes
foughten and made / in co^clusyon so many that many a man has lost his life /
and in conclusyon the king deposed / and the queen with her sone feign to flee
in to Scotland / and from thens in to france / and so to lorayne the pla ce
that she come first fro / Many men deem that the brekyng of the kings promysse
to the suster of the earls of Armynak was cau se of this great loss and
aduersyte.

How the good duk of Gloucestre Humfrey the kings vncl^ was arestyd at the
parliament of bnry, and his death / and how an geo in main was delyuerd /
Capitulo Ducentesimo / liijo. /
IN the year xxv of king henry was a parliament at bury called saint edmondes
burye / about which was commanded all the comyns of the country to be there in
their most defensable array for to awayte upon the king / to which parliament
come the duk of gloucestre vmfrey the kings uncle / which had been protectonr
of England all the none age of the king / and anon after he was in his
lodgyng / he was arestyd by the vysecou^t bemond the conestable of england /
whom accompanied the duke of Bokyngham / and many other lords / And forthwith
al his ser uauntes were commanded for to depart from him, and / xxxij / of
the chyef of them were also arestyd / and sent to diverse prysons and anon
after this said areste the said duke was sone after deed on whose soul god
have mercy amen / but how he deyde, and in what manner the certeynte is not to
me known. so^me said / he deide for so row / so^me said he was murdered
bitwene two fetherbeddes / other said that an hot spitte was put in his
fu^dament / but how he dei de / god knows / to whom is no thing hyd / And
then^e when he was so deed. he was leid open that al men myt see him / and so
both lords and knights of the shyres with burgeyses come and saw him lie deed
/ but wound ne token could they perceive how he deyde, here may men mark what
this world is / this duk was a noble man and a great clerk, and had
worshipfully ruled this reame to the kyn ges behoof, and never could be found
fault to him / but envy of them that were governors / and had promised the
duchye of an geo and the Erledom of main caused the destructyon of this no ble
man / for they drad him that he would have enpesshed that delyuerau^ce. And
after they sent his body to saint Albons with cer teyne lyghtes for to be
buried / And so sir Geruays of clyfton had than the charge to conueye the corpse
/ And so it was b^ed at saint albons in the abbey / and / v / persons of his
household were sent to london / and there were rayned and Iuged to be drawn
honged and quartred / of whom the names were sire Rogyer cha^burlayn knight /
one myddelton a squire / Herbard a squire / arthur a squire / and Richard
Nedham / which / v / persons were drawn from the tour of london through chepe
unto Tyborn. and there ha^, ged / and late down quyke, and then stripped for to
have been heded and quartred / And then the marquys of Suffolk showed there for
them the kings pardon under his great seal / and so they were pardonned of
the remenau^t of the execucion, and had their lives, And so they were brought
again to london / and after freely delyuerd / Thus bygan the trouble in the
Reame of England for the death of this noble duk of Gloucestre / All the
comyns of the royame bygan for to murmr for it, and were not content / After
that pope Eugenye was deed / Nycholas the fyfthe was electr ^o pe / This
nycholas was chosen for Eugenye / yet hangyng the scis me / Notwithsto^dyng he
gate the obedyence of al Christian royames For after he was elect and sacred pope
/ certain lords of Fraun ce and of england were sent in to sauoye to pope
Felix / for to entrete him to cesse of the papacye / And by the special labor
of the bishop of Norwiche / and the lord of saint Iohans he cessed the se cond
year after that pope nycholas was sacred / And the said Fe lyx was made legate
of france / and cardynal of sauoye / And resygned the hole papacye to
Nycholas. and after lived an holy life / and deyde an holy man / And as it is
said almighty god shows miracles for him / This was the xx. ij scysme between
Eugenye and felyx. and dured / xvj / year / The cause was this / the general
counseyll of Basyle deposed Eugenye / which was only pope and Indubytate / for
as much as he observed not / and kept the decrees and statutes of the
counseyll of Constaunce, as it is before said / nether he rought not to give
obedyence to that general cou^seylle in no manner wise / whereof arose a great
altercacyon among writers of this matter pro and contra / which can not acorde
un to this day / One party says that the Counseylle to above the pope / that
other party said nay. but the pope is above yt cou^seil God blessed above al
things give and grant his pees in holy church / spouse of crist amen /
This nycholas was of Iene come^ of sow birth a doctor of dyuyuyte / an actyf
man / he reedefyed many places that were broken and ruynous / and did do make
a great wall about the palais / and made the wall new abonte Rome for dread
of the turks / and the people wou^dred of the ^syng, and resygnyng of felix to
him, considered that he was a man of so humble birth, And that other was of
affynyte to all the most part of Christian princes / whereof there was a verse
publysshed in Rome in this manner / ^ux fulsit mundo / cessit Felix Nycholao /

How Sir Frau^ceys Aragonoys took fogyers in Normandye And of the loss of
Constantynople by the turk / Capitush. CC / liiijo /
IN the year of king henry / xxvij. being trewes between france and england. a
knight of the englyssh party named Sir France is Aragonoys took a town of
Normandye named Fogyers against the trewes / of which taking bygan much sorrow
and loss / For this was the occasyon. by which the frensshmen ga te al
normandye / About this time the cite of Costantynople / which was the
Imperyal cite in all greece was taken by the turks Infydeles / which was
bytrayd / as so^me hold oppiny on. and the emperor taken and slain / And that
ryal church of sancta Sophia robbed and despoylled, and the Relyques and
images and the Rode drawn about the streets / which was done in despyte of
christian feyth / and sone after al christian feith in greece perysshed and ces syd
/ There were many christian men slain / and Innumerable sold and put in captyuyte
/ by the taking of this town / the turk is gretely enhau^sed in pride / And it
is a great loss unto al christian dom / In the year / xxviij / was a parliament
holden at westmestre / and from thens adiourned to the blak freris at london /
and after cristemasse to west mynstre ageyn / And this same year Robert of Cane
a man of the westco^tre with a few ships took a great flote of ships
coming out of the say laden with salt, which ships were of pruys / fla^ dres
/ hola^d and zeland / and brout hem to hampton / wherefore the mar chau^tes of
england being in flau^dres were arested in brugys Ipre and other places / and
myt not be deliud ner their dettis discharged, til hey had made a poynteme^t
for to pay for ^hame^des and hurtes of tho ships, which was paid by the
merchants of the staple every penny, And in like wise the merchants and
goods being in d^s ke were also arested. and made great amends, This same
year the frensshmen in a morning took by a trayn the town of pou^t al ar che'
and therein the lord Fauconbrydge was take prisoner and after that in december
Roan was taken and lost / being therynne the duk of Somersete Edmond / the Earl
of shrewesbury / which by apoyntement left pledges, and lost all Normandye.
and ^me home / And during the said parliament the duk of Suffolk was arestyd /
and sent in to the toure / and there he was a month / and after the king did
do fetch him out / for which cause all the com munes of england were in a
great rumor / what for the delyuerau^ ce of Angeo and mayn / and after losing
of al Normandy / and in in especyal for the death of the good duk of Gloucestre
/ in so much that in some places men gadred to geders / and made hem capitayns
as blewe berd / and other. which were resysted and taken and bad Iu styce and
deyde / And then the said parliament was adiourned to leycestre / and thider
the king brought with him the duk of ^uf folk. And when the common hows
understood that be was out of the tour / and comen thither they desired to have
execucion on them that were cause of the delyueraunce of Normandy / and had been
cau se of the death of the duk of Gloucestre / and had sold gascorne* and guyan
/ of which they named to be gylty / the duke of Suffolk as chyef / the lord
say / the bishop of Salysbury / Danyel and many moo / And for to pease the
commons / the duk of suffolk was (...) out of England / v / year / And so
during the parliament (...) went in to Norfolk / and there took shy^oyng for to
goo out of the re ame of england in to france / and this year as he sailed on
the (...). a ship of war called the Nycholas of tour me^ with his ship and
found him therynne / whom they took out / and brought him in to their ship
tofore the master and Capytayns. and there (...) was examyned. And at last
Judged to the death / and so they put h^ in a Cabon and hi^ chapelyue for to
shryue him / And that done they brought him in to dover Roode / and there set
him in to the boot / and there smote of his heed, and brought the body a land
up on the sondes / and set the heed thereby* And this was done the first day
of may / Lo what auayled him now al his delyuerau^ce of Normandy / And here ye
may here how he was rewarded for the death of the duk of gloucestre / Thus bygan
sorrow upon sorrow and death for death /

How this year was thynsurrectyon in kente of the comyns. of whom Iak ^de an
yrysshman was Capytayne / Cao. / CC / lvo. /
THis year of our lord M / CCCC. l, was the great grace of the Iubylee at rome
/ where was great pardon, in so much yt from al places in Crystendom great
multitude of people resorted thider / this year was a great assemble and gadyng
to geder of the commons of kent in great nombre and made an Insurectyon and
rebel led against the king and his laws / and ordained hem a capytayn call led
John Cade an yrysshman / which named him self Mortymer cosyn to the duk of
york / and this Capytayn held these men to geder and made ordenau^ces among
them / and brought hem to blakheth, where he made a bylle of petycyons to the
king and his cou^ceyl, and showed what Iniuryes and oppressyo^s the pour
comyns suffrid / and al under color for to come to his above / And he had a
great multitude of people, And the xvij day of Iuyn the king many lords
capitayns and men of war went toward him to the blacheth / and when the
capytayn of kent understood the coming of the king with so greet puyssaunce
withdrewe him with his people to seuenok a little vyl lage / and the xxviij day
of Iuyn he being withdrawn and goon the king come with his arm set in order
and enbataylled to ye blakheth And by aduys of his cou^ceyll sent sir vmfrey
stafford knight. and william stafford squire two valyau^t capytayns with certain
people to fight with the capytayn / and to take him and bring him and his ac
cessaryes to the king / which went to seuenok / and there the capitayn with
his felauship met with hem / and fought against hem / and in co^ clusion slew
them both / and as many as abode / and would not yield hem ner flee, During
this scarmuche fill a great varyau^ce among ye lords men and common people being
on the blakheth against their lor des and capytayns / saying plainly / yt they
would go to the capitayn of kent to assiste and help him / but if they myt have
execucion on the traitors being about the king / where to the king said nay.
and they said plainly that the lord say tresorer of england / the bishop of
salisbury / the baron of dudely / the abbot of gloucestre / Danyel and
Treuilyan and many mo were traitors and worthy to be deed / herfor for to
plese the lords meyne. and also some of the kings hows / the lord say was
arestid and sent to the tour of london / and then yt king heryng tidings of
yt death and ouerthrowyng of the staffordes with drew him to london and fro
thens to killyngworth / for yt king ne yt lords durst not trust their own
household meyne / Then after that the capytayn had had this vyctorye upon
these staffordes anon he took sir vmfreys salade and his briga^tyns smyten full
of gylt nails / and also his gylt spores / and arayd him like a lord and a
capytayne / and resorted with all his meyne / and also mo than be had to fore to
the blakheth again / to whom come the Archebisshop of Canterbury / and the
duk of Bokyngham to the blacheth. and spak with hym' And as it was said they
found him wytty in his talkyng and his request / and so they departed / And
the third day of Iuyl he come and entered in to london with all his people / and
there did make cries in the kings name / and in his name that no man should
Rob ne take no mannys good but if he paid for it / and come rydyng through the
Cite in greet pride / and smote his swerd upon london stone in Canwykestrete
And he being in the cite sent to the towr for to have the lord say / And so
they fette him / and brought him to the guyldhalle before the mayre and the
aldermen, where he was examyned / and he said he would and ought to be Iuged by
his peers / And the comyns of kent took him by force from the mayre and
officers / that kept him / and took him to a preeste to shryue him. And (...)
might be half shryuen they brought him to the standard in (...) and there smote
of his heed / on whoos soul almighty god have pity and mercy / A men / And
thus deyde the lord say tresour of England. After this they set his head on a
spear / and bare it about in the Cite / And the same day about the mile end
croume: was beheded / And the day before at after none the capitayn with ^y ne
of his meyne went to phelip malpas hows / and robbed him, and took awey much
good / And fro thens he went to saint mar great ^atyns to one gherstys hows /
and robbed him and took aweye much good also / at which robbyng dyuse men of
london of their neighbors were at it / and took part with them / for this
robbyng the peples hertes fylle from him / and every thryfty man was aferd for
to be served in like wise / For there was many a man in london that awayted and
would feign have seyn a common robberye. which Almighty god forbede / for it is
to suppose / if he had not robbed he might have goone far er he had be
wythstonde / For the king and all the lords of the Royame of England were
departed except the lord Scales that kept the tour of london / And the fifthe
day of Iuyll he did done smite of a mannys head in southwerke / and the night
after the mayre of london / the Aldermen and the communes of the Cite concluded
to drive awey the capytayn and his host / and sent to the lord scales to the
tour and to Mathewe gouh a capytayn of Normandy that they would that night
assaille the capitayn with them of kent / and so they did. and come^ to london
bridge in to southwerk er the capytayn had any knowledge thereof / and there they
fout with them that kept the bridge / And the kentysshmen went to harneis and
come to the bridge and shot and fought with hem and gate the brid ge / and made
them of london to flee / and slow many of hem / And this endured all the night
to and fro til ix of the clock on the morn And at last they brent the
drawebridge where many of them of london were drowned / in which night Sutton
an Alderman was slain / Rogyer heysant, and matthew gouhe / and many other /
And after this the Chau^celer of england sent to the Capytayn a pardon general
for him and another for all his meyne / And then they departed from south werk
every man home to his hows / and when they were al departed and gone. there were
proclamacio^s made in kent / southsex / and in other places that what man could
take tho Capytayn qnyk or deed shall have a M mark / And after this one
Alisander Iden a squire of kent took him in a gardyn in southsex and in the
taking the capytayn Johan Cade was slain / and after byheded / and his head
set on london bridge / And anon after then the king come in to kent / and
did his Justices sytte at Canterbury and enquere who were accessaryes / and
chyef cause of this Insurrexion And there were eight men Iuged to death in one
day / and in other places mo, And fro thens the king went in to suffex / and
in to the westcountrey / where a little before was slain the bishop of Sa
lysbury / And this same year were so many Iuged to death that xxiij hedes
stood at london bridge at ones /

Of the feld that the duk of york took at brentheth in kent / and of the birth
of prince Edward / And of the first batayl at saint Albons' where the duk of
Somer^ was slain, Cao. CC. lvjo.,
IN the year xxx the duke of york came out of the march of walys with the earl
of deuenshyre and the lord Cobham and great puyssau^ce for reformacyon of
certain Iniuryes and wrongs and also to have Justice on certain lords being
about the king and took a feld at bre^theth beside dertford in ke^te which was
a strong field / for which cause the king with all the lords of the land
went unto the blakheth with a great and strong multitude of people armed / and
ordained for the werre in the best wise / And when they had musteryed on the
blakheth / Certain lords were sent to him for to trete and make appoyntement
with him / which were the bishop of Ely / and the bishop of wynchestre and
the earls of sa lisbury / and of warrewyk / And they concluded that the duk of
Somersete should be had to ward / and to ansuere to such articles as the duk
of york should put on him / and than the duk of york should break his feld, and
come to the king / which was al promised by the king / And so the king
commanded that the duk of Somersete should be had in ward / And then the duk
of york brake up his feld / and come to the king / and when he was come
contrary to the promise before made / the duk of Somersete was present in the
feld awaytyng / and chyef about the king / and made the duk of york ride to
fore as a prisoner through london / and after they would have put him in hold /
But a noise aroos that the earl of march his son was coming with x M men to
london ward / whereof the king and his cou^seyl fered / And then they
concluded that the duk of york should depart at his wyll^ / About this ty me
began great dyuysyon in Spruyse between the great Master and the knights of
the duche order which were lords of that country tree / For the comyns and
Towues rebellyd against the lords and made so great werre / that at the last
they callid the king of ^ole to be their lord / the which king come and was
worshipfully received, and laid syege to the castle of Maryenburgh / which
was the chyef castle and strength of all the lord. and wanne it. and drofe out
the master of danske and al other places of that land. And so they that had been lords many years / lost al their seygn^ye and possessions in tho lands /
And the year of the Incarnacion of our lord M CCCC. and, liij on saint Edwardes
day the que ne margrete was delyuerd of a fair prince, which was named Edward
/ That same day Johan Norman was chosen for to ben Maire of london / And the
day that he should take his oath at west mynster / he went thider by water with all the crafts / where before time the mayre aldermen and all the crafts rode a
horsbak / which was never vsyd after / For syn that time they have gone ever
by water in Barges / Ye have well understand to fore how that contrary to the
promise of the king and also the conclusyons taken between the King and the
Duke of york at Brentheth the duke of Somersete went not to ward / But
alode about the king / and had great r^ule / And anon after he was made
Capytayne of Caleys / and rewled the king and his Reamme as he would / wherefore
the great lords of the Reame / and also the commons were not plesyd / for
which cause the duk of york the earls of war wyk and of Salysbury with many
knights and Squyers and much people came for to remeue the said duke of
Somersete and other fro the king / and the king heryng of their coming thout by
his counseylle for to have gone westward, and not for to mete with hem / and
had with him the duk of somersete. the duk of bokyn gham / therle of stafford /
therle of Northumberlond / the lord Clyf ford and many other / And what time
that the duk of york and his felauship understood that the king was departed
with these said lords from london / Anon he changed his wey and costed the
contre / and come to saint Albons the xxiij day of may / and there met with
the king / to whom the king sent certain lords / and desired hem to keep the
pees and depart / but in conclusion whiles they trea ted on that one side /
the earl of war wyk with the march men and other entered the town on that
other / and fought against the king and his party / and so bygan the bataylle
and fyghtyng / which en dured a good while / but in conclusion the duk of york
obtained and had the vyctorye of that iourneye / in which was slain the du ke
of somersete, therle of Northumberlond / the lord Clyfford and many knights
and squyers, and many mo hurt. And on the morn after they brought the king in
great astate to london which was lodged in the bisshops palace of london / And
anon after was a great parliament / In which parliament the duk of york was
made protector of England / and therle of warrewyk Capytayn of ca leys, and
the earl of Salysbury chau^celer of England. And all such persons as had the
rewle to fore about the king were set a part / and might not rewle as they
did to fore, In this same year dyed pope nycholas the fifthe and after him was
Calyxte the iij This Calyxte was a Catalane / and an old man when he was chosen
/ and contynuelly seek / wherefore he myt not perform his zele and desire that
he had against the turk conceived / and the cause of let tyng thereof was his
age and sickness / This Calyxte institued and ordained the fest of the
tra^sfiguracion of our lord to be hallowed on saint syxtes day in August because
of the great victory that they of hungary had against the turks that same day
he was cho sen pope in the year of our lord M / cccc lv / And dyed the year M /
cccc lviij, that same day that he ordained the fest of the tra^sfigura cion to
be hallowed / In this same year fylle a great affray in london against the
lumbardes / The cause bygan because a young man look a daggar from a lumbard and
brake it / wherefore the yo^gman on ^he morn was sent for to come to fore the
mayre and Aldermen / and there for the offense he was committed to ward / And
then ^e mayre departed from the guyldhal for to goo home to his dinner / but
in the chepe the yo^gmen of the mercery for the most part prentyses held the
mayre and shereues still in chepe / and would not suf fre him to depart unto
the time that their felaw / which was co mytted to ward were delyuerd / and
so by force they rescued their felawe from prison, and that done the mayre and
shereues departed and the prisoner delyuerd / which if he had be put in prison
had be in ^opar dye of his life / And bygan a rumor in the cite against the
lumbardes / and the same euenyug the handcrafty people of the town arose and
ran to the lumbardes houses / and robbed / and despoylled diverse of hem /
wherefore the mayre and aldermen come with the honest people of the town / and
drofe them thens / and sent some of them that had sto len to newgate / and the
young man that was rescued by his felawes saw this great rumor / affraye / and
Robberye. ensyewed of his first meuyng to the lumbard / departed / and went to
westmestre to sayntu arye / or else it had costed him his life / for anon after
come de^ an Oeyer determyne for to do Justice on al them that so rebe^ in the
cite against the lu^bardes / on which sat with the mayer: that time william
marowe / the duke of Bokyngham / and many other lords for to see execucyon
done / but the comyns of the cite secretly made them ready and did arm them in
their houses, and were in pur pose for to have rongen the common belle which is
named low belle but they were let by sad men / which come to the knowleche of
the duk of Bokyngham / and other lords / And incontinent they arose for they
durst no longer abide / For they doubted that the hole (...) should have arysen
against them / but yet nevertheless ij (...) in of the cite were Iuged to death
for this robberye / and were honged at Tyburne / Anon after the king queen and
other lords rode to couen^re and withdrewe hem from london for these causes /
And a lytil to fore the duke of york was sent fore to grenewyche, and there
was dischargyd of the protectourship / And my lord of Salisbury of his
Chauncelership / And after this they were sent fore by preuy seal for to come
to Conentre / where they were almost deceived / and the earl of warrewyk also,
and should have been destroyed if they had not seen well to /

How the lord Egremond was take by therles of salesbury^ sons / And of the
robbyng of Sandwiche. Cao. / CC / lvijo.
THis year were taken iiij great fisshes between Eerethe and lo^ don, that one
was called Mors marine / the second a swerd fisshe, and the other tweyne were
whales, In this same year for certain affrayes done in the northcou^tre between
the lord egremo^d and the earl of Salysburyes sons, the said lord Egremo^d
whom they had taken was condemned in a great sum of money to the said earl
of Salysbury / and therefore commysed to prison in new gate in london / where
when be had be a certain space / he brake the prison / and three prysonners
with him / and escaped and went his way / Also this year the earl of warrewyk
/ and his wife went to Caleys with a fair felauship / and took possession of
his office / About this time was a great reformacyon of many monastery es of
religyon in diuse parties of the world which were reformed after the first
instytucyon, and continued in many places. Also about this time the craft of
enpryntynge was first found in Magu^ce in Almayne, which craft is multyplyed
through the world in many places / and books ben had great chepe / and in great
nombre by cause of the same craft. This same year was a greet bataylle in the
marches between hungarye and turkye at a place called septe grade, where
Innumerable turks were slain / more by miracle / than by man's hond, For
only the hond of god smote them / saint John of Capestrane was there present /
and provoked the christian pe ple / being then aferd after to pursue the turks
/ where an infiny te multitude were slain and destroyed / The turks said that
a great no^bre of armed men f^lowed them / that they were aferd to turn again
/ they were holy Angels / This same year the prisoners of Newgate in london
brake their prison, and went upon the leedes / and fought against them of the
cite / and kept the gate a long while, but at last the town gate the prison
on them / and than they were put in feterys and yrons. and were sore punysshed
in ensample of other / In this year also was a great erthquaue in naples / in
so much yt there perisshed xl, M. people, that sanke there in to the earth / Item
in the year xxx vj saint Osmo^d sometime bishop of salysbury was canony sed at
Rome by pope Calyste / And the xvj day of Iuyl he was translated at Salysbury
by the Archebisshop of Caunterbury / and many other Bisshoppes / And in August
after Sire Pyers

THe duk of york / the earls of warwyk / and of Salysbury saw the governance
of the reame stood most by the Quen^ and her counceil / and how the great
princes of the land were not called to collceyll / but set a part, and not
only so / but that it was said through the reame yt tho said lords should be
destroyed utterly / as openly was showed at bloreheth by them yt would have
slain therle of salysbury / Then they for sauaaon of their lives / and also
for the common well of the reame thout for to remedy these things / assembled
them to geder with much pe ple / and took a field in the westcou^tre / to
which therle of warwyk come from Caleys with many of thold soudyours as
Andrewe trollop and other / in whose wysedom as for the werre he much (...) sted
/ And when they were thus assembled and made their feld The king sent out his
commyssions and preuy sea^s unto all the lords of his reame to come and
awayte on him in their most de fensable wise / and so every man come in such
wise that the king was stronger / and had much more people than the duk of york
and the earls of warrewyk and Salysbury / For it is here to be noted / that
every lord in england at this time durst not disobeye the out ne / For she
rewlyd peasybly all that was done about the ky^ / which was a good simple and
innocent man. And then when the king was come^ to the place where as they
were / the duk of york and his felauship had made their feld in the strengest
wise. and bad purposed verily to abyden and have foughten but in the night An
drew Trollop and all should soudyours of Caleys with a great felawship suddenly
departed out of the dukes hooste / and went st^yt unto the kings feld / where
they were resceyned ioyoully for ^y knew thentent of the other lords / and
also the manner of their feld And then the duk of york with the other lords
seeing them so deceived took a counseylle shortly in that same night / and
depar^ from the feld / leuyng behynd them the most part of their people to keep
the feld til on the morn / Then the duk of york with his second sone
departed through walys toward yrlond. leuyng his ol dest sone the earl of the
march with the earls of warrewyk and Salysbnry, which to geder with iij or
iiij persons rood ^yt in to deuenshyre / and there by help and aid of one
denham a squire which gate for them a ship / which cost, cc. xx / noblis /
and with the same ship sailed fro thens in to garneseye / And there refresshyd
them / and from thens sailed to Caleys / where they were received in to the
castle by the postern / ^r they of the Town knew of hit And the duk of york
took shippyng in walys / and sailed over in to yrlond, where he was well
received /

How therles of march warwyk. and salisbury entered in to Caleys / and how
therle of warrewyk went in to Irlond / Capitulo / CC / lxo. /
Then king Henry being with his host in the field not knowing of this
sodeyn departing on the morn fond none in the field of the said lords / sent
out in all have men to follow and pursue after to take hem / but they met not
with them as god wol de / and then the king went to ludlowe. and dyspoylled
the castle and the town / and sent the duchess of york with her children to
my lady of Bokyngham her suster / where she was kept long after / And forth
with the king ordained the duk of Somersete Capytayn of Caleys / And these
other lords so departed as before is said were proclaimed rebellys and great
traitors / Then the du ke of Somersete took to him all the soudyours that
departed from the feld. and made him ready in all have to go to caleys and take
pos session of his office / and when he come he fond therle of warwyck therein
as capytayn / and therles of march and salysbury also / and tha^ he lo^ded by
scales and went to guysnes / and there he was received / and it fortuned that
so^me of tho ships that come over with him co me in to Caleys haven by their
fre will, for the shipmen ought more favor to therle of warrewyk than to the
duk of somersete / in which ships were take diverse men as Ienyn fynkhill /
John felaw / kaylles and purser / which were byheded sone after in caleys And
after this daily come men over see to these lords to caleys and bygan to wexe
stronger and stronger / and they borrowed much good of the staple / And on that
other side the duk of somersete being in guysnes gate people to him / which
come out and scarmuched with them of Caleys / and they of Caleys with hem /
which endured ma ny days / During thus this same scarmuchyng / much people day
ly come over unto these lords / Then on a time by thauys of cou^ seyll the
lords at Caleys sent over master Denham with a gre te felauship to sandwich /
which took yt town / and therein the lord rivers and the lord scales his sone /
and took many ships in the haven and brout hem al to Caleys / with which
ships many maro^ners of their fre will come to Caleys to serve therle of
warwick / and af ter this therle of warwik by thauis of ye lords took al his
ships (...) ma^ned them well / and sailed him self in to Irlo^d for to speak
with the duk of york / and to take his aduys how they should enter in to en
glo^d ayene / And when he had been there. and done his erandes / he re turned
ayene toward Caleys / and brought with him his mother the countess of salysbury
/ And coming in the westcou^tre upon the sea the duk of excestre admyral of
england being in the grace of dieu acco^panyed with many ships of war / met
with therle of war wyck and his flote. but they fout not / for the substance
of the people being with the duk of Excestre ought better will and more favor
to therl^ of warrewyk / than to him / and they departed / and come to ca leys
in saufte blessed be god / Then the kings cou^ceyll seeing yt these lords
had geten these ships from sandwiche / and taken ye lord Ryuers and his sone
ordained a garnyson at sandwych to abide and keep the town, and made one
mou^tfort Capitayn of the town / and that no man ne vytaylle ne merchant that
should goo in to Flau^dres should not go in to Caleys / Then they of Caleys
seeing this / ma de out master denham / and many other to go to sandwiche, and
so they did. and assaylled the town by water and by land / and gate it, and
brout mou^tfort their capitayn over see to Rysebank / and there smote of his
head / And yet daily men come over to them out of al parties of England /

How therles of march. of warwyk, and of salisbury entrid in to england / And
of the field of Northampton / where diverse lords were slain, Capitulo / CC /
lxj /
ANd after this the said earls of March, warwyk / and of Salysbury come over
to dover with much people. and there londed To whom all the country drew and
come to london armed / And for to late the lords of the kings cou^ceyll know
their troth and also their intent assembled them / and told them that they
intended no harm unto the kings person, sauf that they would put fro him such
persons as were about him. and so departed from london with a great puyssau^ce
toward Northampton / where the king was accompanied with many lords / and had
made a strong feld without the town / And there both parties met and was
foughten a great battle / in which battle were slain the duk of Bokyngham
the Earl of shrowesbury / the vysecounte leamond, the lord Egre mond and many
knights and squyers / and other also / and the king him self taken in the
field. and afterward brought to london / And Anon afterward was a parliament at
westmestre during whi^ parliament the duk of york come out of Irland with the
earl (...) Rutland rydyng with a great felauship in to the palace at wes^
mynstre / and took the kings palace / And come in to the parlem^ chamber / and
there took the kings place / and claymed the croun as his propre ^he rytaunce
and right / and cast forth in writing his title / and also how he was rightful
heyr / wherefore was much to do but in conclusion it was appointed and
concluded that king Henry should regne / and be king during his naturel life. For
as much as he had been so long king / and was possessyd. And after his death the
duke of york should be king and his heirs / kings after him / And forthwith
should be proclaimed heir apparau^t / and should also be protector and regent of
england during the kings life / with maother things ordained in the same
parliament / And if king hen ry during his life went from this appoyntement
(...) any article concluded in the said parliament he should be deposed / and the
duk should take the croune and be king / All which things were enacted by the
auctoryte of the said parliament / at the which parliament the comyns of the
reame being assembled in the common hons comonyng and treatyng upon the title of
the said duk of york suddenly fill down the croune which henge then in the
mids of the said house / which is the fraytour of the abbey of westmestre,
which was ta ken for a prodyge or token / that the regne of king henry was
ended / And also the croun which stood on the highest tour of the ste ple in
the castle of Dover fylle down this same year /

How the noble duke of york was slain / and of the feld of wake feld / And of
the second Iourneye at saint Albons by the Queen and prince / Cao., CC / lxij
/
Then for as much as the queen with the Prince was in the north / and
absented her from the king / and would not obey such things / as was
concluded in the parliament / It was ordained that the duk of york as protector
should goo norward for to bring in the queen / and subdue such as would not
obey / with whom went therle of Salysbury / Sir Thomas Neuyll his sone with
much people / and at wake feld in cristemasse weke they were al onerthrowen and
slain by the lords of the Queen's party / that is to wete the duke of york
was slain. the Earl of Rutland / Sir Thomas Neuyll / and many mo / the Earl of
salysbury was (...) ^atayll was slain therle of Northumberlond / the lord (...)
John Neuyl / therle of westmerla^dys brother / andrew (...) many other knytes
and squyers. Then king henry that (...) king / being with the queen and
prince at york, heryng the (...) of (...) feld / and so much people slain and
overthrown / anon forth with departed al three with the duk of somersete / the
lord roos and othere toward scotland / and the next day king Edward with all his
army entered in to york. and was there proclaimed king / and obeyed as he ought
to be / And the maire, aldermen / and comyns sworn to be his lyege men / and
when he had tarried a while in the north / and that all the country there had
turned to him / he returned southward / leuyng therle of warwyck in tho parties
for to keep and govern that country / And about mydsomer after the year of our
lord M / cccc / ^y / and the first year of his regne / he was crouned at
westmestre / and enoyn ted king of england having the hole possession of all the
hole reame whom I pray god save and keep / and send him the accomplisshement
of the remanau^t of his rightful enheritau^ce beyo^de the sea / and that he may
regne in them to the playsie of almighty god / health of his soul / honor and
worship in this present life / and weel / and prouffit of al his subgettis / and
that there may be a vera^ final pees in all cris^ reames / that the Infideles and
myscreau^tes may be withsta^den and des troyed / and our feyth enhau^ced /
which in these days is sore my^ ysshed by the puyssau^ce of the turks and
hethen men / And that af ter this present and short life we may come to the ever
lastyng life in the bliss of henen / Amen /

Thus ends this present book of the Chronicles of England / Enprynted by me
william Caxton In thabbey of westmestre by london / Fynysshed / and
accomplysshyd the / viij / day of Octobre / The year of the Incarnacyon of our
lord God / M / CCCC / lxxxij And in the xxij year of the regne of king Edward
the fourth
